When I remember and take heed of the conversation of us that live in this
wretched life. in which is no surete ne stable abydyng. And also the contynuel
besynes of every man. how he is occupied and daily labors to bylde and
edefye as though their habytacion and dwelling here / were permanent and should
ever endure. and also practyse how they may get temporalle possessions. goods
and rychesses. of which they are never content ne satysfyed as for the most
party. but contynuelly entende and labor by many subtyl means how they may
encreace their said possessions and richesses for to come and attain to
worldly honor and estate. In which they wene be very felycyte and blessydnes
/ and when I have well ouerseen and examyned these foresaid things and life. I
find nothing in them but vanyte of vanytees and all vanyte and yet I merueylle
much of them that been learned wise and noble men in the law. that not
withstondyng their rychesses. and sure living as well in the spirituelte as in
the temporalte contynuelly labor to be enhaunced and promoted to hye
dygnytees and offices. as though therein were perpetuel felycyte. In which ye
may see at eye that al is but vanyte. and they that me^ repute for wysest and
gretest about princes in a moment ben overthrown and brought to naught. Not
withstondyng for the most part. they of the spyrytuelte and also of the
temporalte entende more to get. worldly honors. rychesses and possessions for
to satisfye the appetyte of their inordynate desire here in this transytorye
life / which anon and hastily shall depart fro the corruptyble body. tha^ they
do for theternal life which shall ever endure in Joy or in pain. Then to
the end that every man reasonable remember him self that he is mortal. and shall
without fail depart out of this life hastily and sone. and ought while he is
here living to purueye and ordeyne for the perpetuel life to come / and so to
live according to the law and comandements of our lord and ocupye him self in
virtuous ^^^racyons and works. in eschewyng al vices and sins and all the
branches of the^. that they may after this short and tra^sytorye life attain
and com to the ever lastyng life in heaven / I purpose and attend by the
suffraunce of almighty god to translate a book late delyuerd to me and reduce
it out of frensshe in to our common english tongue. in which every man may be
informed how he ouzt to keep the law and comau^deme^ts of god. to follow virtue
and flee and eschew vices and to pourueye and ordeyne for him spyrituel
rychesses in heaven ppetuel and permament / which book was made in frensshe at
request of Phelip le bele king of france in the year of thyncarnacion of our
lord MCClxxix. and reduced in to englisshe at the request and specyal desire of
a synguler friend of mine a mercer of london the year of our said lord / M.iiij
C.lxxxiiij. which book is entytled and named in frensshe. le lyure royal.
which is to say in englisshe^ the ryal book. or a book for a king. in which
book ben comprysed the x comandeme^ts of our lord. the xij artycles of the
faith / the vij dedely sins with their branches the vij petycions of the
pater noster^ the seven yeftes of the holy ghoost. the vij virtues and many
other holy things and matters good and prouffytable for the well of man's
soul. Then I exhort and desire every man that entendeth to the prouffyt and
seluacyon of his soul / to over see this said book / in which he shall find
good and prouffytable doctrine by which he may the rather attain to come to
everlasting blysse^ and always what that is wryton is under correctyon of
learned men / humbly besechyng them to correct and amend where as is any
d^faute. and so doing they shall do a merytory deed. For as nyghe as god has
given me connyng I have followed the copye as nyghe as I can. and I beseech
almighty god that this said werk may prouffyte the redars. and that is the
special cause that it is made fore / that knows god to whom no thing is hyd
/ which give us grace so to live virtuously in this short life. that after this
life we may come to his everlasting bliss in heaven ame^

Explicit
Here after ben contained and declared the x comandementes of the law which
god wrote with his propre fyngre / and delyuerd them to Moses the prophet for
to preche to the people for to hold and keep capitulo primo
FOr to have and to come unto the knowleche of the x comandementes of the law.
the which every creature reasonable is holden to keep for to have life
pardurable^ is to wete that sith the creaco^n of thumayn creature four laws
have been The first law is called the law of nature. which is none other
thing but knowledge of good and evil by the which we know that / which we ouzt
tensiewe after reason. and also that which we ouzt to flee. that is to do to
other that which we would after rayson should be done to us. and not to do to
other that / which we would after reason should not be done to us. and this law
gaf god to man and to woman in his creaco^n. and that same law every creature
reasonable ought to keep. and by ygnorau^ce he shall not be excused / sith they
have understanding of reason The ij law comes of the devil to destroy the
law of nature aforsayd. and that is said law of concupyscence which was put
in the creature reasonable by the sin of Inobedyence. which was in our first
fader / for tofore he dysobeyed to god by sin. the body humayn was obeyssau^t
to the soul and to reason entyerly. but as soon as he had dysobeyed god. the
body by concupysce^ce dysobeyed to reason. Of which it happeth often. how be it
that the creature by the first law of nature know the good to be done. and
the evil to be eschewed. Always by co^cupysce^ce and folisshe plesau^ce is
left the rizt Judgment of reason. and is enclyned to do the contrary. and
this says saint powle / that he fond a law in his membris^ that is to wete
the said law of concupyscence which gaynsayed to the law of reason which was
in the soul. and of this law of concupyscence set by sin in the creature /
None escaped but only Ihesu and the glorious virgyn marie. The iij law is
said the law wryton. which was delyuerd for the creature / that by the law of
concupyscence would enclyne him against the Judgment of reason to do evil. to
withdraw him to do sin for doubt of punycyon. and this law was delyuerd to
moses and to the children of Israhel / The iiij law is said of love and of
grace which is none other thing but to love god and his neighbor / And was
delyuerd by cause that the law of scripture which for dread to be punysshed
withdrewe the creature to do evil was not suffycyent / for how well that hit
empesshyd the deed / as towchyng the work. Nevertheless it empesshed not to the
creature the will to do evil / the which thing is dedely sin. as often
times as it is concluded in the thing that should be as to the deed. and this
iiij law of love is in ij comandementes pryncypally comprysed. The first is
this / Thou shall love thy god with all thy heart. with all thy soul. with all
thy entendeme^t / and with all thy might. The ij is that thou shall love thy
neighbor as thy self. And these two comandements ben so conjoined. that the
one may not be accomplisshed without that other^

Of the first commandment capitulo ij
FOr to have the knowleche of the said first comandeme^t ought to be known
that ij things enclyne us to love god. The first is to here gladly for to
speak of him and often. for naturelly when we here of any person said great
good. we ben enclyned to praise and love him. and therefore to goo often to holy
church to predycacio^s and sermons / is to a creature great vtylyte and
prouffyt. The second thing is to think often and to have in mind the great
benefaytes that a creature has received. and receives every day of god / for
naturelly we ben enclyned to love them that done us good. This love of god is
acquyred and gotten by these ij things in a creature and is kept and
multeplyed by ij other things. First for to wythdrawe and take away his heart
fro the love of temporal goods / for the heart may not be parfyte in diverse
things. and therefore none may love god and the worldly things together
perfytely / Secondly for to have steadfast pacye^ce in tribulaco^n and to suffer
it for the love of god. for the thing for which love has most trauayl. and by
most pain is gotten / ouzt to be most loved / and most derworthly kept. and
this sapyence is much necessary and prouffytable to al them that will goo with
god. For thus as says holy scripture. by many tribulacions / byhoueth us to
enter in to the royame of heaven. And this manyfesteth and shows to us the
lives of saints. which for to come to god have so much suffered and endured.
After it is to wete / that to thacoomplysshement of the said commandment iiij
things admonessheth the creature The first is to have in mind contynuelly the
goods that the creature has received of god. as said is tofore. For when the
creature consydereth that he has received of god body and soul / and al other
goods that he has. temporell and spirituel / the parylles also which he has
escaped^ The glory of heaven which he has apparaylled to us. the creature
humayn shall Judge that he owes to love god with all his heart The ij reason is
to have in consyderacion the great puyssaunce excellence and noblesse of god.
And with that the great inyserye and pouerte of our self. by the which
consyderacion. the creature shall Iuge^ that when he shall love god with all his
heart he shall serve him with al his might / which yet he does full little unto
the regard of his great excellence^ noblesse and puissa^ce And therefore the
creature humayne ought always the more to enforce him to love. to serve. and to
honor god / The third reason is to take away the love and affection of
worldly things as said is tofore. For where all the heart suffyseth not for to
love god suffysauntly. considered his great excellence noblesse and puyssau^ce
as tofore is said. then he that puts in his heart the love of things
temporelle. which ben not but fylthe and ordure to the regard of god. seems
well that he does to god great vylonye / and in this caas he loves not god with
al his heart after the said commandment. for of so much as the heart of the
creature is set to love other thing than god. of so much is it less in god
The fourth reason is to keep him self and to put from him al sins. and in
especial dedely sin. for no creature being in dedely sin may love god. For
by dedely sin the creature offends god and is pryued and out of grace.
which is thing contrary to his love.

Of the first commandment of the law capitulo iij
WE ought then according to the said first commandment to love god with all
our heart. The which thing the creature does / when in all his werkys his
entencyon is ryghtful and after gods will. For thentencyon of the creature
is of such virtue that he render his works and his operacyon after god good or
evil / and therefore what so ever work that the creature do if his entencyon
be evil. thoperacyon and all the work is without merit. and conuertyd fro
hit. in to evil. hereof it is said in the gospel by our savior Ihesu christ. if
thyn eye be evil al thy body is derke / That is to say if thyn entencyon be
evil / al thy werkys ben derke and in sin and without merit. And therefore
it behooves to render the work of the creature good and merytorye. and that
his entencyon be ryghtful according to goddys will / But by cause that she to
^^ndre the work of the creature good and merytorye according to god /
suffyseth not only good entencyon / But it (...) to have the ryghtful
entencion and good will like as it may appyere in him. that will feel and take
other men^^s good^s for to nourysshe and feed the pour people / For the^te^cyon
of the will to give for gods sake to the pour people is good. But the will
to stele or take aweye other me^nes goods is evil for to so do. And therefore
that deed shall be evil / and may not be excused. For by cause that an evil
werk for any good entencyon may not be excused^ It is said after in the said
commandment. that the creature ought to love god with all his soul. That is to
say that his will accord in all his werkys to the will of god. and this
demand we of god when we say our pater no^^er. when we pray god that his
will be done in us Item by cause that yet for tacco^plisshe the said
commandment. suffyse not only good entencyon and good will / it is after
said in the same comandement^ that the creature ought to love his god with all
his entendement and understanding. That is to say that in thentendement of the
creature be no dedely sins delybered by consentyng ne concluded. For all
consentynges concluded in thing that should be as touching the deed of dedely
sin. though so be that the deed be not done outward as touching the work
that any thing ensie we thereof / yet it is dedely sin. And the creature
being in dedely sin may not love god as above is said / Item by cause that
yet for taccomplysshe the said commandment suffyse not only good entencyon
and good will as touching the works wythoutforth^ and that in thentendement
of the creature grows dedely sin by consentyng / but it behooves that the
creature put and employe all the strength and puyssaunce that he has in good
werkys. Just and virtuous / that they be to thonour of god and to the
salvation of him self and of his neighbor. It is said after in the said
commandment that the creature ought to love his god with all his might and
strength / And therefore al they that put and employe all their might and
strength in the werkys of sin / done against the said comandeme^t and sin
dedely / Thus it appyereth clearly that for taccomplysshe the said first
commandment pryncypal. The creature ought to give to god. entencyon. will /
entendement. and al his strength by the manner aforesaid /

The second commandment of the law is how each man ought to love his neghbour
Capo. iiij
FOr to have the knowleche of the second commandment pryncypal aforesaid
touching the love of his neighbor whom the creature ought to love as him
self. It is to wete that to the love of our neighbor four things ouzt to move
us. First for by cause that we al ben children of god by creacyon. And
naturelly brethern and systers love that one that other. And thus we ben al
members of Ihesu Christ. which is our heed. and one membre loves another
naturelly / Secondly to this ought to bring us the love and obeyssaunce that
we owe to god as said is. which comau^deth us to love our neighbor Thyrdly to
this love ought to bring us the commynycacyon which is emonge creatures
humayn. For one lord has made us al and created / for us al he has suffryd
death. And to us all he has apparaylled the glory and the beatytude of heaven.
if we lose it not by sin. And naturelly every creature of one lykenes / of
one form / and of one semblau^ce loves and ought to love the other. like as
we see in beestys and in birds that each love other. and him that is to him
like and his pareyll. And therefore every creature that loves not his neighbor
mespryseth not only against the law dyuyne but also against the law of nature
/ The fourth thing that to this love ought to bring us. is the prouffyte that
comes thereof / For when a creature loves well another he desires his
prouffyte / his honor. his sauement. and pourchasseth it gladly. By these
four things aforesaid appears clearly that we ought to love our neighbor as
our self. and this love is in five things. First when one loves his neighbor
truly / that is to say for the well of him / and that is in him and no thing
for his owen propre. To the knowleche of which thing is to wete emonge
reasonable creatures. three manners of love been founden /

Here is contained how one ought to love his neighbor capitulo v
THe first is when a creature loves another creature for the prouffyt that he
does to him / and this love is not very. For when the prouffyt faylleth the
love faylleth. The second is when a creature loves another creature for her
beauty. and the play^yr and delight that he takes therein. This love is not
very. For she faylleth when the playsyr or delight faylleth / The third is when
for the love of god and for the well of him the creature loves another
creature / And this love is good and very. and according to god. Secondly when
one loneth his neighbor ordynatly / that is to wete less tha^ god^ Thus as
the creature owes to love him self less than god. And this techeth us our
savior Ihesu Christ when he says. He that loves fader or mother. or suster. or
brother / or children. or any other thing more than me. he is not worthy to
have me / how shall this be known. Saint gregory enseygneth it to us / that the
works of withoutforth done for a creature show the love that one has to him
wythinforth. For naturelly one does gladly which he weneth that hit ought to
plese him or her that he loves And by this it apperyth clearly that when any
creature leueth to do the works. the which according to god he is holden and
bounden. For to do other werkys contrary to the playsyr of the creature /
then he loves that creature more than he does god / And in this doing he
mespryseth against the two commandments aforesaid and synneth dedely /
Thyrdly the love aforesaid is when the creature loves his neighbor by deeds /
That is do say not by words only. But in fayte and deed to procure in him
his prouffyte. and to empesshe and let his dommage with his power. as he
does to him self / Fourthly when a creature loves his neygbour in all times.
That is to understand also well in the time of his aduersyte and of his pouerte
/ as in the time of his richesse and of his prosperyte / For in especyal in the
time of aduersyte and of pouerte / the very friend is proved / Fyfthly when
the creature loves his neighbor holyly / That is to say that the creature
ought not to love another for to draw him unto sin. or for to be his fellow
in evil werkys. As been they that acoompanye them to rob and stele other
mennys goods. or do other evil and wicked deeds. For after reason thou
sholdest not Judge that thou ought do such things. After the five things
that every creature ought to render unto his neighbor after the said second
commandemente. is to wete that two things shown pryncypally the loue^ when it
is in the creatures / The first is for to have pacyence and compassyon in
myschyef and in the aduersyte or pouerte of other. For one excuses and
pardonneth gladly and lightly the defaulte or offense of the person that he
loves. and these be signs of great love. The ij is humylyte which causes
pacyence For comynly when a person is proud he knows not his defaultes /
But despyseth the other by presumpcyon. and may not supporte the defaultes that
he judges in them. But he is Inpacyent. And wythouteforth he shows and
manyfesteth often anger and dysplaysaunce. But by cause that the said
commandment for to love his neighbor as him self was by the Jews and
pharysees evil vnderstonden. and may be and is yet by many either. For they
hold that they ought love them that louen hem. and to hate them that hate hem.
and for their neighbor they understood only their frendys It is to
understand that when love or hate is in a creature / ij things ben to be
considered. that is to wete the nature that he has and the sin or defaulte
of him. every creature of god after his nature. ought to be byloued. but his
sin and defaulte ouzt to be hated / And after this exposycyon ought to be
vnderstonden the commandment that Ihesu Christ maad to his appostles for to love
their enemies / For the nature humayn we ought to love. and to do well to them
that hate us / and pray for them that do to us evil. and that persecute us /
But we owe alweye to hate their sins and their defaultes. Nevertheless we
may well. and is leefful to us to desire the destructyon of a creature obstynat
in evil and in sins. and that destroys holy church. and domageth and
hurts other / For the desire of this. is to desire the good of other. and
nothing the evil. to the end that he seace to do evil / and persevere in evil /
And not only for his destructyon. Such people wha^ they have desired after
thentendement aforesaid ben called after thappostle the mynystres of god /

Here after follows the ten commandments of the law partyculer capitulo vj
NOw it is to wete that these two pryncypal commandments aforsayd were given
to moses / when god delyuerd to him the law in ten comandements particular.
The which comandementes every creature reasonable is bounden to keep for to
have the life and glory perdurable. The three first have regard to the
dylection and love of god according unto the pryncipal commandment tofore
said. And the seven other partyculer apperteynen to the love and to the
dylectyon obhys neighbor. according to that other commandment pryncypal after
ensyewyng / And of the same x comandements there ben tweyne affyrmatyues only
which enduce the creature to do well / and viij other negatyues which defend
to do evil / The cause is for so much as for to keep him from doing evil / is
in the puyssance of the creature for the free will that he has to the which
he may not be constrained. but to do well is not in the puyssance of the
creature. but it is the special grace of god.

Of the three first comandements partyculer capo. vij
FOr to have the knowleche of the iij first comandeme^tes apperteynyng to the
love and dylectyon of god. It is to wete that a very subgette owes to his
lord three things / the which the creature owes to god soueraynly / The first
is feyth or fydelyte. that is to say that thonour / seruyse and obeyssaunce
that the subgette owes to his lord. and the seygnorye that he ought to have
over him be not by him delyuerd to another / For in such a caas he should be
holden for a traytre and for falls and evil / And upon this was given of god to
moses the first commandment which is such. Thou shall not adoure no strange
god. That is to say / thobeyssau^ce. honor and service that the creature
ought to do to god / like as hit is devised upon the first commandment
pryncypalle. he shall in no wise do unto any other than to god.

Against this commandment done and sin mortally all tho people that entremece
them of dyuynacyons. of fortyleges and sorceryes. For after Saint Austyn such
things may not be maad ne done without to have any or sum couenau^tes with
the devil. by the which all such things been said and made / And therefore
al such people be cursyd and excomenyed of holy church. And yet also al they
that hold and believe that the p^anettys and the sterrys govern the souls of
the creatures / For god only governs man and woman / and for to serve man
and woman they ben maad and created / Thyrdly all they that in any other manner
thing what someuer it be that set more their hope in than in god / be it in
goods temporelle or in creatures or that more love them than god^ The which
happeth wha^ for such love / or for to get such a thing / the creature
dysobeyeth to the comandements of god and of holy church Fourthly al they that
for to obey to them and to do their plesyrs. make their subgetcis or
servants to dysobeye the comandementes of god and holy church. Fyfthly and
al they that in such a caas obey to the creature. And yet also all them that
more believe to their own wit than they do to the comaundementes of god^ and
to the ordyna^ces of holy church / as do they that retche not to know the
comandementes of god. the artycles of the feythe. and all other things that
of necessyte ben to be byleuyd / kept and holden for to have glory and life
perdurable / But many believe to get heaven by their folysshe presumpcion / And
therefore they will govern them at their playsyr and will. and yet all they
that for to have the delectacyons and the eases of the flesh and of their
bodies dysobeye to god and to his comandementes.

The second thing that the very subgette owes to his lord capitulo viij
THe second thing that the very subget owes to his lord. and in especyal to
god. is that he ne say ne do thing that may be to his vylonnye / or to his
Iniurye or dyshonoure And upon this was delyuerd the second commandemente
apperteynyng to the love of god which is such. Thou shall not take the name
of thy god in vain / That is to say for to afferme and do believe thing that
thou say or do / thou shalt not swear the name of god. but for things
verytable and for good and Just cause / and yet in caas of need and of
necessyte / For oath is ordained for to set an end in things lytigyous and
debateful. of which feyth or demonstrau^ce may in none otherwise be known but
by oath. And in this was restrained to the christian that^ which was granted to
the Jews / For it was leefful to them to swear and not to be perjured. But to
the christian people is not only defended to pariure and forswere him self. but
also to swere^ Except in caas of necessyte as said is And therefore it is said
by our savior Ihesu Christ if thou wylt any thing afferme or deny late thy
word be. it is thus. or it is not thus. and if thou make oath of habundance.
but in caas of necessyte it is evil and it is sin And the cause of this
restraynte or defense is / by cause that the creature has no membre so feeble
ne to the keeping may by a creature be less set. than in the tongne. And to
this purpoos says Saint James thappostle. that all nature of beestys. of
birds and of serpentys may be dompted and taken by the creature humayne but
none may not ne will not refrain his tongue. ne keep him from evil saying or of
ouermoche spekyng /

And therefore says the holy appostle sweet Saint James that the man is parfyte
and wise that sets to his tongue such guard. that he mespryse not ne sin
not in his spekyng And for that fraylnes the creature that uses or
accustommeth him for to swear periureth or forsweryth him lyghtlye. The which
thing of him self is dedely sin when the pariuryng is made in ernest and by
delyberacyon / and the most grettest sin that is after / is to adoure
strange gods. which is said sin of ydolatrye. And therefore not to take the
name of god in vain by the manner that said is / was the second commandment
given of our lord to moses as tofore is said.

The third thing that the very subgette owes unto his lord capitulo ix
THe third thing that the very subgette owes to his lord and soueraynly to
god / is service / and upon this was deyluerd to Moses the third commandment
apperteynyng to the dylectyon and love of god. and is such as follows / Thou
shalt halowe or sayntefye the sunday / that is to say Thou shall seace the
said day fro al worldly works / and in especyal of the werkys of sin / And
that day thou shalt employe and occupye thy self in the praysyng and in the
service of god In knowlechyng the benefaytes and the grace that thou have of
him / And god would that by the Jews the sabate day should be employed in his
praysyng and his seruyse / In mind of that which he had made and fourmed all
things And the seventh day he had seaced and did rest to make new creatures
/ And by the christian people instead of the said sabat day that the Jews
hallowed The day of sunday has been ordained in mind of the recreacyon of the
creature reasonable maad by the resurrexyon of Ihesu Christ / which aroos on
such a day. And semblably the frestys of Saints. and the solempnytees
commanded by the church to be kept also like as the sunday ought every
creature temploye in the praysyng and loange of god and of his saints and to
seace and rest fro all erthely and worldly works. and in especyal from sin.
And in especyal the creature ought to cease of two things First fro al werkys
temporelle. erthely. and corporelle. except in four caases. The first is for
to have the necessyte of his life The second for the necessyte of the life of his
neighbor / The third for the necessyte of holy church / The fourth for
thauctoryte of his souerayn and for his commandment. when in such days he
comandeth to work for any causes Just and reasonable. In which four caases
it is leefful to a creature on the said days to do work corporelle The second
thing whereof thumayn creature ought to cesse in especyal on the said days. is
to do sin. and in especyal dedely sin. For how well that a creature ought to
keep him self from sin and in especyal dedely / Nevertheless sin done in the
said days is much more grievous than in other days. The third thing whereof a
creature ought to keep him in. the said dayes^ is of ydlenes / For for to be
idle is cause of over much evil and of sins / and in especyal on the said
days ought a creature to occupye and enbesye him in three things. First in
making sacrefyse to god of him self. and of all that he has. and in especyal a
creature ought on the said days to give him self to god by devout orysons
and prayer. And to have great sorrow and bitter repe^tau^ce of his sins.
Secondly a creature ouzt to occupye him in the loange and praysyng of his maker
and creator. And by cause that in the mouth of a sinner / preysyng is not
playsaunt to god. every creature ought to make clean his heart fro al sins by
bitter repentance / by devout confession and by penance Thyrdly a creature
ought to occupye him in the said days in doing almesses for the love of god of
such goods as god has given to him / to them that have need and necessyte.
and more largely ought to be given in the said days than in other / Also yet
in the days of the festys of saints the creature ought to torn his
entendement in the consyderacyon of three things First the creature ought to
consider the great lyberalyte and largess of god that the saint of whom the
feste is / for a lytyl service that he has done to god / God has so gretely
rewarded and guerdoned that he has given to him glory and Joy pardurable^
with him. And with this god will that of his creatures he be honored and
preysyd in this world. And by this consyderacion the creature ought to be al
toward god. and ouzt desire with al his heart. to doubt / to love and serve
deuoutelye and perseuerantly such a lord that pays so well his servants /
Secondly a creature ought in his heart to ymagyne and think of the glory and
of the joy / that the saint has with god. which is so great that heart
humayn may not think ne mowthe express ne speak. and by such consyderacyon
he desire to have such well. and by this the creature desire with al his heart
to serve / love and dread god which for this gives such well to a creature
Thyrdly a creature ought to consider in the said days the great myserye of him
self / the diverse trybulacyons / afflyctyons. maladyes / and evil accydentes.
fortunes and seruytudes / and many moo parylles that been every day in this
pour world. And by this consyderaco^n a creature ought to have the world in
despyte. and not to preyse worldly things. and to serve god with all his power.
And to desire to be out of this myserye / for to have the great Joy and
glory of heaven which the saint has with god /

Here after folowen the seven other comandementes / apparteynyng to the love
and dylection of his neighbor capo. x
AFter the three comandementes aforesaid apparteynyng to the love and dylectyon
of god / Follow the seven other apparteynyng to the love of his neighbor
according to the second commandment pryncypal aforesaid / For to have the
knowleche of them. is to wete. that the creature that loves his neighbor
after the said commandment / ought to have ij things. that is to wete not to
do evil / and for to do well. And therefore of the said seven comandementes
partyculer. the first enduceth and excyteth the creature to do well. But how be
hit that every creature is bounden to do well to his neighbor / Nevertheless
he is most bounden by especyal to do good to tho persons that to him be
most nygh and most conjoined And therefore the said first commandment of these
vij enduceth and admonesteth the creature to do well. and commanded to honor
serve and aid fader and mother. which ben the persons most conioynt to us /
and to whom we be most holden after god. And it is such. honor thy fader
and mother. to the end that thou have good and long life upon the earth / The
cause wherefore we ought to honor our faders and moders / is for the great
benefaytes that we receive of them in iij things pryncypally. First the child
receives of fader and mother his being. For therefore the child ought to bear
to them more gretter honor and obeyssaunce than to any other after god.
Secondly the child receives of fader and mother nourisshyng in his chyldehode.
And therefore the child is bounden to govern them in their old age / and of
his goods to admynystre unto them their necessytees after his power if they
have need / Thyrdly the child receives of fader and mother techyng and
doctrine. And therefore in all things. that be not against god the child owes
to obey to them. and in this doing v things ben promised of god by the
prophet to the child. First grace in this world and glory perdurable in that
other. Secondly long life which ought not to be nombred in the nombre of years
/ but in the nombre of good virtues. And in life which is without sin.
Thyrdly joy and lygnage of children / Fourthly fame or renommee lowable.
Fyfthly rychesses / After it is to wete that sum be not said fader for cause
of carnal generacyon. but for many other causes. Sum ben said fader. and to
each of them we ought to bear honor and reverence / First so^me be said fader
for good and holy doctrine / and good ensaumple that they have given and showed
of good and holy life. As the apostles and other saints. for by their holy
doctrine they have maad us children of Ihesu Christ by feythe. and to them we
ouzt to bear honor. reverence / and obeyssaunce. not only with the mouth.
but by ensyewyng their werkys. and their good and holy lives and doctrine.
Secondly so^me ben said fader for the admynystracyon that they have of god.
like as ben the prelates of holy church. to whom we ought give honor in
obeyeng to them and to their comandements. as to the mynystres of god Thyrdly
sum be said fader for the guard and defense that they ought to do to their
people. as ben the king / the prince / and other lords which have the people
to govern and to keep. and them we ought to love and honor and to them obey
by subiectyon. for their power comes of god. Fourthly sum ben said fader.
and ben to be honored for the weel and good that is received of them / as ben
they that socour the pour in their necessyte / as a fader by pity and by
compassyon. Fyfthly sum be said fader and ought to be honored for their old
age. as been the people which been of great age.

AFter the said first commandment partyculer touching the love and dylectyon of
his neighbor. which enduceth and somoneth a creature to do well. Folowen the
other vj which defend to a creature to do evil / And therefore that emonge
all the euylles that a creature may do to another. the grettest evil is to sle
him / and this was given to moses in the second commandment of the vij. and is
this. Thou shalt not slay. that is to wete creature reasonable of thy propre
will and auctoryte. To the knowleche of which commandment is to wete that
after holy scripture been slain creatures reasonable in many manners / First by
smytyng in the body and hurtyng in such manner that death ensyeweth thereof / and
this is not only against the second commandment pryncypal aforesaid / which
comandeth to love his neighbor as him self. But it is against nature. for
naturelly al things like and semblable love each other. Secondly by gyuyng
counceyl favor or aid and tenduce a creature to slay another bodyly. or to
make him to fall in to dedely sin. Thyrdly in making comfort and aid to a
creature for to slay another corpor^lly. or to cause him to fall in to dedely
sin. Fourthly in consentyng him self to the bodily death of another or
spyrituel. as touching to dedely sin / as to make another to fall. The
which consentyng is understand. as often times as I may let another fro
death corporel or spyrytuel as touching dedely sin and I let him not. By
this it appyereth clearly enough / that a creature sometime sleeth the body / by
iniurye done to his body in such wise that death ensyeweth. and sometime the
soul. for to make it fall in to dedely sin. and sometime body and soul
together. by sleyng him self or a woman great with child living. The second
commandment defends to do evil to a person conjoined in marriage. and that is
this. Thou shall do none aduoultrye / That is to say with a woman conjoined to
another by marriage / Thou shall have no comyxtyon. or flesshly company. Ne a
woman also married with any other man than her husbond / and it is to wete that
man and woman in doing against the said commandment sin first against the law
of god. which has defendyd aduoultrye by the said commandment. and yet they
sin against the law of god / by the which it is said / that this which god
has conjoined by marriage. that by man it may not be deceueryd ne departed. In
gyuyng over his body by carnal copulacyon to another. For after the holy
scripture man and woman by marriage ben constytuted ^weyne in one flesh. Yet
efte they sin against the sacrament of marriage made in the face of holy
church / By the which man and woman promytte their truth to other / By
virtue of which oath the body of the man longs to the woman and the body of
the woman is to the man / and ought not to be abandou^ned ne delyuerd to other
by comyxtion carnal. alweye how well that in the things aforsayd they sin
dedely as said is yet the sin of the woman. that abandou^neth her body to
another man than her husbond by company carnal and co^myxtion. is more gretter
when children or lygnage ensyeweth. than is of the man. For with the sins
aforsayd she commytteth theft / in gyuyng to her husbond heirs for to succeed
to him of another man than of him self / and by this the woman commytteth
sacrelege trayson and theft. And in other caases the sin of the man that
has commysed aduoultrye. is to be reprehended more than of the woman. by cause
that he ought to have more gretter knowleche / and to be more strong for to
keep him from sin / than the woman which is frail and deceived lightly by
concupyscence. And also a man is ordained and constytuted heed and maystre of
the woman / and in doing that sin he gives to his wife evil ensaumple. And
also it is to wete that by the comandeme^t aforsayd is not only deffended
aduoultrye of man and woman assemblyd by marriage / but al fornycacion
comyxtion. and flesshly company between man and woman other than in lawful
marriage is dedely sin. and deffended by the said commandment. and to hold
the contrary is heresye. For to take aweye fro god that which is given and
consecrate in the holy sacrament of baptesme / for to give to a creature / is
more great Iniurye and mysprysion and more gretter sin than to take it fro a
creature / Then sithe that it is defended that such vylo^ye and such
Iniurye made to a creature by more strenger reason. it ought in no wise to be
done unto god. Also yet against the said commandment ne mespryseth not only
man and woman by aduoultrye and fornycacyon as touching the deed or fayte. but
all the times that for to do hit they have the will delyberyd and concluded.
without the deed be done or follow it is dedely sin. and also al byholdynges
touchynges and kyssynges made by deliberacion for to come to the deed of carnal
comyetion and fornycacion as well by man as by woman out of marriage. wihoute
that the deed ensyewe. is dedely sin. and is defended by the said
commandment. The third commandment defends to do evil and hurt to another
in his temporel goods and that is this. Thou shall do no theft Against this
commandment myspryse and synnen dedely al they that pryuely and secretly take
others goods in entencion to reteyne them against the will of him that owe
them / and this manner of taking is theft. Also al they that manyfestly or
openly by force and by vyolence taken the goods of other. and this manner of
taking is called rauyne. and it is gretter dedely sin than theft / In this
sin fallen the princes and lords that without cause reasonable leueye and
reyse upon their people tayllage. aids. and Indue subuencyons / and that for
auaryce maken evil and wicked ordynaunces upon their people / for after saint
austyn / al wicked seygnourye is thefte^ and after the said saint austyn such
people and such lords ben called the great theuys. Also al they that reteyne
the hyre and salarye of other / and that they owe to other. For this is against
Justice. that will that to every man be rendryd that which is his. Also all they
that in fayt of marchandyse by delyberacyon. and in deed aduysed commyse and do
falsehed or damage to other. Also tauerners and sellars of wyn. that put water
with the wyn that they selle / or put in the same of less value and of less
prys than that which is in the vessel. and selle al at one prys Also against
this commandment mespryse and sin all they that do vserye. which is
commysed and made in many manners. Sometime openly. that is to wete when a
creature leneth money to another. and by certain couenaunte shall have prouffyte
thereby sometime pryuely and secretelye / and that is in diverse manners / First
when a creature leneth to another gold or silver or other thing and for the
more gretter surete to be paid ageyn / is delyuerd in his hand sum thing
that of the same comes prouffyt. As ben medowys^ vygnes. or other herytages.
and if he receive the said prouffyt without that he will any thing rebate of
that which is lent. Secondly when for the more surete to have again that
which has be lent / a person has received pledge as horse or other beestes
of whom thusage has done to him prouffyte. and will no thing rebate therefore
as before is said. Thyrdly when ostage is delyuerd to so^me for the payement of
sum fynaunces / And therefore he takes his despences upon the said ostages
during the time Fourthly when any fynaunce is due to any person. and of the
payement of the said fynaunce / he gives delay for certain prouffyt that is
made for that cause / Fyfthly when a creature is accustomed to bye re^tis or
other things. by such condycyon. that if with incerteyn time. his money be
not rendered ne paid ageyn / he shall have that thing / and for the time of the
said being he byeth it for less than it is worth^ And he sees clearly that he
that has sold that has not. ne shall not have at the term power to pay ne
to render that which is lent. And if he have not the power in this hope and
will / he gives him time of rechate or byeng ageyn / that then he shall have
the prouffyte of the thing. and with that he shall have ageyn all that he has
lent wtthoute any thing to abate thereof. Also when any person gives term
of payement for the thing that he has sold. And for the abydyng of his
payemynt he has sold it derrer than it is worth or of value. Also when a
creature byeth any thing that shall be delyuerd to him at certain time to come.
and for thabydyng the delyueraunce of that thing. he byeth it for less than
it is worth. Also when a creature accompanyeth him with another in the fayte
of marchau^dyse. and delyuerth his money by such couenaunte that he shall be
fellow and partyner in the gain. and bear no thing in the loss. And upon
this caas of usure is comprysed the manner for to deliver beestys to deelyng
that shall not deye. which been called beestys of iron. That is to say.
supposed that they deye or perysshe. he that takes them to moison or delyng
shall deliver hem ageyn. and he that has delyuerd them shall not bear no part
of the loss / but in the gain he shall have his part / Also when a creature
byeth any rent. revenue / or other thing that shall be paid to him at certain
term by such condycyon. that if he be not paid at the said term / he shall
give for every day or for every weke sum thing for the forberyng / and for
the defaulte of payement the byerleueyeth and receives the said pain or
thing / Also when for to abide the payement of that which is lent of him that
so owes the pressed or ^ette is received seruyse or werkys and labors bodily /
Also against the said commandment mespryse and sin dedely that bye dygnytees
espyrytuel and benefyces. and al other that commyse symony^ / Also all they
that by force of tyranny holden temporal seygnoryes and lordshyppes / and in all the caases aforesaid. the creature is holden to restore all that which he
has had and received of any other against the said commandment. After the three
comandementes toforesayd which defend to do evil by work follows the iiij
which deffendeth to do evil in hurtyng or doing wrong to other by word. and
that is this. Thou shall not speak against thy neighbor false wytnes. against
this commandment trespacen and synnen mortalle al they that accusen other in
falls Judgment / also al they that Iudgen falsely. also all they that by
detracco^n of saying evil of other take aweye their good name and fame / Also
all they that recyten and taken playsyr and delight in saying and recountyng
that which they have herd say and recyte in deffame of other. also al they
that allow and approuue the words of a creature said in the deffame and
anoyeng of another / Also by the said commandment is deffendyd all lesynges
and lies. the which is commysed in many manners. Sometime in things which
byholden the feythe of holy church to the spyrytuel hurt of another / and to
his dampnacyon in delyueryng to him false doctryn. and against the truth of
the faith of holy church. Sometime in things that been to the damage and
gryef of another as touching his goods temporell. and in these two caases al
lesynges is found dedely sin / Sometime a lesyng is said and commysed in his
propre deed by humylyte. as done sum people which accusen them self in
confession by humylyte of that which they have not done. And fro such a
leesyng ought a creature much for to keep him and for to be ware right gretely
thereof for such humylyte is wicked / For after the saying of saint Austyn /
Like as a creature ought not for to hele ne hyde in his confession that which
he has done / In like wise ouzt he not for to say that which he has not done.

Sometime a creature lies in his own deed for shame. That is to wete when he
says sum thing which he weneth be true / And in saying it he aduyseth him
and knows in him self that it is not so. And nevertheless for shame he dare
not wythdrawe that he has said. according unto the truth And sometime a
creature lies for to have sum prouffyte thereby. or for to escape sum
peril. Sometime for to do prouffyte unto another. Or to deliver or keep him
from sum peril. or for to empesshe his prouffyte. Or to let his dommage /
Also sometime the creatures maken lesynges or lies in Iapes or plays / and for
to glad and enjoy the people which they are in company with al. And fro
all these lesynges after the saying of sweet saint Austyn / a creature ought
always to keep him. For every leesyng is sin. and the two first ben dedely
sins. and the other by evil custo^ may bring a creature to dedely synne^ after
these iiij comandementes aforesaid which defend to do evil by werk and by
word follow the other two which defend the will of lyberte to grieve and do
evil to another^ The first deffendeth the will to hurt another in his goods
temporel / And that is this. Thou shalt not coueyte the thing of thy
neighbor Against this commandment mespryseth and synneth a creature sometime
mortally or dedely. that is to wete as often as by delyberacyon he coueyteth and
would have the goods of another and against reason. Sometime venyally that is to
wete when he coueyteth the goods of another. But he would not have them but by
reason as for the prys that they be worth. and by the good will of him or
them that owe them / The second commandment defends the will delybered or
concluded to coueyte the wife of another man. for to have carnal company with
her. For to have the knowleche of the said comandeme^t it is to understand
that in iij manners concupyscence carnal is in a creature / First in the heart
when it is by consentyng delybered and concluded. To this purpoos says our
savior Ihesu Christ / that he that byholdeth a woman by carnal concupyscence /
that is to say by a will concluded to have her company flesshly in his heart.
he has commysed fornycacyon. and synneth dedely. Secondly in the mouth in
expressyng and declaryng theuyl desire that is in the heart by consentyng. the
which conse^tyng is called dedely sin / thyrdly in work when the evil
purpoos or conse^tyng is done in deed. After it is to wete that iiij things
pryncipally kepe^ a creature fro falling in to the sin of concupyscence. The
first is to flee evil company and all occasyons that given and moeuen cause
of concupyscence. As for to frequente and to see wymmen often and to here speak
of them. The ij is to put out and not remember in his heart the evil thouztes
and the temptacions that come by the things that he has seen. and to chastyse
his body and hold in penance and affliction. The iij is to have recours to
god by devout oryson and prayer when flesshly temptacyon comes in requyryng
deuoutlye his help. The fourth is also in occupyeng him self in good werkys
according to god / And always to flee ydlenes which is cause of all evil /
Thus it appyereth clearly by the comandements aforesaid and declared / that the
creature that loves god has of necessyte for to do three thyngys. First that
he adoure ne worship but one god after the first commandment partyculer.
Secondly that the name of god he receive not in vain after the second
commandment. Thyrdly that he honor god after the third commandment In like
wise a creature that loves his neighbor has of necessyte to do vij things /
The first is that he do honor and reverence due after the fourth commandment
/ The second that he do none evil ne Iniurye by work. First as touching to his
person after the fyfthe. commandment / Secondly as touching the person to him
conjoined after the vj commandment Thyrdly as touching to his goods after the
vij commandment / Also that do not ne bear damage by his word after the viij
commandment / Ne also by thought and will concluded first when he coueyteth
his wife after the ix commandment Secondly as touching to coueyte his things
after the x commandment / The which god give us grace to accomplysshe Amen.

Thus enden the commandments of the christian law which each man ought to
hold and keep entyerly for to have the life and glory pardurable / Deo gracias.
These been the xij articles of the christian faith which every man ouzt to
believe fermely. For otherwise he may not be saved. if he have understanding and
reason in him self. and they ben xij articles after the nombre of the xij
apostles. which establysshed them to hold and keep. of whom the first
apperteyneth to the fader The second to the sone. and the iij to the holy
ghoost. For this is the foundement of the faith to believe in the holy trynyte /
That is in the fader. and in the sone^ and in the holy ghoost one god in iij
persons. Al these artycles ben contained in the great Credo and in the little
credo. the which the xij apostles made. of which each of them made and set
a clause of whom the first is this /

The first article of the faith capitulo xj

I believe in god fader almyzty creator or maker of heaven and earth / this
article made saint peter / saying Credo in de u^ patre^ omi^pote^te^ creatore^
celi and terre. The ij apperteyneth to the sone as touching his deyte / that he
is god / and that is this I believe in our lord. sone of the fader. and in this
we ouzt to believe that he is se^blable and egal to the fader and to al things
which apperteyne to the deyte. and is one thing with the fader. saut the
person which is other tha^ the fader as touching thumanyte / this article made
saint andrew saying. Et in Ihesu^ ^p^m filiu^ eius vnicu^ dn^m nr^m The iij
article is of the co^cepcion of cryst^ and was conceived of the holy ghoost and
borne of Marye That is to say that he was conceived in the vyrgyn marie. And by
the virtue of the holy ghoost and no thing of man. and that the vyrgyn marye
abode always virgyn and tofore and after. This article set in saint James the
more saying / Qui conceptus est de spiritu sancto natus ex maria virgin / The
fourth article apperteyneth to the passion of Ihesu christ. that is to say that
he suffered under pylate his passion. The which pylate was preuoste and Judge for
the time in Iherusalem for the romans / And of him was Ihesus christ Judged
wrongfully at the request of the right felon Jews. and crucyfyed and deed.
and laid in the sepulcre and descended in to hell. This article maad saint
Johan theuangelyst saying Passus sub poncio pilato crucifixus mortuus / and
sepultus descendit ad inferna The fyfthe article is of the resurrection of
Ihesu Christ. That is to say. the third day he aroos fro death / This article
maad Saint Thomas saying. Tercia die resurrexit a mortuis The syxthe article is
of thascencyon of Ihesu Christ / That is to say he ascended to heaven and
sytteth upon the right side of god the fader almighty. This article maad Saint
James the less saying / Ascendit ad celos. sedet ad dexteram dei patris
omnipotentis The seventh article is of the coming of Ihesu Christ to the dome.
That is to say / From thens he is to come to Judge the living and the ded /
This article made saint Phelyp saying / Inde venturus est iudicare viuos and
mortuos The viij article is to believe in the person of the holy ghost. This
article made saint bartylmew saying. Credo in spiritum sanctu^ The ix article
is to believe in the holy church of rome. and in thordynau^ces of holy church.
This article made saint mathewe saying. Sanctam ecclesiam catholica^ The x is
to believe in the holy sacrament and by the same holy sacrament is made
remyssyon of sins to al them that receive him worthily. This article made
Saint Simon saying. Sanctorum co^munionem remissione^ peccatorum The xj article
is of the general ressurection in propre bodies This article made saint Jude
brother of saint simon / saying Carnis resurrectionem. The xij and the last
article is to believe heaven to be life perdurable / This article composed and
made saint Mathye saying vitam eternam Amen /

Thus enden the twelve artycles of the feythe
Of the beast that saint Johan theuangelyst saw in thappocalyps capitulo xij
THe holy appostle Saint Johan the euangeliste in the book of his reuelacio^s
which is called apocalips says that he saw a be which issued out of the sea merueyllously desgysed and much dredeful. For the body of the beast was of
a lyepard. the feet of a beer the throat of a lyo^. and he had vij heedes / and
x horns above. and above the x horns x crowns / and saint Johan saw that
this cruel be has power and might to fight against saints and to overcome
them / and to conquer them. This be so cruel / so conntrefayted. so diverse
and so dredeful / signefyeth the devil of hell. which is full of sorrow and of
al bytternesse^ The body of this be was as says saint Johan semblaunte unto
a lyepard. For in like wise as the lyepard has diverse colors / In like wise
has the devil diverse manners of engynes for to deceive and to draw the people
to sin. The feet of the beast were of a bear. For in like wise as the beer
has the might and strength in his feet and in his arms. and holds
strongly. and byclyppeth fast that which he has under his feet and enbraceth.
In like wise does the devil them that he embraces and has beten down by
sin. The throat of the lion was in him for his great cruelte. The vij hedes
of the said be ben the vij chyef dedely sins. by the which the devil
draws to him as it were all the world. For oftyme it happeth that many
persons fall in so^me throat of these vij hedes / That is to understand of
the seven dedely sins. and therefore says Saint Johan that the said be had
power against the saynces. for in the earth is none so holy a man that
parfytelye may eschew all the manners of synnes^ that of these vij heedes. and
of the vij dedely sins descend. without specyal pryuylege and grace of god
/ like as it was in the virgyn marie / which never did sin / or in another
saint after the specyal grace that he had of god / like as the glorious vyrgyn
marye had specyal and synguler grace of god above al other creatures. The x
horns of the beast sygnefye the brekyng of the x commandementes of the law of
our lord. which the devil pourchaceth as much as he may that the creature
break them. in like wise as he purchaceth that the creature fall in the vij
dedely sins toforesayd. or in so^me of the branches of them. The x crowns
of the said be sygnefyen the vyctoryes that the devil has upon the sinners.
by cause that he has made them for to break the ten comandements of the law
of our lord.

Herafter follows the deuysyon of the vij dedely sins ca xiij
THe first heed of the beast is pride / The second Envy. The iij ire or wrath.
The iiij slouthe. The v auaryce / The vj glotonnye / The vij lecherye / Out of
these vij sins dedely descenden all manner of sins and therefore be they
called chyef of vices. for they ben chyef of al vices and of all sins be
they dedely or venyal. Eueryche of these seven dedely sins is departed in
many parties. and first we shall speak of the sin of pride. This was the first
sin and the beginning of al evil when the angel lucyfer for his great beauty
and his great understanding he would have been above all other angels and would
compare to god that so good and fair had made him. and by cause he took such
pride in him he fyl fro heaven in to hell and became a devil. And all his
company with him / All proud men resemble this lucyfer / which will be above
the other / and be more preysed. more allowed and more enhaunced than the
other^ which been better and of more valewe than they be / This sin of pride
is over perylous. for it blyndeth man and woman / so that they know not ne see
not the peril wherein they be by sin / This is the right strong wyn of the
devil. and the most especyal of which he enyureth or makes drunk the great
lords and ladyes^ the bourgeyses. the rich / the noble and valyaunte
persons. and generally al manner of people. But in especyal the great lords
and ladies in such manner that they know not them self / ne see not their
defaultes / ne their folyes. ne their sins. This is the most perylous
maladye and sickness of all the other / Certeynly he is in great peril to whom
all tryacle torneth to venym. like as doctrine and chastysyng does to the
proud. For the more men chastyse and blame them of their defaultes. so much
more ben they angry and defend them. Pride is the first daughter of the devil.
and she that has most grettest part in his heritage / Pride warreth against
god and his goodness and al graces / and ageyn all the good werkys. that been in
the man. for pride makes of alms sin / and of virtue vice. and thus is
pride a thief to god / and with the goods that one ought get heaven. he makes
him win hell. This sin is the first. For it assaulteth the knights of our
lord. and that last leueth them. For when the knights of god have ouercomen
and vaynquysshed all other vices and sins / Then assault them most
strongly the sin of pride and of vain glory.

The branches of the sin of pride. ben these capo. xiiij
THe sin of pride deuydeth him and departs in so many parties that uneath
they may be nombred. But there ben in this sin vij pryncypal parties / which
been as seven branches that issue and grow of an evil rote. of which the
first branch of pride is dysloyalte or untruth. The second despyte / The
third is surquydrye which so^me call presumpcion. The fourth folehaste.
which is called ambycion / The fyfthe vain glory / The vj ypocrysye. The vij
evil and foul shame of well doing. To these vij parties and branches
apperteyne all the sins that grow of pride. But eueryche of these vij
branches have many small bows.

The first branch is dysloyalte or untruth capo. xv
THe first brau^che of pride is dysloyalte. which deuydeth him in to three
branches / The first is evil. The second is werse. The third is werste. That
one is vylaynnous / That other is wode / The third is renyeng. Vylaynnous
generally is in all sins. for no sin is without vylonye / But the
vylonye of which we speak here specially that grows of pride is a party of
dysloyalte. which is called of clerks Ingratytude that is unkindness. That is
to say forgetyng of god and of his yeftes / that men thank not our lord ne
give him laud and praysyng thereof. But he forgeteth and renders evil for good
and vylonye for curtesye / This vylonye does every creature to god / when he
forgeteth his goodness. grace and yeftes / and yeldeth not to him therefore
praysynges and thanks like as he ought to do. But oftymes fyghteth in evil
custom and usage against the will of god. This is much great vylonye when a
person receives great bounte and goodness / and daygneth not ones to say
gramercy. yet is the vylanye gretter when one sees. and when he forgeteth. But
that slouthe is over great when a person receives all way the bountees and
renders always evil for good / who then bethought him well and took head often
of the bountees and goods that god has given and done to him and does
contynuelly fro day to day. for he has no goods. but god has given them to
him / Ne goods of nature. as beauty / health. strength of body / clear
understanding and natural wit as of the party of the soul. Ne goods of
fortune. like as rychesses. honors. and hawtesses. Ne goods of grace. like
as ben virtues / grace. and good works / well ought such a person to preyse
and thank god / and honor doubt and love him with al his goods / for one
bounte requires and asks another.

Of the second bough of the first branch capo. xvj
THe second bough of dysloyaulte that grows of pride is woodnes. That man is
holden for wood that is out of his wit. in whom reason is goon and
departed. Then is he a right great fool and well may be said out of his wit
and wood that in good ernest wastes destroys. and sets in evil usage the
goods that been not his. but ben the goods of his lord of which he must
straytely count and give a rekenyng^ th^^ is to wete the time that he has
lost. and how he has em^loyed his time. and of the temporelle goods how he
has used them. the which he has had in his keeping / and has despended them
in folyes. in oultrages. and in evil vsages tofore the eyes of his lord that is
god / Ne has not pourueyed him to render his acompte. and knows well that he
must rekene and wot not whenne. ne the day. ne the hour. Such folly is
called forsenerye or woodnesse. Of this vice and of this sin been the great
proud men that use right evil the goods that god has lent them.

Of the third bowh of dysloyaulte capitulo xvij
THe third bowhe of dysloyaulte that comes of pride is renyeng he is well
renyed that the lord which he holds of his lord puts in the hand of his
enemy. and does to him homage. This sin do al they that sin mortally or
dedely For in as much as in them is they do homage to the devil / And become
servants and caytyues of the enemy. and render to him all that they holden of
god. both body and soul And al other things that they have they put in the
service of the devil. And how be it that such folk say and call them
christian. they renye god by work / and show that they been not. But in three
manners a man is called renegate or renyed / and falls christian / Or for by cause
that he byleueth not that he ouzt like as does the bougre or the heretyke. and
the apostata that renyeth his feythe. Or by cause that they break the feythe
that they believe / like as done they that been pariured. and be lie their faith
/ Or by cause they believe more than they ought to do / like as done deuynours
/ Sorciers and the charmerers which use and work by tharte of the devil. and
al they that in such evil werkys believe and set their hope sin dedely. For
all these things ben against the feythe / and therefore holy church for bedeth
and deffendeth them. These been the manners of desloyaulte which is the first
branch of pride /

The second branch of pride capitulo xviij
THe second branch of Pride is despyte. which is a much great sin / and
how well that dedely sin be not without despyte of god. Yet alwey after that
we here speak / in this despyte specially may one sin in three manners Or by
cause that a person preyseth not ryghtfully another in his heart like as he
ought to do / Or by cause he bears not reverence ne honor there as he ouzt
to do. Or by cause he obeys not a right them to whom he ought to obey. Now
think right well dylygently in thyn heart how oftymes thou have mesprysed herin
that which thou have in thyn heart. thyn own self and other falsely preysed.
And the bettyr despreysed and despyted and the werse preysed. and think hou
often thou have despised in thyn heart them / that been of more valewe tha^ thou
art / And how thou have despised them for so^me forayne grace that god has
given to the / Or for noblesse. or for beauty / or for prowess. or for
strength of body. or for lyghtnes / Or for what someuer other good that it be
/ by which thou have* preysed more thy self than thou ought to do / and the
other thou have less preysed than thou ought. After think hou many times
thou have borne little honor and reverence to them that thou ought to do.
First to god and to his sweet mother and to all the angels and saints of
heaven. For there is none but thou have trespaced to by despyte or by
irreuerence In that thou have often times evil kept the festys and holy days.
After think hou many times thou have served evil our lord Ihesu christ. Or in
that / that thou have not gladly herd his service. ne said his hours ne herd
his sermons. And when thou wenest to here the mess in the church or the
sermons. thou Ianglest and bourdest tofore god / and let other to do well.
after think how thou have many times done little honor to the body of Ihesu
christ when thou see him. or when thou receyuest him. In this that thou art
not worthily apparaylled ne made ready by confession and by repentance. Or by
adventure that werse is thou have received him in dedely sin thy self wytyng.
The which thing is as great despyte unto god as to crucyfye him. After think
how unto thy sweet fellow / and to thy good kep^r thyn angel which is always
with the / and always keeps the / how many vylanyes thou have done to him / in
so much as thou have commysed sin tofore him. after think how oftymes thou
have be inobedyent to thy fader and to thy mother and to them to whom thou
ought obey and bear honor. If thou wylt in this manner record thy life
thou shalt see that thou have ofter sinned in this manner of pride which is
called despyte / than thou can recounte or tell /

Of the iij branch of pride. which is arrogance capo. xix
THe third branch of pride is arrogance which is called surquydrye or
presumpcyon. that is to wete when a man weneth more of him self than he ought
/ That is to say that he weneth to be of more valor than he is worth. or to
know more. or to mow more than other. This sin is the fortress of the
devil. For he keeps and nouryssheth all the great sins. This sin shows
him in many manners by work and by word. But namely he shows him in vj
manners. That is to wit in syngularyte / For the proud surquidrous that weneth
to be more of valewe and of power. and to know more than the other. daygneth
not to do as the other do which ben of more valewe than he is. Also he will be
synguler in his werkys. This is the first sin for which surquydrye shows
him in work or by deed. The second folly is enterprise of great dyspences of
his owen or of other for to be preysed and renomed. And that he be holden the
more large and the more curtoys / The third evil that grows of surquydrye is
folysshe empryse of leude stryffe. For thus says Salamon. emonge the proud
men been always stryues and plees. The iiij bough of this branch by which
the proud man shows the pride of his heart is auauntyng / which is a much
foul sin to god and to the world. he that auanteth him is like unto the
cuckoo that can sing no thing but of him self / this sin is foul in him.
that by his own mouth auaunteth him / of his wit or of his parage. or of
his werkys or of his prowessys. But this sin doubleth in them that follow and
flatre these vauntours and losengers / and suffer them for to preyse them and
for to say of them that they durst not say and for to lie / and for to cry
their oublyes The fyfthe tacke of this branch is derisyon. For that is the
custom of the proud surquydrous / for it suffyseth not enough to despise the
other in his heart / that has not the grace that he weneth to have / but he
makes his mockeryes. and derysyons And yet that werse is he scorneth and
mocketh the good wise men / and them that he sees be good and honest. which
is a much great sin and perylous. For by their evil tongues they let much
people to do well. The vj boughe of this branch is rebellyon / That is when a
man is rebelle to all them that would him good. For if one repreue the proud
surquydrous he deffendeth him. if one chastyse him anon he is angry. if one
counceyl him he byleueth it not but his own wit. This is a peryllous maladye
that may not suffer that he be touched. and to whom every medycyne torneth to
venym / Hit is an evil thing to murmr. but much werse is rebellyon.
Rebellyon is a vice of the heart which is hard and froward and diverse. that
will always that his will be done and his sentence holden / and will that all
other bow and enclyne to him / and he shall not bow ne humble him self to no
person This is the hard heart of the word of salamon which may not faylle
to come to an evil end. and like as murmr is against god and ayenste man.
right so is such an heart that is rebelle against god and^ against the men /
This sin and this vice which is called rebellyon departs and deuydeth him
in to four branches. Such an heart is repugnante and rebelle to believe
counceyl and to suffer chastysyng / and to receive doctrine if any of their
friends would counceyl and show their prouffyte or their defaultes. he deygneth
not to take heed thereto ne to here it / But by cause that they have spoken he
will the more gladly do all the contrary. And on the other party they be much
rebelle to the counceylles of our lord / as to the counceyl of the holy
gospellys of the other holy scryptures. and of sermons / To which they be
bounden to do and to accomplysshe the will of god for to have glory
perdurable / And the devil leyeth tofore them either Impotence. or yongthe or
age. or other evil reasons / so that at the last they may no thing do. After
wha^ men repreue and chastyse them / they defend them as a boor / so that they
will not know their folyes. and so much more as they excuse them. so much
more is their sin. Also it is wha^ god smyteth chastyseth or corrects hem
to the end they should know their sins and their defaultes. and that to the
end they repent and amend them. They con him no thank but despise him
saying. O what have I trespaced. what will god do with me. and thus they
murmr against god. Thus done and say the fools / For that which should be
tryacle and purgacyon of the soul / it torneth to hem venym. and the medecyne
torneth to the death / After they be of so diverse wits that they know no
good doctrine / But always defend their sentence what someuer it be / and in
that wise they fall often in error and in false oppynyons / in heresies and in
myscreaunce / Blasphemye is also as says saint Austyn when one byleueth that
which he ought not to believe. But especyally we call blasphemye when one
myssayeth of god or of his saints / or of his creatures or of his sacraments
that be made in holy church. this sin blasphemye is done in many manners as
in the saying in his mind or thought. as done the heretykes / or when it is
said by couetyse of wynnyng. As done the enchauntours or the sorceriers. Or
when it is said by dyspyte as done these great swerers. that sweren so
vylaynously by god. by his blessed mother and by all his saints. which is a
much horrible thing to here and to herkene. Such folk ben like an hounde
enraged and wood that byte and know nothing their master ne lord. This sin
is so great that god punyssheth it sometime openly like as we have said
tofore. when we speak of the evil and wicked people / Of this sin says god
in the gospel. that it shall never be perdoned ne foryeuen in this world ne in
that other. That is to say uneath he shall be forgyuen. by cause that uneath
he repe^teth him. or it may be perauenture that he shall never repent him

Of the iiij branch which is ambicion capitulo xx
THe fourth branch of pride is ambycyon / That is an evil desire to amounte
and rise high. This sin is the pan of hell in which the devil fryeth his
frytours. this branch stratcheth him in many manners on the right side and on
the lift side. For they that desire to wax hye and rich will playse sum.
and thereof grown many sins. like as it were on the right side / That is to
wete losangerye. flaterye seduction. adulacion. folyly geuyng. and folyly
despendyng. by cause they should been holden large and curtoys / unto other they
will noye and grieve / and thereof comen and sourde the sins on the lift side /
As for to myssaye of him whom he will gryeue for tenhaunce him self. and give
to that other blame. And that wers is. that he desires the death of him. that
holds that thing for which he entendeth and desires. and of this branch
grown stryues / Trayson / evil counceyl. and conspyracions.

The fyfthe branch is vayn glory capitulo xxj
THe fyfthe branch of pride is vaynglorye. This is folysshe playsyr of vayn
praysyng. That is when any feleth in his heart a reioysyng of that / that is or
weneth to be preysed of so^me thing that is in him or weneth to have / And
would be preysed of that. of which he ought to preyse god / And by that vayn
glory takes aweye fro god that which is his. For of al manner goods what
someuer they be. he ought to have the honor and the glory And to us the
prouffyte. Vaynglorye is the great wind that beteth down the great toures and
the great steples. The great castellys and the great forteresses / and dryueth
down to therthe the great forestys / and makes the great montaygnes to quake
and shake. These been the hye men and the most valyauntes / the great princes
and the great lords. This is the penny of the devil by which he byeth all the
fair wares in the fair of this world. These been the good werkes^ and by
cause that there ben iij manner of goods that the man has of god. and that the
devil will bye them with his penny. Therefore this branch departs him in three
bows out of which sourde so many sins that no clerk may nombre them.
These iij manner of goods that the man has of god been the goods of nature.
the goods of fortune and the goods of grace. The goods of nature ben the
goods that a person has by nature. as toward the body / or toward the soul
/ The goods of the party of the body ben. health beaulte strength prowess
good facond / good wys and lyghtnes of body. The goods of the party of the
soul ben clear understanding. clear wit to understand and reteyne. Subtyl
engyne for to find good memory and mind. and the virtues naturel by which a
man is more naturally curtoys than another or more large or more ^ebonayr. or
more attempred. or more gracyous. or to be well ordeyned^ Of all these yeftes
ought every man to praise and thank god / serve and honor him / For fro god
comen al these goods that we may have but the proud man sells them to the
devil for the false money of vayn glory / And fyghteth often ageyn god with
all the goods that he has lent to him. which ben here above declared / How
many persons have accustomed to sin often by vayn glory in diverse manners.
every man may Judge in him self. In the goods of fortune ben highness /
honors rychesses / delyces and prosperytees. which ben called in many manners.
For when dame fortune has turned her whele And has raised a man / and has
set him in the most highest degree of her whele as a wynd mylle does. and
unto the most highest mount and come all the xij wyndes and blow meruayllously
with the wind of vaynglorye. For when he is so hye raised in prosperyte / he
thinks in his heart on his great dygnyte / After in his prosperyte. after in
his richesse / After on the great company that follows him. after on the
fair meyne that serves him. After in his fair manoyrs. After on his fair
horse. after on the plente of his fair robes after on thapparayl of his
lodgyng in vessel and in beddys / and in other manner of harneys that is fair
and noble. after on the great presents and on the great festys that been made
to him oueralle where he goth. after on his great renomee and his great loos
and praysyng which flees al about / wrerin he ioyeth and glorefyeth the
very caytyf in his heart that he wot not where he is. These ben the xij
wyndes of vaynglorye. That is to say manners of temptacions of vaynglorye /
which they have that been in this hye estate / or in the world or in relygyon /
or clerk or lay man / The goods of grace ben virtues and good works /
Against these goods blows sometime the wind of vaynglorye and often time
throws down the most gretest trees and most hye / These ben the most wise
men. and it is to wete that in good virtues and good werkys the devil tempts
by the sin of vaynglorye in iij manners. That one is in the heart within forth
when a person enjoys him of the good that he has done pryuyly. as of
prayers and orysons or of pryue good works / and weneth that he be bettyr with
god than he is. That other is when he suffers a folisshe gladness come in to
his heart of that he hereth or sees his good fame or renomee. and that he is
reputed and holden for a good and noble wise man / The third is when he
desires and secheth and purchaceth preysyng loos and good fame. and in that
entencion he does his good deeds and werkys no thing for god proprely but for
the world

The vj branch of pride is ypocrysye capitulo xxij
THe vj brau^che of the sin of pride is ypocrysye. this is a sin that
shows good deeds wythoutforth which ben not withinforth. then they ben
ypocrites which countrefayte the wise man withoutfort.) / and they be nothing
so wythinforth. For they do more in the entencyon to have the name of a good
man than the truth and the holiness. And this is departed in to three parties
/ For there is one ypocrysye folysshe. one foul. and one subtyl. They be foul
ypocrytes that done the ordures and fylthes of sin secretelye in hyd places.
and countrefete the good men tofore the people. Our lord calls them in the
gospel sepulcres painted and gylte They ben folysshe ypocrytes that keep them
clean enough as toward their body. and do much great penance and good works
pryncypally for the praysyng of the world. by cause they would be reputed and
holden for good and holy / Such people ben well folysshe. For of good metal they
make false money. They ben subtyl ypocrytes that will mou^te in hye estate. and
taken aweye and stele the dygnytees and offices. They do all that a good man
ought to do so subtylly. that no man may know it unto the time that it be
achyeued and gotten. and al ready mounted and raised in to hye estate and
dygnytees. and then they show their vyees their fayntyses and the ypocresyes
that were in them within their heart. That is to wete pride auaryce and malice
and other evil werkys by which may be clearly known their wickedness and
their ypocresye. And that the tree was never good. and that all the work and
deed of such a person was fayntyse and ypocresye of that he had showed tofore.

The seventh branch of pride is fool dread capo. xxiij
THe seventh branch of pride is fool dread and fool shame that is when one
leueth to do well for the world. to the^de that he be not reputed and holden for
an ypocryte and a papelart. and fereth and doubts more the world than god.
This shame comes of evil playsaunce / when one will playse the wicked and evil.
