And therefore is she daughter of pride. And the seventh branch pryncypal
makes a person oftymes to leave to do well. for to playse wyckedly the world.

The ij heed of the beast of hell is envy capitulo xxiiij
THe second heed of the beast of hell is envy. This is the serpente that
enuenymeth all / Envy is mother of the death And by the envy of the devil
came the death to the world. This is the sin that most right makes a man to
resemble unto the devil his fader / For the devil hates nothing more than the
well of another. And loves no thing but the harm of another / And by this
sin the enuyous man may not see the well of another. no more than the oule may
see the clerenesse of the son. This sin is departed in to three branches
pryncypal / For this sin poysenneth first the heart of thenuyous person. and
after the mouth / And after that the werkys. The heart of the enuyous is so
poysonned and ouertorned that it may not see the good of another / but that it
gryeue his heart wythinforth. and Judges evil that which he sees. or that he
hereth. he takes and demeth always the werste. And in all this he does his
owen harm. The heart of an enuyous person has so many venymous thoughts and
falls demynges and Iugementes that they may not be nombred. After this when the
enuyous person does or hereth any evil of any other what someuer he be. is
hit of harm of his body / as evil of his death or of his sickness or of evil
fortune. as of pouerte or evil spyrytuel like as when he hereth that sum
which have been holden for good men been blamed and deffamed of sum vices
and deffaultes. Of these things enjoys the enuyuos person in his heart.
After when thenuyous person hereth and sees the well of another. Then
comes to him a sorrow and an heaviness to his heart that he may not be eased
ne make good chere ne fair semblaunte. Now may thou see that the venomous
heart of thenuyous person synneth generally. In malice in gladness and joy of
the harm of other / and in sorrow of the well of another. Thus synneth the
enuyous by his mouth / For needs must such wine come out of the tappe as is
within the vessel. And by cause that the heart is al full of venym. it byhoueth
that such issue out of the mouth. Then by the mouth of thenuyous person
issue three manners of venymous words / of whom dauyd spekyth in his psaulter /
that the mouth of thenuyous person is full of maledyctyon / For of the good
and well of another he myssayeth. appayreth and lasseth as much as he may. Of
hurtyng / For all the harm and deffaultes of another he secheth and sercheth.
and shows forth to his power / Of Trayson / For all that he sees or hereth
he peruerteth to his power. and tourneth it to evil and Judges it falselye.
After the enuyous person has three manners of venym in work. like as he has
in his mouth and in his heart. For the nature of the enuyous is to quench and
to destroy to his power. all goodnesses. be they lytyl / be they great / or
myddle or perfyght. Then he is of the nature of a basylyke that may suffer no
verdure nygh unto him. neither herb ne busshe ne tree / Then after the
gospel the good or well has in him self three estates / For it is first as in
the herb after in the ere / and after it is full of grayn. Then al thus there
be so^me that have good beginning to come well forth / and to prouffyte well. and
ben like as the herb. Them the enuyous thinks to destroy if he may. the other
ben also like theerys of corn that flower well and prouffyte well to god and to
the world / And them the fend cries to destroy and to shame to his power.
The other been perfyte in great estate. and do much good to god and to the
world. For to beat down their good loos and renomee and for to mynysshe their
good deeds. thenuyous dresseth all his engynes. For as much gretter as the
goodness is / So much more sorrow he has. This sin is so perylous that
uneath may one that uses hit come a right to very repentance. For this
sin is contrary to the holy ghost. which is fontayne of all goodnesses. And
god says in the gospel who that synneth against the holy ghoost he shall never
have for yeuenes ne mercy in this world ne in that other. For he synneth of his
propre malice. And it ought holy to be understand that there is no sin how
great it be. but that god foryeueth and pardons in this world if a person
repents with good heart. But uneath it happeth that any repent of this
sin. For such one warreth with his power the grace of the holy ghoost / in
that. that he warreth the spyrytuel good of another. In like wise as the Jews
warryd against our lord Ihesu Christ for the good that he did. And ye ought to
know that there be vj sins specially against the holy ghoost. That is to wete
presumpcyon which enlarges ouermoche to sin. and preyseth little the Justice
of our lord. and ouermoche to trust in his mercy. And therefore much people
sin in hope. The second sin ageynste the holy ghoost is in despayr / which
bynymmeth and takes aweye from god his mercy. Like as presumpcyon takes from
him his Justice. The third is obstynacyon. This is hardenesse of heart / when
one is so enharded in his sin and in his malice. that he may not be humbled
ne meked ne bow and will not repent him ne amend / The fourth sin against
the holy ghoost is despyte of penance. That is when a man purposes in his
heart. that he shall never repent him of his sin. The fyfthe is to war
against the grace of the holy ghoost in another. The vj is to war against
truth in ernest wetyngly. and in especyal the truth of the christian faith.
Al these sins ben against the bounte and goodness of the holy ghoost / and
they been so great that uneath they come to very repentance. And therefore
been they uneath forgyuen and pardoned.

The iij heed of the beast of hell is Ire or wrath capo. xxv
THe third heed of the beast is Ire. But thou owe to know that there is an
ire which is virtuous / that the good men have ayenste this sin. which
geten the virtues against the vices / There is another Ire which is a much
great vice / that is felonnye of heart. out of whom yssuen many branches.
And in especyal four wars that the felons have /

Of the first war of the sin of ire / which is such xxvj
THe first war of the sin of ire / is to him self. for when Ire surmounteth
the man / she tormenteth the soul and the body so much that the man may not
sleep ne rest / Sometime ire takes away the etyng and drynkyng. and makes
one to fall in a fever or in so great heaviness or malancolye. or despayr that
he takes the death. This is a fire that wastes all the goods of the hows The
second war that the felon has that is to god. For ire and felonnye surmounte
and fire sometime all the people. by aduersyte temporalle. or by maladye and
sickness. or by death of frendys. Or by any manner of meschaunce that his
will is not done. that he grutcheth and murmureth against god our lord and
says maugre / and in despyte of god and of all his Saints. And swereth and
blasphemeth against god and his blessed saints / The third war of Ire that
the felon has / that is unto them that been under him. that is to his wife and
to his meyne and breketh pottes and cups like as he were out of his wit /
and so is he. The fourth war is wythoutforth to his neighbors and bydwellers
about him / and of this branch grow vj bows / For when Ire ryseth between
two men. there is then stryf. dyscorde. words. vylonyes. wrongs / And after
rancour which dwellyth in the heart / after comes hate / medlyng and
bataylle. after desire for tauenge him / after otherwhyle homycyde and
manslaughter. After comes often mortalle war emonge the friends. out of
which yssuen often euyls in diverse manners / and many that may not be amended
For when there is war between two hye great men hit happeth often that many
men be slain / which never had blamed ne ^^espaced. monasteryes and chyrches
broken up. and sometime burnt. towns destroyed and burnt. Abbayes and great
pryoryes destroyed / men wymmen and children dysheryted and put to pouerte^
robberyes. wymmen married. and maidens defouled and corupte / and over many
other euylles that been do for that cause. And all this be they bounden to
render and to make amendys. al they by whom so many myschyefs and harms have
be done. And al they that have been in their help in such wicked and evil
works / and therefore be they in great peril of dampnacyon. and far fro
their sauacyon / For they may not amend ne render the da^mages that they have
done. and they behoue to restore or to be forlore /

Of the sin of slouthe which is said accydye capo. xxvij
THe fourth heed of the beast of hell is slouthe. which is called of clerkys
accidye / This sin is grievous to do well / This sin is an over evil rote /
and casts out many evil branches / For this sin causes a man to come
unto evil amendment / and more evil beginning. and over evil endyng / The
slow person has evil beginning by vj manners of sins. The first vice is
fayntnes. that is when a man loves lytyl and fayntly our lord. whom he owes
to love ardantly / and this happeth when he is flawe. latchous and slowful to
do well. The second vice of slouthe is tendrenesse. that is the bed wherein the
devil rests him and says to the man or woman. Thou have be ever tenderly
nourysshed thou art of over feeble complexyon / Thou may not do great
penaunces / thou art over tender. thou sholdest anon be d^ed. and for this
the caytyf suffers to be cherysshed / and to do all the eases and the delight
of his body. The third vice is idleness. This is a sin of whom comes many
euyls as the holy scripture says. For when the devil fyndeth a man idle he
puts him anon in his werkys. that is. he makes him first to think evil.
to desire vylonyes rybaudryes. lecheryes to lose his time. and to leave to do
much good that he might do by which he might get heaven. The fourth vice of
sloth is heaviness. when a man is so heavy. that he secheth nothing ne loves
so much as to lie down rest and sleep. Sometime how well he be slowe^ they been
wakre and quycke enough to the needs of the world / But they be al slepy to the
needs and werkys of god. and for to do the werkys that should be to their
sauacyon. and these manner men had lever lose three masses than a sweet or a good
sleep. The fyfthe vice of slouthe is shrewdnes or cursydnes that is when a man
lies in sin and feleth the temptacyons of the devil and of his flesh that
assaylle him. And for very shrewdness he will not lift up his head ne his
heart to god by contrycyon / Ne cry to god deuoutelye by confession / Ne
stratche up his hands to god by satysfaccio^ To such slouthe resembles the
wicked man that had lyeuer rote in foul stynkyng prison / than to take un him
the labor to goo up the steyer. or the degrees for tescape and goo his way

Of pusyllanymyte. of delay. and werynes capitulo xxviij
THe vj vice of slouthe is pucyllanymyte / In this vice be they that have fere
and dread of naught / and dare not begin to do well / for they have dread that
god shall fail them This is the fere and dread that so^me people have of their
dreme They resemble him that dare not enter in to the path or way for fere of
the snaylle that shows his horns / And resemble also the child that dare
not goo in the way for gaglyng and syt^yng of the ghees / These ben the vj
vices that take aweye fro a man good begynyng. And for vj other vices the slow
person may not have good amendment. These been the vj tatches or condycyons
of evil servants that so do that no good wise man ought to receive in to his
service. that is to wete when he is delayeng. neclygent / forgeteful. slow
latchous and fayllyng to do well /

Of delayeng to do well capitulo xxix
THe first vice is delayeng. For when god puts in the heart of a man good
will to do well. Then comes the devil that says to hym^ Thou shall recoure
well enough. thou art young and strong thou shall live long enough By this
manner the devil destroubleth a man to do well.

Of the vice and sin of neclygence capo. xxx
AFter delayeng comes neclygence / For who so makes delayeng it is no wondre
though he do a thing neclygently / This is a vice of which all the world is
entatched if it be well taken head of. For there be not many that be dylygent to
do that they ought to do anenste god and their neighbor /

Of the vice of forgetyng capo. xxxj
AFter neclyge^ce comes oublye^ce or forgetyng. for who is not retchyng and
neclygente he forgeteth often. by these two sins of neclygence and forgetyng
happeth often that so^me person can not well confess ne shryue him self. For
when a man is not remembryng ne not retchyng and neclygente to confess him. He
forgeteth his sins whereof is great peril For no person may have pardon
without very confession And he may not have very confession that has not
repentance in his hole heart of all his sins. knowleche of his mowthe. and
obedyence in works / This amends and this satysfaction ought every man to
do. Ne there is none how good and wise he be. if he sees and consydereth well
his defaultes but that he fyndeth enough to say al way in his confession. But
neclygence and forgetyng blyndeth the people / that they see no thing in the
book of their confession and of their conscience. / After comes fere or dread
which comes of deffaulte of heart. and of evil custom that byndeth so a man
that uneath he puts him self to do well. and sometime this comes by defaulte
of dyscressyon / and of folysshe fervor by which a man takes on him and
tormenteth so his body by fasting. by wakyng. by penaunces^ and by other
works that he falls in to langour and in such maladye and sickness. that
he may not labor in the seruyse of god / and of this he falls in such
fere. that he has no savor of devotion to do well.

Of the vice of latchydnes capitulo xxxij
AFter comes latchednes that makes a man latchous. and appayreth fro day to
day so much that he is al recreant and defayllyng. and this is the vj vice of
which the evil servant is entatched when he faylleth tofore that he come to
the end of his term / and it is said comynlye. who that serves / and serves
not to the end loses his reward.

Of the evil points of accidye and of slouthe capo. xxxiij
YEt there ben vj evil points in the sin of accydye and of slouthe^ that
brings a man to his end. The first is inobedyence. when a man will not do
that which is charged him in penance / Or if he be commanded sometime to do a
thing that him seems hard. he escuseth him that he may not do it. Or if he
receives or accepts it. be does lytyl or naught. The second point is
Impacyence / For in like wise as he may no thing do by inobedyence. Right so
may he no thing suffer by Impacyence. Right so that no man dare speak to him
of his prouffyte / The third point is murmr for when he is spoken to of his
prouffyte he anon wexyth angry and murmureth and him seems that he is
despised / And then he falls in to heaviness / that all that ever is said
to him. and all that is done to him. and all that he sees al greueth him. and
thus he falls in langour and it annoyeth him to live. so that him self
desires the death After al these sorouful points of slouthe gives the devil
the mortal stroke and puts him in despayr / by which he him self purchaceth
his death and sleeth him self / Or else he plays with him self like as al
despayred. that he abandonneth or gives him self to all wyckednes. And
fereth not ne dredeth not to do any manner sin /

Of the sin of auaryce or couetyse capitulo xxxiiij
THe fyfthe heed of the beast toforesayd is auaryce which otherwise is called
couetyse. which is rote of al euylles like as saint poule says. This is the
maystresse which has so great a soole that al goon thither for to study. like
as says the holy scripture / For all manner of people study in auaryce /
Prelate. Clerk. Lay man and relygyous / Auaryce is a love of dysordynate
hauoyr and richesse / This dysordynau^ce shows him self in iij manners
generally. In getyng arda^tly In retaynyng straynably. and in despendyng
scarcely. These been the three branches pryncypalle that grow out of this
rote. But especyally and proprelye yssuen out of this rote of auaryce many
bows which been much great dedely sin. The first is usure / The second
theft / The third raueyne. The iiij challenge. The fyfthe sacrylege / The vj
Symonye^ The vij malygnytees. The viij marchandyse. The ix in wicked crafts.
The x in evil and wicked plays / and eueryche of these bows departs him in
to many manners.

Of diverse manners and spyces of usure capo. xxxv
THe first bough of usure departs him in to vij twigs / For there is one
manner of usurers lenyng openly which lene their money for other money / And
above the catel they take and leueye their gain. or in money. or in horse. or
in whete or in wyn or in fruit of therthe. which they take in gain without
to rekene the fruytes in payement. And yet that werse is. they will rekene two
times in the year or thryes for to areyse their vsures. and will yet have
bountres or rewards above for every term / and thus be they helped above that
they lene pryncypally / Such people ben usurers couched and vylaynous. But
there ben other manner usurers. lenyng and curtoys which lene their money
without making of any couenaunte / Nevertheless they entende to have
prouffyte and rewards therefore / in money or in catayl. or in gold or in
silver. or in yeftes or in presents. or in robes or in tonnes of wyn or in
fat swyn or in seruyces / Or in labor of horses or of oxen or asses or of
carts or waynes / Or of prebendes for their children. or in other things. and
in all these and such things is usure / when it is lent for occasyon to have
sum prouffyte. This is the first manner of usure. that leneth his good
wyckedly and shrewdly /

The second capo. xxxvj
THe second manner of usure is in them that lent not the money in their own
person / But that which their faders or their moders. their wives or their
husbondes / or their predecessors have gotten by usure they reteyne it. And will
not render ne yield it ageyn. The third manner of usure is in them that deygne
not ne will not lene by their own hand. but they make their servants and
other people to lene for them their money. tho ben the maystre vserers / Of
these sins be not quyte the great and hye lords that keep and sustain the
Jews and lombardes of pyemou^t and other places / which destroy the
contraye. and they take the rewards and great yeftes and sometime the raunsons
or redempcions. which been of the catayl and cheuessaunce of the pour people.
The fourth manner is in them that lene other men's money. or that borow it
with little cost. Such people been dyscyples of usurers which learn this
foul and wicked stynkyng craft. The fyfthe manner is in marchaundyse. when
one sellyth any manner thing what somener it be for more than it is worth for
the abydyng of the term than he would do for ready money. and that more is the
untrue sellar and wicked when he sees the people more at great myschyef.
then he shall selle his ware the more derrer. ye twyes or thryes more than it
is worth. Such manner people do over much harm. For / for their long term
they destroy and appourysshe the knights and hye men that follow
thassemblees. the wars and the tournoyes that they deliver to them their
lands and their herytages in gayge and wedde. and so lyeng in gayge they deye
and never quytte ne paid. The other sin in byeng the things as corn wyn or
other things less the half than it is worth for the money that they pay
tofore hand. and after they selle the same three or four times more dear than
the thing was sold and delyuerd to them fore / Other merchants bye the
things wha^ they be at no prys and good chepe. as whete in harvest. wyn in
the vynyerde or other marchandyse / for to selle ageyn in the time when they
shall be more dear / The other by^ their whete in the stalkys and eerys and the
wyn in the flouryng when they show fair forth / by such couenaunte that they
have their achate sauf and their mesure. The vj manner is of them that deliver
their money to merchants in such wise that they shall be fellows and part in
the gayne^ and no thing in the loss. Or that deliver their beestes to halnes.
so that they be as iron. That is to say that if they deye or perysshe he that
takes them to halnes shall set and put other beestys in their place. of so
much and as great of valor and prys as were they that been deed or perysshed
at his propre charge and dyspence. The vij manner is of them that put and set
their next neighbors in their work and labor. by cause that they have lent
them gold or silver or corne^ or has done to them any curtosye or frendshyp.
and when they see them pour and nedy. then make they with them bargayns for
their avail. and for the money that they deliver to the pour man / or for a
lytyl corn that they selle to him well dear and for more than it is worth in
the market. He will have of him syx penyworth work or labor for two pens /
These been the bows that grow out of the evil branch of vsure^

Of theft capitulo xxxvij
THe second branch of auaryce is theft / this is to take or reteyne other
mennys thing wrongfully without knowleche or ayenste the will of him that
owes it. And this sin may be done in four manners after four manners of
theuys. For there ben sum theuys openly So^me covertly Sum pryuelye and
so^me telawly / The common and open tbeuys ben they that stele in such wise
that there is Justice done on them when they been taken. and of them ben diverse
manners. as well on the sea as on land. The convert theuys ben they that take
aweye secretelye and conuertly great things or small things / by their
barate. trayson or by subtyl wit and engyne. The preuy thieves ben they that
take aweye no thing from strangers. but of their neighbors and known / and
of them been both great and small as the untrue receyuour / Shereuys.
prouostes / Eschetours. Bayllyes / sergeantes. and other such as taken the
amends. and restrain the rentes to their lords. and acounte much in costs
and despences and less in receytes and rentes / Thus done the great officers
which been in the howses of the great lords and rich men that maken great
costs and dyspences. and give largely the goods of their lords and masters
without their knowing and against their will / In this sin synneth the wife
which causes by her sin that the child which she knows well that she
has had of another man than of her husbond enheryteth and has therytage where
he has no right thereto. In this sin also synneth the wife that takes aweye
the goods of her husbond. for to dyspende and put it to evil usage / That
other thief is the little thief that takes aweye out of the hows the breed or
wine and other things. or fro their neighbors their capons or hennys / or the
fruit out of their gardyns or other things. Such been they that reteyne the
things that they have founden and known well to whom they belong. and
therefore they should not reteyne them / But they ought to do by the counceyl of
holy church. or by the counceyl of their confessor. The theuys that been
fellows ben they that parten their theft. or by composycyon or by yefte / or
by achate or by other manner. Also they that consent to the theft. or
counceylleth or that commands it to be doou / Also they that cou^ceylle the
theuys or deffende them or sustain them in their malice / or receive them in
to their house or in to their land. or that gadre together the theft. Also the
wicked Iustyses that suffer them for yeftes / or by prayers or by ouy other
evil reasons and will not ne dare not do Justice /

The third branch of the sin of Auaryce is Rauyne as follows capo. xxxviij
THe third branch of auaryce is Rauyne. which has many bows / The first is
an evil executour of testamentes. Such people rob them that been deed. which
is over great an untruth The second is in wicked and evil lords. be they
knights or other lords or bourgeyses which ete and flee the pour people by
tayllees / by aids Imposycyons amends or by other manner / which seche and
purchase that which may grieve their subgettis. and accomplysshe their evil
will / and they ought to keep and deffende them In this sin ben the great
princes the great barons / which by their might taken away fro the pour and
other that they may subdue their castellys their rentes and their baronnyes /
And also other rich men that take away by strength fro their propre
neighbors lands vygnes and other things / And taken on all sides so that
no thing may escape them The third been robbeurs of evil hostryes or Innes
which rob the pylgrymmes and the merchants. and other that pass and walk
by the cuntreye.

The fourth is in them that will not pay that they owe And that reteyne
wronfully and without cause the hyre or wages of their servants or of them
that do their work / The fyfthe is in these great prelates that pylle their
subgettys. and that raunson them by over great procuracions^ or by other
exactions and extorcions that they do in many manners. These ben the wulues that
destroy the sheep that they should keep The syxte theft is in bayllyes
Shereues bedellys sergeantes and other offycyers. which do the great rauyne
and extorcions upon the pour people and bye the great heritages. and so much
there is of other manner of rauyne which should be ouerlonge to reherce here.
But the most great part is contained in the things above said.

Of the sin of challenge capitulo xxxix
THe fourth of Auaryce is challenge. that is to run on another wrongfully / To
this sin apperteyneth al barate trycherye and falsnesse that happeth in
plees. In the clergy has dame Auaryce many scoliers. and in especyal seven
manner of people that estudye therein.

Of seven manners of the sin of challenge capo. xl
THe first ben the false psedours that make the false partycyons and demaundes.
and seche the false Iuges. and the false wytnessys. and the false aduocats. and
false letters for to trouble other / and trauaylle the people wrongfully in the
spyrytuel court / or in the temporal court / The second been they that put
aweye and set at naught that is right. And sechen barats and delays for to
take aweye from other their chyuaunce. The third been the false and untrue
witnesses / For they maken the false and unright maryages / They taken away the
herytages. They do so much harm and domages that none may amend it / and al
this they do for their great couetyse. The fourth been the false advocates
that sustain the evil causes al wytyng. and empesshe and let the good
people. for the hyre and the yeftes that they take on both sides / And they
make often the good causes to be lost. and the quarelles of good men. and maken
of right wrong / and of wrong right by their wickedness and couetyse like as
they that been masters of the barate and of the trycherye / The fyfthe ben the
false notaryes that make false letters and Instruments. and falsen the seals
/ and make false lybellys and many other vntrouthes. The vj theft done the
false Iuges that entende and ben more favorable against reason more to one
party than to another. for yeftes for promesses for propryertees or for love
or for hate or for dread or for favor / if they delay the causes and the
quarylles wrongfully and make men to do great costs and dyspences. and taken
great yeftes and sometime of both parties. and sellen their Justice / or they
leave to do Justice / and done to pour people so great domages and hurtes that
they may not ne can not amend ne repair The vij ben the evil accessours
which given evil counceylle to Iuges. and causen that the causes and quarellys
be lost by the offices and seruyces that they have. Al these persons tofore
said ben bounden and holden to render and yield again all that which they have
thus had and taken evil of other / and also all the costs and domages that the
other have had and suffered for them.

The v branch of avarice is sacrilege capo. xlj
THe fyfthe branch of Avarice is sacrilege / when one breketh or hurts or
trayteth vylaynousy the holy and blessed things or the persons of holy
church. or else the holy places. which been appropred or longyng to the
service of god / and this does the sin of couetyse in many manners First when
one treats vylaynsly the body of our lord / like as done the heretykes. the
Sorciers or wytches. and the wicked priests for wynnyng / in like wise say I
of the other sacraments. Also when one breketh takes aweye or treats
vylaynsly the sayntuaries. the crosses / the chalyces. the cresme / the
corporalls. the hallowed vestymentes and other things mysteryes of the church
/ Also when one brenneth and destroys chyrches / or monasteryes / or holy
places. or chyrchyerdes* or howses of relygyon / or when any draw out them
that been fled for refuge or socour in to monasteryes or chyrchyerdes for
their surete or warrante Also when one makes medlees or bataylle in the
church so that blood be shed. or when the sin of lecherye is done therein /
Also when hand is laid in wrath and evil on priest or clerk or on any man or
woman of relygyon. Also when one steleth or bears aweye by any reason out of
holy place any holy thing blessed and hallowed / or unhallowed what someuer it
be. Of this sin be not quyte they that the goods of holy church the
patrymonye of Ihesu Christ despenden in evil usage. Ne they that reteyne it by
auaryce. when they ought to give it to the pour people in holy church or put
it in good usage / Ne they also that take aweye or reteyne with wrong or with
force. the things which are longyng to the pour in holy church. Or who that
pays them evil. like as the rentes. the offerynges the dysmes / and the other
ryghtes and dutees of holy church. Of this same sin be not quyte they that
break the sunday and other festes commanded. For the holy days have their
fraunchyse like as have the holy places. These been the bows that grow out
of the branch of sacrylege.

Of the sin of Symonye capitulo xlij
THe vj branch of auaryce is Symonye. Symonye has taken the name of an
enchauntour which was named Simon. which would have bought of saint Peter
thappostle the grace for to do miracles. And therefore he offryd to him great
hauoyr and good / And therefore been they called Symonyaks all they that will
selle or bye any things spyrytuel which is emonge all dedely sins one of
the grettest and this branch has many bows.

Of the first boughe of Symonye capo. xliij
THe first is in them that selle or bye the things hallowed or blessed or the
body of our lord or other sacraments of holy church. The second is in them
that selle the word of god. and preche pryncypally for money. The third is the
sin of them. which by yeftes or by promesses. or by prayers of friends do so
much that so^me be promoted to dygnyte of holy church. like as ben bishops
Abbottes Deene archedeken or other which ben made by electyon. The fourth is
the sin of them that for yeftes or for promesses for prayers or by force of
arms / or for seruyses dyshonest give the prebendes the cures or other
benefyces of holy church. The v is the sin of them which by couenaunte made
enter in to relygyon / and in them that in such manner receive them. There ben
many other diverse sins in symonye. but it apparteyneth more to clerkys than
to lay men. and this book was more made for the lay men than for the clerkys
which know and have the books. yet nevertheless it is necessary and need to
lay men that they keep them fro this sin in iij causes. One is when they will
aid and help their kynnesmen and their friends to rise unto dygnytees of holy
church / The other is when they give the prebendes that been of their yefte.
and the benefyces / The third is when they set and put their children in to
relygyon / in these three points if they give or receive yeftes or prayers not
leefful or evil seruyse. they may sone fall in this sin of Symonye. For like
as says the law wryton / There be three manners of yeftes of Symonye / yeftes
of the hand. like as gold or silver or other Jewel / Yeftes of the mouth as
ben prayers. yeftes of service dyshoneste. I call yeftes dyshonest where the
sin is done pryncypally for things spyrytuel.

Of the sin of malygnyte which comes of auaryce capitulo xliiij
THe seventh branch of auaryce is malygnyte. when a man is so wicked that he
fereth not to do a great sin dedely and horrible. or to do great harm to
other for little conquest of prouffyte for him self. This branch has many
bows. The first is when any person for dread of pouerte or for couetyse of
wynnyng he renyeth and forsakes god or for to deny the christian feythe. and
bycometh heretyke or Jew or sarasyn. To this sin apperteyneth the sin of
them that for money done call the deuyls and make the enchauntementes and
maken to look in the sword or crystal / or in the vngle or nail of the fyngre
/ for to atteyne and find the theft or other things lost. And of them also
that pourchace the charms by sorcerye or by any other wicked craft what
someuer it be when persons been in marriage hate each other and may not dele ne
have company one with that other by marriage / Or persons that be not in
marriage hate each other by sin folyly The second is the sin of cursyng. or
by evil saying by trayson or by detractyon. when a man for wynnyng or for hyre
does thing. for which any person is put unto death. or by sword / or by
venym. or by ouy other manner. The iij sin is of them that for to win.
brenne howses or towns castellys or chyrches. or destroy the vygnes or
corns. and do other diverse great dommages / The iiij is the sin of them
that often pourchace the plees debates and the wars in cytees or in castellys
in chapytres. or emonge other hye and great men by cause that they wene to get
and win more in war than in the pees / The fyfthe is the sin of bayllyes
and such officers that accuse and challenge the pour people and make them to
be raunsoned and tormented for a little gain that they have thereof. To this
sin apperteyneth the sin of the false Iuges. of falls men of law and
advocates. and of falls questys and witnesses of which we have spoken tofore /
and in many other manners is the sin of malygnyte. But it were over long for
to write it here. And better may each man read and consider his sins and many
other* in his conscience than in the skin of a sheep or in paper /

Of marchaundyse capo. xlv
THe viij branche of anaryce is marchandyse wherein men sin in many manners for
temporal goods / and specially in seven manners. The first manner is to selle
as dear as he may The second is to lie swear and forswere the more for to selle
his marchandyse. The third is the deceyte and fraud that is done in the
weyghte and in the mesure / and this may be done in three manners / The first is
when a person has diverse weyghtes and diverse mesures. and byeth by a more
gretter weight and longer mesure and sells by a less / The second is when
one has a true weight and a true mesure and wayeth or meteth untruly and
falsely / like as the tauerner which fylleth his mesure with scum and foam. the
iij manner is when they that selle by weyghte. pourchace and do so much by
deceyte and fraud. that thylke thing that is weyed seems to be more of
weyghte than it is. The fourth manner for to sin in marchaundyse is to selle
the derrer for the term. hereof we have spoken tofore / The fyfthe is to selle
otherwise than the mustre is and worse / like as these scryueners and wrytars
done. that at the beginning show and write good letter. and after make werse
and shende al. The vj is in hydyng and concelyng the truth of the thing that
is sold. and so do these brokers and coorsers of horse. The seventh is to make
and pourchace that the ware or thing that is sold seem much better than it
is. like as done the merciers and drapers that chosen and make the places derke
where as they selle their clothe and ware. And in many other manners may men
sin in marchandyse. but it should be ouerlonge to say here /

The nynthe branch of auaryce capo. lxvj
THe ix brau^che of auaryce is in many mesteres or crafts. In this synneth
much people and in many manners like as done these commyn wymmen. which for
little wynnyng abandonne and give them self al to sin. Also these hazardours.
bawdes. kepars of forboden games and many other w^yche for temporel prouffyte
abandonne them to dyshoneste and unthrifty crafts. which may not be done
without sin as well of them that do it as they that sustain hit. The x
branch of auaryce is in evil plays and games. as the dyse quardes tables or
what someuer games that men play at for money or for gain temporelle. Such
manner plays in especyal of dyse and tables been deffended and forboden by the
decrees and law for many perils that comen thereof. The first is couetyse /
the second over great usure as xij for vj. and not at a month or three days /
but many times in one day. The third sin to multeplye lesynges and vain
words. and that werse is great blasphemies of god and of his saints / The
anger and wrath the oftymes has be taken to correct and chastyse the other.
For sometime their vysage has be turned bacward and behind. Sometime so^me have
lost their eyes. Sum their speech. There was a knight that swear by the eyes
of god / and anon the eyes of his head sprange out and fyl upon the
eschequez. There was also an archer by cause he had al lost at play. in
despyte he drew his bow and shot up toward god an hye. and on the morn
when he was set ageyn at his play. the arowe fyl donn upon the eschequyer al
blody of blood and threste out his eyes. The fourth is evil example that they
which play given to other that behold the play. The fyfthe is to lose the
time which ought to be employed in good werkys and many other wyses. One
thing ought not to be forgeten. that is that he that wynneth at such games
may not ne ought not in any manner to reteyne his gain. but he ought to give
it al for gods sake / but if it were in such manner that he played for
another or by deceyte or by force like as does he that makes another to play
with him by force / In this manner he ought to render it to him that has lost
it / In like wise I say of that which is won at tournoys / These been the
branches of auaryce. there ben enough of other but they appertain more to
clerkys than to lay men. and this book is made more for the lay men than for
clerkys that know the scryptures One thing ought ye to know that the
auarycious man has a devil to whom he serves. which is called in the gospel
ma^mona. and that devil makes to his servant syx commandments. The first
is to keep well that he has. the second that in no wise he mynysshe it / The
third is that he encreace it always be it day or night. the fourth that he give
no thing ne do alms for gods sake / ne curtosye to any other. The fyfthe
that he ne lene ne give to the pour and nedy any thing / ne put not in peril
and Ieoparde that which he has in his possessyon. The vj that he refrain him
self and restrain his meyne fro mete and drink for to spare his good /

Of the sin of lecherye which is love dysordynatly xlvij
THe vj heed of the beast of hell is lecherye / which is oulttrageous love and
dysordynate in flesshly delytes. Of this sin the devil deceyueth a man in vj
manners. like as says Saint gregory. First in folysshe and false beholdynges.
After in folysshe and lewd talkyng and words. After in false touchynges.
After in falls kyssynges / after comes the deed. For fro folysshe beholding
comes the commynycacyon and speech and fro speech to touching / and fro
touching to kyssyng / and fro kyssyng to the deed. Thus subtylly brings the
devil that one to that other. First this sin is divided in two manners For
there is lecherye of heart and lecherye of body. Lecherye of heart has four
degrees. For the spyryte of fornycacion which is the fire of lecherye enbraceth
the heart / and makes first to come the thoughts the fygures and the
ymagynaciyon of sin in the heart and in consentynges. after the heart delyteth
him in folysshe thoughts. and yet he delyteth how well that yet he will not do
the dede^ and in this thought he abides and this delight is the second degree.
which may be a dedely sin so great may be the delight. The third degree is
the consentyng of the heart of reason and of will. and these consentynges
concluded been dedely sin in caas that the deed be dedely sin / after the
consentyng comes the desire / and the great brennyng of the flessh that they
have to this sin. and done many sins in the day in seeing the ladies and the
damoysellys rychely and fresshly apparaylled / which often desgyse and array
them proudly for to make the fools and musardes to muse and behold them. And
certes they sin much grievously / for by their couetyse by their pride and by
their cause perysshen many souls / and much people put to death and to sin.
For thus as says the proverb / dame dator is the arblast to the tour^ For she
has not a membre in her body but it is a grynne of the devil. As salamon says
/ whereof must be given acomptes at the day of Judgment of the souls which by
thoccasyn and cause of them be dampened. That is to understand when they be
occasyon and cause other to sin by their entysyng and labor. Lecherye of the
body is departed in to the lecherye of the eyes of the eerys. of the mouth. of
the hands / and of all the five wits of the body. and in especyal of the
vylaynnous deed and werke^ To this sin apperteyneth all the things of the
flesh. that moeuen and desire to do this sin. As done these oultrages and
the excess of mete and drink. of sweet beds and soft / of delycyous robes
and in all manner of excess of body without necessyte

Of diverse estates of the sin of lecherye capo. xlviij
THe sin of lecherye has many estates. and is departed in many branches
after the estate of the persons that done it / And it goes mountyng fro
degree to degree. and fro evil in to werse. The first is of syngle man and
syngle woman that holden no bond of vow. ne of marriage / ne of order ne of
relygyon. ne of other thing. This is the first sin of lecherye / The second
sin is of common wymmen / and this is more foul and more abhomynable. For by
cause such wymmen ben sometime married and have left their husbondes. or
sometime ben of relygyon / and refuse no man ne brother ne cosyn ne kynne ne
other. The third sin is of the man syngle with a wydowe. or the reuerse /
That is a wydower with a syngle woman / The fourth to defoule a vyrgyn. The
fyfthe is with a wedded woman. This is the sin of aduoultrye which is much
grievous / For there is brekyng of feyth that the one ouzt to keep to another.
After there is sacrylege when the sacrament of marriage is broken. and hereof
happeth sometime dysherytaunce and falls marriage / This sin doubleth him
somtyme^ when it is of a wedded man to a woman married to another man. The vj
sin is when a man uses his wife in thing deffended and dysordeyned ageyn
nature and order of marriage / A man may sle him self with his owen sword So a
man may sin dedely with his own wife / For this cause god smote Onam the
neuew of Jacob with an evil deth^ and the devil which was named asmodeus
strangled the seven husbondes of the holy damoysel Sara which after was wife to
young thobye. For all the sacraments of holy church ought to be treated
clenly and holyly / and to hold and keep them in great reverence. The vij
sin of lecherye is to have flesshly company with his godsyb. or goddoughter.
ne with the children of them. for such persons may not assemble without
sin. ne also by marriage. The viij is of a man with his kynneswoma^. and this
sin encreaceth / and dyscreaseth after that the kynne is nyghe or far. The
ix is of a man with the kynne of his wife. or the reuerse. the wife with the
kynne of her husbond. this sin is much peryllous. For when the man has had
company with such a woman / he may not after have his marriage of the cosyns
of his wife. And if he take her the marriage is none after the law / and if he
take a wife after her cosyn. he loses the right that he has to his owen wife.
in so much that he may not ne ouzt not to dwell with her. if she require it
not tofore / The x of a woman to a clerk. This sin aryseth and aualeth much
after thordre and after the dygnytees ordered. The xj is of a man of the world
with a woman of relygyon. or the reuerse. a woman of the world with a man of
relygyon. and this sin encreaceth and dyscreaseth after the state of the
persons that done it / The xij is of the prelates. which ought to be form
and ensaumple of clennesse of chastyte and of holy life to all the world / The
last is most foul and so abhomynable that it ought not be named / This sin
is against nature / which the devil enseygneth and entyseth a man in many
manners which ben not to be named for the matere. which is ouermoche
abhomynable. But in confession it ought to be said / if it be he or she to
whom it has happed. For of so much as the sin is more great and more
horrible. of so much auaylleth the more the confession. For the great shame
that a man has to say his sin. is a great part of the penance. after the
holy scripture This sin dyspleseth so much to god. that he did do rain fire
brennyng and stynkyng sulphre upon the cytees of sodom and gomor / and did do
synke for this sin five cytees down to hell / The devil him self that
purchaced this sin. has shame and abhorred it when it is done.

Of the sin of glotonye capitulo xlix
THe seventh heed of the beast of hell is the sin of the mouth. otherwise
called glotonnye which has two offices. of which that one apperteyneth to the
taste. as to ete and drink. and that other is in spekyng / Therefore this vice
and this sin is divided in two parties pryncypally / that is to wit in the
sin of glotonye / which is in etyng and drynkyng. and in the sin of the
shrewde tongue. that is in foul and folysshe spekyng. And first we shall say
of the sin of glotonye / which is a vice that much pleases the devil. and
dyspleaseth to god. By this sin has the devil great power in man whereof we
read in the gospel that god gaf license to deuylles for to enter in to swyn.
and when they were entered they drowned them in the sea. This sygnefyeth that
the glotons that led the life of hogs and of swyn the deuyls have leave to
enter in to them and to drown them in the sea of hell. And makes them to
ete so much that they breast / and drink so much that they be drowned. when
the champyon has overthrown his fellow. he holds him by the gorge. by cause
he should not relyeue. Right so is hit of him that the devil holds by his
sin in his mete the devil renneth to his gorge like as the wolf does to the
sheep for to strangle him. like as he did to Adam and Eve in paradys terrestre.
This is the fysshar of hell which takes the fysshes with the grynnes by the
throat / This vice dyspleseth much / For the gloton does to him great shame
when he makes his god of a sack full of dunge. That is his belly which he
loves more than god and doubts and serves it. God commands that he should
fast. The belly says nay. thou shat not / but thou shalt eete long and by
leyzer / God commands to rise erly. his god his belly says thou shalt not. I
am over full me list to sleep The church is none hare he will not flee away.
and it is not yet open. It shall well abide and tarry for me^. And when the gloton
aryseth he begins his matyns and his prayers and says. O god what shall we
ete this day. shall we not find that is any thing worth / After these matyns
comen the lawdes and says / A lord god how well drank we yester even the good
wyn. and how good mete ete we. Then after this by wepeth the gloton his
sins and says. Alas says he I wend well this night to have deyed. The wine
yestereuyn was over strong / mine heed aketh. I shall not be eased till I have
dronken. This god of the womb of glotonye is over evil For first he bycometh a
tauern gooar / and frequenteth tauernes. after he plays at the dyse. and
after he sells his good away / after he bycometh a rybaulde / an holyer and
letchour and at the last he hangs on the galowes. This is the salarye and
the scotte that is often paid for the sin of glotonye This sin is departed
after saint gregorye in to v branches For there is sin in five manners in
etyng and drynkyng. and therefore sum drink tofore time. or without reason or
mesure. or over ardantly or over plentyuously or over curiously Then the
brau^che of this sin is to ete tofore time. Ouermoche to ete is a foul
thing to a man that has age and dyscreco^n when he may not abide a due hour
for to ete and drink By great excess of glotonye it happeth often / that a man
that is hole and strong of body drynketh and eteth without cause reasonable
tofore time ordained. and that he comes to the mete as does a dombe be /
And much sin and maladyes bodily happen often by the customs. and thereof it
comes that this gloton says that he may not fast ne do penance. For he
says he has an evil heed and an evil heart also. and certainly he says
truth. and for to break the fasting days and vygils commanded is right a
great sin. For he dampneth him self. and also will have company with him. and
withdraws and lets them to do well. and ledeth them with him unto hell.
For he makes them to break their fastes. and do glotonnye. which they would
keep if it were not the evil company and felawshyp / For these glotons and
these letchours emonge al other euylles that they do / done a sin that is
proprely the craft of the devil. that is when they let and wythdrawe al them
that they may fro well doing. and mock and skorne all them that love to do
well. These glotons say that they mow not fast. but they lain falselye. For
little love of god causes them to say so / * For if they loved as much the
very glory of heaven as they do the vayn glory of the world / For like as
they fast for their worldly occupacyon and temporal goods often unto the night.
as well might they fast unto none for gods love if they loved him. And that if
they desired their salvation. But they be like unto the child that all day
will have breed in his hand. / And truth it is that like as one synneth by
etyng and drynkyng over erly. Right so one synneth by over late souper. These
people that so much love to wake by night and waste the time in ydlenes. and
goo late to bed. and arise late synnen in many manners / First in this that
they waste and lose the time and torn it. when they make of the night the day.
and of the day the night. God curses such people by the prophete^ For men
ought on the day time to do good and occupye him in good and holy werkys. And
in the night to preyse god. and to pray to him deuoutelye. and to yield him
thankynges of his yeftes / But they that then lie in their beds when they
should be up and risen must needs sleep when they should pray to god and worship
him. and here the service of our lord / and thus lose all the time. and the day
and the night / Also in these great wakynges ben commysed many sins. as to
play at chesse tables and at dyse. and then is there spoken many folysshe
words and corrupt. of which many sins follow and ensyewe / And also the
caytyues waste their bodies their time their soul their wit and their good
The second branch of glotonye is to ete and to drink oultragyously and
without mesure. These that so do been like unto a goulf that swaloweth all in.
like as an abysme. It is over great wysdom to keep mesure in etyng and
drynkyng^ And also it is great health for much people dye often tofore their time
by oultrageous etyng and drinking. and by such excessys and such oultrages
comen and sourden many maladyes and sekenessys. But he that will know and take
this mesure / he ought to know that there been many manners for to live in the
world / So^me lyuen after the flesh and after the eases of the body. Sum
after their Iolyte / Other after their ypocresye. Other after physyke. Other
after their honest. Other after that their sin requires / Other after there
spyryte. and after the love of god They that live after the flesh as Saint
Poul says sleen their soules^ for they make of their belly their god / They
reteyne neither reason ne mesure. and therefore they shall have in that other
world pain and torment without mesure / They that live after their Iolyte will
hold company with toles. such folk can not may not ne will not hold ne keep
mesure ne reason. They that live after ypocresye ben they that been marters to
the devil. such ypocrites have ij mesures. For the ij deuyls that tormenten
thypocrite ben much contrary that one to that other. that one says ete enough
so that thou be fair and fat. The Other says thou shall not but thou shall
fast so that thou be pale and lene. to the end that the world hold the for a
good man / And that it may appyere that thou do much penance. Now it
byhoueth that the ypocryte have ij mesures. one little and one great of which
they use the little mesure tofore the people. and the great mesure they use so
that no man see them. they reteyne not the true mesure that been auaricious In
such manner as the mouth will. which is lady of the house and comandour. Then
between the belly and the mouth of the gloton ben three dysputacyons / The belly
says I would be full the mouth says I will not be full / the belly says to him I
will that thou ete and take enough and despende largely. The mouth says I shall
not. I will that thou restrain the. and what shall the sorry caytyf do which is
servant to his two evil lords. Two mesures maken the pees. The mesure of the
belly in an other man's house good and large. and the mesure of his mouth in his
owen house sorouful and over s^ars. They that lyuen after physyque kepen the
mesure of ypocras. which is little and streyte / and it happeth often that he
that lives by physyke deyeth. They that lyuen after honest they keep and
hold the mesure of rayson / and lyuen honorably in the world. For they eten
in time and hour. And taken in gree and at worth that which they have.
curtoyslye. clenly and gladlye / They that live after that their sin
requires keep such mesure as is charged to them in penance. They that live
after the spyrite ben they that for the love of god rule and govern hem self
like as the holy ghoost enseygneth and techeth them to hold and keep mesure
reason and order / They have the lordshyp and seygnorye over their body which
is so dysciplyned and endoctryned by penance and so well chastysed that he
demands none oultrage. and does that which the spyrite commands and
without contradyction. Now may thou see by that which we have here said
that the devil has many engynes for to take the people by their throtes and by
their glotonye / For first he shows to them the wynes and the metes which ben
fair and delycyouses / like as he did to eve the apple^ and if it be not worth
he says to him Ete and drink like as did such one. Thou must needs hold
company wylt thou that men mock and scorn the and will thou ben holden a
popelard. Or he says to the. thou must nedys keep the health of thy body / who
has not his health has no thing. Be not an homycyde of thy self / Thou owe
to thy body his sustenaunce / Or he says to him otherwise Behold and
consydere the good that thou do and what thou may do. Thou etest not for
the delytes of thy body. but for to serve god / Thou ought to keep thy
strength to god like as dauyd the prophet says. Of these reasons abouesayd
be sometime atteyned and deceived the most wise men / The third branch of
this vice is to run and to take over gredyly the mete. like as the hounde
does the caroyn. and how much gretter is the gredynesse so much gretter is
the sin / For like as it is not sin to have the richesse Justly gotten and
truly but not over much to love them. ne to use them evil / right so it is not
sin to ete. But that it be not over gredely ne over dysordynatly. Al manner
metes ben good unto good people. to them that by reason and by mesure vsen them
without any excess and without oultrage / and alwey we ouzt to preyse god and
render tha^kynges to god of his goodness and of his yeftes / and by the swetenes
of the mete we ouzt to think on the sweetness of god. and on that celestyal
and sweet mete of glory perdurable which fylleth and accomplyssheth the desire
of the heart. Therefore men read in howses of religyon at mete / by cause that
when the body takes his refection on that one part. that the soul should take
his spyrituel mete and refection on that other part. The iiij branch of this
sin of glotonye is of them that over nobly will ete and drink. and which
despende and waste that whereof an hundred pour men might be suffycie^tly fed
Such people sin in many manners. First in great despences that they make.
After in that / that they use over great gredynes and over great delight. After
in the vayn glory that they have. But this is not only thexcesse of the
throat / but it is often for bobance and for great pride / and for the praysyng
of the world that they seche so dear metes and multeplye so many messes whereof
often times grow many sins. The v brau^che of glotonye is the curiosite of
glotons / which think on none other thing but for to delight them in metes.
they ben proprelye lychorous which seche not sauf only the delytes of their
throat and mouth. In iij things namely lies the sin of such people / First
in the great charge that they have in pourchasyng and in arayeng their metes /
After in the glory and in the great playsyr that they have in seeing and
beholding them / and that they may recounte what dylygence they put to that.
that the metes been well arrayed. and that eueryche have his right and propre
saw^e. and how they may of one thing make diverse messes dysguysed for the
delycyousnesse of the mouth / and when the messys or the metes come^ in one
after another. then be said the bourdes for entremesses and thus goes the
time. and the caytyfs forgete them self and. reason slepeth and thinks no
thing of the death. ne on the sins that they do. their stomach cries and
says. Dame throat ye slay me / I am so full that I am like to break. Then the
lychorous tongue answers though thou sholdest to breast I shall not suffer this
licorous mete escape me. after the lycorousnes of mete comes vaynglory that is
to remember it. Then desire and wesshe they that they had as long a neck as
a crane / and as great a belly as a cow that they might yet devour and swalowe
more mete / Now have thou herd the sins that comen of glotonye and of
lycourousnesse. and by cause that these sins sourden and comen often in the
tavern. which is fontayne of sin. Therefore I will a little touch the sins
that been made and done in the tavern. The tavern is the scole of the devil
where as his dyscyples study. and his propre chapel where as his service is
done. and that is the place where he shows and does his miracles both day
and night. such as apperteynen the devil for to do. At church our lord god
has a custom to show his virtues and to make his miracles like as ye may see
in many places. the blind for to see. the lame and crooked to be redressyd. to
mad men their wit. to dombe men speech / and to deef men their heryng / But
the devil in the tauern does all the contrary. for the tavern is his chapel as
is aforesaid where men does to him service. for when the man goes to tavern
he goes all right. and when he retorneth he has neither foot ne hand. by
which he may him self bear ne sustain. and when he goes thither he speaks
well. hereth and understands. and when he retorneth he has lost all this /
like as he that has neither wit ne reason ne memory in him self. Such been
the miracles that the devil makes in the tavern. and what lesson is read in
the tavern I shall say to you. There is read learned herd and seen all fylthe
and ordure of sin. that is to wete glotonye lecherye sweryng forsweryng lyeng
myssayeng renyeng god and his saints. mysherkenyng brawlyng and many other
sins. Then sourden and comen stryues homycides or manslaughter. there is
lernyd to stele and to hang / the tauern is a fosse and a pytte of theuys. and
also it is the fortress of the devil for to war against god and his saints
and the tauerner that susteyneth such people dysordynate ben partonners of all
their sins that they do in their tauernes. And certain if a person said as
much shame to his own fader or to his mother or to his knave / as such manner
people do to their fader of heaven and to our lady and to the Saints they should
be much angry. and find and set other remedy than god does.

Of the sins of the tongue capitulo L
WHo that will know and think of the sins of the tongue. him byhoueth to
think and acounte to thynk what the tongue is and fro whens she comes and
what harm and evil she does / For it happeth that sometime the word is sin
in him self. by cause it is evil / and happeth by cause that it is sin / men
sin for as much that she yssueth and comes of an evil heart. And also it
happeth that the word is great sin by cause it does evil. how well that it
be fair and well polysshed / Now thou ought to know that the evil tongue is
the tree that god curses in the gospel. by cause he fond thereon no thing but
leeuys. By the leeuys ben under stonden in holy scripture words. And like as
it should be a thing dyffycile and hard to nombre the leeuys of trees / Right
so it is Impossyble to compte and nombre the sins that grown of the tongue.
But we shall set and put ten chyef branches which grow out of this tree.
And these x branches may thus be named / ydlenes / auauntyng / losangerye.
detraction. lies or lesynges / Forswerynges. contencyons murmr. rebellyon.
and blasphemye.

Of the sin that been in idle words capo. lj
THey that abando^ne them to idle words geten great dommage and great peril
/ which they apperceyue not. And also they lose the time which they may never
recouere. And lose also the good deeds that they should and might do unto their
own salute and health.

And lesen the joy of heaven / and the tresour of their heart / and replenysshe
it of vanyte and of sins / They dyscouer the pot and the flies enter
therein. They call them idle words / but they ben not. For they ben much
costyous damageous and perilous as they that avoid fro the heart al goodness.
and replenysshe it with vanyte. For they shall render reason and yield acompt of
them to god straytely at day of Judgment. like as god says in the gospel /
This is not then a little thing ne little ydlenes / when hit byhoueth to yield
reason and accomptes at the day of dome unto a little thought. and in so hye a
court as is tofore god and al his saints. In this idle words men sin in vj
manners. There been sum vayn words. of which sum tongues be so full that so
much speak before and after that they be like the clyket and the clappe of a
mylle which may never rest. and also so^me words ben so curyous of them
that gladly heren tidings told. that they often set their heart to the
desease of them that here them. so that the recounters been often holden for
fools and liars. After comen the rehersayl and the fair words / wherein is
much vaynglorye. in them that can subtylly show and say them. for to make the
herars to laughe / after ben the truffes bourdes and lies full of fylthe of
ordure and of sin which ben called idle words. but they be not / for they
be peryllous and greuable / After ben Iapes. the esbatemens and plays not
leeful. that say sometime upon good men and upon them that would fayn do well / by
cause that they might wythdrawe fro their heart the goodness that they have
conceived and purpose to do / These be not idle words / for thou art like an
homycyde if thou wythdrawe by thy tongue a man or a woman or a child fro doing
well or fro doing a good deed. And god shall conne the as good thank as the king
should do to the if thou had slain his own sone or stolen aweye his tresour.

Of the sin of auauntance capitulo lij
AFter comes the sin of auauntyng which is much great much foul false and
much vylaynous / it is much great. For he that auau^teth him self is much
hateful to god for he takes away his glory. Also as we have said tofore this
is a much false sin. for his goods of which he myzt get heaven he gives
for a little wynde^ and so it is a much foul sin. For all the world holds
him for a fool for a vylayn and for nyce. and this branch has.v. leuys.
There ben v manners of vauntours That one is of time past / This is the sin of
them that so gladly remember their werkys and their prowesses. and that which
they wene to have done well or said well. That other is of time present. this is
the sin of them that no thing do gladly. ne pain them to do well / ne to
say well when they be not seen ne herd. They in doing or in saying or in
syngyng auaunte them self and selle for nouzt all that they have and done. To
this man apperteyneth the sin of them that so auaunte and boost them of the
good that they have. or of that which they wene to have of their noblesse or
of their richesse. They ben like to the Cuckoo / that can not sing but of him
self. The third is of them that been surquydrous and that think and say in them
self. I shall avenge me hereof. I shall make hills and valeyes. The fourth is
more subtyl. that is of them that dare not preyse them self for shame But all that ever that other done and say they blame and despise like as no thing were
worth / but that which they can do or say The fyfthe is yet more subtyl. that
is of them that will when that men preyse them. and they dare not say it
openly / they make it all contrary and make them self humble and say that
they be no thing worth and sinners three times wers than they be. by cause they
would be preysed and for that men should hold them for well humble and meke. Alas
says Saint Bernard that this is a sorouful auauntynge. They make them self
deuylles by cause they should be reputed for aungellys / and feign them self to
be evil. to the end that men should repute them for good. But certeynly a man
should not more anger them. than to say ye say truth To this apperteyneth the
sin that sechen the advocates for to preyse them. and to cry their oublyes.
by whose mouth they speak more hardely.

Of evil saying of other capitulo liij
LOsangers ben the nouryces of the devil that give souk to the children and
make them sleep in their sins by their fair syngyng / They enoynte the way
of hell with the honey of flaterye by cause that the sinners should goo it the
more hardely. This sin is departed in to five parties that been like as five
leuys on this branch. The first is of these flaterers. that when they see
that he or they. that they see dyspose them to say well or to do well. anon they
show and tell it to him. by cause that he should have thereof vayn glory. But
his defaultes they shall never say ne tell him / The second sin is that the
little good that the children do they double it. That is to say / that them that
they preyse and feed by flaterye / they encreace it and double it / and
adiouste thereto so much that it is more lesyng than truth. and therefore
been they called false witness in holy scripture The third sin is when they
make a man or a woman to understand that he has in him many good virtues and
much grace / where as he has none And therefore holy scripture calls such
flateres enchau^tours for they enchaunte so much the man or the woman / that
they believe them better than hem self and that they believe bettyr that they
here than that which they see / and that they say to hem better that they
know and feel / The fourth sin is when they sing always the placebo of
flaterye / That is to say / my lord or my lady ye say truth. my lord does
well. and torneth al thing by flaterye what someuer he does or says be it
good or evil. and therefore ben they called Ecko / That is the so^n that
redoundeth in hye mountayns and woods and accords always to that which is
cried and said. be it true be it falls / The fyfthe ben the flaterers that
defenden excusen and couere the vices and the sins of them that will flatere
and preyse. and therefore ben they called in writing taylles. for they cover the
ordures and sins of the rich men for sum temporal good. and therefore ben
they lykenyd in scripture to the tayll of a fox. for their flaterye barate and
tryeherye.

Of losengerye and of flaterye
LOsengiers and myssayers ben of one soole. These ben the ij seraynes otherwise
called mermayde^s. of which we find in the book of the nature of beestys
which is a monstre of the sea that is called serayns. which has the body of
a woman the taylle of a fysshe. and vngles or claws of an egle / and they
sing so swetely that they make the maronners to sleep. and after they devour
them. These ben the losengyers and flaterers which by their fair speech make
men to sleep in their sins / There been sum serpents which have the name
of serayns. that run more swyftely than an horse. and sometime they flee / and
their venym is so strong that tryacle may not avail against it. For sonner
comes the death than the bytyng of the serpent is felt. These ben the
myssayers of whom Salamon says. that they byte in trayson like a serpent.
with this ben slain three at ones. That is he that says it / he that hereth it
/ and he of whom is myssayed / This is the right cruel be that is called
hate. which fynyssheth destroys. and brings out of the earth the bodies of
the deed men and eteth them. These ben they that byte and ete the good men of
relygyon that been in the world / Such manner people ben more cruel than is
hell which deuoureth the wicked / but these people run upon the good and
deuoureth them. Such manner people resemblen the sow. which when she has
pigs gladly will byte a man clad with whyt clothes. They ben like the huppe
which makes his nest in the ordure of a man and there rests him / and like
the dorre or waspe that flee the flowers. and louen dunge and ordure. and this
branche has five leuys. The first is when they contryue the lesynges and evil
for to hurt blame and defame other. The second is when they have herd the
blame and harm / they say it forth and report it to the people / and adiouste
more of them self thereto. The third is when they quench and set at naught
all the good that a man has done. and make it to be holden for evil. they ete
the man al hole. the other ete him not all. But they byte him and bear aweye a
pyece This is the fourth leef of this branch. which is proprely called
detraction / For he always wythdraweth and cutteth of a pyece of good that he
hereth spoken of other. For when any good is spoken of any other tofore him /
always he contryueth somthynge to say to his reproach. and gives thereto a but
as thus. he is right a good man and I love him well / but there ben such
defaultes in him certainly I am sorry therefore. This is the scorpyo^ which
blandyssheth with his face and prycketh with his taylle. The fyfthe is when he
peruerteth and torneth al to the wers party / and the good in to evil. And
therefore he is a false Judge and untrue.

Of the sin to say lesynges capitulo liiij
LEsyng falseth a man. like as one falsed the seal of the king. or the bulls
of the pope. and by cause that such men falsen the money and beren forth false
letters he shall be Iuged at the day of dome as a false man. The liar is emonge
the good true men as the false penny emonge the good. and as the chafe emonge
the corn. The liar is like to the devil which is his fader. like as god says
in the gospel for he is a liar. and the fader of lesynges as he that forged the
first lesynge. And yet he forgeth and techeth them forth all day / The devil
shows him in many manners and in many fourmes. and transfygureth him self in
many guyses for to deceive the people / Right so does the liar / Then is he
like the plouyer which lives of the wind and of the air. and has no thing
in his entraylles but wind. And also to every color that he sees he
changes his sowne^ In this branch been three bows. for there is one manner
leesyng brennyng. another playsaunt. and another noyeng. and in all three is
sin. For like as says saint austyn / how well he that lies. and with his
lesyng does good and prouffyte to another. nevertheless he does his own hurt
and damage. then the lies ardaunt ben sins / But the lies playsaunte ben
more gretter sin. like as ben the lies of losengiers of flaterers of
mynystrellis. of trufars which that sayen these bourdes lesynges and derysyons
for to solace the folk and to make them laughe. and it is no doubt for to
take heed and to here them it is a sin. But the lesynges greuyng and noyeng
ben dedely sin / when they be said ernestlye with a for thought for to harm
and hurt any other / To this branch apperteynen all the falsetees the
fallaces the deceytes and guylles that been done and said thorugh out all the
world for to deceive and hurt any other in soul or in body in hauour in
renome or in fame /

Of the sin of forsweryng capo. lv
IT is an evil to lie / But it is much werse and gretter sin a man to
forswere him self. It is a peryllous thing to forswere him self. and therefore
our lord deffendeth it much. not for that by cause that one may in no wise
swear without sin. For often to swear makes a man often to forswere him and
often to sin. For in vij manners may a man sin in making oaths. First when
one swereth ardauntly / this is by despyte and gladly / like as it seems that
he delyteth or that he were fro him self. Therefore defends Saint James not
only to swear when it is of need. but the will to swear. Also when one
swereth for naught It is for naught. when one swereth lightly without cause
and without reason. This is deffended in the second commandment of the law.
which god wrote in the tables of stoon with his blessed fyngre and delyuerd
them to Moses the prophet for to preche them to the people. After when one
swereth accustomably / like as many done that been evil taught and that can no
thing say without sweryng. For for to swear nys none other thing but to
call god to witness / the cause ought to be much great. reasonable and true.
where as should be called or dare call so great a lord as god is to witness.
his glorious mother and his saints / Also when one swereth folyly / and this
comes and happeth in many manners as where swereth by ire or suddenly / of
which when he is repreued he repents anon. or wha^ one swereth for a thing
which he may not keep without sin / Such swerynges ought to be left. and
of them do penance of the folysshe oath. Or when one swereth certeynly of the
thing of which he was not certain how well it be true. Or when one swereth
certainly of that which he knows not. or that he may not accomplysshe. Or
when one swereth by the creatures. as so^me say by the son that shyneth / or
by the fire that there bre^neth Or by my heed Or by the soul of my fader. Or
such semblable things. God deffendeth al these oaths in the gospel. For to
that which I ought to conferme. I ought not to take to witness but the
souerayn truth / that is god which knows al. and no thing the pure
creatures which be no thing but vanytees / For when men swear ernestly by
them. they do dishonor to god / For thonour of god ought alweye to be kept in all things. But when men swear by the holy gospellys. men swear by him of whom
the words ben that be there wryton. And when one swereth by the holy relykes
or by the saints of heaven. they swear by them and by god that enhabyteth in
them / After when one swereth vylaynsly of god and of his saints. In this ben
the christian men werse than the sarasyns. that ne sweren in no manner. ne
suffren that any swear vylaynsly tofore them of Ihesu like as christian men do
And who that swereth in their law Mahomet their god he shall be stoned. The
christian men been in this more cruel than the Jews that crucefyed Ihesu Christ /
For they brake none of his bones. But they that swear by him rende and make moo
pyeces of him than is made of a be in the boucherye. And there be many false
christian men that in like wise break in pyeces our blessed lady and other
saints in sweryng vylaynslye And certeynly it is merueyle how christ may suffer
it After when one swereth falsely or bears false witness to his wytyng in any
manner that he swereth covertly or openly. or by art color or sophym. For the
law wryton says / God that loves symplesse and truth in such a thing. he
receives the oath and understands the word. as they that say entende it. and
which symply and without barate understand it Much is the great debonayrte
of god. when such men swear that / which they know well is not truth. Or
that promytteth a thing which they will not hold. that the devil strangle
them not anon. For when they say as god keep me. or as god will me help / he
puts him self out of the grace of god and of his aid and help. Now ought
they of very right to lose wit and mind / and all that they hold of god.
The last branch of this sin is when one breketh the feyth that he has
promised and creanted. by his faith or by his oath. For faith lied and oath
broken is all one /

Of the sin and peril that is of chydyng capitulo lvj
Saint Austyn says that there is none so like to the devil as is the chydar.
This craft without doubt pleseth much the devil / and dysplayseth much
unto god which loves above al other things pees and concord. This branch
departs him in to vij bows / of which the first is to strive The second to
chyde The third ledenger. The fourth to curse / The fyfthe to reproach or to
repreue / The sixte to menace or to threte. The seventh dyscorde and to r^yse
hate. This is when the devil sees pees and love between two persons it much
desplayseth him. and for to make them dyscorde he does his power to make them
to strive. and when they begin to strive the devil begins to blow the
sire of anger. Then after the stryffe and anger comes the noise and chydyng
/ Then as the fire is light and the smoke is up anon comes the flamme and
lepeth out / Stryuyng is when that one says to that other. It is so. it is not
so / it was so / it was not so. Chydyng is when they demene and say one to that
other great words After comes the ledanges that is when they pynche and shoue
that one to that other and say great vylanyes and great felonyes For there be
sum so felou^s that have their tongues more cuttyng than a rasour. and more
percyng than arowes or alles Such folk resemble the porpyn which is al full
of pryckes and sharp poyntures. and is over fell and angry / and when he is
wroth he launceth and casts his pricks like arowes out of his body and
throws on the right side and on the lift side. Also he resembles the felon
mastyf that byteth and barketh on al them that he sees goo by the way / After
this comen the curses and maledyctio^s. this is when that one curses that
other. And this is so great a sin as the scripture says that who curses his
neygbour. he is cursed of god. And Saint poul says that such folk may not
have the royame of god. And Salamon says that their mouths ben like as the
pot that boylleth and casts out on al sydes^ and scaldeth them that be
about him. After comen the reproaches which ben yet more sin that is when a
man reprocheth another of his sins and his defaultes or of his folyes. his
pouerte. his pour kynne. or other defaultes that he has in him / he wexyth
angry and synneth. After comen the menaces and thretenynges and then begin
the medlynges and wars. But above all the sins that we have here named /
passes the sin of them that by their wicked tongues areyse and moeue
dyscordes deuysyons and evil will emonge them that been friends to gyder. and
that destourbe and let the pees and accordes / God hates much such people
as says the scripture.

Of the sin of murmr capitulo lvij
WE see that it happeth often time / that they that dare not answer ne chyde.
begin to murmr and to grunte with his teeth. Therefore after the sin of
chydyng we set the sin of murmr. how much this sin is great and how
god takes vengeance and correction of it we shall show / For god oftymes
has taken vengeance on such / like as the holy scripture records. For. for
this the earth opened and swolowed in dathan and abyron. and they descended all
quycke in to hell / And for this sin god sent a fire from heaven that burnt
