chore and al his fellows / that is to wete ij hundred and xl thousand of the
grettest that were in the host of our lord in deserte. For this sin lost
the Jews the land of promyssyon which god had promised. So that of vj.C /
thousand that god had delyuerd and put out of seruage of the king of Egypt
pharao. and that had nourisshed them xl year in deserte with the manna of heaven
/ Of al them there entryd in to the holy land of promyssyon but two persons
only. which were named Caleph and Iosue. but al deyed with sorrow in deserte.
This sin has two branches. For so^me murmr against god. and sum against
man / The sin of murmr against man is in many manners like as servants
ayenste their lords and masters. and chamberers and wymmen against their
ladies and maystresses. children against fader and mother / The pour against the
rich. The vylaynes against the nobles. The lay people against the clerks and
against the prelates. And the cloysterers against thabbottes. pryours and the
o^fy^ers. And this murmr grows against these persons of inobedyence. by
cause that there is made to them over hard commandementes. or of dread / or of
inpacience by cause all things be not done ryghtfully. or of envy. or of
felonnye. by cause that one is auau^ced more than another. and many other evil
rancours. Murmr against god has many occasions that is he that lost grace
and patience and would be more than god / For such ^hynge as god has made in
earth. if he has not made it after his will. anon he grutcheth against god.
and syngeth the deuyls pater noster / For like as the holy ghoost enseygneth
and techeth his chosen to sing in their heart the sweet song of heaven / that
is deo gracias. of all that he has made and given us. and of all that he sends
us / In like wise the wicked spyrite makes his dyscyples to sing the song of
hell. That is of murmr that always shall dure in hell. Certain such a man
is a much fool and wood that will that god should give to him acomptes of all
that he has made. if he send to him pouerte or maladye or dear time. or if he
take fro one and give to another. and all this be not done at his deuyse. anon
he takes against god and murmureth against him. and can him maulgree / and what
marvel is hit though god avenge him on such folk when they would take fro
him his seygnorye. his sapyence and his puyssaunce.

Of the sin and peril that is in rebellyon capo. lviij
EVyl thing is it of murmr. but much more evil is it of rebellyon.
Rebellyon is a vice that comes fro the heart. which is hard. froward. and
diverse / and always will that his will be done and his sentence holden / and he
that will that other humble and bow to him. and he will not bow ne enclyne to
no man. This is an heart diverse of which salamon says that he may not faylle
of an evil end. and like as murmr is against god and against man / Right so
is such an heart rebelle against god and man / This vice has iiij branches.
for such an heart is froward and rebelle to believe counseyl. and taccomplysshe
and do the comandements of god / and to suffer chastysyng / and to receive
doctrine. Of this vice thou have herd in the chappytre of pride.

Of the sin of blasphemye capo. lix
BLasphemye is as says Saint austyn as much as it grows etc^. Seche all the
condycions in the chappytre of pride tofore wryton in the rubyche of arrogaunce
in the end / Now we have showed x manners of sin of the tongue / of which
the first is idle words / and the last is blasphemye. And this is that Salamon
says / that the beginning of the evil tongue is folly. and the end shall be
over evil / here fynysshe then the dedely sins and all the branches that
descend of them / and know ye for truth that who should well study in this
book he might well prouffyte and learn to know al manner of sins and to
confess him self well. for none may confess his sins well / if he ne know
hem not / Now thou ought to know that he that redeth in this book ought to
think and take heed dylygently if he be culpable of any of these sins
aforesaid. And if he find him culpable of any he ought to repent him and
anon to confess him dylygently. and to keep him to his power fro other sins
in which he is not culpable. and also he ought to preyse and thank god
humbly. and to pray him deuoutelye that he will keep him by his sweet grace.

How this life nys but death as hit appears capo. lx
Grievously dies he that has not learned to deye / learn then to dye if thou
shall conne live / for no man shall can live. that has not learned to dye / and
he is by ryzt called a caytyf that can not live ne that knows not to dye. if
thou wylt live freely and surely learn to deye wyselye / if thou say how shall
it be learned. I shall now tell to the / Thou ought to know that this lyfnys
but death. For death is a departing / this knows every man And therefore it is
said of a man when he dies that he departs / and when he is deed he is
departed^ This lyfnys no thing but a departing. ye truly a much short
departing. For all the life of a man if he lived a thousand year. is not only a
moment to the regard of that other life. which always dureth. In torment or in
joy perdurable. This witnesses to us The kings The dukes The earls The
princes and the Emperors which had sometime the glory of this world / Now
weep they in hell. Cry and howl. cratchen and sayen alas / what auaylled us
our power / honor noblesse Joy beaultees and al rychessys. Sone is al this
departed and faylled as a shadow or smoke. and much faster fled fro us than
birds fleyng. or quarelles out of a cross bow. Thus departs aweye our
life. Now we were / and anon we ben deed. and all our life was not a little
moment. Now be we in perdurable torments Our Joy in weeping Our carolles and
feestes in sorrow. Roobes hoodes feestes dygnytees games Rychessys and al
welthes ben faylled us. Such been the songs of hell like as holy writ
recounteth / For to show to us that this life is no thing but a departing. and
this death is no thing but a departing. and to live is no thing but to
depart. Then the living in this world is no thing but for to deye. and
this is true as the pater noster. For when thou beganst to live / anon thou
beganst to deye. and to approach the death. and al thyn age and all thy time
which is passed / the death has conquered and retained. Thou saeyst that thou
have xl year. that is not truth / the death has them. Ne never shall he yield
them to the ageyn / Therefore the wit of the world is folly. And certain the
clerkys seeing. seen no thing at al. day and uyght they done one thing / and
the more they do the less they know. always they deyen and can not deye^ for
night and day thou deyest as I have said to the. Yet in another manner I shall
teache the this clergy. to the end that thou know well to live and well to deye.
Now take heed and understand the death is no thing but the deceueryng of body
and soul. this knows well every man and understands / Now techeth us Cathon
the wise man. learn says he to deye. To depart and deceuere often thy soul and
thy spyryte fro thy body. like as did many of the great phylosophres that so
much hated this life and despised the world and so much desired to deye that
they slew them self by their own agreement. but it auaylled them no thing.
For they had not the grace ne the faith of our lord Ihesu Christ. But the holy
men which love god and dread him / of three dethes have they passed the tweyne.
For they ben deed as touching sins. and deed as touching the world. Now abide
they the last death that is the third / and that is the deceueraunce of soul
and body / Between them and heaven is but a little wall. for they pass it by
thought and by desire. And though the body is in this world on this side. the
heart and the spyryte is on that other side in that other world. there where
their conversation is in heaven. like as says saint poule. Their solace their
I^ye / their consolacion is by thought on the ferther side in heaven where their
conversation is like as says saint Poule. And therefore they hate their life
which is but death / and desire the bodily death / For this damoysel bears Joy
that is the death which crowns all the saints and set them in joy
perdurable. Death is to a good man end of al his euyllys / and yate and enter
of al goods. Death is the river that departs death and life / Death is on this
side life / and on that other side also / But the wise men of this world which
ben on this side of the river of this world seen so clear. and on that other
side they see no thing. and therefore been they called in scripture fools and
blind / For this death they call departing / And the death that is comune to
good they callen the end. And therefore they hate so much the death. For they
know not what it is. ne on that other side of the river they have not
conuersed / ne know no thing what gooeth there out. Then if thou wylt
know what is good and what is evil. issue out of thy self. issue out of the
world / learn to deye / Dysseuere thy soul fro thy body by thought. Send thyn
heart in to that other world That is in heaven. in hell / and in purgatory /
There shalt thou see what is good and what is evil / In hell thou shalt see
mo sorrows and diverse tormentys than any man may or can deuyse. or any heart
think.

In purgatory also thou shalt see moo torments than any may endure / In
heaven thou shall see more Joy and glory than any may desire. In hell shall be
showed and enseygned to the how god vengeth dedely sin. Purgatory shall show
and enseygne the how god purges dedely sin. In heaven thou shalt see clearly
virtues good werkys. how hyely they ben guerdoned and rewarded / And in these
three things understand how and all that. that the byhoueth to know to live
well and deye well /

How men live dyeng in this world capo. lxj
NOw behold and take heed yet a little. and ennoye ne grieve the not at these
three things. Therefore to know and will to hate sin. Forgete thy body one
time in the day and goo in to hell living. to the end that thou goo not thither
at thy death. Thus done often the good men and the wise There thou shalt see
all that the heart hates / cold hete hungre thyrst and diverse torments. as
wepynges syghes and wayllynges. that the heart may not think ne tongue deuyse /
and all way shall endure without end. and therefore is this pain by right
called death perdurable / which is always death in living. and life in deyeng. when
thou shall see then that this one dedely sin must nedys be so dear bouzt /
thou had lever be flayne al quyck. tofore thou sholdest consent to do one
only sin / After goo to purgatory. there shall thou see the pains of
souls. which have had very repentance of their sins in this world. but they
were not parfytely purged / Now make they the remenau^te of their penannce unto
they be clear and net / like as they were at time and hour wha^ they were
baptized / but this penance is much horrible and hard / for all the pain
that wymmen ever suffered in trauayllyng and delyueryng of their children. and
also saint bartylmewe suffryd to be flayn al quyck. saint stephen to be stoned
with stones. saint laurence and saint vyncent to be burnt and roasted upon
brennyng cooles Al these martyrdoms and torments ne ben not but as a bayne in
cold water after the witness of scripture to the regard of torments of
purgatory. where as the sowles brenne until they be purged of al their sins.
like as gold and silver be purged and fined in the fire. till no more be found
to be purged. For this fire of purgatory is of such nature / that all that
they find in the soul is it of deed of word and of thought that has corned
to any sin little or great. all is there burnt and purged / And also there
ben punysshed and purged all the sins venyal. which we call little sins.
which we often do / Like as foul thoughts. idle words Iapes trufes lies and
all other vanytees so long till the soul have no more to be purged of / and
that she be so clean so pure so net and so worthy that she be sayntefyed for
to enter in to heaven. where as none may enter but if he be right fine right
clean and right clear. This fire dreden all they that to their power keep them
fro dedely sin. and that keep holyly their body / their mouth their eerys
their eyes. and al their five naturel wits fro al sins. And also lyuen as
they should every day dye and come tofore the Judgment. And by cause that none
may live al without sin. like as says Salamon / For seven times in the day
falls the ryghtwysman. And therefore by holy confession. by teerys by orysons
by almesses and other good deeds ought every man to be relyeued and put away
fro sin and amend his life. and to Judge him self of his sins / to the end
that he abide more surely the last Judgment Also to learn to know evil. and to
flee it and all sin great and little. And that he be then in the great
dread of god. which is the beginning of all good and of good life.

How we ought to live holyly and learn to do well capo. lxij
Now it is not enough to leave al sins and all euyls. but that it be lernyd to
do good. and if we learn to get the virtues by which we may cast and put
aweye the vices and all sins without which virtues no man may live well ne
rightfully. Then if thou will learn to live well after virtue / learn also to
deye as I have before said to the / deceuere thy spyryte fro thy body by thought
and by desire / And goo out of this world deyeng And goo in to the land of
living / where as none shall deye ne never wexe old. that is in heaven / There
is learned to live well. and al wysedom and all curtesye. For there may enter no
vylayne. There is the glorious company of god and of the glorious virgyne his
mother saint marye. of Angellys and of saints. There surhabounde all goods.
beaultees Rychesses honors strength lyghtnes science fraunchyse virtues
wit glory and joy perdurable. There is no point of ypocresye ne of
trycherye / ne of losengerye / ne of dyscorde. ne of envy ne hungre ne thryst
ne hete ne cold ne evil ne sorrow ne dread of enemies / But always feste and
ryall espousaylles song and joy without end. This joy is so great. that
who that shall have tasted one only drope of the most lest joy that is there
/ he should be fyred and so entalented in the love of god that all the joy of
this world should be unto him stenche and torments. and rychesses dunge / and
honors but fylthe and vyletees / And the desire for to come thither shall make
him an hundred thousand times more arda^tly to hate sin. and to love virtues
and to do well / For love is more strong than dread / and then is the life
fair and honest / when a person flees al euyls and sins. And enforces him
to do all the good that he may. not only for fere to be dampened but for the
desire of the glory perdurable and for the love of god And for the great
clennesse that virtues have and good life / and them whom the love of god
ledeth. much hastelyer sonner and more ardantly comen thereto. and less
costeth / than they that serve god for dread / The hare renneth and so does the
grehou^d That one for dread that other by desire. That one flees that other
chaceth / The holy man renneth to god like a grehounde. For he has always his
eyes and his desire to heaven / where he sees the pray that he chaceth. And
for that he forgeteth the goods of this world. like as the gentyl hounde when
he sees his pray / This is the way and the life to the five good and true
lovers of god / to gentyl hertes that so much louen virtues and haten sins.
that if they were certain. that they ne should ne might know the sins / ne
that god should not avenge them. yet they would not deygne to do ne to consent
to sin / but al their thought and pain of their heart is to keep them clean
f^o al sins. And to apparaylle them that they be worthy to see and to have
perdurably the glory of heaven. where as heart vylaynous entached with sin
shall never enter. ne fool ne felonous ne proud man.

Of iij manner of spyrituel goods capitulo lxiij
NOw have I well showed to the how one should learn to deye and led and use good
and holy life. and for to get virtues so that a man know well and euydently
clennesse. and what is sin. what is alms and what is virtue. Also that one
know well and certeynlye. and to Judge what is evil. and what is sin and what
is good. and to co^ne deuyse the very good and the great good fro the little.
For a thing not known is neytherhat^d ne desired. and therefore ought thou
to know that the scryptures sayen that there been sum small things that be
called the lityl good and sum the myddel good And sum the great good. and
sum very good that is ryghtful to al. the world is sometime deceived. For
they give the great goods for the lytyl. or the great for the myddle / For
this world is as a fair. where as ben many folysshe merchants / and fools
that bye glass for sapphires / and leed for gold. and bladders for lanternes.
But he is a good marchaunte that of every thing knows well clearly the
truth and the propre virtue / like as the holy ghoost enseygneth us. and
another maystre techeth us to know the great things fro the small. the
precyouse fro the vile. the sweet from the bitter /

Of the goods of fortune capo. lxiiij
THey call the small goods the goods of fortune. which dame fortune has
about her whele. and always takes a weye and gives / and torneth that which
is above to fall under / These ben the procyouse stones that the fools have
bought for rubyes for saphyrs and for emerawdes / These ben also as Jewels /
and young children which god gives to us for to solace us with. and for to
draw our love to him By cause that he knows well that we ben tender and t^ble
and that we may not hold the sharp ways of penance. of anguysshe and of
martyrdom / like as done the good knights of god which conquer the royame of
heaven by strength. and take it by ttheyr prowess and their good virtues.
Then that is not the great good ne well ryghtful. For if that were the great
good and very / Then were fools the blessed children of god Ihesu Christ
which chosen pouerte shame and sharpness for to give and to show to us
ensaumple. And refused the joys the honors and the rychessys of this world.
if these goods transytorye worldly and temporalle ben very good. then be
not all the very goods in heaven / Then is not god parfytelye good and happy
by cause he will not use such goods. Then god is not good ne naturalle by
cause he gives not these worldly goods to his friends / but he gives them
more largely to his enemies. if these were very good. then were foles all the
saints. all the good clerkys and the wise phylosophres that fled fro such
worldly goods and despised them as dunge. if these be very good / then
fails the holy scripture that calls them lies and vanytees. nets and
grynnes of the devil / and this is as true as the pater noster / For these ben
the engynes of the devil. by which he deceyueth the souls in a thousand
manners. and byndeth them and takes and holds them But the wise marchaunte
that is the wise man / whom the holy ghoost enlumyneth by very knowleche.
that oueralle knows and can decerne what every thing is worth. ^he sees
right well and understands that all the world is not a good morsel for to
fylle the heart of one man. and that there is therein much evil and little good.
And therefore he beholds the euylles and perils that been therein. and knows
well that it is truth that is comunelye said / who that gives not that which
he loves / he takes not which he desires. Such folk given the world for
to have heaven. and forsakes oueral richesses for joy. fylthe and ordure for
gold. and leave all for gods sake / rychesses delyces and honors. and
bycome pour in this world for to win good and for to get the richesse of
heaven. This is the most fairest life and most sure that may be in this world
There ben other that see that in many manners may one do his prouffyt and his
sauacyon with goods temporelle. and that he may have without ouermoche to love
them For god commands not a man to leave al / They reteyne them / but lytyl
they preyse them / They use them / but lytyl they love them / like as did
Abraham Job and Dauyd / and many other which eschewed and fled the perilles.
And they do spyrituel prouffyte with temporalle goods. and will bye heaven with
their almesses and other good deeds. They can bye out their sins and help
their neighbors. They can the more love god dread and doubt him for the
perils that they be in. and the more humble them self when they see and
consider their sins and their deffaultes. when in sharp and streyte weyes of
penance they dar not goo^ when so little for gods sake they will suffer and
give / which so much suffered to save them. and would xxxij year in this world
be pour for to enryche them in heaven. They save them well but it is hard to
do / For it is a more light thing to leave all the goods attones. than to
reteyne them and not to love them.

Of the goods of nature which follow here. capo. lxv
THe moyen or myddle goods ben the goods of nature and of doctrine. Of nature
like as beaulte of body / prowess. force or strength. vygour / lyghtnes.
debonayrte / clear wit and clear engyne for to find. good memory for to
reteyne well. and good wys for to sing well. All these goods aforsayd nature
brings them in the natyuyte or birth of a person. Doctrine clergy and al
other goods be gotten by study or by accustomaunce. like as been good virtues.
good manners and other virtues. But these ben not yet very good ryghtful. For
they do not that which is perfytelye good. For many a phylosophre. and great
clerkys. Kings. Emperors and other many princes and other lords that had
many of these goods been dampened in hell. Also these goods has our lord
given to his enemies as well as to his friends. To Sarasyns To Jews To false
christian men like as he has to good men. Also this is not very good that
faylleth at need. and that may be lost maulgre him self And though theuys may
not take them and rob them. yet the death takes them away at the last. Also
I say that the very goods ayden always and greuen never / but certeynlye
such goods and such graces foreign been often damage and grieve them that have
them / if they use them not well according to god. For sum auaunte them and
been proud and despysen the other. when they to whom god has given such
graces and such goods as I have tofore said and named. if they use them not
well and Justly according to god. they shall be in gretter tormente in hell And
straytly they must acompte and yield a reckoning at the day of dome / of that
they have done. and how they have used and despended it / Notwythstondyng they
have gotten goods that god has lent to them for multeplyeng and encrees /

Here after is showed of the goods of grace capo. lxvj
NOw have I shortly showed the little good and the moyen good. Now will I show
to the which is the very good ryghtful and parfyte. This does he which has
the good with right and vnderstondyng^ For without the which was never no
good with right. This good is called the grace of god and virtue and charytee^
Grace by cause that she gives life and health to the soul / For without that.
the soul is deed. For like as the body is deed without the soul So is the
soul deed without the grace of god. It is called virtue by cause it adourneth
the soul with good werkys and with good manners / it is called charity by cause
it joins the soul to god. and also does al thing as it were with god. For
charity is no thing else but a dear unity / That is the perfection and the
beneurte to which we ought to entende. Much were deceived the ancient
phylosophres that so curyously dysputeden and enquyreden who was the souerayn
good in this life. and never could they find ne know hit / For sum set
their study and their wit in the delytes of the body / The other in
rychessys. the other in honest / but the great philosopher Saint Poul which
was rauysshed unto the third heaven and passes all other phylosophres techeth
us by many reasons that the souerayn good in this life. and that the queen of
virtues is to love god and to have very charity in him self / For without
this good ne auaylen all the other goods right naught / And who that has
this good of charity he has all other goods / and when al other goods
shall faylle / this good shall not faylle. and above all the great goods that
been this charity is lady / Then the grettest good that is under heaven is
charity. After by cause that thou will and desyrest this good which by right
is called virtue / and that thou desyrest to love it most. and to seche it
above all other goods. I will yet show to the his valor. It is acustomed to
deuyse three manners of goods in the world. that is to wit goods honorable /
goods delectable. and goods prouffytable There be no moo goods ne very ne
good ne fair but these three manners / And this see thou openly of the world.
that none desires ne loves any thing but that he wene that it be honorable
or delectable or prouffytable / The proud secheth thing honorable. The
covetous man secheth things prouffytable / The delycious secheth things
delectable. And when they sechen this thing vaynlye. Every man ought to know
that vert^es have these three propretees. For virtue is much honorable and
delectable and pro^ffytable /

what virtues ben goods honorable capo. lxvij
Which virtues ben goods honorable. this may thou see in this manner. Six
things been in this world much desired by cause that they seem much
honorable. that is to wete beaulte wit prowess power fraunchyse and
noblesse. These ben vj fontanyes of vanyte. Of vayn glory comes and sourdeth
a plant. Beaulte is a thing much loved. For it is a thing much honorable.
and nevertheless beaulte that the eyes and the body see and love / is a thing
falls covert and vain. It is false for he or she is nothing fair But our eyes
ben vayn and feeble that see no thing but the skin wythoutforth. Then who
might see as clear as a be that is called a lynx which sees thorugh out a
wall he should cl^rely see that a fair body nys but a white sack full of
stynkyng dunge^ and like a dunghylle couerd with snow or with grene grass.
Also I say to the that this beaulte is much short and not abydyng. For it is
sone faylled and anon passed as a fume or a smoke. and as the flour of the
field or of the medowe. Anon as the soul departs fro the body. fare well all the beaulte is faylled and gone / Then the beauty that the body has. the
soul has given it to him / And therefore much fools been al they that for
the beaulte of the body gloryfye them self. But the beaulte of the soul is the
right beauty. which always encreaceth and never shall faylle. This is the v^ray
beaulte by which the soul pleases god and to the aungellys that seen the
heart / This beaulte renders and gives to the soul graces virtues and love
of god. For she reformeth reparaylleth and renders her right enprynte. That is
the image of her maker / which is beaulte without comparyson. and who best
resembles in getyng the virtues. in pluckyng up and cast from him all
sins. and keep his commandments entyerly he is most fair. Then the
most fair thing that is under god. is the soul which has parfytely his
right form and his right clerete. color of flour. clerenesse of the son /
figure of man. and playsaunce of precious stones. And all that the eye of the
body sees of beaulte is fylthe and foul to the regard of the soul / and all that may be thought of beaulte may not be compared to the soul.

Of very sapyence capitulo lxviij
Wit and clergy is a thing much honorable. and much do be preysed. But
and if thou will be wise a right and learn very clergy. do so that thou
have very good. that is grace and virtues. That is the very sapyence that
enlumyneth the heart of a man. like as the son enlumyneth all the world.
This wit passes and surmou^teth all the wit of the world. like as the son
passes the clerenesse of the moon / For the wit of the world nys but folly.
like as the scripture says / and chyldehode and wodenesse. Folly is in them
that so much louen the world and his beaulte / and that can not know the day
fro the night / Ne Judge between great and little. and between precious and vile.
They wene the moon to be the son / For they wene that the honor of the world
be very glory. and a little apple to be a great montayne. for they wene that
the world be a great thing / But to the regard of heaven it nys but pouerte.
They wene that a glass be a saphyr And they wene that their strength and
their power be much great. which is more feeble and more fraylle than is
glass / Also I say that this chyldehode the wit of the world is in them that
so much make them wise for to keep and ease the body and to be in delyces.
which lyuen as a child / that seche nothing else but to do their propre
will. In such people reason is deed / and therefore they lyuen as beestys. for
their wit is al turned and corrupt / like as is the taste and savor of a
seek man or of a woman great with child. which fyndeth more savor and
appetyte in a sour apple than in bread made of whete. and more savor in a
cool than in good metes / Also these people may not believe that there is more
Joy and delight in loving god and to serve and to honor him / than in doing
the will of the caroyne of their body / For they can not ryghtfully Judge
between sweet and bitter. Also I say that the wit of the world is wodenesse
in them that so much be subtyl in fyndyng malice for tengyne and deceive
other. be it by strength or by plee or by barate. And that ne think ne study
sauf to auaunce and enhaunce them self / and to grieve other / This wit as
says saint James is the wit of the devil. which always payneth him self to
do harm to other / But the very wit that the holy ghoost enseygneth and
techeth to the friends of our lord is in knowing without mysprysyng what every
thing is worth. he shows that the world is vayn in being foul in valor /
in loving it and sauouryng it / The rychessys ben vile and transytorye. And the
delytes been bitter. After he gives feelyng that the love of god and virtues
is a thing very precious and sweet. very for she fylleth the heart
nouryssheth and susteyneth it. She is precious for one may bye god and all that
he has. She is sweet. for it is the manna that al things makes sweet. labor
sorrow wepynges shames trybulacyons aduersytees martyrdoms and al pains / And
all that one may think to love. it makes it savor like su^re / This is the
wit and the sapyence whereof the scripture says. This is the sapyence out of
which grows purete and very conscience /

Of the prowess of the knights of Ihesu Christ capo. lxix
AFter I say that virtues and charity given very prowess / Then there is no
prowess by right. but in the knights of god which the holy ghoost adoubeth
and armeth with virtues and charity / In prowess been three parties. Hardynesse
Strength and Stedfastnes / There is none noble by right but if he have these
three things / but if he be hardy prudent and entreprenau^t of great things.
and strong and puyssant for to pursiewe them. and ferme and stable to fynysshe
them. But without wit and without purueaunce nothing auayllen none of these
iij things. For like as says the book of the art of chyualrye. Error
without bataylle may not be amended. For it is anon compared. Folyssh
enterprise is where as lies little prouffyte. much despence and great pain and
peril. These been thenterpryses of them that been called wise and hardy in
this world. that their bodies and their souls putten in sin in peril and
in pain for to get a little loos and preysyng which is much vain. and little
endures But virtue makes a man of great heart and of wise enterprise. when
she makes a man which is nothing but earth so hardy. that he dare enterprise
to conquer the royalme of heaven. and to vaynquysshe all the deuylles of hell
that been so strong This enterprise is good wise and much prouffytable / For
there is therein little peril. and little pain but there is glory honor and
prouffyte inestymable. and perdurable without mesure. who has no virtue has
no great heart. but he is like him that is aferde of naught. Such ben they
that doubten the euylles / the aduersytees / perils / and trybulacyons of the
world. And that have dread to lose that / which they may not long keep They
have no great heart that give hit over for naught. like as done they that give
their hertes for to love the goods of fortune / which in truth been right
naught / but fylthe charge and ordure to the regard of the goods and glory
perdurable Then such people been like a child. that loves better an apple
or a myrrour than a royame / But virtue gives great heart by right / For virtue
makes them to conquer heaven. despise the world / and to bear great deeds of
penance. And to supporte and gladly suffer all the euylles of the world and to
endure them for gods sake / And also for to wythstonde and resyste all the
assaults of the devil / Like as the wise and prudente Seneke says. wepynges.
myschau^ces / sorows. trybulaco^ns / harms shames. perils. and all that
which evil fortune may menace and do. have no more power against virtue / than
one drope of water should do in the sea. virtue makes a man hardy as a lion /
strong as an holyfaunte. ferme and durable as the son which always renneth
and is never weary. Then there is no prowess ne strength but in virtues.

Of very seygnorye which gives grace and virtues lxx
THus is there none very seygnorye. but in virtues. A great lord is he that
knows all the world. Such a lord gives to a man such virtues and grace.
For he sets a man in his right estate. in which he was first set in and
made. The man was made in such honor and in such seygnorye. that he was lord
over al creatures that were under heaven. to whom al things obeyed. and to
whom no thing might noye ne grieve. and this is the right estate to the man
and to his seygnorye. but he lost this seygnorye by sin. And might not
recover it ageyn but by virtue. But virtue sets a man on high. and sets
the world under his feet. and makes him to converse in heaven. virtue makes a
man by good right gretter lord of the world / than the king is of his royame /
For of the goods of the world he has as much as his heart desires. he has
his usage and his sustenaunce. and as much as he may have for suffysaunce. and
more suffysantlye than the king has in his royame / For all that the good has
and the evil / al is his. Therefore of all he does his prouffyte and preyseth
god and thanketh and loves him the more. and doubts and serves. And in this
he sees and knows that every creature is made for to serve him. Also there
is another seygnorye much great / without whom there is none by ryzt lord.
for he is emperor and lord of him self. that is of his body and of his heart.
which he Iustyceth and holds them in good pees and does his will / For his
heart is so joined to the will of god / so that of all that. that god does he
thanketh him. and it playseth him well / And this is the seygnorye that virtue
gives to him that has it. Of this speaks seneke and says as great honor
gives god to the / when thou art lord and emperor of thy self and more tha^ a
king / ha lord god how many kings emperors and other great lords have been in
the world and also barons / that have citees / castellis. and royames that have
not this seygnorye. For they be not lords of their hertes. By cause that it
tormenteth often. by wrath or by maletalente. or by couetyse. or by desire that
they may not accomplysshe.

Here is spoken of very fraunchyse capo. lxxj
AFter this I say that there is none that has very frau^chyse / if he have
not grace and virtue. Then if thou will know what is very frau^chyse of a
man and of a woman by right. Thou ought to understand that a man has iij
manner of fraunchyses / One of nature. another of grace / and the third of
glory. The first is free will by which a man may chese and do freely good or
evil. This fraunchyse holds every man of god so freely that no man may do it
wrong ne all the deuylles of hell may not enforce a man ayenste his will to
do a sin without his accord and consentemente. For if a man did evil against
his wylle^ he should have thereof no sin. for as much as he in no wise might
eschew it. like as says saint austyn / This fredom and fraunchyse has every
man / But this fredom is not in children. ne in wood men. ne in fools. by
cause they have not the usage of reason by which they can chese the good from
the evil / A man puts away from him this fraunchyse in great party when he
synneth dedelye. For he sells him self unto the devil for the delight of his
sin / And yeldeth him self unto him. and bycometh his servant by sin. so
that he may not cast him self out. ne put him fro his will. for he has
deserved the death of hell. if the grace of god help him not. The second
fraunchyse is such that the wise man has in this world / whom god has
frau^chysed by grace and by virtues from the service of the devil. and fro
sin. that they be not bond to gold ne to silver / ne to temporalle goods
of this world. ne to their bodies which is caroyn. ne to the goods of fortune
/ which the death may sone take away. but they have their hertes lift up and
given to god. so that they preyse no thing the goods of the world. ne the
honors. ne the vanytees / ne king / ne duc / ne meschaunce ne pouerte. ne
shame. ne death / For they been now deed to the world. and have the heart so
deceueryd and taken away fro the love of the world. that they desire the death.
like as the werkman his payment of his Journey or days labor. and the
labourer his hyre. and also like as they that been in the torment and in the
fortune of the sea. desire to come to port salve / And like as the prysonner
desires good delyueraunce / and as the pilgrim desires to come ageyn in to
his contreye. And if they be parfytelye free in this world like as a creature
may be. then fere they ne doubt they no thing but god. and been in greet
pees of heart. For they have then their heart in god and been in heaven by
desire / And this fraunchyse comes of grace and of virtue. But yet all this
fraunchyse nys but seruytude to the regard of the third. fraunchyse that they
have that been in glory / They be verayly free. For they be verayly delyuerd
fro all perils and fro all torments. fro fere of death and of death. fro the
grynnes and empessheme^s of the world fro myserye / fro pouerte. and fro al
pain of heart and of body without retornyng. Of the which thing there is
none free in this world / how parfyte that he be /

Of very noblesse capo. lxxij
WHo that shall have the second fraunchyse of which I have spoken shall come to
great noblesse / The very noblesse comes of gentyl heart. Certain none heart is
gentyl but if he love god. There is no noblesse but to serve and love god and
to keep him fro al sins and from the seruage of the de.+uyl. Ne there is no
vylanye but to anger god by sin. There is no man by right gentyl. ne noble of
the gentylnesse of his body. For as touching the body we ben al sons of one
mother. That is of the earth and of fylthe of which we al have taken flesh
and blood. Of this part there is none gentyl ne free. But our sweet fader
Ihesu Christ which is king of heaven that fourmed the body of the earth and
created the soul to his image and semblau^ce. and al in like wise as it is of
the carnal fader. that is much glad and joyous when his sone resembles him /
Right so is it of our fader Ihesu Christ. For by the holy scripture. and by his
messagers he techeth us. that we should pain our self to resemble him. And
therefore he sent to us his blessed sone Ihesu Christ in to therthe for to bring
and give to us the very exemplayre. by which we may be reformed to his image
and semblaunce like as they that dwell in the hye cytee of heaven / That been
the angellys and the saints of heaven / where eueryche is of so much more hye
and more noble. As more proprely he bears this fair image / And therefore the
holy men in this world pain them self to know god. and to love him with all
their heart. and purge them cleanse and keep them from all sins. For of so
much as the heart of a creature is more pure and more clean without sin / of
so much he sees more clearly and more euydently the precious face of Ihesu
christ. and of so much he loves more ardauntly. of so much he resembles
more proprelye. And by that he has the more gretter glory. And this is the
very noblesse that god has given us / And therefore says right well Saint
Johan the appostle and euangelyst / that then we shall be the sons of god /
and we shall resemble him proprely. wha^ we shall see him euydently like as he is
/ This shall be in his glory. when we shall be in heaven. For no man sees so
dyscouerd ne so clearly the beauty of god. like as says saint poule / But
then we shall see him face to face proprely and clearly when we shall be in
glory in his Joyous company The very noblesse of a man then begins by
grace and by virtues / and that is parfyght glory / This noblesse makes the
holy ghoost in the hertes that he purges and culumyneth in truth and in
parfyte charity / These been the grettest goods that god has done to
aungellis like as saint Denis says. by which they resemble their maker / Thus
werketh the holy ghoost by grace and by virtue in the hertes of good men / by
which they be reformed to thymage and to the semblaunce of their maker Ihesu
Christ as much as it may be in this mortal life / For they reyse them self so
in god / and enbrace them self so with the love of god. And al their
entendement. al their entencyon / their will / their memory is all converted
to god / And this love and this enbracement and desire which encreaceth
Joins and vnyeth so the heart to god. that they may no thing will. but
that. that god will For there is not between them and god but one self will.
And then he has thymage and the semblaunce of god as much as may be had in
this world. And this is the most great noblesse and the most hye gentylnesse
to which one may atteyne or mount. Ha good god how far from this noblesse
and fro this hyenesse ben they that make them so noble and so queynt. Of this
pour noblesse that they have of their mother the earth which bears and
nouryssheth the hogs as well as she does the Emperors and the Kings. And
they auau^te them of their gentylnesse. by cause they wene they be of more
gentyl fylthe than the other. and of this kynrede and parage conne they right
well recounte and tell / But that other side and that other noblesse they
behold no thing at all. of which comes the very noblesse and the gentyl
parage They should behold and take heed to their very exemplayr Ihesu Christ /
which more loved and honored his mother. than did any other man. And
nevertheless when one said to Ihesu Christ. Sir your mother and your cosyns
stonden without to seche you. he answered to them and said. And who is my mother
and who is my fader and cosyns / who someuer do the will of my fader that is
in heaven. he is my brother / he is my fader. my suster / and my mother. for this
is the noble side and the gentyl kynrede / by which comes and grows to the
heart very glory. and of that other grows vain noblesse and pride.

How charity is grettest of virtues capo. lxxiij
NOw I have suffysauntly showed to the that there ben no goods honorable by
right but virtues and charity. This is the fair love of god / For there is none
other good prouffytable without this virtue of charity. This witnesses to us
saint poul that says thus. If I have as much science so that I knew al
clergy and al langages. and spoke as well as men or angellys. and knew all the
scryptures and the counseylles of god. and if I delyuerd my body to martyrdom.
and gaf all that I had to pour people / and if I did by miracles that the
montaygnes lepen from one place to another. if I had not the virtue of charity /
all this should not auaylle me. Now behold then and take heed that saint
Poul whom we ought to believe. has here named the grettest things and good
that one may do. and that most auaylle and prouffyten. That been penaunces of
the body. to suffer martyrdom to aid the pour people. to convert sinners. and
to have science of langages / and thappostle says al these things auayllen
not without charity. and if such and so great goods auayllen not. how should
less god auaylle. That same may thou know by reason. Think on this
proverb which is comunely said. As much is a man worth as his land is of
value. This is as true as the pater noster / who well under stands. how the
man is of no value. or sum thing or more or less. And this is no doubt
but it be that he have love and the charity of god. and who that has most is
most worth. and who that has less is less worth. and who that has naught
is naught worth. For how well that a man has temporalle goods. like as is
gold or silver or other rychessys / or of spyrytuel goods or naturalle. like
as art. engyne science clergy strength prowess or other goods / How shall I
say that they prouffyten. for they been the most part more cruelly dampened.
by cause they use not aryzt the goods that god has lent to them for to
multeplye and for to win than ben they that no thing know. Also if he do
bodyly werkys / as don the laborers the mynystrelles and other werkmen. or if
he do spyrytuel werkys as to fast wake clothe the pour were hayer. if this be
without charity all this auaylleth nothing. For he shall never have thereof
merit. But he that has virtue and parfyght charity / of all that that god
sends him in this world he does his prouffyte. and with al conquereth grace
and glory. Charity is good and sure marchaundyse. For oueral it wynneth and
never leseth / She byeth all the good wares. and makes al hyrs. and always she
has her penny ageyn. This is the love of the heart which is the penny / with
which she byeth all the goods of the world. and it remains always in the
almerye. love of charity has in all places his sales. Charity wynneth in all
quarellys. and has vyctorye in all bataylles / She does so much that it is
as much worth to her to give a penny. as to another an hundred pound / And
also charity does so much that it auaylleth one as much to fast one day. as
another all the lent. and to say one pater noster. as another to say a
psaulter^ And this is for none other reason. but by cause that as much is a
man worth as his land is of valewe. and so much ben worth his werkys / for so
much as a man has very love in god. so much he wynneth more every day. The
love that a man has to god is the poys and weight of saint Mychel. For none
other thing may not waye^ when one takes every day his wages. but the love
and charity. And therefore I say that there is none good prouffytable. proprely
to speak by right but fair love and charity.

Of two manner of delectable goods capitulo lxxiiij
IN like wise as god made man of body and soul. Right so has he given two
manner of delectable goods for to draw his heart to him. and in whom is all the very delight The sum goods comen wythoutforh and by the v wits of the
body / by seeing by heryng by smellyng by tastyng and by touching. These v
wits ben also as five conduytes / by which the goods delectable of the
world entren in to the heart for to delight him and for to lycke and draw to the
very delyces which ben in god to serve to love and to honor him. for all the
delight of this world that the five wits have / been not but a drope of dew
to the regard of the fontayn. that is Ihesu christ / But of the great see of
these goods. descends the drope of dew / when one sees hit a far
resemble to a precious stone. But when one weneth to take it. it falls to
ground and bycometh naught. Thus is it of the delytes of the five wits
bodily. when one thinks or fygureth or wyssheth or when one desires them /
it appyereth much precious. But when a man has and holds them. anon they be
lost. and bycome truffes and dremes. Think on the delight of the last year. and
of thy dreme to night. thou shall see that al is one. anon they passen. and
anon they comen ageyn. and in no manner may they fulfylle the heart of a man.
And if in a drope be as much sweetness / that it is the sweetness of all the
fontayne / Then is that a delectable good / And therefore the wise and holy
men in all that they saw in this world / and sauoureden of the delectable
goods of the world preyseden god. and most desyreden the love of him. and the
more that they saw the dropes sweet / the more they desyreden to come to the
fontayne celestyal. And therefore it is well known / that the more that one
forgeteth the drope. the more he loves the fontayn. and the reuerse / The more
that one loves the drope the more he hates the fontayn and forgeteth it. And
the more that the sweetness of the world playseth to a creature which he so
much desires / the less has he of the sweetness of god. Therefore the good
men take the less of the sweetness of the world as much as they may and will
not use the flesshly delytes / ne the deduytes that comen by the five wits
bodyly / A good lord god how much been they fools. and more than beestys.
that know well that the body of a man is the most foul thing that may be.
and that the soul of a man is the most noble thing. the most precious / and
the most noble creature that may be. Therefore they should not wene that the
goods that come of the body be more delectable and sweet. than they of the
spyrite / which ben very good. pure / and perdurable / and may fulfylle the
heart and replenysshe it. Such goods gives god to a man in this world. when
he gives to him pees of heart and vyctorye against his sins and against
thenemyes of hell. And gives to him glory of conscience and apeasyble heart
/ when he replenyssheth the heart with love and spyrytuel Joy / Of such Joy
ne of such delight. no semblau^ce ne no comparyson may be fou^den in the joys
of the world / ne been not but dropes to the regard of the fontayne of
sweetness which is Ihesu Christ. This is the fontayne of sweetness of which
our lord speaks in the gospel. who that shall drink of the water that I shall
give him. he shall become a living fontayne. which shall make him lepe in to
the life perdurable. This is the fontayn of joy of sweetness and of charity.
which may fylle and replenysshe the heart. And none other thing what someuer
it be may not fylle it Of this fontayne has tasted Dauyd the prophet which
says in his psaulter. O lord god how much is the multitude of thy great
sweetness / which thou kepest to thy servants. and departest to thy
friends. And certain who had well tasted and sauoured this sweetness that god
has given to his friends / he should despise all the delyces and all the Joys
of this world / and should chese and reteyne the spyrytuel Joy. And should do
like as they that bulte the mele and deceuereth the flour fro the bre^ne and
grous. and as they that make the oil / that take the clear pure fat. and
leave the gross matere. For Joy of the heart that comes of god to love / to
serve and honor him which is very Joy parfyte / like as says the proverb.
That none has parfyght Joy if it come not of love / And therefore this joy is
called oylle in holy scripture. like as our lord says by the prophet. I
shall give says he Oylle of Joy for weeping. This is joy of heart pure and
very for weeping of penance. Of this oylle ben enoynted they that god has
made kings and lords of the world and of them self / And then is a man
parfyte christian when he is enoynted with holy cresme. For of crisme is said
cries. and of christ is said christian / that is of Ihesu Christ And who that is
enoynted of such oynement. that is of Joy and love of god. he lives in god
and god in him. like as the appostle says / And this is then the life of a
Christian / that is to speak right. the life of a man / This is a good life and and
blessydnes that al christian men ought to seche and desire for to get the life
perdurable. ye know much well that he is not in life. but in langour / that
always lives in pain. in thought and in anguysshe. This is no thing. but now
weep. and anon laughe. Now is ease. now is he at mysease / now is he in anger.
now is he in pees. now in Joy. now in sorrow. Then who that will led a good
life / and live Justly without sin. seche he that he have the very good.
then he shall have life honorable / delectable and prouffytable. And then he
shall live as a man reasonable. That is to say holyly / ordynatly. wisely
Ioyously and meryly / Meryly without anger. wisely without errour^ and Ioyously
without sorrow. and this life has one by grace and by virtue / and none
otherwise /

Here after is spoken of virtues in especyal capo. lxxv
NOw I have showed to the generally here tofore the dygnyte and the valor of
the virtue of charity. and wherefore one ought to get it. For great prouffyt
comes for to have it. as Joy. honor. and glory perdurable. But by cause men
know not the thing so well in general as they do in specyal Therefore is mine
entencyon to speak of virtues in especyal. in such manner that eueryche that
will study in this book may ordeyne his life by virtue and by good werkys. For
otherwise little should auaylle to know the good if he do it not. For like as
says Saint James the appostle. who that knows the good and does it not / he
synneth and mysdoeth / he is a fool that knows the right way. and ernestly
gooth out of hit The holy scripture says thus. The wise man or wise woman
has a fair gardyn full of verdure and fair trees and of good fruytes^ whereof
god says in the book of love to the holy soul. My suster. my friend thou art
a gardyn enclosed of two closures. That is of the grace of god and of angellys.
This gardyn planted the great gardyner / That is god the fader when that he
admolysshed and made soft the heart of the creature humayn. and made it sweet
and traytable like wax chauffed / and as good earth well arrayed and cultyued.
and worthy that good ympes should be therein planted. These ympes been the
virtues which the holy ghoost bydeweth with his grace The blessed sone of god.
which is the very son / by the virtue of his clerenesse makes them to grow
on hye and prouffyte These three things be necessary to all the things that
grow in earth. that is to wete. earth couenable / humor nourysshable / and
hete reasonable / without these three things spyrytually may not the ympes of
virtues grow ne bring forth fruit. These things makes the grace of the
holy ghoost in the heart of the person. and makes to wexe grene / to
flourysshe and to fructefye. and it makes him as a gardyn much delectable full
of good and precious trees. But in like wise as god planted in paradys
terrestre plente of good trees and of fruit. And in the myddle he planted a
tree. which was called the tree of life. By cause that his fruit had strength
and virtue to keep the life to them that should ete of hit without deyeng. and
without ever to have any maladye or sekenesses / Right so does he spyrytuelly
in the heart of a person. The great gardyner / that is god the fader. For he
planted the trees of virtues / And in the myddle he set the tree of life /
That is Ihesu christ. which says in the gospel. who that eteth my flesh and
drynketh my blood has life perdurable. This tree enuerdureth and embelyssheth
by his virtue all that which is in paradys / By the virtue of this tree grown
and flourysshen and fructefyen all the other trees. In this tree is al good /
as much as there is / This tree is to be preysed and to be loved for many
things. For the rote. for the fruit / for the stock / for the flower. for the
odor. for the leef / and for his fair shadow. The rote of this tree is the
right great love and the oultrageous charity of god the fader / of which he
loved us so much. that for to bye ageyn his evil servant / he gaf his right
blessed sone and delyuerd him to death and to tormente / Of this rote speaks
the prophet and says thus. That a rod shall issue of the rote of Iesse /
This word is as much to say as embracer of love. The stock of this precious
tree. is the precious flesh of Ihesu Christ. The heart of this tree. that was
the holy soul in which was the precious marghe of the sapyence of god. The
bark of the tree was the fair conversation wythoutforth. The droppynges of
this tree and the body. weren three precious things and of right great virtue /
which yssueden and dropped out of the precious members of Ihesu crist that
were the water. the teres. the sweet and the blood / The leuys of this tree
weren the precious and holy words of Ihesu Christ which heleden al maladyes /
The flowers were the holy thoughts of Ihesu Crist which were fair / honest
and beryng fruit / The fruit weren the twelve apostles / which fed all the
world and nourysshed it with their holy doctrine. by their examples. by their
good werkys. and with their benefaytes. The branch of this tree in one sens.
been all the chosen that ever were / and that been. and that ever shall been / For
like as our savior Ihesu Christ said to his appostles. I am said he the vygne.
and ye ben the branches In another sens. his branches were his fair virtues.
and his gloryouse exemples / which he showed by work / and taught them with
his mouth. These were the parfyte virtues and full of very beneurte and
blessydnesse / which Ihesu Christ showed to his pryue friends to the xij
apostles. whom he led in to the montayne / and there he satte as says the
gospel. and his dyscyples were about him. And then the debonayr Ihesus
opened his mouth and said Blessed be the pour of spyryte. for the royalme of
heaven is theyres. Blessed be the debonayr for they shall be lords of the
earth. Blessed be they that wepen / For they shall be comforted. Blessed be they
that have hungre and thurst for Justice / for they shall be full fed. Blessed
be the mercyful. for they shall find mercy. Blessed be they that be clean of
heart. for they shall see god. Blessed be the peasyble. for they shall be called
the sons of god. These ben the seven branches of life of the blessed sone of
god Ihesu Christ. In the shadow of this tree ought the fine. and good heart to
shadow him. and ought to see and behold these fair branches. which bear
the fruit of life perdurable / In these branches and in these seven words is
enclosed all hyenesse. al perfection of grace. of virtue and of blessydnesse. as
much as may be had in this world. and to have and atteyne in that other. For
these ben seven rules of holy life which Ihesu Crist taught to his children.
This is the very phylosophye that the maystre of angellys enseygned to his
dyscyples In these words is enclosed all the sum of very perfection of the
new law of love and of swetnesse. And it is well said new. For it may well
wexe old. like as did tholde law to the Jews. And by cause that the soul
was woxen old by sin. it is made young ageyn and bycomen new by these
words aforesaid. It is very new and desguysed fro the other laws. law is
said by cause it is bounden / But the other bynden. and this unbinds / The
other chargen / this dyschargeth. The other laws men^cen and threten / this
law promyseth / In other laws is plee / In this new law is pees / In other
laws is dread / In this new law is love / The other laws have maledyctyon
and cursyng. this new law has benedyction and blessyng / Then is this new
law al full of beneurte and blessydnesse / And therefore ben blessed all they
that keep it and accomplysshe it. this says Salamon. For all they that keep it
well wynnen the tree of life perdurable. Then these vij words abouesayd which
god said ben called blessings / For they make a man to be blessed as much as
he may be in this present life. and yet more blessed in that other. Now have
thou herd what the tree of life is. which is in the myddel of paradys which
god planted in the holy soul / In the shadow of this tree grows and
prouffyteth the fruit; The tree of virtues which god the fader. that is the
great gardyner / planted in this gardyn. and bydewed it with the fontayne of
grace. which makes it wexe grene. grow and to prouffyte / and holds it in
virtue. and in life / This fontayne is departed in to seven ryuers. These ben
the vij yeftes of the holy ghoost. which arowsen and watren all the gardyn. Now
behold the right great curtosy of god. which came in to this world. for to
seche and save that which was lost. by cause that he knew well our pouerte
and our feblenesse. by which we may fall in to sin But by our self we may
not relyeue us ne issue out of sin ne get virtue ne do none other good / but
if it be by the grace of god / or that it come of his yefte. and therefore he
cesseth not to excyte us that we pray and require him of these yeftes. And
promyseth much to us / that if we require and demand him any thing that is
good for us / and that it be ryghtfull we shall have it. And yet the debonayr
Ihesus does unto us more of his curtosye. For he is our advocate that forms
for us our request and our petycyon. For we have not the wit if he formed it
not to us. The petycion. the request or oryson that the sweet Ihesus informed
and taught us with his blessed mouth / is much fair. much good / and but
short by cause we should reteyne it well / That is the pater noster. wherein been
vij petycyons and requestys. by the which we require our good fader Ihesu
Christ. that he give us the vij yeftes of the holy ghoost / that he deliver us
fro the vij dedely sins. and that he take them away fro our hertes. And instead of the said sins. that he by his grace will plant there and nourysshe
the vij virtues / which bring us to the vij blessings of perfectyon and of
holy life. by which we may have the promysses that the debonayr Ihesus maad and
promised to his chosen people in the seven words aforesaid. Then our
entencyon is with the aid and grace of the holy ghoost. to speak first of the
seven petycions of the holy ghoost which been contained in the holy pater
noster. After I purpose to say of the yeftes of the holy ghoost / After of the
seven virtues. against the seven dedely sins / The seven petycyons and
requests ben like as seven fair maidens that never cesse to draw the living
waters out of seven ryuers for to watre and arouse these seven trees that bear
the fruit of life perdurable /

The seven petycyons an drequestes that been contained in the holy Pater noster
capitulo lxxvj
When a lytyl child is set to scole. at begynni^g he lerneth his pater
noster / who that will learn of this clergy and know it. he must be little and
humble as is a child. For our good master Ihesu Christ techeth his scolers
this clergy which is the most prouffytable and the most fair that is / who
that this doctrine well knows. understands / and well reteyneth hit For such
there be that wene well for to understand it. that no thing know thereof / by
the bark or rynde wythoutforth That is the lettre which is good. But little is
hit worth to the regard of the margh^ / of the goodness and of the great
substance which wythinforth is so sweet / It is much short in words and
much long in substance / light to say and subtyl for to understand. This
prayer and oryson passes and surmounteth all other in three things. That is
to wit / In shortness / In dygnyte / and in prouffytablenesse The dygnyte is
in that. that the right blessed sone of god made it. to god the fader in short
words. God the holy ghoost touching his demand. he will that it be short in
words. by cause that none ne excuse him to learn it and to conne it / And also
by cause that none should be grieved to say it wyllyngly and often. And for to
show that god the fader hereth us right soon / and grau^teth it gladly when
we pray him with good heart. so that it be not of long ryotte ne of words
polysshed ne rymed / For sweet Saint Gregory says Verayly for to work is not
to say fair and glosyng words with the mouth. but to cast out wepynges
and deep syghes from the heart. The valor and the prouffyte of this oryson or
prayer is so great / that it compryseth and encloseth in words much short /
all that which may be desired of heart. and prayed and demanded of mouth.
That is to be delyuerd of all euylles. and replenysshed with al goods Thus
begins the holy pater noster. Fader our that art in heaven. Behold now how
our good advocate. and our right good and blessed master our Lord Ihesus
Christ which is the sapyence of god the fader. and that knows all the vsages
and all the laws of his court / techeth us for to plete well. and to speak
wisely / subtylly. and shortly. But certeynly if the first word that thou
say. fader our that art in heuen^ yt that it be well vnderstonden and well
poursyewed he shall give to the all thy request and all thy demand / For
Saint bernard says that the oryson that begins by the right name of god the
fader / gives to us hope to Impetre and get all our prays and requestys
This sweet word fader. which makes sweet all the remenaunte. shows to the
that. which thou ought to believe / and somoneth the to that. which thou
ought to do. And these two things saves the man when he byleueth well and
a right And when he does after that he ought to do. when thou call him
fader / thou know that he is lord of the house. that is of heaven and of
earth. and capytayn and beginning. And fontayne of whom all creatures and
all goods comen. Thus knowlechest thou in that. his puyssaunce and might /
After I say by cause that he is a fader / he is ordeynour. governor. and
pourueour of his meyne. and specially of his children / that is of the men
whom him self has created. made and fourmed to his semblau^ce. and in this
thou knowlechest his sapyence / yet also sithe that he is a fader by nature and
by right. he loves that which he has maad. Like as says the book of
Sapyence. And he is debonayr and loves and nouryssheth his children / and
does their prouffyte better than they can deuyse / And he beteth and
chastyseth them when they mysdoon for their prouffyte as a good fader. And
gladly he receives them unto mercy and to pardon. when they have trespaced /
and return to him by great repentance And by this we know his bountee and
his great debonayrtee Now I have showed unto the then this word. when thou
say fader. his Puyssaunce. his Sapyence^ his bountee and his debonayrte / On
that other part he remembers thy self. thy noblesse. thy beaultee. and thy
richesse. Of more great noblesse ne may thou not be sone Ne unto so great a
king. Ne unto so mighty or puyssaunt an Emperor as is god. For more gretter
richesse may thou not have. than to be heir of all that he has. More great
beaulte may thou not have than to resemble him by right. The which beaulte
is so great that it passes the beaulte of man and of angellys. Then this
word fader remembers the that thou art his sone. by cause that thou paynest
thy self to resemble him. as a good sone ought to resemble his fader and to
ensyewe thy good fader. in all good virtues and in all good werkys. That is
to say that thou be wise and noble. vygorous strong and puyssaunte to do well
/ to keep the from all sins. and strongely resyste against the temptacyons of
the fend / And that thou be wise and aduysed. large. curtoys. sweet and
debonayr. clean without vylonye and with out sin / like as is thy fader our
lord Ihesu Christ. And that thou hate sin and fylthe and al evil. as does
thy good fader Ihesu christ. so that thou forsake him not. This word then
fader. remembers the all the times that thou say it. that if thou be his
good and true sone. thou ought to resemble him by nature. by commandment
and by right. For thou owe to him love. honor. reverence and dread. seruyse
and obedyence. Now think then when thou say thy pater noster / that thou
be to him a good sone and true if thou will that he be to the a good fader
and debonayr. hit is said to a knight. think whose sone thou art / for to give
to him the gretter courage. when he enters in to the tournoyeng. here see
thou how this first word when thou say fader. how sweet it is. and how it
admonesteth the. that thou be valyaunte and noble. and techeth the what thou
sholdest be.

wherefore thou say fader our. and not fader mine lxxvij
NOw demand I of the wherefore that thou say fader oure^ and thou say
not fader mine. And unto whom thou accompanyest the / when thou say give to
us and not give to me / None ought to say fader our. but he that is his sone by
nature without beginning and without endyng. That is the blessed sone of god
Ihesu Christ. But we ben not his sons by nature. but in as much as we be maad
to his image and to his semblaunce / So ben the sarasyns and the Jews. we
been his sons by grace and by adopcyon. Adopcyon is a word of law / For the
law of the Emperors. when an hye man has no children / he may chese the sone
of a pour man if he will. and make of him his sone and his air if he will by
adopcyon / This is by aduoerye. And by that he shall be his herytyer and his
heyr and have his heritage This grace has given to us the sone of god the
fader without our deserte. like as Saint Poul says / when he maad us come to
baptesme / where as we were pour and naked / and all sons of wrath and of
hell Then when we say fader our / and we say give to us / we accompanye with
us all our brethern by adopcion. which been sons of holy church / by the
faith that they received in baptesme / Now we show then by this word
ours. the largess and the curtosye of god our fader. which gives more
gladly enough than little. to many than to one / whereof Saint gregory says.
that the prayer that is common is much worth and prouffytable. In like wise as
the candel is better employed and is more prouffytable that serves and
lyghteth many men / than that which serves and lyghteth but one man allone
This word fader our admonesteth us to yield thankynges with all our hertes
of this grace which god has done to us. by which we ben his sons and his
heirs. and that much ardauntly we ought to love our brother and fader Ihesu
christ which has accompanied us with him to this grace. This word our
admonesteth that we keep in our hertes the holy ghoost which is our witness
of this adopcyon / And like as he were a gayge or wedde. This says the
appostle Saint Poule. By whom we be sure. that we shall have the heritage of
our fader our lord Ihesu Christ. That is the glory of our fader of heaven. This
word fader our techeth us and says that we been all brethern. both great
and small. Pour and rich. high and low. of one fader and of one mother /
That is of god and of holy church. And that no man ought for to despise. ne
mespreyse another. but to love him as his own brother. And that one ought to
aid and help another. like as the members do of one self body / And also we
ought to pray the one for that other like as says the blessed appostle Saint
James. and in this our prouffyte is much great / For when thou say thy
prayer in common. thou have part in all the comynalte of holy church And for
one Pater noster that thou say. thou wynnest more than an hundred thousand.

This word ours techeth us to hate three things in especyal. Pride. Hate. and
auaryce / Pride puts a man out of company / when he will be above all
other people. Hate puts him out of company. For when he hates and warreth
one. he warreth all the other / Auaryce puts him out of companye^ For he
will not him self. ne that his things comyne with other / And therefore such
people have no part ne company in the holy pater noster^ This word our.
shows that god is ours. if it be not in our deffaulte. if we will. The fader
the sone and the holy ghoost. That is if we keep his commandementes like as the
gospel says.

why we say. qui es in celis capitulo lxxviij
When that I say. qui es in celis. that is to say. which art in heaven. I say
two things. like as I shall say / The king is at paris. I say two things.
that he is a king and that he is at paris. Right so when I say that he is in
heaven. I say that he is. and that he is in heaven It is founden in holy
scripture in two books of the law that god appyered to moses the prophet in
a montayne and said to him. Goo thou in to Egipte and say to king pharao on my
behalue that he deliver my people the children of Israel from the seruage.
wherein he holds them. Sir said moses if it be demanded of me how ye be
named what shall I say / I am that I am. said god. Thus shall thou say to the
children of Israel. He that is sends me to you. Now sayen the holy and good
clerkys. that emonge all the hye names of our lord this name is the first and
most propre / And that most aryght techeth us what god is. For all his other
names. either they speak of his bounte. or of his excellence. or of his
sapyence / or of his puyssaunce. or that he is such or such That is the right
good. the right wise / the right fair / the right puyssant / and many other
words as been said of him to his loange and preysyng. which say no thing of
the being of god / But we that been gross and rude to speak of so hye a thing
/ speak of god. like as one speaks and deuyseth of a man of whom he knows
not the name / Thus as it is said / he is a king he is a duc. he is an earl /
he is so great / he is so fair / he is so rich. he is so large. And many
of such propretees and Accydents. How and by what manner one may know what he
is / and what manner man / But he says not his propre name a right / But thus
as we speak of god we find many fair and sweet words. The which show unto
us sum thing of him / But there nys no word so propre / as this same word
here following / qui est. which so proprelye is showed to us and so subtylly.
In as much as our entendemente may stratche and compryse / For our blessed
Lord Ihesu christ is he. that is only. like as Job says. he is only. for
to say right. For he is only perdurable without beginning and without endyng
/ But this may not be said of none other thing. After he is very truth. For
he is way and truth. All things created. that been creatures. ben vayn and
vanytees as Salamon says / and be naught to the regard of him / and to naught
shall they come. fro whens they came if he sustain them not. and keep them by
his virtue. yet also he is only establement and steadfastness. For he is
always him self / and in one self point without trouble without to change
him / without to moeue him in any manner. this says Saint James. Al other
things been moeuable in sum manner of their nature. Then is he proprely
called / that is. For he is verayly without vanyte / establysshement. without
beginning / without end. without he was. and without he shall be. for in him
is no departing. Now ought thou here understand that he is And that there
is no thing that may better be known than this. that god is / And therefore I
counceyl the that thou muse not tenquyre ferther / For thou may sone err and
goo out of the way. late it suffyse to the that thou say. Fader our that art
in heaven / Troth it is that he is oueral present. in earth in heaven. in see.
and in hell. like as he is in heaven / But it is said that he is in heaven. by
cause that he is more seen there. more known. more byloued / and more honored
After I say that the debonayr Ihesus is in persons spyrytuel and devout That
is in the holy hertes. that been hye / clensyd / clean and purged from all
sin as is the heaven / For in such hertes is he seen. known. honored and
loved. Now have thou herd these iiij words Pater noster qui es in celis / The
first word somoneth the to honor god. The second to love god. The third to
redoubte god. For how well he be fader and our. always he is Just and not
meuable. The fourth word somoneth the to engyne thy self to him and to encorage
and enforce the. for ^yth he is so hye and thou art so low / if thou be not
hardy and vygorous to vaynquysshe al sins / to resyste all the temptacions of
the enemy / and to keep holy his commandementes. thou shalt not come in to
the glory of heaven / The first word abouesayd shows to us the length of his
eternytee. The second the largess of his charity. The third the depnesse of
his veryte and truth / And the fourth the hyenesse of his mageste. who
someuer shall have these four things attained without doubt he shall be well
blessed.

How Sanctificetur nomen tuu^ is expowned capo. lxxix
Now have thou herd the prologue of the holy pater noster which is like unto
an enter in to a town. A lord god who that well could al this song / he should
find therein many sweet notes / For it is no doubt that in the prayer and
song spyrytuel which the sapyence of god made. he that taught the birds to
sing / has many notes and words subtyl and sweet in his holy song and
prayer of the holy pater noster. how well that it conteyneth little letter. In
this song and excellent oryson ben vij notes. which ben the seven petycyons
and requests of the holy pater noster. which get and Impetre the seven
yeftes of the holy ghoost / which put away and destroy the seven vices
capytal of the heart. those ben the seven dedely sins. And they plant and
nourisshe the vij virtues. by the which one may come to the seven blessings /
Of these vij peticions and requests The three first make a man holy as much as
he may be in this world / The iiij after makes him parfytly Just / All the
holiness of a man that is made to thymage of the holy Trynyte after three
things that been in the soul. that is to wete / memory. entendement and will
is in iij things / In this that the soul be parfytely purged. and the will
parfytly enlumyned. and the understanding parfytly confermed in god. and with
god in the memory. And the more the soul receives of god these iij things.
the more habondantly and more proprely she approaches more to his right beauty
naturelle^ That is to the semblaunce of the fader and of the sone^ and of the
holy ghoost. That is when god the fader confermeth unto him his memoire. God
the sone enlumyneth to him his understanding. God the holy ghoost purges in
him his will These three yeftes we require in the iij first peticions of the
holy pater noster. when we say / Sa^ctificetur nomen. we show to our good
fader curtoysly our pryncypal desire. which we ought always to have. That is
that his glorious name be sanctyfyed. and that it be confermed in us. Then
when we say Sanctificetur nomen tuum. we show to our good fader Ihesu Christ
curtoysly our desire / That is to say Sir this is our souerayn desire. This
require we above all things that thy blessed name be sanctyfyed in us. That
is thy good reno^mee / thy knowleche. thy faith be confermed in us. In this
first petycyon we require the first and the pryncypal yefte of the holy ghoost
/ That is the yefte of sapyence which makes steadfast. and confermeth the
heart in god. and Joins him so to him that he may not be desioyned ne
deceuerd. Sapyence is said of savor and for to sauoure / for when a man
receives this yefte. he tastes and assauoureth. and feleth the sweetness of
god. like as is felt the sweetness of good wine by the taste better than by
the sight. But to this that thou understand better what it is to say. Thy name
be santyfyed. Thou ought to know that this word / Saint is as much to say
as pure. as gold. as earth / as dyed in blood. as confermed. In these five
manners is sayntyfyed the holy ghoost of sapyence in the heart of a man. First he
cleanses and purges like as the fyrefyneth and purges the gold and the
silver / after he takes it away fro the earth. that is fro al carnal
affections. and makes al to bycome lothely that which he was wont to love /
like as the water is hated to him that is lykorous to the good wine / After he
haloweth him self all to the service of god. For he leueth al charges. and
puts him self al to think on god and to love serve and honor him. like as
the church and the monasterye is hallowed to the service of god. So that he
ought none other thing do but to serve and honor god. After he dies him
self in blood / For he puts him self in one so strong and ardant love and
in so sweet love of Ihesu Christ / and of devotion. that when he thinks on him
and on his passion / he is as he were all drunk of the precious blood that
Ihesu Christ shed for him in his holy passion like as is a soppe of hot
