bread / when it is put in wine. This is a new bapteme / For to dye and to
baptyse is all one. After he confermeth him in god so strongelye / that
nothing may dysseuere ne desioyne him. Now then / will thou to say this word
/ thy name be sayntyfyed in vs^ That is to say give to us the yefte of sapyence
by which we may be so fined as is the gold. and the silver in the fornays /
and cleansed fro all ordures of sin. by which we be dronken of his love and
that al other loves be to us bitter / by which we be so given to the and to
thy service. that we never retche of none other charge. to the end that we be
not only wesshen fro all sins / but dyed in grain. renewed and rebaptysed
in the precious blood of Ihesu Christ by devotion of fervent love / to this that
the blessed name of our good fader Ihesu Christ be so confermed in us / that he
be our good fader. and we his good sons and his servants. as very obedyent
to all his commandments. and in such manner. that no thing what someuer it
be / may come ne happene to desioyne this fastnes ne this grace. Much is great
the grace of god wha^ the will of the creature humayn is so rooted in god and
confermed that it may not wagge ne moeue for no temptacyon / Much gretter a
thing it is / when one is so affermed in the love of god and so dronken in his
sweetness. that no soulas. ne no comfort / ne no playsaunce may not be had
but in him. and then is the heart parfytelye confermed in god. when the
memory is so fastened and joined to him. that it may not think on no thing
but on him / And this require we when we say / Sanctificetur nomen tuum. that
is to say / Sir thy name be sayntyfyed in us.

Here is the second petycyon and request of the holy pater noster capitulo lxxx
ADuemat regnum tuu^. This is the second petycyon and request of the holy
pater noster. where we pray and require. that the royame of god come in us.
and be within us Our lord says in the gospel to his dyscyples. The royalme of
god is now within you. Now understand well how this may be / when god gives to
a person in his heart the spyrite of understanding. Thus as the son takes
away the derknesses of the night. and wastes the clouds and the mystes in
the morning. Right so wastes this spyrite and takes away all the
derknesses of the heart. and shows him al his sins and defaultes great and
small / like as the rays of the son shows the motes and the duste that is
in the house / Also this spyrite of understanding shows on that other part.
not only that which is within him. but that which is under him. hell. and
that which is above him / heuen^ and that which is about him. all the fair
creatures / which al preysen god and wytnessen how god is fair. good. wise.
puyssant. sweet. and great. And who that sees most clear the creatures. is
most desyryng to see god. but let him consydere that he is not pure ne worthy
to see him. Then the good heart / true and devout chauffeth him / and is
angry with him self / Then he begins to enter in to his heart. and to
examyne him. And there he fyndeth so many sins. vices. pouertees /
deffaultes. troublynges of heart and of thoughts and evil will / that he is
angry with him self by great contrycyon and desplayser that he has of his
synnes^ And then he begins to cleanse his heart and purge him of al ordures
of sin by bitter repentance / and by devout confession / and after by
sharp and condygne penance / But when he has long led this life. and has
cast out al his sins by very confession / Then he fyndeth pees and rest
and consolacion. And tereth so much god to fall ageyn to sin / that him
seems that all the world be to him hell to the regard of this clerenesse
and this pees that he fyndeth in his heart. And this demand we of god when we
say. Aduemat regnum tuum / that is to say. Fair fader plese it to the that
the holy ghoost will enlumyne in us the heart. and cleanse and purge it fro al
sins / And that he vouchesauf to come and dwell as a king and a lord /
governor and commaundour in our hertes. so that all the heart be his / and
that he be king and lord and always that we may see him. For it is a life
perdurable to have the royame of god within us. Therefore says our lord in the
gospel / that the royame of god is as a tresour hyd in a field. that is in the
heart of a good man. which is more great than all the world.

The iij peticion and request of the holy pater noster lxxxj
FIat voluntas tua sicut in celo and in terra. This is the iij peticion and
request / where we pray our lord that his will be done in us / like as it is
done in heaven / that is as in holy angellys which ben in heaven / which ben so
enlumyned and confermed in god / that they may will none other thing but that
which that god will. we may not have this peticion ne this perfection but we
have the yefte of counceyl / which is the third yefte of the holy ghoost.
which techeth us to do his good will / and that he convert our caytyf and
fraylle will so that in us grow no propre will. but that his will be only
lady of all the heart holy / and do in us what someuer he will / like as his
will is done in holy aungellys of heaven which may not sin. And that always
done the will of god without mespryse and gaynsayeng. Now have thou herd the
three petycyons and first requests of the holy Pater noster. which ben the
highest and most worthy. In the first we demand the yefte of sapyence. In the
second the yefte of understanding. and in the third the yefte of counceyl. like
as I have tofore showed / These iij things we require not. by cause we should
have them in this mortal life parfytelye. But we show unto our good fader Ihesu
Christ our desires. that they be always in heaven where they ought to be. To the
end that these three requests and petycyons be done and accomplisshed in us in
the life perdurable / we demand them in this present life In the other four
petycyons that comen after we speak another langage^ For we say to our good
fader Ihesu Christ Give to us / Pardone us. keep us. and deliver us. For if we
have not of Ihesu Crist these four petycyons and requests in this present
world. we ben but deed^ For they be necessary to every person in this mortal
life.

The iiij petycyon and request capitulo lxxxij
PAnem nostrum cotidianum da nobis hodie / well techeth us our good master
Ihesu Crist to speak humbly and wisely. For he techeth us to say. Fair fader
give to us this day our bread cotydyan or daily. what may the sone less
demand of his fader. than only bread for to pass forth the day / he
demands none oultrage. ne wine. ne flesh. ne fysshe. but he demands
bread and no more not for a year. ne yet for a weke. but for to pass with the
day only / This seems that it is a little thing that we demand. but
certainly we require a much great thing. when we require of an abbot the
bread of an abbay / or require the fraternity. the company the part and the
right in all the goods of the abbey. Right so is it of him that demands of
god this daily breed / he has fraternity. part. company. and right in all
the goods that been in heaven. This is the blessed bread of heaven. of that
blessed couente / The bread of heaven / The bread of angellys. the bread
delectable / the bread of life perdurable. For it gives life understanding.
never to deye. and preserves a man / whereof god says in the gospel / I am the
bread of life which descended fro heaven. who that shall ete of this bread shall
always live without deyeng / This breed is right good mete. For hit stauncheth
all the hongres of the world / and fylleth a man and replenyssheth. this does
not other mete. this is the breed and the mete that thou take at the
sacrament of the altar. And this mete thou ought to take in great ardour
and in great devotion of heart. and in great desire / That is to understand
that thou ouztest to believe feythfully that this mete so much precious is the
very body of Ihesu Christ. and the soul. and the godhede al together without
error and without to demand or ask any ferther. For god may more than man
may understand. After a man ouzt to understand and chewe this precious mete.
like as the ox fedeth of the grass and cheweth his cudde / and then he
takes it in / That is to say that one ought to remember deuoutlye and often by
parties / the bountees and graces of our lord. and all the sorrows that Ihesus
Christ suffered in earth for us / Then the heart fyndeth the savor of this
precious mete / and causes a right great ardour of the love of god in right
great desire and will to do and to suffer all that he may for him / and more
than he may. And al this does the virtue of this blessed bread (...) the
sacrament of the mass which is the very precious b^^y of Ihesu Christ / This
is the bread that comfort and ^^^orceth the heart to that^ that he be well
strong to suffer and (...) do gr^te things for the love of god. But this may
not be (...) if he have the fourth yefte of the holy ghoost. which is (...)
the yefte of strength / which armeth and encorageth the ^nyght of god. and
makes him to re^ne gladly to martyrd^^ and to suffer Ioyously the torments.
Now may thou see. when we demand this bread of angellys. we demand the
yefte of strength. For like as the bodyly bread or materyal sustain the body
and enforce it. Right so the yefte of strength makes the heart strong to
suffer and to do great things for god. This bread celestial of angellis. we
call our / for he was made of our paste. he was sone of god the fader. and was
sone and borne of the glorious vyrgyn marye. Blessed be this glorious vyrgyn
fro whom came this blessed flower. For that was the debonayr Ihesus. which
was fried and crucyfyed on the cross for to redeem the world fro the pains of
hell / And this did he for the great brennyng love that he had unto us. This
is the bysquyt of which he garnysshed his ship of holy church to pass the
great see of this perilous world. he is ours. for he left to us at his
departing and leave taking at his last testamente the sweet Ihesu Christ. the
right large as the most great and most rich tresour that he might leave to
vs^ For he gaf him self to us as the most fairest Jewel that he might give to
us / And we ought deuoutelye. clenly and reverently keep him without sin. and
of this bread of angellys we ought every day to use for the love of him / and
in mind of his holy passion / he is verayly ours. For no thing may he take
away fro us against the will of ours. that is him self. we call our bread
cotydyan. that is to say of every day. that is to understand the cotydyan
distribucyon that he gives to his preestys and relygyous people every day
which done his seruyses and sing his masses and his hours. that is to all
good christian men and wymmen that every day by very love deuoutely make
remembrance of the dolorous passion of Ihesu Christ that he suffered for us. The
groos of the prouende of this bread of aungellys we take in harvest. that is in
heaven when we shall see the sweet Ihesu Christ dyscouerd / in his right great
beaulte like as he is / Therefore is it said cotydyan / that every day is to us
necessary. And every one ought to take the holy sacrament of the altar like
as done the preestys / which ben thereto ordained. Or otherwise every good
christian man or woman ought to take him by right faith / This bread is right
precious. right noble and right well arrayed / This is mete ryal in which been
all manner of delyces and al good savors like as says the book of sapyence.
This is none erthely mete that ought to be given to raskayll. but to hertes
gentyl and and noble which ben purged and cleansed fro al ordure of sin by
very repentance. by devout confession. and by entyer satysfactyon and
penance Of the virtue of this bread of angellys says Saint matthew
theuangelyst. and calls it bread sursubstancyal / That is to say. that it
passes and surmounteth all substance and all creatures of praysyng and of
virtue / of all dygnytees / and in all manners of valor / Nor none may better
name it ne descryue it ne more suffysauntlye than to call hit. breed
sursubstancyal /

It is said that a mete is substancyous. when there is therein enough of
substance and of nourysshyng / And for so much more as it is nourysshyng.
so much more it is said that it is substancyall. And by cause that in this
precious breed of Aungellys is more of nourysshyng of virtue. and of good than
ever may be thought and said is not said only that hit is substancyous
between any understanding and supposyng. but it is said sursubstancious This
bread require we at our good fader Ihesu Christ and we pray him that he will
give it to us in this day. that is in this present mortal life. to the^de that
we may make a good Iourneye. and abide more gladly our reward. that is in the
end of our life the glory perdurable.

Here follows the v petycion and request of the holy pater noster capitulo
lxxxiij
DImitte nobis debita nostra. sicut and nos dimittimus debitoribus nostris. In
this request and petycyon we require and demand our good fader of heaven that
he will pardonne and foryeue us our sins and our trespaces. like as we foryeue
them that have trespaced to us. or that trespass to us. Then we say thus
fair fader quyte to us our debtes like as we quyte our dettours^ Our dettes ben
our sins which we have increased upon our souls. This is the best and most
dear wedde that we may fine. whereof the synnar for one dedely sin which is
so sone passed as to the delight or as touching the deed. is bounden to so
great usure that he has no power to pay ne to fynyssbe^ that is the pain of
hell which is without end. After he owes unto god whom he has dysplesed
so great amends that he has no power to pay it. For in all his life if he
lived an hundred year or more he might ne could not make suffysau^t penance
For one dedely sin onely^ if god would use his ryghtful Justice. it should
never be fogyuen to the And therefore it byhoueth that in bitter and great
repentance the wicked synnar return unto the mercy of the debonayr and
blessed lord Ihesu Christ. And that he cry him mercy and demand pardon and
foryeuenes. For by the right of the court of Justice. the sinner shall be Iuged
and condeuipned unto death perdurable / And therefore our good fader Ihesu christ
which is soft and debonayr for to foryeue and pardone / large and curtoys for
to give / we pray him that he will pardone and foryeue to us our sins and
trespaces. But think and consider well how thou prayest / For thou say
pardone to us our sins and our trespaces. like as we pardone to them that to
us have trespaced. God shall not foryeue ne pardone to us / as he him self says
in the gospel. if we foryeue not and pardone to other that have trespaced to
us. Then he that says his pater noster if he keep in his heart rancour and
felonnye he prays more against him self than for him self / For he prays to
god that he forgive him not his sins. when he says foryeue me like as I
forgive. and therefore all the times that thou shall say thy pater noster tofore
god that sees thyn heart. Thou ought to forgive al evil talentes and cast
out of thyn heart al Ire and all rancour. Otherwise thy prayer is more against
the than with the. if it seem to the an hard thing and grievous to foryeue and
pardone to them that hate the / and that will the evil. or that have much
trespaced to the. or myssayed. Think that god pardoned his death to them that
crucefyed him / for to give to the an exaumple for to forgive. and more yet for
to pray for them that have trespaced to the / that god forgive them. and more
yet for to do well and good to them. and to help them if they have need / For
as he says in the gospel. that it is not a great thing ne great merit against
god to do good to them. that do us good / ne to love them that love us / For so
done the paynyms and the Sarasyns / Jews and other sinners. But we that been
the children of god by faith and by grace and been named christian of our blessed
Lord Ihesu Christ. and been heirs with him of the heritage of heaven. ought for
to foryeue each other. And also ought for to love our enemies. That is to say
their persons and pray for them and to do good to them if they have need.
For so comandeth god in the gospel. Then we ought only hate the sins and
to love her souls. Like as the members of one body love and supporte each
other. if one membre hurt that other by adventure / that other aduengeth him
not / And therefore we that been al one body in Ihesu Christ like as thappostle
says we ought to love and supporte each other. and not to hate ne to grieve.
and who that does otherwise he is an homycyde of him self. this says the
scripture / Such there be that can say their pater noster. that it were better
for them and more auaylable that they could say it aryght. For who that
pardons not. ne foryeueth with heart and with mouth. he moeueth his Judge
against him. In this prayer that we make to god. we require of him the yefte of
science. which makes a man wise and cunnyng. This spyrite shows to him.
what he is. fro whe^s he comes. whyther he gooth. and what he has don. and
what he has trespaced. how much he has lent. and how much he owes. And
when he sees that he has not whereof to pay. then this spyryte makes him
to repent. to weep and to syghe. and to cry god mercy and say. O good lord
foryeue and pardonne to me my debtes. that be my synnes^ for I am much
endetted unto the. for the euylles and sins that I have commysed and done.
and for the good deeds that I have forgoten and left to do. which that I
ought and might have done and for the goods and benefaytes that thou have done
to me^ and the great bountees which I have al day received and evil used them.
and have evil served the. And by cause lord that I much dread and doubt to
make my payement. I require the to pardone me that. which I owe unto the. when
this spyryte of science has thus enlumyned him that he knows his defaultes
and sins. Then he casts out of his heart all hate and rancour. and
pardons all his evil will and anger if he have any. And if he have any. and
is in will and in purpose to pardone and foryeue with good heart if any have
trespaced to him. Then may he well say / Fair fader forgive us our trespaces /
like as we do to them that have trespaced to us.

The vj peticion and request of the pater noster capo. lxxxiiij
ET ne nos inducas in temptacionem / Brent child fire dredeth / and he that
sometime is fallen in to sin. when his sin is pardoned him. he is more
doubtous and more aferde / and has more dread of the temptacyon of sin than
he had tofore / and therefore he prays to god to whom he has so much
trespaced. and also that has forgyuen and pardoned him. that he will keep him
fro falling in to hit ageyn. and says thus / Et ne nos inducas in
temptacionem. That is to say Fair sweet fader. suffer not thou that we enter
in to temptacyon. and that we consent not to any sin. The devil is the
temptour of sin. for it is his craft. of which he serves in the house of god
to preue the new knights of god / And if the temptacyon were not good and
prouffytable to good people. God which does al thing for our prouffyte. would
never suffer that temptacyon should come. But as saint Bernard says when our
temptour smyteth us on the back / He forgeth to us our crowns of glory /
like as he that smyteth on the back of a good knight / forgeth to him his
praysyng and his glory. The devil tempts a man proprely to the end that he
take him aweye and depart him holly from the love of our lord Ihesu Christ
Therefore prayed and prays to us Saint Poule the appostle. and unto his
dyssyples. that they be founded and term as a toure. and roted as a tree. in
charity. and in the love of god so that no temptacyon may moeue them ne make
them for to stakre ne quaure. And therefore in this petycyon and request we
require and demand the aid and help of god in our bataylle against the
fend. that he will give to us the yefte of pity / That is a grace that arouseth
and bedeweth the heart. and makes him sweet and pyetous. and makes him al to
render and wexe grene / and to bear fruit enough of good works wythoutforth.
and wythinforth / And within to make steadfast and ferme his roots in the land
of living people. That is like as the good cyment of which been maad these
walls sarazynoys / which may not be broken ne defeated with pykoys ne with
hamer when we say then. Et ne nos inducas in temptacionem. That is to say
sweet fader make our hertes ferme and stable. that they moeue not ne quauer for
no temptacion that come to them by the grace of the yefte of pity. we pray
not / that we be in no wise tempted / For that were a folysshe prayer and
shameful. like as the sone of a lord / or of another noble man. that should be
adoubed a new knight. and he should say to his fader. Fair fader I pray you
that ye me deporte or forbere and keep that I never see batayl ne tournoye / we
ought well will to be tempted. for it is our great prouffyte in many manners.
For we been the more humble and the more doubcous and the more wise in many
caases. and the bettyr proved and the more hardy. For as Salamon says the. who
that has not be tempted / he may know no thing a right but like as one
knows of the batayl of troy by here saying for he may not know him self ne
his Infirmyte / ne the strength of his enemies. ne their subtylte. ne how god
is true and (...) at need to aid his friend. ne how and many times he has
kept us from many perils and sins / and by all these reasons be shall not
co^ne love god aryght. ne thank him of his yeftes if he be not tempted. but
pray we him that he keep to us our hertes that they enter not in to
temptacyon. that is to say that the heart consent not thereto. and as touching
our self we be so pour. that we may not an hour of the day susteyn thassautes
and the diverse temptacions of the fend without the help of our lord. And
when he faylleth for to aid and help us we enter in to temptacion / And when
he helps us we resyste and we fight and vaynquysshe the fend our enemy when
that we consent not to sin.

The seventh petycyon of the pater noster capo. lxxxv
Ed libera nos a malo amen. saint austyn says that all the other temptacyons
ben to us either for to do well or for to leave to do well. But all the yeftes and
all the good that a man does. or that he can get / is for to put away and
destroy pride and al sins and euylles. And therefore when god has given to a
man this that he has required of god in the vj requests aforesaid. Then
certaynlye it is of very need that god deliver him from the puyssaunce of the
fend. fro all his engynes. and from al his temptacyons. And therefore comes
at the last this petycyon and request as the ryergarde which says thus. Sed
libera nos a malo amen / that is to say / Fair fader Ihesu Christ deliver us
fro al evil / fro all sins and fro all perils passed. present. and to
come. And fro al thengynes of the fend our enemy. that we lose not by pride
the goods that thou have given to us.

In this request we pray to god that he give to us the yefte of holy dread.
By the which we may be delyueryd fro the fend and from his temptacyons. and
fro all manner of evil. that is fro all perils and fro al sins in this
world and in that other amen. So be it as we have said / so much is it to say
this word amen. Now have thou he^^ the seven petycyons and requestys. which
god made wy^^ his blessed mouth. for to enseygne and teache us to learn all that
which we may and ought to pray and demand for the body and for the soul
and for this world and for that other / And al is contained and comprysed in
the holy Pater noster Now keep the well that thou say it aryght with heart and
with mouth. For great good shall come to the thereof. if thou so do.

Thus ends the seven petycyons of the holy Pater noster
Of the seven yeftes of the holy ghoost capitulo lxxxvj
AFter the peticions and requests that been contained in the holy Pater
noster. us byhoueth to speak in great reverence of so hye a matere as of the
holy yeftes of the holy ghoost. like as he him self of his grace shall
enseygne and teache us. And we shall say first which ben the yeftes of the
holy ghoost. After wherefore they be called yeftes. and wherefore they be called
of the holy ghoost. After wherefore they be seven yeftes of the holy ghoost ne
moo ne less / After we shall say of the goods that the yeftes of the holy
ghoost do. Custom it is. reason and curtosye. that a man hye. rich. valiant.
and noble when he will goo to his spouse that he loves with al his heart. that
he bear to her of his Iewellys. Ysaye the prophet saw in spyrite the
gloryouse espowsaylles that were made in the belly of the blessed vyrgyn marye.
when the blessed sone of god espoused her / and took in her our blood and our
flesh / our humanyte and our nature. So recounteth to us the said prophet of
the Iewellys and the fair yeftes that he brought with him for to give to his
espouse and to her parents / And says thus the said prophet much
curtoyslye. Fro the rote of Iesse shall issue a rod that shall bear the flower
of nazareth. That is to say. out of the great charity. and fro the great
enbracyng or brennyng of the love of god shall come to us a rod which shall
bear the flower of flowers. For Nazareth is as much to say as a flower / and
Iesse is as much to say as enbracyng or brennyng. And upon this flour shall
rest the holy ghoost. the spyryte of sapyence and of understanding / the
spyrite of strength and of counceyl / the spyryte of science and of pity. and
the spyryte of the dread of god. These ben the graces of which he was al full
fro the hour that he was conceived in the precious belly of his mother / like as
the great see is full of water. and is well and fontayne of all the fresshe
waters and salt. of which he arowseth and watreth all the world / Right so was
he as says Saint Johan theuangelyst so full of grace. of veryte or truth that
of his plant we take al These vij spyrites and these seven yeftes we take them
and receive in the holy baptesme But thus as the graces corporelle which god
gives to children. in wit / in bounte / in strength. and in other graces.
which he gives at his playsyr^ to eueryche he shows him lytyl and lytyl.
like as a child grows and comes forth. Right so is it in spyrytuel graces.
after that / that eueryche prouffyteth and grows in good werkys. and gives
all his heart / and all his thought to god / after that. god gives to him
more of his graces. and that shows the same yeftes by werkys. sum in one /
and other in other. at the playsyr of the holy ghoost as says saint Poul the
appostle. Then in our beginning these graces and these virtues been low /
and rise on heyght / That is fro the spyryte and yefte of dread unto the yefte
of sapyende. For holy dread is the beginning of sapyence. Like as dauyd says
and Salamon. But in Ihesu Christ weren always all the graces and all the
virtues plenerly without any mesure. And therefore the prophet sets them in
descendyng each yefte after the order of his dygnyte. like as the petycyons and
requests of the holy pater noster ben set forth after the order of their
dygnyte. the hye tofore. and the lower after.

why they be called yeftes. for three reasons capo. lxxxvij
SVche manner graces have to name yeftes. for iij things and for three reasons.
First for their dygnyte and for their valor. if a man at the court of the king
give a robe to a child. or to a pour man a dysshe of weight. This is no thing
that ought to be called the yefte of a king. Therefore calls Saint James
thappostle all the other temporel goods that god gives / not a yefte / but
little yeftes which ben moeuable and passing / But these graces abouesayd he
called them yeftes parfyte / For god gives them to no creature / but that he
gives to him / him self. The second reason is by cause that the other graces
and the other yeftes he leneth them to us for to use them in this present life.
But these seven yeftes toforesayd ben very yeftes by right without reprysyng
and reprehendyng / for when all the other yeftes shall faylle. these vij yeftes
shall abide always in their ferme estate. Then they be so proprely ours that
we may not lose them ageyn our will. like as we may lose the other / The third
reason and the pryncypal is. that the selue yeftes be given purely for love.
And thou know well that a yefte leseth the name of yefte when it is not given
purely for love. For when the yeuer yeueth any yefte for his own prouffyte /
that is not a yefte. but it is marchandyse. when he beholds bounte received
or seruyse / that is not a yefte. but it is bounte and curtosye. received to be
rendered and yolden ageyn. But when the yeftes is gyneu freely and lyberally
without entencyon to have prouffyte and without dread and without any doubt.
Then is it by right called yefte / hereof says the phylosophre that a yefte
is a yefte without gyuyng ageyn / or without to awayte any reward but only
for to get love. In this manner. god gives to us these yeftes purely for the
love that he has to us. and for to get our hertes and al our love to him.

why they be called the yeftes of the holy ghoost capo. lxxxviij
NOw for what cause been they called yeftes of the holy ghoost. and not the
yeftes of the fader and of the son. for all their werkys and their yeftes ben
common. To this purpoos ben two reasons. That one like as the works of
puyssaunce and might ben appropred to god the fader. and the works of sapyence
to god the sone. right so ben the werkys of grace and of bounte appropred to
the holy ghoost. For bountees ben like as says saint denis. to spend and to
give him self / For if a man give that. which cost him naught / that is not
great bounte. But by cause that the holy ghoost by these seven yeftes expendeth
and gives him self in our hertes. Like as says saint poule. like as it were
by seven stremes / therefore ben they called proprely yeftes of the holy ghoost.
For he is the fontayn and they ben the stremes That other is by cause that the
holy ghoost is proprely the love that is between the fader and the son / and
by cause that love is the propre. the first. and the pryncypal yefte. that a
man may give. then with right in this yefte ben given all the other. and
without this yefte none other is not called yefte truly ne ryghtfully.
Therefore is the holy ghoost a yefte. and yeuar. For he gives him self and is
yeuen in eueryche of these seven yeftes. which that he gives for to conferme
our love unto his. so that it be fervent. fine very and clean.

why there be vij yeftes and no moo ne less capo. lxxxix
FOr two things a man is saved fro to flee the evil. and to do good. For to
hate and to flee the evil causes us the yefte of dread. The other vj yeftes
cause us to do good. The yefte of dread is the vssher at the great mass / that
is to say at the great menasse of the sentence of god / and of the pains of
hell / which is always ready and apparaylled against the synuars this is the
watch of the castle which never slepeth / This is the wedar of the gardyn that
wedeth and plucketh up al evil herbys / This is the tresourer that keeps the
heart and all the goods that been therein / These be the other vj yeftes that
make us to do all the good deeds. Now ought thou to know that like the
clerenes of the sonne^ which thou see with thyn eyes yeueth clerenes to the
world and virtue and enuygoure and strength all the things that grow and come
in to the world / Right so does the holy ghoost which enlumyneth in heaven and
in earth al them that been in grace / men. wymmen. and angellys. and al in like
wise as there beu in heaven three estates of aungellys as saint denis says of
whom one is most hye. that other moyen or myddle / and the third more low.
The most hye ben like them that been of the kings cou^ceyl. They be always
with god more nerre to him than the other and see him and here him and his
secrets. The moyen or myddle ben as barons and bayllyes that govern love and
kepen all the royam and gone and comen. and learn of them of the cou^ceyl that
which they comande^ and make it to be done to other. the lowest ben like as
servants and officers which have their crafts / and done their offices and
messages as is said to them. By this manner and ensaumple there ben iij estates
of the children of god in earth the which the holy ghoost ledeth and conduyteth
as says saint Poul. The one estate is of them hat ben in the world^ and lyuen
after the commandementes of god. and of holy church. and after that they here
and believe of their prelates. The other estate is of them that been parfyte.
that al have their heart out of the world and of this mortal life. and have their
conuersacyon in heaven and their body in earth. and their heart with god. The
third ben in the myddle estate which govern them self well and other. and
lyuen after the counceyl of the gospel. and not only after the commandments.
These three manner of people techeth the holy ghoost. and ledeth and governs by
these vj yeftes. and departs to them his graces. to eueryche after his
benygne volente and will as says thappostle. The two first of these vj yeftes
apperteyne to them that been of the first estate The yefte of science techeth
them. and the yefte of pity makes them to work. The ij myddle apperteyne to
them of the moyen estate. The yefte of counceyl governs them and the yefte
of strength accomplyssheth the works. The ij last apperteyne to them of the
most hye estate. The yefte of understanding enlumyneth them. and the yefte of
sapyence confermeth them and Joins them with god. Another reason there is
wherefore there ben vij yeftes. for the holy ghoost by his seven yeftes wedeth.
plucketh and takes away the vij sins and vices fro the hertes of the
persons. and planteth there and nouryssheth vij virtues contrary which make
perfytely a man to be honored. These ben the goods that the holy ghoost
makes in the hertes where as he descends by these seven yeftes. But tofore
that I descend unto the virtues. which ben contrary to the seven dedely
sins. I will shortly speak of seven other virtues. of which three ben called
dyuyne. and the other four been called the four cardynal virtues.

Of seven virtues of whom there been three dyuyne. and four cardynal capitulo
lxxxx
THe three first virtues dyuyne. Saint Poul thappostle calls them / Faith.
hope. and charity. And they be called dyuyne by cause they be godly and ordeyne
the heart to god. faith like as saint Austyn says sets us under god. and
makes us to know him. and knowleche him a lord of whom we hold all that
which we have of good. Hope says he enhaunceth us to god / and makes us
strong and hardy. and to entrepryse for the love of god that. which passes
the virtue and strength of man / Charity. says saint Austyn Joins us to god
/ For charity is none other thing but chyere unity. that is. dear onehede. for
she makes the heart and god all one as says saint Poul. Faith byholdeth in
god souerayn unity hope beholds in god souerayn hyenesse. and charity
souerayn bounte / These iij virtues ben divided by iij degrees of love / for
for iij things a man is loved. One is by cause that one has herd or hereth
great good of him. Or by cause that he has received great good of him. Or by
cause he entendeth to have great good of him. These iij manners of love ben in
these iij virtues. Love of faith hereth and werketh. love of hope feleth the
savor and requires it. love of charity takes and sees it. and tastes and
holds it.

Of the four cardynal virtues. by which a man ought to govern him capitulo
lxxxxj
OF the four cardynal virtues speken much the ancient phylosophres. but the
holy ghoost gives them and enseygneth them better an hundred times as says
Salamon in the book of sapyence. The first of these iiij virtues is prudence.
the second attemperaunce. the iij strength. and the fourth Justice / These
iiij virtues ben called cardynallys / by cause they ben the most pryncypal
emonge the virtues of which the ancient phylosophres speken. For by these
iiij virtues a man governs him self in this world. Like as the pope governs
al holy church by his cardynalles. Prudence keeps a man that he be not
deceived by none engyne of the enemy. Attemperaunce keeps a man that he be
not corrupt by none evil loue^ Strength keeps him that he be not vaynquysshed
ne overcome by wrath. or by dread. or by sorrow. This is that holds a man in.
good estate toward him self. Justice sets a man in right order and in right
estate anenst him self and and other. for Justice renders to each man that.
which is his These ben the iiij toures at iiij corners of the house of the good
man that makes it strong. sure / and good. Prudence garnyssheth it toward the
eest by pourueaunce for perils. Attemperaunce garnyssheth it toward the south
against the evil heetys. Strength garnyssheth it toward the north for the evil
coldes. Justice garnyssheth it toward the west against the evil raynes.

Yet ageyn of the four cardynal virtues as follows lxxxxij
THese iiij virtues have diverse offices. and been much diverse in their werkys.
like as says an au^cyent phylosophre named plato in his book that he made of
these four virtues. and deuydeth the^ much subtylly. and says that prudence
has iij offices. For by this virtue. all that which a man does says. and
thinks is ordained al and led by line / rule / and reason and in all his
werkys he pourueyeth. that he use them after thordynaunce of god that al sees
and Iugeth. A great lord should he be as me seems that should have this only
virtue. and by these three things should govern him.

Of the virtue of attemperaunce capitulo lxxxxiij
THe virtue of attemperaunce has iij offices / for the heart that has this
virtue will not ne coueyteth not to do a thing of which he ought to repent.
In no things he breketh not the law dysmesurably. but puts him self always
under the yoke of reason / And no thing doubts of all the couetyses of the
world / That is to say. who has this virtue he keeps him that he he not
corrupt by the three things that foulen and shamen the world.

Of the virtue of strength capitulo lxxxxiiij
THe virtue of strength has also iij offices. for a man that has this virtue
in his heart. he lift him self upon hye above the perils of this world^ and no
thing doubts he sauf vylonye and sin. he bears aduersyte and prosperyte /
and suffers without to bow on the right side ne on the lift side. Much
good should be the knight of god that in these three things should be well proved.
These iij virtues armen. ordeyne. and adourne a man as touching the three parts
of the heart which ben called. reason. love. and vygour / Prudence keeps the
reason that it be not deceived / Attemperaunce keeps the love. that it be not
corrupt / Strength keeps the vygour or might that it be not overcome /

Of the virtue of Justice capitulo lxxxxv
IVstyce makes a man to live ordynatly emonge the other. For like as plato
says the phylosophre / This is the virtue that makes that a man does unto
every man that which he owes to do. For he renders reverence and honor to
them that be above him. Frendshyp pees and concord to them that been like to
him. grace and pity to them that been under him By these iiij virtues says the
said phylosophre / that a man is then worthy that he be governor of him
self. and after of other. In these iiij virtues studied the auncyen
phylosophres which despyseden all the world for tacquyre and to get virtue and
wysedom / and therefore were they called phylosophres^ which is as much to say
as love of sapyence / O good god how should this confound us and make us aferd
that they that were paynyms and without law wryton and nothing knew of the
very grace of god ne of the yeftes of the holy ghoost. and nevertheless they
styed up in to the montayn of perfection of living by force and by their propre
virtue. and daygned not to take heed of the world ne to do evil. ne to consent
to sin / and we that been christian men that have the very faith. and know the
commandments of god / and have the grace of the holy ghoost if we will and our
sins cause it not. that we may more prouffite for our health anenst god in a
day. than they might in a year. we defoule our self. and lie here bynethe as a
swyne in mire / and in the ordure of this world. and sin in the fylthe and
donge of delyces of this world. Therefore says saint Poule that the paynym that
is without law shall Judge us at day of Judgment. that have had here the law
/ and we neither hold ne keep it. and by cause they had not ryzt faith ne the
grace of the holy ghoost ne no virtue ne quycke ne very faith. they may not well
know how these virtues be good and fair. for as much dyfference as is between
a brennyng cole. and a deed cole. and a living man and a deed man. So much
dyfference is there between virtue that is without charity. and virtue that is
with charity. which is the bou^te. the valor and the life of other virtues.
whereof saint austyn says when he speaks of these iiij virtues. he deuydeth
them by iiij manner of loves and by iiij things that very love does. and says
that the virtue of prudence is the love of hert^ which verily and wisely
refuses all that which may grieve and ennoye him. and cheseth all that which
may aydeto have that which he loves. that is god / The virtue of attemperau^ce
is the love of the heart. by which he gives him self entyerly and without
corruptyon to that which he loves / that is god. The virtue of strength is
the love of the herte^ by which a man serves only that which he loves /
that is god. and for him sets a man al other things under his foot. and
despyseth them. Then the virtue of Justice sets a man in his right estate /
that is above al things. and under god / without these iiij virtues / there is
none that may mount in to the montayn of perfectyon. for who that will mount
so hye. him byhoneth / that alther first he have prudence which makes a man
to despise the world / and that he have with hit the virtue of strength. which
gives to him great heart strong and stable courage to enpryse and to pursiewe
great things. and on that other party that he have the virtue of attemperaunce
/ by cause that he be not over charged ne evil carried. and that he have with
him the virtue of Justice that may led him by the right path. and by a good and
Just way / that he be without sin. and that he show to him how by holy
werkys he owes to conquer the royame of heaven. like as god did to Jacob / as
says the book of sapyence. who that thus may have these iiij virtues he shall
be well parfyte and blessed in this world. and more in that other. for he shall
be in pees of heart and in joy spyrytuel / and no thing shall faylle him. but
he shall habou^de in the grace of god that he shall have with him. in whom he
shall delight.

Here after follows how a man may take aweye and put from him the vij dedely
sins. and get the virtues lxxxxvj
NOw late us come ageyn to our matter. and pray we with all our heart to the holy
ghoost that he will inspyre and enseygne our hertes / that he be our advocate.
and teache us to show. how he by the vij yeftes of the holy ghoost he pluck
out and take aweye the seven dedely sins fro our hertes / and that he therein
will vouchesauf to plant the seven virtues.

Of the yefte of holy dread which makes a man Just lxxxxvij
THe yefte of dread is the first of the yeftes. for he casts out of the heart
all the sins like as we have said tofore. But proprely this yefte of dread
plucketh out. takes away and destroys the rote of pryde^ and planteth
there in his place the plant of humylyte. Now behold and understand well how
the synnar that holds him and slepeth in his sin. is like to a rybaulde
that slepeth and is dronke^ and has al lost at tavern. and is al naked and
so pour that he has no thing but he feleth no thing ne complayneth not. but
weneth that he be a much great lord. But when he has slepte and comes ageyn
to him self. and that he is out of his drunkenness / Then feleth he his
harm and knows his folly. Now complayneth he his loss and his damage. This
is the first good that the holy ghoost does to a synnar when he vysyteth him.
For he gives to him ageyn his wit and his mind. and brings him ageyn to
know him self. So that he aduertyseth and sees what goods he has lost. and
in what pouerte and in what peril he has be for his sin. like as did the
sone of the good man. which wasted and dyspended his heritage in dyssolucyon
and rybauldrye. In such confusyon and myserye he became that him byhoued to
keep the swyne and feed them. and to live of their releef and mete. like as our
Lord Ihesu christ shows us by exaumple in the gospel. Yet also the synnar as
says Salamon is like to him that slepeth in the myddle of the sea. and is in
great peril and tormente. and he feleth no thing ne has no fere thereof.
But when the holy ghoost awaketh him. he felyth and sees his peril. and
begins to have dread of him self. Yet also the synnar is like to him that is
in prison feteryd in yrons. and is in boltes and has many kepars. like as
Saint Peter was in the prysone of King Herod. And the caytyf synnar thinks
no thing on the prouoste. ne on the Justice. ne on the galowes that tarry for
him / but he slepeth and dremeth that he goes to a weddyng and to a feste /
But the grace of the holy ghoost is like to the aungel that awoke saint Peter.
and delyuerd him fro the hand of king Herode^ For the grace of the holy ghoost
awaketh the synnar and delyuerth him from the hand and fro the puyssaunce of
the devil of hell / yet also the synnar is like to him that weneth to be
strong and hole. and he has the death under his teeth. For he has the
humors evil and corrupt within the body / then dies he within a month.
that wend to have lived xl year. Like as says Elyuans in the verses which
speken of the death and sayen thus. Go ye away ye whystelars and gapars. for
such be couerd under their clothes. that wene to be hole and fat that shall
not live unto march. But the holy ghoost is like unto a good physycyen that
shows to him his maladye and sickness. and moeueth fro him his humors. and
gives unto him a bitter drink which heleth him and renders to him his life.
Right so troubles our lord the synnar by bitter contrycyo^ wha^ he helyth him
fro his sins by the bitter drink like as says the prophet in his psaulter
/ and fereth him. and brings him ageyn to know him self / like as did Adam
our first fader. when he hid him emonge the trees of paradys terrestre. And
then said god to him. Adam where art thou / Three other demau^des made god by
his angel to the cha^bryer of holy Abraham which was named agar when she
fled fro her lady. The aungel said Agar fro whens come thou. whyther go
thou / what do thou / These iij demaundes makes the holy ghoost to the
synnar. when he awaketh him of his sins / where as he was aslepe / and he
reyseth him / and opens to him the eyes of his heart / and gives to him ageyn
his wit and his mind. where art thou says he. that is to say. behold
caytyf in what sorrow and in what peril thou art in this world. For thou art
like to him that peryssheth in the sea slepyng in a ship. ne feleth ne
understands ne apperceyueth his perylle^ That is to say caytyf behold ageyn
thy life fro now bacward. For thou come fro the tavern of the devil. where as
thou have wasted thy life. and lost thy time. and all the goods that god has
given to the. what doste thou. That is to say. consider how thou art faint and
frayl weary and slow toward thy body and toward thy soul. Thou wenest to be
hole and strong. but peradventure thou have the humors corrupt in thy body
which shall led the to thy death And in the soul thou have evil manners. that
shall led the to the death of hell if the grace of god keep the not. After
whyther ghost thou. that is to say caytyf think behold and understand that
thou go to thy death / wherein thou shall fall in the hondes of herod / that
is the devil of hell and of his meyne / Thou ghost to the Judgment where thou
shall see the Iustyse of god so cruel. so strayte and so puyssaunte. Thou go
in to hell where thou shall find fire and stynkyng sulphre and moo than a
thousand torments that never shall fynysshe to tormente the. Thus does the
holy ghoost to the synnar to opene his eyes. and to behold above him and under
him. and tofore him and behind him. These been four strokes of death which
fereth the synnar and makes him to tremble and to have dread. And these four
beholdynges and consyderacyons proprely been the four stremes of the rote of
the virtue of humylyte that the yefte of dread planteth in the heart of the
synnar when god vysyteth him.

Here follows of the four roots of the sin of Pride capitulo lxxxxviij
THe iiij thoughts and consyderacyons toforesayd pulle out. take away from
the rote out of the gardyn of the heart the iiij roots of pride. that is the
proud man weneth to know much thing. or to be of the valoyr of much
thing. or that he may do much thing. or to have much thyng^ These ben the
iiij horns. that is to say the iiij cowardyses that shamed the contre which
god showed to zacharye the prophet / but the iiij things that he showed him
proprely after that they came for to beat down these iiij horns. been the iiij
thoughts and consyderacyons tofore said. For when a man thinks fro whens he
comes / and understands and knows the pouerte / the vylete / and the
fraylte of his birth / how he was conceived in sin / of so foul matter made
and formed. In so pour a house her berowd. in so great pouerte borne. In what
pains nourisshed in what labor he has lived / and how he has lost his time.
he sees and considers the great nombre of his sins. and knows clearly
the good deeds which he has left / and not done by his slouthe and
neclige^ce. Then the grace of the holy ghoost makes him to feel. to Judge and
to know in his heart. that he is of no value ne no thing worth. after when he
thinks where he is. and sees this world which is nothing but an exyle. and a
desert full of beerys and lyepardes. a forest full of theuys and engynes a see
full of tempest and perils. a fourneys brennyng and enbraced with fire and of
all sins. a field of bataylle and of anguysshe. where always byhoueth to
live in war and fight ayenste the deuylles which been so subtyl and so
sage. Then the grace of God makes him for to feel aryght and perceive that
he felt no thing for to govern him well touching his salvation. Yet ageyn
when the synnar thinks consydereth and knows his sins and his deffaultes
that he is full of sins. and wide of all good deeds and works. Then the
holy ghooost makes him to feel and to know his pouerte. and that he has no
spyrytuell good in him / After when the synnar sees tofore him which way he
goes / and he sees the death. to whom no man may gaynsaye On that other
part the synnar sees the Justice and the vengeance of god so Just and so
ryghtful. which is so much to be doubted. by whose hands he must pass. he
sees and knows the pains horrible of hell. from whom the synnar may not
escape. Then god gives him to know that the power of a man and of a woman
is naught / and that they may do no thing without the specyal grace of god.
Then the synnar begins to have the spyryte and yefte of dread. In these
thoughts and consyderacyons ben the branches of the rote of the tree of
humylyte. This tree is planted beside the fontayne of the dread of god. of
which it is always arowsed and watered as well in winter as in somer. Now
ought thou to know that these vij virtues / of which I purpose to speak of
have each of them seven degrees. by which it prouffyteth. aryseth. and grows
in the heart of a creature. and his good werkys by which it shows outward /
For virtue grows on hye. like as does the palmer / the cypres or the cedre.
and after spredeth and casts his branches on al sides.

Of the virtue of humylyte capitulo lxxxxix
OF the virtue of humylyte speaks saint Ancelme. and says that it has vij
degrees / by which it mounteth on hye before that it come to perfectyon. Now
understand well how the first degree of humylyte knows his pouerte. his
sins. and his defaultes. For like as says saint bernard humylyte is the
virtue that makes a man to mespryse and despise him self / and hold him for
vile when he knows him self verayly This knowleche grows of the iiij roots
tofore said. But there ben sum that know well their deffaultes and their
sins / and their pouertees. but they feel them not. Therefore the second
degree of humylyte / is to feel and to compain his sins. his defaultes /
his sorrow. and his maladye he renneth gladly to the leche. that feleth him
self hurt of a wound. and in peril of death. and he renneth much sone to the
physycyen that is seek. and that has evil humors in his body for to have
health and guaryson. and is much glad and Joyous when he may purge them and
cleanse them. and therefore the third degree of humylyte is for to confess
deuoutelye and often his trespaces. and to bewail his sins gladly in great
contrycyon and repentance and to purge his heart fro al sins. But there ben
sum that know well their defaultes and feel them and ben well sorouful for
them but they will not for any thing. that no man should know them. Therefore
is the fourth degree of humylyte holden for vile and despytous. but there ben
yet sum that well know feel and tell their deffaultes. and say well and Judge.
I am wicked and a synnar and such and such. But if another said so to them.
Certeynly that is truth that thou say / they should be dysplesyd and wexe
strongly angry. Therefore is the fyfthe degree of humylyte. to here gladly
truth spoken of him self / and that one say to him his deffaultes / And this
is that saint bernard says that the very humble would be holden for vile. and
would not be praised that he is humble. Therefore is the vj degree of humylyte
when a man suffers in pacyence that he be foul treated and as a person
despised / like as did the good King Dauyd. which suffered swetelye a servant
named Semey which threw at him stones. and said to him great vylonyes. and all that he knew of evil and harm. Yet there is a degree in which is there sum
of this perfectyon and of this virtue of humylyte / That is will certeynly and
desire of heart with out fayntyse to be reputed for vile and byholden simple and
fowly to be treated. That is a right pouerte of spyryte and humylyte of heart /
Much loved this pouerte in this world the rich king of heaven Ihesu Christ.
Much loved he it when he bought it so dere^ which would and vouched sauf to be
borne in a stable horrible and abhomynable with the oxen and asses / and would
have xxxij year in pouerte. The sweet Ihesu Christ loved much humylyte. when he
him self that never did sin he that never had deffaulte faught and came
emonge the theuys. That was between the sons of adam our formest fader. And
the sweet Ihesu Christ clad him with the clothes of a sinner and malefactour^
by cause he was fowly treatyd Then he said the night of his cene or souper to
his apostles with great desire I have desired this pasque. That is to say this
death. this shame and this departing. More hye may not this trees mount in
humylyte. And who shall be raised unto this degree of humylyte. without doubt
he shall be well blessed in this world and in that other^ For he that says this
is god. may not lie. For he is the perfayte and souerayn veryte which says
with his blessed mouth in the gospel. blessed ben they that be pour of
spyrite. and how that is he techeth and shows to us when he says. learn of
me and not of other to be meke and humble of heart / as I am. and ye shall find
rest to your souls. This rest and this blessydnes none know it but they
that learn it. Then if thou wylt know what it is. do pain with all thy
heart so much to vaynquysshe thy self. that thou be mounted in to the seventh
degree of humylyte Then may thou gadre of the fruit and ete of the tree of
life. like as it is said in thapocalyps /

Of the rote of the virtue of humylyte capitulo C
OF the rote of humylyte grow vij branches. For this virtue shows him in
seven manners. First in honoring god / in praysyng other. In adouryng and
prayeng god. In loving pouerte. In gladly seruyng. In fleyng praysyng. and him
self trustyng al in god. The very meke and humble honors God in three manners
/ For he byleueth him symply. he prayseth him truly and he prays him
deuoutelye. he honors him first in that. that he byleueth him symply and
steadfastly of all that / which is said in holy scripture. like as a little
child byleueth his master / And for this reason has our faith merit. Then
who byleueth well. it does him great honor. like as he does great honor to a
man when he byleueth him upon his simple word / And this is the beginning of
well doing. which is necessary to al them that will save them self. as says
saint Poul. That is to believe god on his simple word. that al is toewe what
someuer is said of him only. without to seek other reason or to require other
proof. Therefore ben the heretykes and proud men dampened / For they would not
believe god without good wedde. That is to understand. if that they see not
quycke reason in all that which god says / but to the quycke reason they
holden them. like as the usurer holds him on his pledge or wedde that will
trust no person by his simple word. And hereof ben comen all the evil heresies
and vnbyleue / For the proud Aungellys that would compare their wit to the
sapyence of Ihesu christ. daygned not to believe that god said. but if he showed
to them quycke reasons or good open miracles. But we that keep the very faith
believe an hundred fold better. this that he says that may not lye^ that is
god / than we do the miracles ne rayson. ne that which we see. God says that
every person shall be Iuged after his werkys. god says that of every idle
word. us byhoueth to give acomptes at the day of Judgment. But the meke and the
humble that this hereth and byleueth and dredeth and doubts and does pain
to keep his heart. and so his mouth. and al his werkys / shall not be Iuged.
After the very humble prayseth god truly for all the goods that he has done
to him and that he does to him daily* and that he yet shall do. after like as
we have showed before in the trayte of pride. The humble person is like a pour
man. which of a little alms has great Joy. and thanketh with al his heart
his benefactour. Then when the humble sees nothing in him. by which he is
worthy to have good or bread or other thing of which he uses / he knows
sees. understands / byleueth. and doubts not of all that god sends /
yeueth and leneth him. and by cause that the very humble draws nothing to him
self of the goods of his lord. which passen by his hand. therefore is he a
true servant as saint bernard says. After the very humble adoureth god and
prays him deuoutely / that is to say with very teerys which comen of the
grace of god and of right felyng of the heart. For him seems that he is like a
child that is al naked tofore his maistre and that can not his lesson / or
that he is like to the pour man endetted. which is fallen in the hands of his
credytour / and has not whereof he may fine ne pay his debte. Or that he be
like a thief proved that is taken with an hundred trespaces. and that has the
cord about his neck. or that he be like the lame man that lies at church
door / which has no shame to show his maladye and his soores to them that
pass by. for cause that each body should have pity on him / If thou will
then learn to pray god. pray and adoure him aryght / these iiij things
aforsayd shall enseygne and teache the that is to wete / the chylde^ the man
endetted / the thief. and the lame man.

Of him that is very humble and meke capitulo Cj
THe custom is of a very meke and humble man to praise another and to give him
loos. to put him before. allow him with his mouth / and by werkys to bear him
honor. he is like the little be that makes the honey / which escheweth
stynkes. and secheth flowers of the field and souketh the dew and the
substance of them. and makes honey for to garnysshe with his house / Thus does
the very humble. which takes none head of the stenches the sins and the
deffaultes of other. But all the goods that other do. he heholdeth them
loves and prayseth. and souketh the swetenes of devotion of his heart with
which his conscience is replenysshed. The very humble sees none so evil a
thing. ne so hard. ne so synful. but that he can draw matere to allow and
praise god / In his heart he preyseth other in iij manners. For he byleueth more
the wit of another man^ than the wit of him self. he will that the will
of other men be do sonner than his own. All the contrary does the proud man
like as we have showed tofore. After also the very meke and humble man
allows and prayseth other men by word. The good deeds that other have done
he enhaunceth and prayseth them. and the evil deeds he excuses and makes them
less. The very meke man torneth the mean thing in to good. and understands
them always to the best / and this is against the evil tatches of the myssayers
/ which enhaunce the evil deeds and mynysshe the good. and the moyen preuerten
and torn to the werste. The very meke and humble prayseth by work. and
honors in deed eueryche as he ought to do and as he may do without mysdoyng
/ Thus does not the proud man. but all the contrary. like as we have said
tofore in the trayty of the sin of pride.

Of him that is humble of heart capitulo Cij
THe custom is of him that has an humble heart. that al his good deeds he
has behind him at his back. and al his evil. his sins and al his
deffaultes he has always in mind tofore his eyes. and the good deeds of other
he has all way tofore his eyes. and the evil deffaultes and sins of all
other he sets them behind him at his back as in oublyance or forgetyng.
And hereof happeth oftymes that the very meke and humble man the more he
prayseth other and honors. so much more he dyspreyseth him self. The very
humble and meke person of heart is like the auarycyous and covetous man that
has always his eyes on the goods that other have. and that they do And always
him seems that he has no spyrytuel good in him. For like as there is an evil
proud man / So is thece very meke and humble / He that is very humble of
heart is like as a lytyl child which is sone of a king and heir of the
royalme. which wepeth and cries. and knows no thing of his hyenesse ne of
his richesse. He is also like unto the simple sheep. in whom al is good and
prouffytable. the wulle the fell / the flessh. the milk. and his dunge. and
the sheep no thing knows of hit. ne thinks on it. and in this manner says
the great patryarke holy Abraham of him self. that he was no thing but ashes
and pouldre. And holy Job which was so great and rich in the world said in
like wise. And Saint andrew that said also of him self / what am I but ashes.
duste. fylthe. rotynnesse / a worm / wind. shadow leaves that the wind
bears away. and dry stupple which is nouzt but for the fire / And like as
the very humble person of heart prayseth and honors other with his heart and
mouth and also in deed as we have said. Right so despyseth he him self in
these iij manners. It seems to him like as saint Iherome says of him self.
when that Iete or drink. or that I wake or sleep. always me thinks that the
fereful trompe of the day of Judgment blows in mine eerys saying. come to thy
Judgment. come to thy Judgment. and by cause that he will not be Iuged of his
sins. he seeseth not but every day purges him self keeps and cleanses him
from all sins and Iugeth. condempneth / and repreueth al his werkys and his
wordes^ he cries and nombreth. poyseth counterpoyseth and repreneth^ for he
fyndeth more chafe than grayn. that is to understand more of sins than of
good deeds. And by cause that he will not be Iuged at the death of Justice. will
he not leave but that little and great be examyned and said / and also Iuged in
the court of mercy / that is in holy confessyon^ In that court who counts
well aryght / is al quyte of his sins. But in the court of Justice which
shall be at the day of Judgment / whom someuer he owes he must pay. Ne never
shall he mow be aquyted. and therefore he shall be perdurably dampened / For he
must render or pendre. that is hang / Alas caytyf what shall he pay that has
no thing. but the body which is charged and al full of dedely sins. who that
well understood and felt these things / he should hold and keep him fro al
sins. and should wythdrawe him fro mockeryes and lesynges. which they
contryue against the very meke and humble persons which dread god and love
him. by cause they fere and dread him. they will keep them clean without ordure
of sin and confess them gladly and often. but little auaylleth confession
without repentance. and without penance. and without good Judgment / and
that Justice be not done truly. and therefore al in like wise as the very meke
and humble person makes of him self very Judgment in bitter coutrycyon of
heart and in very confession of mouth. and in satysfaccyon and penance of
very Iustyce^ he Iuged him self as a thief and puts him verayly on the
gybet of penance without fayntyse. and without ypocrysye.

How a man ought to hate pride capitulo Ciij
WHo that hates pride. he loves pouerte / and sets his heart allow and in
humylyte. and therefore al they that been very humble louen pouerte. and ben
pour of spyryte. The very humble person loves pouerte for three reasons.
that is to wete. for the perils that been in gouernyng of rychesses. for the
goods that been in good and very pouerte. and for by cause that god loves so
much pouerte. as wha^ he was here in this world he loved it and yet loves.
and al them that love it. like as holy scripture witnesses it. whereof Ihesu
christ says by dauyd in his psaulter / that god hereth the prayers and desires
of pour me^. and pourueyeth to them mete swetely in good savor For he is their
refuge and their savior. Job says that god is the fader of the pour / and
has given to them power to Judge the other. And our lord at the beginning of
his fair sermon says that blessed be the pour. and then be accursyd the
rich that have here their heaven / But the very heaven celestyal he has given
to the pour. so that they may give it and selle it and the world will not
believe that god say trouthe^ ne that pouerte be blessed. But god says thus in
the gospel. fair fader I pray the and thank the / that thou have hyd these
things fro the wise. and have manyfested and showed it to the humble and meke.
The humble and pour of spyryte seen god / here him well and believe him well. and
louen better an hundred fold their pouerte / than the covetous man loves his
rychessys. In iij things shows a man that he loves pouerte. when he loves
and holds gladly the company of the pour. and loves them and holds them
company / like as Ihesu Christ did as long as he was in this world. for
naturelly the lambs flee fro the wulues and wythdrawe fro them. and the
children wythdrawe them and flee the company of great people. and the humble
and meke people withdraw them gladly fro the proud people / The life of a pour
person is little and pour. for he requires not ne demands precious metes
ne oultrageous vesture ne clothyng / ne he secheth no bobaunce, ne no pride.
in roobes ne in rydyng. ne in householde. ne in meyne ne in feast ne in
companye^ And it suffyseth to the very pour that he have only his
sustenaunce. The very pour person suffers in pacyence hungre and thryste /
cold and hete. lothynges and vylonnyes. and many bitter trybulacyons for the
love of Ihesu christ and of his passion. And al these the evil pour man does
and suffers against his will. The very humble and the very pour suffers
gladly al euyls and al aduersytees for the love of god Yet ageyn it is the
custom of a pour man. that if he have no thing. and may get ne win no
thing. he is not ashamed to ask and demand. and the very humble beggeth al
day and requires the prayers and the orysons of good people and of the friends
of god. and the very humble trusts more in their aid. than he does in his
own good deeds.

Of diverse estates of pride capitulo Ciiij
Pride loves the hye place above. Humylyte loves the low place bynethe. This
is the dyamont of the noble nature that dayneth not to sit in gold. but in
pour metal as in iron. in like wise is the sheet of whete beten. The grain is
under. and the chaf is above / But our lord shall selle his whete at the day of
dome al wynewed like as says the gospel / and he shall cast the chafe in to
the fire of hell. and the grayn in to the garner of heaven. how much more the
gold is fine and pure^ so much more is it heavy. and the more it wayeth the
sooner it goes down to the bottom. and the more that a man is meke and humble.
the more loves he the low place / like as did Ihesu christ and his sweet
mother. which gave to us ensaumple to serve and to obey / Not only to the
grettest but to the least. And how much more the seruyse is vile and
despysable so much gladly does it the humble and meke. Therefore our lord Ihesu
Christ taught his appostles to wesshe the feet by humylyte. Then humylyte is
proprely mother of obedyence and nouryssheth it. enseygneth and keeps it that
it be not corrupt by vayn glory by heaviness nor by murmr. ne by propre wit.
ne by propre will. ne by aduersyte. ne by any other manner / and it is to wete
that there be vij adournements of obedyence. The first that one obey anon
prestly. gladly. symply purely. generally. vyly. and vygorously / The humble is
pour tofore his eyes and naked. and has not to do for him self. and therefore
he is always ready. as the maro^ners in the sea in their ships that anon as
they here the voys of the governor / they obey to him and run as they were
enraged / The humble obeys gladly. that the pains. the perils. and the
death he receives to his power with great joy for the love that he has to
obedyence. Therefore said dauyd the prophet in the psaulter. that he loved
better the commandments that god made / than he did gold ne silver. ne
precious stones. The humble obey al symply. as does the hors^ or the sheep.
whom the shepeherde ledeth where as he will. and that never says. wherefore goo
I more here than there. For one of the most honest daughters that humylyte
has is holy symplesse. The humble is right true to god. like as is a right
good wife to her husbond. which will to no man obey folyly. but to her husbond
only And therefore none obeys so Justly ne in so good ente^cyon as does the
very humble. which hates not. but for to playse the world. and desires no
thing but to plese god. After the very humble is right vygorous. right swyfte
and open / when he bears the virtue of obedyence and the love of god and does
it to his prelate. But when his own will bears him and ledeth. Then he is
heavy and slow to do wel^ like unto the sterre named saturnus. which renneth
as much in one day with the fyrmament. when the fyrmament ledeth her. as she
does in xxx year in her propre ^ours. Also the very meke and humble obeys
generally oueral and in all places. where he byleueth that it playseth god. and
in all things like as does the ass of the mylle / that as gladly bears
barley as whete^ and led as gold. and whete to a pour man as to a rich man.
Also the very meke and humble is made strong / For he changes his strength
with the strength of god. like as says the prophet ysaye. And therefore there
is no thing but the very humble may well bear. For god bears him and his
deeds. Then he obeys vygorously and perseuerantly. For he is never weary
no more than the son is. which god ledeth and conduyteth. and the longer it
lives the more grows her force and her vygour / Now may thou see clearly
how humylyte techeth the well and parfytely to serve and obey god /

Of the techyng and doctrine of our lord capitulo Cv
IHesu christ the great maystre of humylyte. when he had preched and fed his
people. and heled the seck men and lame / Then he fled away fro the people
in to the montaygne / for to be in orison for to enseygne and give us an
ensaumple to flee the praysyng of the world and therefore the true humble heart
like as he payneth to do well when he obeys. Right so he payneth him to fle
the praysyng of the world. and to hyde him for to keep him from the wind of
vaynglorye. And to fyxe him in the shadow of the roche. like as ysaye the
prophet says fro the tempest of evil tongues / This roche is Ihesu Christ him
self. which is the refuge and the charity to the humble and meke. To this
roche. that is Ihesu crist flees the humble heart charged with thorns like as
is the yrchon. that is of sharpnes of penance This is the dounehous in to
which fleen for refuge. the dounes of our lord. That been the meke. humble. and
simple hertes that flee thither to refuge for the fowls of proye or rauayn That been the deuyls which always seche to da^pne the souls when an humble heart
has done so much that he is entryd in to this roche as the down in to a
dounehous. that is when he remembers well the life of Ihesu Christ / and his
blessed passyon^ then he forgeteth al his sorrows / and prayseth little all that the world has and is worth / and may be of valu. A good heart that has
assayed this. desires no thing so much as to be forgoten to the world. The
world is to him a charge. and besynes^ for as says the wise man. The good man
is never more sure. than when he is al allone. ne more in werkys than when he
is idle. For he is then with ij of his best frendys. that is with god and
with him self. There a devout heart treats of his great quarellys and
complayntes by which al other works semen to him truffes and naught. and al
vanytees. There he acompteth with god / and god with him by holy thoughts and
by fervent desires. Then he seleth the great swetnes of consolacio^s and
comfort that god gives to them that dread him. and love him. like as Dauyd
the prophet says in the psaulter / Then al langages and al words ennoye
and grieve him. if they be not of god. to god. or for god. Thus begins the
soul to love solytude and scylence And then comes to him in his heart an
holy shamefastnes which is one of the fair daughters of humylite. for all in
like wise as a damoysel that loves paramours with great shamefastnes when she
is apperceyued and she hereth that it is spoken of. In like wise the humble
person and devout when he hereth that one speaks of him. and of his
spyrytuel goods that god has done to him. and no thing less does he. than
the maid does which is ardantly surprysed of love. for what someuer the world
say to him / it is known. Nevertheless he secheth his corners and hydles like
as he that requires none other thing. but to be rauysshed in god like as was
Saint Poule.

Of the pryuyte that god has to an holy soul ca Cvj
OF this acquaintance and of this preuyte^ this holy soul begins to have
of god / between her and an holy pride. For when the holy soul is rauysshed
unto heaven / she beholds the earth fro far / like as says ysaye the
prophet. and there sees it so little to the regard of the gretenes of heaven
/ so foul to the regard of that great beauty. so troublus to the regard of
that great clerenesse. so wide to the regard of that great plente / Then he
despreyseth and despyseth certeynly all the rychessys of the world. beautees.
honors. and noblesses. Then it seems to him that it is but a play of
children that play in the way* and much trauayllen them self and win
nothing. It seems that al is but wind and dremes as says salamon. Then he
begins to deye to the world. and live to god as says saint Poul. Then is
the soul so pour of spyryte that it has naught. For god has his spyryte
taken fro him and rauysshed it / and replenysshed with his yeftes. as he did to
thappostles on whytsonday / Then the holy ghoost gives to him so great an
heart / that the prosperyte ne aduersyte of the world he prayseth no thing at
al. and with this he gives to him so holy and so ferme a conscye^ce. that he
awayteth hardyly the death. and he has in god so great faith. and hope and
love. that there is no thing but he dar enterprise it for the love of god.
For he has that faith of which god speaks in the gospel / which is lykened
to mustard seed. by which he may comande to roches and montaygnes / and they
shall obey to him.

Of the comparyso^s of mustard seed to the love of god Cvij
THe seed of mustard is much little. but it is much strong and sharp / And
it is hot in the fourth degree as the physycyens sayen. By the hete is
vnderstonden love The first degree of love as says saint Bernard / is when a
man feleth no thing of love but of him self. and of his owen prouffyte. The
second is when he begins to love god. The iij is when he knows best god /
and loves him proprely for his bounte. The fourth is when he is so esprysed
with this holy love. that he ne loves him self ne none other thing but god /
or for god. or with god. And unto this love brings him very humylyte. Now
may thou see clearly that the pour of spyryte ben blessed. For they be so
humbled and void of their spyryte. that their spyryte is all mynuysshed / for
god has it al. and the holy ghoost has replenysshed the house of his heart. and
is there lord. and enhaunceth them that been pour of spyryte. These been the
very meke and humble. whom he makes to regne in heaven by holy hope and by
holy conscience. and therefore says our lord in the gospel / that the royame of
heaven is theyres. Not only by promise / but by fyn certeynte. like as they
that began sometime to receive the fruytes and the rentes how they should be
blessed in that other world. That may no man know unto the time that he be
there. For the heart of a mortal man may not think it. ne express with mouth
/ ne here it with his cerys.

Of the yefte of holy dread and of pity capitulo Cviij
THe first yefte of the holy ghoost makes the heart humble dredeful and to
doubt god and hate al sins. and therefore it is named the yefte of dread. The
second yefte of pity makes the heart sweet debonayr and pyteous. And therefore
is it named the yefte of pity. And that is proprely a dew and a tryacle against
the venym of felonnye. and in especyal ayenste the venym of the sin of envy.
of which we have spoken tofore. For this yefte of pity takes away and
plucketh out of the heart the rote of envy. and there heleth it parfyghtely.
Then the heart that receives this yefte / and feleth in him a dew. which
makes him to germyne a sweet rote and ryzt well atempred. that is good love.
out of which grows a fair tree beryng great fruit. that is a fair virtue and
good that is called in latin mansuetudo. That is to say sweetness and
debonayrte of heart. which makes a man sweet. debonayr. charytable and
amyable. For this virtue makes a man to love his neighbor parfytely. and him
self after god / This tree has vij degrees by which he mounteth on heyght /
These vij degrees shows to us saint Poul^ there where as he admonesteth and
prays that we do pain to that / that we be al one in god / The first reason
is that we have al one heart the hye and the low. the pour and the rich.
That is that we have al one fader in heaven. That is god which made us al
comunely to his image and to his semblaunce / and by cause that we al have one
creator and maker. which maad us al of one matere and of one form. and to
one end. that is that we be al in him and with him. like as he says in the
gospel. It is much great reason that we love each other / for the bestys and
the birds each loves his semblable^ The second reason is that we be al
christian and baptized in the sacrament of bap^esme pour and rich. That is that
we be al wasshen with the precious blood of Ihesu Christ. And we were redeemed
with one manner money. and as much cost that one as the other. Much then
owe we to love each other and to honor. For god has much loved us and
praised us. and has made us of great dygnyte / The third reason is by cause we
have al one faith and been bounden all to one law which all is
accomplysshed. like as Saint Poul says in this word / love thy neighbor as
thy self. Of this debte is no man quyte for any thing that he can do. this
