debte owes each man to other / and who that most renders most owes. The
fourth reason is that we have al one maystre and one lord that is god of whom
we hold al. body and soul. and all that we have. he has made us al and
formed. and has us al redeemed of a like prys. he shall Judge us al^ and reward
largely to al them that shall have kept and holden his commandementes. and that
have loved each other truly. The fyfthe reason is by cause that we be al
fellows in the host of our lord / And we ben al his knights and souldyers.
which we al abide one reward. that is the glory perdurable. and love and
company of all saints. The vj reason is that we live all of one espyryte
spyrytuelly. like as we live all of one air corporally. By this spyryte we
ben all sons of god by adopcyon. That is by aduoerye. and sons of holy
church. brethern germayn of fader and mother. a spyrytuel fraternity. which is
better worth than a carnal fraternity. like as the spyryte is of more value
than the body. The seventh reason is by cause that we been al members of one
body / of which Ihesu christ is the heed. and we been the members which lyuen
al of one mete. That is of the precious flesh and blood of Ihesu Christ.
which so much loves us / and us holds so dear / that he gives to us his
precious blood to drink. and his precious flesh to ete. Therefore remembers
us so often saint Poule this love which he shows to us. For a more quycke
reason ne more fayrer example may he not show to us of very amytye and
frendshyp. if thou will think well on these reasons. thou shalt find vij
degrees of amytye and frendshyp which comen of the yefte of pity.

Of vij manners of spyrytuel love capitulo Cix
OF this stock and out of this rote grown vij branches / For this virtue
shows him in seven manners. like as love is known. which is emonge the
members of a body in vij manners / First the one of the members keeps and
countregardeth the other. that it do to him none evil. ne that at faylle him
not / ne that it do him none harm ne do^mage to his power. and herin we
understand our Innocencye / which we ought to keep each anenst other / For
this commandment is wryton in the heart of every person. That is that thou do
to another after god that. which thou would that he did to the. and that
thou sholdest not do to another. otherwise than thou would should not be done
to the. Ne that thy right hand should smite thy lift hand / Also that one
membre suffer swetelye that other that it do to hit no harm. ne no vengeance
ne wrath. But if that one membre have harm or hurt. that other members feel
it / And in this understand we parsyght debonayrte which has iij degrees /
The first is that he revenge him not / The second that he reteyne not wrath ne
ire. The third that he ne feel no moeuyng of hate ne ire toward his neighbor
for any thing that he does / Also the members obeyen al to their souerayn. For
they do al to their power that. which the heart comandeth them. and the cyen
enseynen them / In this understand we the virtue of obedyence of which we have
spoken tofore. which ought to be apparaylled in love and in charity like as
says Saint Peter. Also the one membre helps that other. and serves that
other without danger. without contradyctyon and without auaryce. And herin we
understand the virtue that is called charity. of which a man then helps
and socoureth another gladly with the power that god has given him. or he
enseygneth or counceylleth with the wit that he hath^ Or he gives and
departs largely for gods sake the goods that he has. Than is said of him
that he is much charytable. and thus commands to us saint peter. that the
graces that god has given to vs^ that we admynystre them to our neighbors /
whereof Tullyus the phylosophre says. we ought to feel all that which is in
the world and grows / al is made for to serve man. And the men be made that
one to aid and help that other. For the one is engendered of the other. Let
us then do that for which we be borne. and that which nature enseygneth us
/ and seche we all the common prouffyte. for thus as says Saint Poule. we been
all members of one sole body. All the members felen and draw to them that
which is done to eueryche / be it good. be it evil. be it Joy. be it
anguysshe / when one smyteth the foot. the mouth says ye gryeue and hurt me /
By this we understand the virtue of very pity. which we ought to have
commynly. which has two offices as says Saint Poule. That is to wete to Joy
for the good that other do and have / And to sorrow for the euylles that other
feel and make / Also if a membre be seek or hurt / all the other helpen it to
the end that it may be guarysshed and hool / In this understand we the virtue of
Justice and of correctyon / without the which the body of holy church may
not endure / For the roten members defoulen the other that been hole. who that
will then chastyse his brother and his neighbor. and repreue and punysshe his
subgette. late him take heed at him self / when that a membre is seek or hurt.
the heart has great compassyon^ and feleth great sorrow / And that is for the
great love that he has to it. he set hand to. much swetely and often. And
like as says Seneke. like as all the members of the body ayden and bear up
each other / Right so ought every man for to supporte his neyghboue. and to
correct and pluck away the wounds of sins that been in his heart. First
there ought for to be laid thereto the oynementes and thenplaystres of sweet
admonycyons.

Also if this be nouzt worth there must be laid thereto the sharp pouldres
and poynaunt of hard reprehencyon / And if that help not / then let come
the sword to dysseuere. or for to excommynye him / or to bannysshe him out of
the contreye or to wythdrawe fro him.

Also the members honor and keep that one that other. and do worship like as
says saint poule. we owe to bear and do reverence one to another. and
specially they that have great need to be supported^ These been the most
folysshe and most feeble. Them ought men most to supporte. Then the wise men
and sage beren and supporten always the fools and the feeble. like as the bones
beren the feeble flesh. and as the pyler bears the house / This is against the
myssayers. that so gladly cryen and sayen the deffaultes and the sins that
they see in other. Also that one membre deffendeth that other at need and put
him tofore to save that other. for at need is seen who is a frende^ when that
one foot slydeth. that other helps it anon. wha^ that one would smite the
heed. the hand put him tofore. In that understand we parfyght and pure amytye
whereof god says in the gospel / who may do gretter amytye or frendshyp. than
to set his life for his friend / This frendshyp shows us Ihesu Christ the
very friend. which for us set his soul and his body to death shameful^ And
that did be to give to us example. like as says Saint Peter. and also Saint
James. that god has set his soul for us / And right so we ought to set
our souls for our brethern and for our neighbors. if we be aryght the members
of the body of Ihesu Christ. which is our heed / who that has this virtue a
right / I shall say appertly that he is well blessyd^ This is the virtue that our
good maystre Ihesu Christ enseygneth us. when he says in the gospel^ blessed
be the debonayr. For they shall possess the land of them that lyuen in glory
without end / Now understand well this blessyng that the debonayr has in
this world. For the parfyght debonayr been now in possessyon of therthe. That
is to understand in iij manners. First of the earth of living people. That is
god him self. which is the heritage of them that live perdurably that is of
the saints and of good people. in like wise as the earth is habytacyon of
beestys and of men. And by cause that god him self is the earth of living men.
he has the debonayrs in his possessyon. For they do no thing but that which
pleseth god. Therefore it is right that they have god in their possessyon / Like
as Dauyd the prophet says in his psaulter. The debonayrres says he shall have
the earth in possessyon and in heritage. and also they shall have delectacions
in multitude of pees. And Saint Anstyn says that no man shall have god in his
possessyon. but that first he shall be in his. Also the debonayr have in this
world the land of their heart in possessyon / For they be by right lords of
their heart. The felon is not lord of his heart. and the debonayr has the
maystrye of his heart and of his evil manners. And Salamon says that he is more
valyaunte. that maystryeth well his heart than he that takes a strong castle
and cytees.

Also the debonayres ben lords of therthe / that is of worldly goodes^ For if
they lose them they shall never be troubled ne angry therefore. But they that
been angry when they lose worldly goods / be not lords of them ne of their
heart. But been servants thereto. and therefore it is right and reason that they
that have here the goods temporell and spyrytuel / have in them self their
possessyon of the herte^ But now understand and behold that this that God
gives unto the pour of spyryte is the heaven. and to the debonayr the earth /
where shall be the auarycyous men then and the felons. but in the torments of
hell.

Of the seven yeftes of the holy ghoost. and first of the yefte of science
capitulo Cx
THe first yefte of the holy ghoost is the yefte of science. which makes a
man humble and dredeful. The second makes him sweet and pyteous. The third
makes him clear seeing. and connyng. and therefore it is called the yefte of
science. For it makes a man wise and connyng in mesure in all things. when
this yefte descends in to the heart of a person. he extyrpeth and casts out
the rote and the sin of ire and of felonnye which troubles the heart. and
makes a man like as he were fro him self so that he sees no thing ne for him
self. ne for to conduyte other. But this yefte enlumyneth the heart on all
parts so that he may not be deceived of any person / like as the yefte of
pity makes the man Innocent. so that he will none deceive. whereof saint Johan
says in thappocalipse in spyryte. that the holy man that was al full of this
espyryte. was al full of eyes tofore and after. And an angel showed to zacharye
the prophet a stone wherein were seven eyes These ben the eyes that the good
men have. for they see clear within their heart and al about them / That is to
say under and above. on the right side and on the lift side. This yeft of
science is maystre of the werkys. and that is to say of virtues of the soul.
For he makes al Just to a point by line rule and plombe / he takes first
his bound and his point. and that is that the wise man sayth^ In all that thou
begynnest. behold the end. and to what end thou shall come. after he holds
the line. For he goes by right way before and by right entencyon. After he
makes all by rule. For he makes it all plain and by mesure. For he loves
the common way of good people without to find noueltees. After he preueth his
sight and his work by plombe / For he takes head that his body enclyne not
toward the right side by prosperyte. ne to the lift side by aduersyte / This
yefte of sapyence is like to the priour of a cloystre of the soul. which
keeps thordre. and makes it to be kept oueral. First in the heart. and after
in other offices In this heart ben two sides and two things. the understanding
and the will / the reason and the affectyon / when these two sides and these
two things accorden to gydre. they make much sweet melodye and much fair
seruyse. That is when the will. will all that. which the understanding
enseygneth to good / and that affectyon feleth all that. which reason
understands. if they understand well in these ij sides which ben in the
soul / when. and how. they ouzt to accord In one side ben iiij locks. and in
that other side iiij. for reason has four offices. That is to inquire. to
Judge. to remember. and to show that which they understand by word. This
yefte enseygneth the reason that. which he ought to learn and to inquire. and
in what order. and in what manner and what end. and this is a much great
craft / For the mesprysyng in these things is much peryllous. hit byhoueth
to understand the reason / and to learn that which is necessary prouffytable
and honest. and to wythdrawe fro the contrary O god how a creature leseth his
time / and dyspences for to learn things that been of no value / but vaynglorye
and sin. But the holy ghoost by this yefte enseygneth lightly. and makes a
man to learn ordynatly that / which is most necessary to the prouffyte of
the soul. And that ledeth him most right unto the love of God for the health
and the prouffyte of his soul. and to help his neighbor.

Also it byhoueth the reason well to inquire the truth of the things / And
also how he ought for to believe / well to believe is. when a man byleueth symply
and steadfastly all that which god says and commands without ouermoche to
inquire. and without to enserche the counceylles of god / and the profoundnes
of his Iugements. the heyght of his mageste. and the reasons of his sacraments
/ well to believe is when one byleueth not over hastily. ne over late. ne to
eueryche / ne to none. for that one and other is vice as says seneke / After
good enquyryng comes well to Judge. For to Judge well it apperteyneth that one
afferme no thing. unto the time that he has inquired the truth of the thing
/ and that he be well encerteyned / and that he entremete not to Judge that.
which apperteyneth no thing to hym^ like as ben the secret things and hid
/ thentencyo^s of hertes^ the things that may not be turned on the right side
ne on the lift side. that yet they be vnderstonden to the better part. Of
which the spyryte by this yefte makes the reason to Judge well. and to know
the right / and to determyne between good things and evil things between the
little things and the great things. for he must praise every thing after his
valor. Also this spyryte makes the reason to remember. For he remembers a
man all that is nedeful to him. like as god says in the gospel. The things
that been passyd he must remember and bring ageyn to memory. The things that
been present he must understand and remember and ordeyne^ The things that
been to come he must purneye fore / ordeyne and advise. These ben the seven
parties of the virtue of prudence. after that which the phylosophre says. Also
he makes the reason to speak by mesure / and be stylle gladly. and not to
speak till it be need. So that the word be tofore well aduysed and well thought
or it come to the tongue^ And that the word be wayed and poysed as good money
and preued like as Salamon sayth^ So that the word be according unto god and
without sin of good matere and of good form. That is that it have not
ouermoche. ne over little. And that it be well employed. For good money ne a good
word ought not to be given for naught. Hereof says God in the gospel that we
should not cast the precious stones tofore hogs. That is to understand the
precious words of our lord god before them / and to such persons that set
them self not to work for their health. But lyuen in the ordure of their
sins. therefore holy scripture calls them hogs. This yefte before said
ordeyneth and accords that other party of the heart. That is the will where
it has iiij parties. love. dread / joy and sorrow. That is that one love
that^ which he owes. so as he owes. as much as he owes. and that he dread
not also that which he owes / and that he have no joy ne delight sauf in that
he owes after god and also how he owes / and as much as he owes. And that
he have no sorrow ne heaviness / but in that which he owes / and also how he
owes. and as much as he owes. when these four parties been accorded. then
it is said that a man is well attempred when he is not over cold ne over hot.
ne over dry. ne over moist. And in like wise as to the body of a man comen
over many maladyes. for the dysate^peraunce of these iiij qualytees / or of
these iiij humors / Right so to the heart of a man comen to him the vices and
sins by the dysatemperaunce of these four manners when these ij sides of the
heart ben accorded and ordained / that is the reason and the will. Then is a
man ordained within him self / These ben the ij sprynges of the rote of a much
fair virtue which is called equity. Equity proprely is that which is done by
Judgment good and true. not over soft / ne over rude^ without bowyng and
enclynyng unto that one party. ne to that other. when one goes forth aryght
as a line / for equity is none other thing but unity. that is egalte / al egal
/ who has this virtue is a true Judge and wise / For he does nothing but it be
inquired and examyned like as a good Judge ought to do Then the first degree
of this virtue / is that a man be a good Judge of him self. for he ought to enter
in to him self. and behold his conscience. and well to examyne his thoughts
and his wylles. whether they been good or evil / and to ordeyne all to the
regard of reason. so that will and reason be at one accord / For like as
saint Bernard says. virtue is none other thing but thassente of reason and of
will. That is that will without gaynsayeng. say and doo^ and also put in
oeuure. that is to say in deed and work. that which reason says / shows.
and enseygneth.

Of the second degree of equity and of ryghtwysnes Cxj
THe second degree of this virtue is. that a man be a rightful Judge. and hold
the right line of equity between himself and that which is under him. That is
his body which he has in keeping which he ought here to nourysshe. that it
may serve. and be so dyscyplyned and chastysed that it will of all and in all
things obey unto the soul. like as a good chambryere obeys to her
maystresse. and a good dyscyple to his master without gaynsayeng. For the
reason ought to be like as a true arbytrour between the soul and the body.
which ought to keep the right of either part. In such manner that the spyryte
be a good lord. and the body be a good servant and very subgette and
obeyssaunt to the soul / Now is it great necessyte to hold in this party
oueral equity and ryzt mesure in drynkyng and etyng. in clothyng and in
arayeng. and in all the things that the body commands. For it enclyneth more
to ouermoche than to ouerlytel. After. him byhoueth the v wits of his body
well to conduyte and to govern by reason and by equity. so that eueryche serve
in his office without sin and without mesprysyon. like as with the eyes to
behold. the eerys to here. the noses to smelle. the mouth to taste and to
speak. the hands and all the body to touch. when these v wits be well kept
from sin / Then is the castle sure and ferme. For these ben the yates of
the soul. These ben the wyndowes by which death enters often in to the soul
This witnesses the prophet.

Of the iij degree of the virtue of equity capo. Cxij
THe third degree of the virtue of equity is that a man be a good Judge and that
he hold equity. between him self / and that that is tofore him. That been the
temporal things. which often destroyen body and soule^ as when a man sets
his love ouermoche on them like as done the auarycyous and covetous men. and
al they that above mesure louen worldly things / For they have their hertes
knytte in the nettys of the devil. as Job says. That is to plees and
quarellys^ and forayne works. wherein they ocupye them so and in such manner.
that in the life spyrytuel ne to their sauacyon they conne naught do / ne may
not ne will not entende. so much ben they blind / and bounden in their
sins. whereof it happeth that which Seneke the wise man says. That by this
we sin and goo out of the way. that as touching the parties of the bodyly
life. every man thinks and is besy. but for to ordeyne his life spyrytuel for
to have glory perdurable no man thinks ne studyeth / Now is then much
great necessyte. that a man set not ouermoche his heart in forayne things /
for who that so ouermoche does. he falls in the charges and in the couetyses
of the world. which is the rote of all vices.

Of the fourth and fyfthe degree of the virtue of Equity capitulo Cxiij
THe fourth degree of the virtue of equity is that a man see clearly on his rzht
side. that is that he take heed and take example of the good for to govern
him. which ben like as at his right syde^ And of the good and wise men he take
wit and example / But in this side behooves to hold dyscrescyon and equity /
For all the people may not goo by one way / ne all the good. ne all the wise. have
not one self grace. like as the members of a body have not one self office. and
hereof been many persons nouyces deceived in their heart. like as says the book
of collacyons of holy faders. which treaten of the perfectyon of virtues / for
wha^ they see a man well parfyght much prouffyte in one estate and in one
grace. Anon they entende. desire. and will resemble him. and when they see
another. which in another estate does also much good. also they cry and
run after. and also to the third and the fourth and with none they abide ne
rest / They be also like as the young grehounde / which is yet all young.
that renneth after every be that he sees tofore him / and does no thing
but makes him weary and leseth his time. hereof tells ysopus a tale or a
fable. of a little hounde and of an ass. which ass saw the hounde that as
oftymes as his lord came home. he ran ayenste him and lepe upon his neck.
and the lord played with him and made him great feste. and the ass thought
saying. More ought my lord to make to me feste which serve him al day. than to
this dog which serves of no thing It was not long after that this ass
saw his lord come to his house. And he ran against him / and cast his ij
forefeet about his neck. and began strongly to lycke and fawn him. The
servants of the lord which saw this / ran with great staves and beten
right well the ass. And of that. of which the ass had supposed to have had
grace. honor. and prouffyte. he had shame and dommage. By such fables the
wise men were wont tenseygne and teache them self by such ensaumple. And by
this ensaumple he shows / that no man should desire such graces as he may not
attain ne come to. and the same techeth Salamon saying. Sone cast not thyn
eyes to rychesses / That is to the graces that thou may not atteyne. Therefore
he has great need of dyscrescyon that he see of whom he takes ensaumple.
Also it is necessyte that a man see clearly on his lift side. and that is the
fyfthe degree. For one ought to behold the fools and the shrewes which ben
as on the lift side. for they be on the werse side. To them ought one to take heed. First by cause that a man should have pity and compassyon / Also that one
should not ensyewe their folly ne their predycyon. so as the wise Salamon says.
I passed said he by the vyneyerde of the slouthful fool. and saw that it was
full of thorns and nettles. and by this ensaumple I have learned wit and
prouydence. Also that one love most god by whom he is quyte of such sins
and of such perils. But him byhoueth on this side to keep dyscrescyon and
equity. For when I see a fool and a synnar. I ought to have pity and
compassyon. and not to make of him mocquerye ne derysyon / I ought always to
hate the sin. and love the persone^ and much I ought to keep me that I will
no grief ne harm in my heart to no person ne to condemn him. Ne compare my
self to another that is so evil. For he is this day evil that shall be to morn
good and such is this day good that to morn shall be evil. Also I ought as
much as I may without mysdoyng unto other enploye my self. humble and
condescende in werkys and in words for to win him to god. and to wythdrawe
him fro sin. For like as says Seneke and Saint Gregory we may not better
relyeue them that been fallen. than by that which is aforesaid. and late us not
will our self how that it be^ enclyne toward them.

The vi degree of the virtue of equity capitulo Cxiiij
THe vj degree of the virtue of equity is the vj eye that the wise man has.
That is that he see clearly behind the net and the engynes of the devil /
which been to us as behind us. For the fend sees us and we may not see him.
The fend our enemy that is the deuyl^ which is much strong / wise. subtyl.
and besy for to deceive us / For he cesseth never day ne night. but always is
in a wait for to deceive us by his craft and by his engynes that he uses in
moo than a thousand manners. And like as says saint austyn. The deuylles see
much subtylly thestate of a man and his manner. and his complexyon and to what
sin. and to what vice he is most enclyned. by nature or by custom / and to
that part whereto a man enclyneth him self. Thereto the devil assaylleth most
strongely / The coleryke man to wrath and Ire. The sangueyn man to Iolyte and
to lecherye / The fleumatyke coglotonnye and to stouthe. and the malencolyke to
envy and heaviness / And therefore every man ought to deffende and keep him fro
that part where he sees that his house is most feble^ And against this vice
and this sin ought one to fight and resyste most / of which he is most
assaylled. And how much more he shall resyste strongely ayenste all sins.
So much more merit shall he have in paradyse or in heaven / and understand
well that the enemy of hell spares no person / For he is hardy and aygre^
as he that assaylleth our lord Ihesu Christ in temptyng him. Know thou says
our lord to Job. in how many guyses the fend desguyseth him. and in how many
manners / Like as he should say. No man knows but I only. For like as says
saint Denis. All the angellys the good and the evil. and all the spyrytes of men
ben like as a myrrour spyrituel. Then like as a myrrour receives all the
fourmes and thenpryntes that comen tofore him / Right so does a spyryte of a
man. be it in slepyng be it in wakyng. Now then took a myrrour and set it
against another. Anon all the forms that been in that one / thou shall see in
that other In such it is said that the devil shows to a man such fygures
and such fourmes as he will that god suffers him And the soul receives
maulgre him self sometime in thouzt and in ymagynacyon / like ayenste my will.
me byhoueth to see and receive in the sight of mine eye the form that comes
before me. Now is it a right great grace of god and a right great yefte of the
holy ghoost to understand well all the langages of the devil and to know all
his temptacyons. and all his engynes. For like as says saint Bernard / It is
over subtyl a thing to know and to dyscusse between the thoughts that the
heart conceyueth and brings forth. and them that the devil planteth^ And the
fend shows to a man how the sins been playsaunte and delectable. lightly
may a dyscrete man and reasonable know this / But when the fend comes to
tempte a man in guyse of an Angel. And shows to him good for to draw him to
evil. Then is the temptacyon most strong. And therefore says saint Johan
that one ought not to believe all spyrytes. but they ouzt to preue and well
examyne them tofore that one believe them and to consider if they be of the
part of god. Right so done they that have their confessors good and holy
men. wise and well approved in their fayt / To which confessors they that
confess them. shown often their thoughts which come unto their heart. both
the good and evil. For like as Salamon says Blessed be they that all so
doubten that they sin not. ne mysdoon. And he says also in another place /
Do by good counceyll all that thou shalt do. And then thou shalt not
repent the.

The seventh degree of the virtue of equity capitulo Cxv
THe vij degree of Equity is the seventh eye. which he must have that will have
this virtue. That is that he behold upward on hye. And that he have god all
way tofore him. Of such our Lord says in the gospel^ if thyn eye be pure and
simple / All thy body shall be clear and shynyng. And if thyn eye be derke and
tenebrouse. All thy body shall be derke obscure and tenebrouse. That is to say
if the entencyon of thyn heart is pure and simple. and gooth forth the right
lygne after god by all the degrees that we have tofore named. All the mass
and substance of thy works and of thy virtues shall be fair clear and
playsaunt to god. And if the entencyon be not good but froward and evil. and
reployeth bacwarde. all the work shall be derke and tenebrouse. For without
good and ryghtful entencyon. Alms bycometh sin / and virtues vices /
Thentencyon is simple when a man makes his works good right for gods love.
and it is obscure and derke. when a man does his works for to playse the
world or for vain glory. It is crooked and not right in two things. that is
when one holds one part to god. and that other of the world. For thentencyon
retorneth bacward / when a man secheth his own prouffyte in all thing that
he does. Now have thou herd the seven degrees ol ^hys virtue of Equity by
which this tree reyseth on heyght

Here folowen the virtues ayenste the seven dedely sins capitulo Cxvj
THe branches of this tree ben the seven virtues pryncypal / which answer
unto the seven dedely sins. like as meekness or humylyte does ageynste
pride. Amytye or frendshyp ayenste enuye^ Debonayrte and pacyence against ire
and telonnye. Prowess and dylygence ayenste slouthe / Largess ayenste
auaryce. Chastyte against lecherye^ and Sobrenesse against glotonnye. These seven
virtues keep and conduyde much right the spyryte of science which ledeth and
conduyteth them by the way of Equity as Salamon says. By the which way
dyscrescyon and reason which is the charytour and the conduytour of virtues as
says saint bernard and the governor of the ship of the soul ledeth and
governs them that they goo not out of the way ne on the right side ne on
the lift. And thus prouffyten they / grow and brings forth fruit
plentyously / Then the virtue of Equity. shows him by dyscrescyon in all the
works of other virtues. that without this virtue. the name of the virtue
bycometh vice. I say well that in another sense. these seven virtues beforesayd
been the branches of Equity. and all the fruytes and the good works that
grown thereof apperteynen to this tree. Now understand well how the great
maystre of virtues speaks to us of this virtue. For he says not in his rule.
blessed be they that holden equity oueral. and in all things have dyscrescyon
and mesure without mystakyng For there is none but he mysdoeth in many manners
/ And therefore our Lord Ihesu Christ recomforteth us. when he says not.
Blessed be they that sin not / and that mysdoo not. but done all by equity
and by right lygne. but he says much curioysly for to recomforte the synnars.
Blessed be they that weep / for they shall be comforted / That is to say. They
been and shall be blessed that seen. known and vnderstonden well their sins
and their deffaultes in all the points of equity which we have here tofore
named / And thereof wepen and be sorouful that they find Inyquyte and
wickedness. there where as they should hold and find equity. And therefore
this world is called the valey of teerys. that none in the world may live
without teerys. which has received the yefte of science. whereof we have
spoken tofore. But it byhoueth as says Salamon. that who that most knows
and most sees the euylles and sorrows of the world / he has most sorrow at
his heart. teres and wepynges.

Thus began the world to grieve and annoye. and to whom this transytorye life
most annoyeth ans greueth / he most desires that other life which is
wythouten end. Now ought thou to take here six manner of teerys which an
holy man had here in this world by the yefte of science / The first teerys
comen of that. which a man has oftymes angered god. by thought. by word. and
by work. The second teerys comen of that. which one byholdeth the great
torments / horrible and perdurable of hell which thou have deserved by thy
sins. of which each person ought for to have great dread. The third teres
grow of the euylles. that a man see the good suffer. of whom we ought to have
pity and compassyon^ The fourth teres comen for the sins that the evil people
do. The v teerys comen for this life which is peryllous. and for that other life
which is without end in glory perdurable. that we tarry so long therfro /
The syxthe teres comen of devotion and of great plente of spyrytuel Joy of the
presence of Ihesu Christ. and of the feelyng of the holy ghoost. These been a
right well blessed that thus wepen. For they shall be comforted as says the
gospel. like as the nouryce comfort the child that wepeth and cries. For
she dries the eyes and kysseth him / and makes him to laughe by force. Right
so shall our lord do to them that wepen by bitter contrycyon for their sins
like as I have said / The debonair Ihesus shall dry their eyes. that they shall
never weep more / Ne they shall never feel harm ne sorrow. But all way they
shall be with our Lord god in pees / in laughyng and in Joy pardurable.

Here after follows how that a man ought for to live in moyen astate capitulo
Cxvij
NOw have we spoken of the yeftes and of the virtues that govern them that
live in this world in the lowest of these three estates of which we have spoken
tofore / Now owe we by the aid of the holy ghoost to speak of the yeftes and
of the virtues. which most proprely apperteyne to them that despise the
world. and tenden to the montayne of perfectyon. Of them says proprelye the
holy man Job. That the life of a man upon the erthe^ is as a knyghthode. for the
life of a man in therthe is laboryous. Now behold and take heed of a young
bourges. and of a young knight / These two manner men have much diverse
thoughts. and diverse ententes. The bourges entendeth to marchaundyse. for to
bye and selle. to win and to get good / and the end of his entente is all
for to be rich and noble and honored in his cite or town.

The new knight gooth all another way. For he desires and entendeth to do
curt^syes and to give largelye. To learn chyualrye and for to use arms. To
suffer pain and disease / and to show prowess. to conquer loos and honor
and to mount in to hye estate. These two estates we see openly in these two
manner of people / Of which sum been / that will keep them from great sins
/ for they will do penance and give alms / and hold and keep the
commandments of our Lord Ihesu Christ and of holy church. And well should
suffyse them. if they might for so much save them at the last. There been
other to whom the world ennoyeth and greueth for the perils sins and the
pains of which it is al full. So that none may have pees of heart ne sure
conscience. They see ageyn on that other side / that there is no tresoure
which may be compared unto the love of god. Ne no swetnesse so great / as is
pees of heart. Ne no glory mondayne ne worldly. that may compare to the glory
of a pure conscience. It seems to them and truth it is that who that might
get these three things he should be more than an Emperor.

This is a great thing. but there been but few that dare take this empryse /
But when god gives to a man this grace and this yefte. which is called the
spyryte of strength he gives to him a new heart. a noble heart. and an hardy
heart. Noble for to despise all that. which the world may take and give. And of
this hardynesse speaks our Lord in the gospel / when he says. blessed be they
that have hungre and thyrste for Justice / Salamon says that he is Just that
despyseth his do^mage for his soul or for his friend. and saint bernard says
that he is not Just that sees not that his heart feleth and understands.
that he is bounden in his heart anenste god to love him above al things. They
that verayly desire with all their heart to render this debte to god. been
they of whom our Lord speaks in the gospel. when he says that blessed be
they that have hungre and thyrst for Justice. He says not blessed ben they
that done Justice. but that have hungre and thyrst to do Justice / For this
Justice may not be holden. ne plainly rendered in this world / But in this world
it shall be desired. and in that other paid. Therefore our Lord says not they
be blessed that shall render and yield this Justice / but he says more
curtoysly. As he that well knows our pouerte. Blessed be they that of this
Justice have hungre and thyrste. For Ihesu Christ requires not that we pay to
him here his debte. but it suffyseth to him if we have good will and desire to
render and yield. And how shall I say that they be Iuste^ that render not that
/ which they owe. ne have no will ne hungre to pay. This desire when it is
very in the heart / him byhoueth that he show it by work For like as Salamon
says. No man may bear fire in his lap but if that his gown brenne. This
demonstraunce may not be without virtue and without prowess. For by
witness. ne by pletyng ne by preef may not be that one be a good knight. but
by many good feetes of arms / and by much suffryng and enduryng of
trybulacyons and myschyef. And this is the fourth virtue that the holy ghoost
gives to a man to extyrpe and pluck all out the fourth dedely sin. That
is the sin that is called in clergy accydye. that is slouthe / This virtue
aforesaid is of so great dygnyte. that emonge all other virtues. this only
bears by him self proprely the name of virtue. For virtue and prowess is al
one. God gives this virtue of prowess to his servants when he suffers and
will make them knights / like as he did his apostles at pentecoste or
whytsontyde. Of whom we read that they were so cowarde tofore that they had
received this virtue of prowess. that they durst not goo out of their lodgyng.
unto the time that they were armed with this virtue. but after they had this
virtue of prowess they suffered gladly al martyrdoms and al manner torments.

Of the deuysyons of virtues after the phylosophres Cxviij
THe phylosophres that treat of these virtues. depart^ this virtue of prowess
in vj parties. which ben like vj degrees whereby this virtue mounteth and
prouffyteth. but our master which maad the phylosophres and the phylosophye.
that is Ihesu Christ. he put to the seventh point of prowess. The first
point of prowess is called magnytude The second is affyance. The third
surete. The fourth pacyence. The fyfthe constaunce. The syxte magnyfycence. And
the seventh which our master Ihesu Criste adiousted. that is hungre and
thyrst of Justice / This virtue may not so proprely be named in english. as
thentendement or understanding of the world is said in latin.

The first of the virtue of magnanymyte capitulo Cxix
MAgnanymyte. is hyenesse. gretenesse. and noblesse of courage by which a man
is hardy as a man of great empryse. This virtue has two parties / That is to
wete to despise great things. or naught to preyse. and more gretter things to
enterprise and to chese / Of the first party says Saint Austyn. Prowess is
when courage despyseth all that which he has not in his power / That is all
that he may lose ayenste his will / And Seneke says. in worldly things there
is no thing great / but the heart which despyseth great things / Of the
second party says the phylosophre. that magnanymyte is reasonable empryse of
hye things and ferdful. who that has this virtue. he byholdeth the world fro
far. as says Ysaye the prophet. And thus him seems that all the world be a
little thing. like as a sterre seems to us a little thynge^ Then all the
world. and all the charges. and the great works and needs of the world semen
to him as naught. whereof salamon says when he had well enserched the world /
and had desputed of al thestates. of the fools and wise men. He said his
sentence in this manner. vanyte of vanytees. and all that I see is vanyte. That
is to say that all the world is vanyte / and all full of vanytes And a man him
self for whom the world is made. be peryssheth with al vanyte. for in him is
al manner of vanyte and of ordure^ Like as dauyd says in his Psaulter. vanyte
by mortalyte. For his life flees away as shadow. vanyte by curyosyte / For
his heart is as a dreme. vanyte by wyckydnesse / For sin makes him more to be
holden and reputed naught. than any thing that is in the world. Now is then
the first party of this virtue that has made him to despise the world. Like
as have sometime done in time passed. the phylosophres. the paynems. the
sarasyns. And holy christian men / That other party is so that he do get the
way of perfectyon: and to chese the life that is so openly sharp and
dredeful. This is the way that ledeth a man unto the montaygne of god. that is
in thestate of perfectyon. This is the way of the pryue counceyl of our lord
Ihesu Christ. which he showed in the montaygne to his appostles / whereof this
traytye speaks. This way chese they / to whom it suffyseth not only to
keep the commandementes of god / to which they be bounden by true debte like
as they doo^ that leave all that they have for gods sake. and abandonne them
self to dye for the love of him that deyed for them in the cross. that was
sweet Ihesu Christ. Or for to goo unto the holy land or ellis where. as they do
that leave and despise all for the love of god both hauoyr. friends. and them
self. and make them servants of other and pour that were rich and might be
in the world and put them self to suffer great sharpenes! which hadden in the
world great eases and great delytes / and al these things done many and have
done with good heart that been in relygyon for little auaylleth it to be in
relygyon or in sharpenes of penance if the heart be not there. For the habyte
makes not the monk. ne the arms the knight / but the good hertes and the
purneaunce and garneson of good works.

Of the virtue of affyaunce spyrytuel capitulo Cxx
THe second degree of this virtue is affyaunce / For who that has emprysed a
good way or any good works / him byhoueth that he hold him fermelye in his
purpoos / And that he achyeue that he has begone. This virtue is called
fyaunce. Fyaunce is necessary ayenste thassautes of the world. of the flesh
/ and of the devil of hell. which much strongely assaylen a man at the
begynnyng^ The flesh says to him I may not endure this life. my life has
custom to live such a life / The world renneth after for to withdraw him fro
doing well / like as one renneth after a thief. when he escapes fro prison. The
devil says to him. Caytyf what will thou do. wherefore wylt thou thus sle thy
self / thou may well save thy self otherwise. These ben the first assaults
that the new knights of god suffer. which entende and draw to conquer the
royame of heaven. and when they entende and abide with god by good and term
affyaunce. they retche not For he is the right true friend that can. may. and
will keep his friends / and whom god will aid and help / none may noye ue
grieve.

Of the virtue of surete capitulo Cxxj
THe third degree of prowess is surete. Surete as says the phylosophre is a
virtue by which a man redoubteth not ne dredeth the euylles ne the perils
which been tofore his eyes. and this is the third good and well that the yefte
of strength makes. For when the holy ghoost armeth his knight with his virtue
he gives to him first a noble heart for to enterprise great things. after he
gives to him a great ardour and a desire to poursyewe it / and great affyau^ce
to bring it to an ende^ after he makes him sure and hardy as a lion so that he
has no dread of peril ne of pain. ne of dethe^ ne of torments. but
desires them like as does the new knight the tournoye. Thus dyden the holy
marters like as it appears in their lyues^ Emonge other we read of Saint
agathe that had as great Joy when she went to the torments. like as she
should have gone to a weddyng or to a feste. and in like wise of thy holy
apostles and other holy marters without nombre.

Of the fourth degree of the virtue of prowess Cxxij
Right as the holy ghoost makes his knight sure for to abide the torments and
the sorrows that been to come Right so makes he him strong and pacyent to
suffer them when they come. and this is the fourth degree which is called
pacyence. By this virtue a man ouercometh his enemies. The devil. the flesh.
and the world^ and all that they may do and say. For these be the sheldes of
gold to him / which for the love of god suffers that they couere on al sides
/ Like as dauyd the prophet says in his psaulter / so that no stroke may
hurt him / This virtue has no man but if he has be tempted^ For trybulacyon
forgeth sapyence as says saint Poule. like as the fire makes the tyles hard.
without this virtue is none proved. Thus without pacyence none may come to
perfectyon. without pacyence no man has vyctorye. For who that leseth
pacyence is vaynquysshed. Of this we see example in all the crafts that been
made with hand. Many a stroke of the hamer suffers the cup of gold tofore
or it be set on the table of a king. And also a chalyce or it be blessed and
set on the altar. Much suffers the tonnes and pypes many great strokes
tofore the wyn be put therein / Much is defouled with the feet of the fullers
the fine scarlet cloth. tofore or the queen is clad wythal. and as many
examples may thou fynde^ as there ben in london crafts. By this virtue is a
man strong as iron. which all other metalles softeth and maystryeth / and he
is maad precious as gold. which the more it is in the fire. the more is it
pure and clean. clear and traytable. as the salamandre in the fire. and as the
fysshe that lives in the water of trybulacion in which he swymmeth and is
nourysshed.

Of the v degree of the virtue of prowess capitulo Cxxiij
THe v degree of the virtue of prowess is called the virtue of constance / this
is a very virtue that makes the heart strong and stable as a toure founded
upon a ferme roche. and as a tree rooted in good ground. that meueth not. ne
waggeth for no wind that may blow. That is to say. for none adventure ne
temptacyo^ that may hap or come. good ne evil without this virtue none comes
to virtue ne to vyctorye. For when the knight of god has made or done so^me
prowesses Then assaylleth him the devil by vaynglorye. And then is the
bataylle in the heart only to vaynquysshe. that he fall not by vaynglorye /
that all the first temptacyon was not so strong / as is this vaynglorye. Of
which Dauyd says in his psaulter. that the devil beteth down the strong on
the lift side by aduersyte. And the right strong on the right side by
vaynglorye. This virtue prayseth much Seneke the wise man which says. That
there is no virtue but that which gooth tofore proudly between that one
fortune and that other. and to the great despyte of that one and of that other.

The vj degree of the virtue of prowess capitulo Cxxiiij
THe vj degree of prowess is magnyfycence^ this virtue expresses and declares
also the phylosophre saying Magnyfycence is an hye work and happy achyeuyng.
Our Lord Ihesu Christ the souerayn phylosophre calls this virtue perseueraunce^
by which the good knight of god endures the euylles unto the ende^ in that
hye way of perfectyon which he has emprysed. Of this virtue says saint poule
that all the virtues run / but this virtue wynneth the sword All they fight
but this has the vyctorye and the crown. All werken. But this virtue of
perseueraunce bears away the reward and the merit. For our lord Ihesu
Christ says. who that shall persevere unto the end he shall be saved and none
other. The phylosophres could no ferther declare this virtue of prowess. But
the dyscyples of our great maystre Ihesu Christ seen much more ferther. For
like as Salamon says when they have all remembered and performed / Then
them seem that al is to begin ageyn. The virtues and the prowess of
phylosophres were al for to vaynquysshe the sins and vices / and for to get
the virtues / But the prowess of saints was not only to vaynquysshe sins
and vices and to get virtues. but with all this pryncypally for to keep Iustyse
and truth toward Ihesu Christ. He is not true ne Just. that renders not
that he owes to his power. And certeynly it is a thing much ryghtful and
reasonable that I give my life and my death for him that gaf his life and death for
me. And as much as he is of more value and is more worth than I / so much I
am more redeuable to him by right Iustyse. Like as says Saint ancelme. This
Justice I owe to desire but I may not here render it ne pay it fully^ as we
have said tofore. And therefore is the seventh degree of this virtue this which
our lord Ihesu christ has put to. To the which the phylosophre might never
atteyne. when he said blessed be they that have hungre and thyrst of Justice /
They then be blessed that be mounted in to these seven degrees of prowess /
and have hungre and thyrste and great desire to their power to mount unto the
seventh degree.

Of the spyrytuel bataylle against sin capitulo Cxxv
IN this tree like as in the other we find vij branches for in vij manners the
virtue and the prowess of the good knight of god shows him / For by vij
manners of bataylle there comen vij manners of vyctorye. and by seven manner of
vyctoryes. he conquereth seven manners of crowns of glory These been the
rewards and the seven merytes of which speaks saint Johan thappostle and
euangelyst in thapocalypse For as Saint Bernard says. Much is he a fool. and
over wenyng that without vyctorye attayneth to have the crown and that without
batayl weneth to have vyctorye / whereof Saint Poul says. That he shall never be
crowned in glory that fyghteth not truly ayenste sin and vices / which is
the champe of battle in this world. The maystre of this ^elde of bataylle is
Ihesu Christ. which preueth his new knights like as it is wryton in the book
of kings. This maystre is the debonayr Ihesu Christ. which is ryzt true as
says saint Poule. and knows well the power of every man wherefore he suffers
not that any enemy or tend tempte us above our power / ne that no aduersarye
assail us so. but that we may overcome him if we will by thayde of god why^he
increases our strength in the bataylle as says saint Paul. and saint Johan
also as we have said and devised vij vyctoryes and vij crowns / That is to say
vij manner of rewards and of merytes which god promyseth to them that overcome
the sins and the vices.

Of the first bataylle against al vices capitulo Cxxvj
THe first bataylle that a christian man has / is ayenste dedely sin. There is
none ouercomen ne vaynquyshed in this bataylle / but if he will / For who that
will not consent to sin he vaynquyssheth the battle. which is light to do
to a good heart vygorous / and much hard to him that is slow and latchous and
evil encoraged to do well and to the seruyse of god. which is not strong by
dread. ne hoot in prayer to god and in well dooyng as Saint Johan says. For who
that falls and is vaynquysshed in this battle. has much to do and is more
hard for him to releue him and to defend him. than he that is in hye
spyrytuel estate. For he has no power to releue hym^ but if it be by the grace
of god For like as the fysshe enters by him self in to the net. yet may he
not issue ne goo out / but if he be cast or put out / Right so a man
falls by him self and by his will in to sin. but he may not issue ne goo
out without the grace of our lord and his aid and help / as when he gives
to him repentance to do penance for his sins. and that is the armor that
saint Poul comaundeth to take in this bataylle. Now ought thou to know.
that when a man is armed for to vaynquysshe and overcome hardely sin and
parfyghtly him byhoueth that he have three things which ben in very penance.
The first is repentance of heart / The second confession of mouth / The third
is satysfactyon and penance. that is the amends of sin. if one of these
three faylle the confession is nothing worth.

Of very repentance of heart capitulo Cxxvij
Repentance requires great sorrow and great bywayllynges of heart of that
which he has angered and dyspleased god. and of so much as he has more sinned
and dysplesed god. so much more ought be the sorrow. and the repentance
gretter. Thus repented him the good King dauyd when he said in his psaulter. I
have labored and trauaylled in my bewayllyng / and have wasshen in the nyghtes
my bed and my couche with my weeping teerys / He that has dysplesed god by
dedely synne^ ought to weep and waylle in the depnesse of his heart. and with
great syghynges cry god mercy like as the thief. the murdrer. and the traitor
that has deserved to be hanged on the gybet of helle^ The synnar is the thief
to god. For he has stolen and mysused the goods of his lord which been but
lent to him for to win with. Tho been the goods of nature / of grace / and
of fortune. of which he must render and give acompte and rekenyng much
straytly / how he has folyly dyspended them. and has put them to evil use.
Also he is a murdrer of the daughter of the king. that is of his own soul.
which was daughter of the king of glory by grace / whom he has slain and
put to death by dedely sin / Also he is a traytre. For the castle of his heart
and of his body which god has given him to keep / he has yolden to the devil
which is his mortal enemy. well ought he to demene great sorrow that is in
such peril. and ought often to wasshe his bed / that is his conscience.
These teres chase and drive away the devil out of his heart. like as the
scaldyng hot water dryueth a dog out of the kechyn. After the repentance
ought to come the confession. that is the good chambryere which makes clean
the house. and casts out all the ordures with the besomme of the tongue.
whereof dauyd says in the psaulter / Now understand well how a man ought to
confess him /

Here after is contained how that a man ought to confess him capitulo Cxxviij
Unto that / that confession auaylleth unto the sauacyon of the soul byhouen
six condycyons. The first is that it be made wisely / and this is in two
things / the first that he take good head. to whom he ought to confess him:
and after whereof he ought to be confessyd. Saint Austyn says. that it which
one should do for to eschew and flee the death of the body / ought one do for
to eschew the death and the dampnacyon of the soul / The seek man for
teschewe and to fle the death. and for to have health. secheth gladly the best
physician and the most wise that he may find. Thus says Saint Austyn. who so
wisely will confess him and find grace anenst god. he ought to seche such a
confessor. which can and may bind and unbind. and also counceylle. That is
that the confessor can well know sin. and counceylle the synnar. and that he
have power to assoylle him / and to give him penance after the sin. For
according to his sin he ought to have penance. Also who so will confess him
wisely he ought dylygently remember his sins tofore or he confess him and
enserche al his heart and his conscience. how he has dysplesed god and his
blessed mother and al his saints. and ought to remember all his life in great
dread. Like as did the good king Ezechyas which said thus. I shall remember al
my years in the great bytternes of my soul and my heart. The synnar ought to
enter in to the house of his heart / and not to pass thorough like a mynystrel
which abides not gladly in his house. For he has no werse home than his
own. But in his own heart a man ought to dwell and consider all his sins
and his deffaultes. whereof he ought to yield acompts and reason truly to god
and to his confessor. and ought to remember to ordeyne well his acompte / like
as he that is adiourned tofore his lord for to render acompte of al his
receytes and payementes. And also well to take heed tofore the writing of his
conscience / that he faylle not to account all his life. For if he faylle of
his acompte god shall not faylle of his when a man has dylygently remembered his
sins. and beholden how and in how many manners he has dysplesed god / and how
oftymes. and how gretelye he has sinned / And how long he has abyden in
sin / Then he ought to confess him anon and hastelye And this is the
second condycyon that ought to be in confession. The king Dauyd rose at
mydnyght for to confess him. like as he says in the psaulter. and abode never
unto a month. ne to the end of a year. And the wise man says thus in another
place / Ne tarry thou not to convert to god. ne withdraw the not ne seek no
delays fro day to ady. For in taryeng is much peril for many reasons. First
for the condycyon of sin. For sin is a fire brennyng. which may not be
quenched but by lacrymable confession / And much were he a fool that saw his
hows brenne. and would not hastily run to fetch water for to quench the fire.

Also it is a great maladye and sickness to dwell in sin and the very
medecyne is confession. And certain little prayseth he his health. that sees
him self seek to the death / and desires not to be guarysshed and helyd. Also
the death which is nyghe and all about to espy the synnar^ ought to moeue
and excyte him hastelye to confess him. For he knows not the day. the hour.
ne the point or mynute when the death shall come. which surpryseth often the
synnar. there. where he takes none head. And certeynlye who that knew what
day he should deye. he should make him ready in the best and hastyest wise that
he might / Also if a synnar saw well the peril wherein he is. For he is in
the hold and prison of sin and in the throat of the lion of hell. and of
the dragon that will devour him / he should hastily goo to confession / and that
as soon as he might. Also a synnar ought to see what he has lost by his sin.
the goods perdurable and the goods spyrytuel. His time and him self which he
might al recoure by devout confession. Much then were he a fool if he
hasted not to recouure that which he had lost.

Also the mercy of god that abides for the synnar. and knocks at his door as
says the apocalypse. For that he ought to haste him to be confessyd / For of
as much as god abides so long the synnar. of so much is his Justice more
hard and more cruel when he sees him slow and neclygente. For like as the
archyer gives to his bow more bente / and tharbalester to the cross bow so
much more smyteth it the harder and stronger. And certeynlye god has his bow
bente and ready to loze as says the Psaulter for to slay the synnars if they
will not convert them. and if they take not good head Also the synnar that
ouerlonge taryeth to confess him / forgeteth often his sins. So that it
happeth that uneath that he is well and truly confessyd. For he forgeteth many
sins which he shall never remember. and so of them shall he never repent. ne
never be confessed / of which it is to him great peril. Also when a synnar
is tofore his confessor he ought to express and say his sins clearly. so
that his confessor see euydently his heart / and al thentencyon of him that
confesses him. For the seek man ought to dyscoure his maladye unto the
physycyen. else the physycyen might not work. Ne the Surgyen ne might not
hele the sore but if he saw the wound. And therefore says the wise man / if
thou wylt that the Surgyan hele the. thou must dyscouere to him thy wound or
sore. Then the truaunte and the lame ^echen the to confess the which shown
their maladyes. and lay forth the foulest tofore for to have alms. Thus
then ought the synnar to dyscouer his sins to his confessor for to have
mercy^ and this is the third condycyon. that ought to be in confession. Also
the synnar ought to confess him entyerly and holy / this is the fourth
condycyon. For he ought to say all his sins great and little and all the
cyrcumstaunces of the synnes^ Then he ought first to byholde the dedely
synnes^ of which I have spoken tofore. and to confess him holy of eueryche
of them / after that he feleth him culpable. without to hyde any thing. and
without saying more / and without excusing hym^ and without to accuse any
other. Right so confessyd him Dauyd that says in the Psaulter / I shall
confess me and shall say all my sin against me. and not against other. like as
ypocrytes which put always the fairest outward / and tell their good deeds
and hyde their evil deeds. And accusen other of that. which they them self be
more culpable of. For they see well a little festue or a little mote in the eyes
of other. and behold not a great beme or block which is in their owen eyes /
that is to say the great sins that been in them. Such was the pharyse of
whom the gospel says that he remembered his good deeds. and despised the
publycan that humbly smote his breast in the temple. and cried God mercy and
said. Lord god have pity and mercy on me pour synnar. Thus ought the synnar
Judge him self tofore god. and not aledge his sin but to agryeue. poyse^ and
recounte clearly without lyeng. Also confession ought to be hole. and not
departed to diverse confessours^ For it ought to be said all to one confessor
/ and not one part to one / and another part to another god loves not such
departing. Also a man ought not to say only the sins. but all the
cyrcumstaunces which agreuen much the sins. For the sins ben perauenture
more great in one person than in another. as in a relygyous man more than in a
seculer. In a prelate than in a simple man. Also this is more great sin in
one place than in another / as in a monasterye^ or in any other holy place^
more than in an unhallowed place / also in one time more than in another. as in
lent or on festeful days / Also when one synneth wytyngly and in ernest. he
synneth more than when one synneth ygnorantlye. Also one ought for to say the
condycyon of the sin. For it is gretter sin with a wedded woman than with a
syngle. Or in a man or woman of relygyon^ or in a person ordained a priest or
a deken. after that the order and the estate is more great. so much is the
sin more great. Also if the sin be ayenste nature and how long time he
has duellyd in the said sins. also he ought to say if he have little or
naught resysted and with stand te^ptacyon / or if he have souzt te^ptacyon. or
if he have be beten in te^ptaco^n^ Also he ought to say the cause and the
ente^cyo^ that moved him to do the sin. and all the other occasyons of the
sin. Also a man ought for to think and consydere by all his members how he
has sinned. First he ought to goo to his heart. and say all his sins what
someuer they be carnal or spyrytuel. Spyrytuel as against the faith or of
vain glory. or of Envy. of auaryce. of rancour. or of other manners. of whom
there be many. The sins carnal or bodily / apperteynen to the delytes of the
flessh of the body or if he have not kept him well in all thoughts. that
therein has been consentyng^ or long abydyng. Or delight. which sometime is as
much as the consentyng. and of all these thoughts he ought to confess. Also
one ought to take heed if he have sinned by the me^bres of his body. for a man
synneth in them in many manners. First in the head / when one sets over great
cure and great costs to dress it. as done these ladies and wymmen. which so
curyously array their head with precious adournementes for pure vanyte and for
to playse and draw men to sin. In which they sin often grievously. and
specially they that make them hye horns of their here. or of other thing /
which resemblen common wymmen. There be vanytees enough about the heed. in
wasshyng. in kembyng in dyeng and in pouryng in a myrrour / of which things
god is often dyspleased / Of this vanyte and folly the men be not all quyte.
For they arraye their here like wymmen. and force it to be yelowe. and if they
be blacke^ they by craft make them blounde and abourne. and late them grow
long more like to a woman than to a man. which is a sign of great evil and
much pride. And of all this and such things a man ought for to confess
him. and of all other vanytees and keep him that he do them no more.

Also a man ought to remember and well consydere to the five wits of his body
/ wherein he has often sinned in many manners / By the eyes in folyly seeing and
beholding. Or by the eerys in heryng gladly the myssayers / losengers. liars.
and other folyes. Or by the mouth in folly spekyng. in oner much drynkyng and
etynge. Or by the nose in ouermoche delytyng him self in sweet odours or
wicked odours. Or by folyly touching in him self. or in his wife. or in other
that is werse. be it man or be it woman / Also a person ought to confess him
of the oultrageous array of his robes and of his garments in hosyng and
shoyng. and of all other defautes. of which he has mind. And thus the
confession is good and hool. when one says all his sins great and little.
and this is the fourth condycyon that ought to be in confession. The fyfthe
condycyon is that one ought for to confess him humbly / For the synnar speaks
to god which sees al his heart. Then the confessor is but the ere of god
and that which he hereth. ne knows not as a man^ but as god. And the synnar
ought to tell his sins with great dread. and ought to opene his heart and
pour it abroad that it flow over. like as one shedeth out a full pot of
water wha^ the water is poured out there abides no colour^ as does of milk
ne odor. as of wyn ne savor ne taste as of hony^ thus should no thing be
retained of the sin. sithe it has be said in confessyon^ Ne the color. That
is an evil manner that is had in spekyng. or in byholdyng / or in following evil
company. or in other thing that has color of sin. Also one ouzt to leave
the savor and taste of sin. he reteyneth the savor of synne^ that thinks
on the sins that he has done / And delyteth him in the remembrance of them
and pleseth him / But he ought for to think upon them in great dread. that he
fall never no more in them. And also he ought to remember them in great sorrow.
And he ought for to confound him in him self / and to have great shame tofore
god of his sins. And ought to have ferme purpoos that he should never return
to his sins though he should be desmembred. Also he ought to leave and fle the
odor. There been so^me that leave well their sins. but yet they here gladly
spoken of them. but who that well repents him / will not gladly here speak of
them but he ought to have great abhomynacyyon of them. The vj co^dycyon is
that one ought ost to confess him for many reasons. First for to get more
gretter grace and more merit against god. like as the lynnen cloth which is
often wasshen / is the more white. Also for the venyall sins that one falls
in often / he ought to wasshe him. Also for to chase and drive away the devil
fro him. and for to be out of his thraldom and of his net. The bird
wythdraweth him and departs gladly fro the place where as his neste is broken
and deffeated / and fro thens that his eggs been taken away. Also for to
learn forto confess him well. For the usage makes a master. like as it
appyereth in these crafts. Also by cause that one knows not if he have be
well sorry and well repentaunte / therefore he ought to have recours unto his
confessour^ and to confess him of all things suffysaun^lye Also for to humble
him self. for to get the more grace and more merit ayenste god. wherefore one
demanded of a monk wherefore he confessyd him so often. and he answerd^ by
cause said he that I have always fere that I be not well confessed. and also I
remember me often of so^me things that I have not said in confession by
forgetyng. and also by cause that after my confession I find my self always
the more humble and meke / Now have thou herd how one ought to confess him.
Now ought thou to know that five things specially e^pesshe and letten
very confessyo^. The first is shame that one dare not say ne tell his sin
for shame^ and this makes the devil. that puts shame tofore for to close
his mouth like as a thief does / which that casts unto the hounde a little
glewe. by cause he should not bark ne baye / For the litel glewe is of such
nature that it makes an hounde dombe and to be stylle when it is put in his
throat. but the synnar ought to think that the shame that he has to tell his
sin / is a great part of his penance and of thamende. Also the synnar ought
gladly to suffer and drink a little shame for to escape the great shame. that
al synnars shall have at the day of Judgment when all the world shall see al their
sins / The ij thing is evil dread to do great penance. the which the devil
puts in the ere of the synnar saying. thou may not do this sharp
penance. and thou may not leave thy customs. Such people resemble the shough
horse which is aferde of the shadow that he sees. And certeynlye this penance
that we do here in this world is but a shadow to the regard of the pains of
hell or of purgatory. The third thing is the wicked love that the synnar
has enlaced that he loves so much his delight that he will not les^e it. and
thinks that for no thing he will confess him. but slepeth in his sin like
a swyn in the dunge. The iiij thing is hope of long life. whereof the devil
says to him. thou art a young man. thou shall live long. thou shall well
recoure a confessor. but he takes none head ne sees not the death that
awayteth him and shall take him sonner than he weneth / for god which promyseth
pardon to him that repents. promytteth not to morn as saint Gregory says /
Then the devil plays often with the synnar^ like as the catte does with the
mous when he has taken him. For when he has long played he strangleth and
sleeth him. The v thing is despayr. in which the devil puts the synnar. but
he ouzt to remember that god fory^ueth to them that repent lightly and more
gladly he gives pardon than we demand him. After the confession comes the
satysfaction. That is thamendes and the penance that one ought to make and
pray for his sin. after tharbytrement and will of the confessour^ which
ought to Judge the amends of the trespaces / In fastings. In almesses. or in
prayers. or in other good things after that the sin requires it. and the
seek man ought gladly to obey to the physycyan to have health / And the good
sone ought gladly to do the will of his ghoostly fader for the sauacyon of his
soul. Now have thou herd three things that holden together the hauberes of
penance. with which been armed the new knights of god for to vaynquysshe
the battle against sin / And who that shall vaynquysshe this bataylle shall not
retche of the second death. Like as Saint Johan says in thapocalypse. but he
shall have very rest. that is the glory perdurable. The first death of the
soul is to love sin. which is vaynquysshed by penance / by which one
escapes the second death / that is the death of hell. where one may not deye.
This is the first branch of the tree of prowess in them that vaynquysshe
sin. After this bataylle comes another. For when a man repents him of his
sin. then comes a new wrastlyng to his heart. what penance he may do.
and what life he may led / And there be many of them that in this bataylle be
recreaunte. For like as god says in the gospel. Now they believe. Now they
believe not. Now they will / now they will not. Now they purpose / Now is all
naught. For they be not ferme ne estable. ne perseueraunte. But when a man
Joins him to god / and affermeth his heart and his good purpoos to him /
then is this bataylle good and gotten / and then god makes him ferme and
stable as is a pyler in the church. as says saint Johan. This is the second
vyctorye and the reward that answers to him. after this wrastlyng comes the
iij wrastlyng that a man has to his flesh. which much complayneth wha^ it
begins to feel the hardness and sharpness of penance. and it reenforceth
to come ageyn to her old customs. the flesh is an evil wife. whereof salamo^
says. who most does the will of the flesh. the wers it is. and more is to
him contrary. And who that suffers his flesh to overcome him. he enters
and puts him self in great seruytude. For there is none so foul a thing as
to be ouercom of his flesh / who that vaynquyssheth this bataylle. god
promytteth to him a new crown whyt of chastyte and of Innocencye. and
brings him to rest / that is the glory perdurable like as he says in
thapocalypse. after this batayl comes this world and dame fortune with her
whele^ which assaylleth a man on the right side and on the lift side / which
been two strong bataylles. where as much people ben vaynquysshed / and moo be
vaynquysshed on the right side than on the lift side / like as dauyd says in
his psaulter. For more strong is the temptacion that comes of the right side.
than it that comes on the lift. as dauyd says in his psaulter. For more
strong is the temptacyon that comes of honor of rychesses and of delytes
which the devil offreth and sets before. tha^ that which comes of
aduersyte. like as pouertres and the maladyes and the sekenesses that god
sends / and he that vaynquyssheth and that despyseth with his heart the
prosperytees of this world. God promytteth to him honor and hyenesse in
glory. for he shall make him sytte with him in his trone as says thapocalipse
To him that shall vaynquysshe that other bataylle which is on the lift side in
thaduersytees of this world god promytteth glory which no man may take fro
him. The vj battle which is much strong / is against the wicked that been in
the world which ben the members of antecryste which warren against the good men
by their might. like as did of old time the tyrau^ts. against the marters and
good christian men. for uneath shall none dar reclame him christian for the
strength of Antecryst and of his members. This is the beast that Johan saw
that warryd the saints of which we have tofore spoken^ The members of this
be shown them in wicked princes and evil prelates. which by their great
couetyse defoule flee and eten their subgettes. so that the good men that been
under them have enough to suffer and many dyseases and great myschyeues^ But
they that take al in good pacyence without murmr as did Job. and trust al in
god they vaynquysshe this batayl. and to him that shall overcome it. god
promytteth to him that he shall give to him power over his enemyes^ like as
saint Johan says in thapocalyps. After all these bataylles comes the last
which is most strong. for the devil which is malycious and much subtyl.
when he sees that a man is mounted upon the moutayn of perfection. and has
ouercomen al these bataylles aforesaid. Then assaylleth him the fend by
vaynglorye / and by presumpcion. for then it seems to him that he is a much
good man. and great friend of god by this that he has al suffered for him by
which he falls sometime from hye to low as did lucyfer / and therefore it is
great necessyte that a man be wise. and that he keep him from the sin of
vaynglorye. which makes the ryergarde. For in the taylle lies often the
venym. and thenconforaunce. and sometime the ship that is nyghe to the port
peryssheth^ which went surely in the hye see. Then him byhoueth that he
tarry and address his saylle. That is al his entencyon and all his heart at
the port of health. That is to Ihesu Christ by the wind of fervent love and
of great desire of god. This is the hungre of Justice of which we have spoken
tofore. which comes of the yefte of strength and of the virtue of prowess.
As the good Knight which is noble and hardy / that has a good heart. and that
has been in many presses. which has great talente and great hungre to show
his strength in tournoyes or in bataylles for to get to him pryse and renomee
/ And certeynly who that has great love to god and great hungre and desire of
his health he ouercometh lyghtlye this last bataylle. he will not ne desires
not in this life. but that which is unto the honor and to the glory of God.
And to the health of his soul. and who that vaynquyssheth this bataylle shall
win the reward. of which saint Johan speaks in thappocalypse there where
our lord says. that to him that shall vaynquysshe he shall give to him to ete of
the tree of life. which is in the myddle of paradyse. That is Ihesu Christ him
self that gives life perdurable of which all the saints lyuen in the glory
of heaven. and al been fulfilled and been in rest / And this is the blessyng of
which the debonayr Ihesu Christ promytteth in the gospel to his good knights
when he said. blessed be they that have hungre and thyrste of Justice / that is
to serve god and to love him / For they shall be fulfilled of the fruit of the
tree of life. That is the end and the perfectyon of this virtue which is called
prowess. to which ledeth the yefte of strength.

Of the virtue of the yefte of counceyl. and of the good and merit that is
therein capitulo Cxxix
Like as the holy ghoost gives strength and vygour to empryse great things.
Right so yeueth he counceyl by which a person comes to a good end / of that
which he empryseth^ This is a great grace that the holy ghoost gives which
is called the yefte of counceyl. by which a man has great aduysemente and
great delyberacyon and aduys in all that. that he empryseth / and in that.
that he be not over hasty in his empryses. For like as says the phylosophre.
Great things be made and done not only by strength ne by arms but by good
counceyl / And another phylosophre which was named Socrates says that of
hasty counceyl men repent hem after. And therefore says Salamon do no thing
with out good counceyl / and after the deed thou shall not repent the. This
grace shows him in a man in three manners. First in sechyng gladly good
counceyl. thus thoby cou^ceylled his sone / Fair sone said he ask counceyl
always of a wise man. And Salamon says that there where as is no good
governor. the people faylleth anon and is anon destroyed / but it is sauf
when there been many good counceylles. and the wise Tullyus says that little is
worth the arms withouteforth / if there be not good counceyl wythinforth. But
keep the well says the scripture fro evil counceyllours / and cou^seylle the
not with fools. For they love no thing but that which pleseth them. and not
that which pleases god. Also the scripture counceylleth that one should ask
and seche counceyl of the old and auncyen men. and not of the young men which
ben not proved in the works. For in the auncyen men that have seen and proved
many things / is good wysdom and good counceyl. By cause that Roboas the sone
of Salamon left the counceyl of the old and auncyen men that were wise. and
took the counceyl of young men / he lost the most party of his royame. Also
who that has this yefte late him examyne and consydere the counceylles that be
given to him. and think with great aduysement if he be well counceylled and
truly / and not lightly to believe to the cou^ceyl of one man ne of tweyne / how
well that they be of his pryue friends / Therefore Seneke says that a wise man
examyneth his counceylles. and byleueth them not lightly. For he that byleueth
lightly. he fyndeth that he is often deceived. Also who that has this yefte. he
obeys to good counceyl when he fyndeth it. For for naught asks he counceyl.
that has no will to do thereafter. whereof says salamon. It seems to a fool
that he be in the right way. but the wise man hereth gladly good counceyl.
that is to say / that the wise man obeys to the good counceylles / which the
foles despise / The most prouffytable cou^ceyl that a man may have. is the
counceyl that our good master Ihesu Christ which is the fontayne of all
sapyence of whom comes all good cou^ceyl. that is in the holy gospel when he
says. if thou wylt be partyte. goo and selle all that thou have and give it
to the pour people. and come follow me / and thou shall have great tresour in
heaven / and behold and think who gives such counceyl. For he is as I say
the fontayne of sapyence. The very god that came in to therthe for to
counseylle the. and for tenseygne the the right way for to goo to paradys.
That is the path of pouerte of the spyryte. by which the holy ghoost ledeth
them whom he enlumyneth with the yefte of counceyl / Truth it is that in
another manner a man may be sauyd / As by the way of the commandments of
our lord to hold and keep them. One may be saved in marriage. or in wedowhode /
or in rychesses of the world when they be well used. But the holy ghoost by the
yefte of counceyl ledeth and conduyteth more right and more surely by the way
of very pouerte of the spyryte. by which one despyseth and put under foot all
the couetyse of the world for the love of god. this yefte takes away fro the
