heart the sin of auaryce and of couetyse / and so planteth the fair tree of
mercy. which is to have sorrow and compassyon of other men's harm / and of
other men's suffraunce.

Of the degrees of the virtue of mercy capitulo Cxxx
THis tree of mercy has seven degrees like unto the other^ by which it
grows and prouffyteth. These ben seven things which moeue much and draw a
man unto mercy. and to have compassyon of others harme^ The first thing that
moeueth a man to mercy is nature^ For as the book says which speaks of the
nature of beestes. No bird eteth another bird of his own nature / Ne a be
also eteth not another be of his own nature / Also the same book says that
a mare nouryssheth the fool of another mare. when she is deed. Also it has
often be seen and preuyd that a wulfe has nourysshed the whelps of another
wulfe / and has defended them fro other beestes. well then ought a man to
have pity and compassyon on another. of his evil and harm / which is
semblable to his nature. For we al be made of one matere and one form and one
image. The second thing that ought to draw a man to mercy and to compassyon
of another man's harm is grace. For we al be members of one body / that is of
holy church by grace / and one membre helps another naturelly. and has pity
and compassyon. Also we be bouzt and redeemed with one prys. that is with the
precious blood of Ihesu christ. that henge on the cross for to redeem us fro
death perdurable / when our saueour Ihesu Christ was then so pyetous and
mercyful toward us. well ought we then to have pity and compassyon one of
another. and to aid and socour that one that other. Also we ben al brethern of
fader and mother by faith and by grace / For we ben al sons of god and of holy
church. and the one brother ought to help that other when he sees it is need.
for at need is seen who is a friend. The third thing that ought to moeue a man
to mercy is the comandeme^t of the holy scripture which cou^ceylleth and
commands the works of mercy above all other things / whereof the wise
Salamon says. See well to says he that thy head be not without oylle. for by
thoylle that nouryssheth the fire and the lamp. is vndersto^den mercy. which
ought always to be in our tonnes. For in like wise as the oylle surmou^teth in
the lamp. above al other lyquours. Right so mercy surmou^teth the other
virtues. And also as the oylle nouryssheth and keeps the fire in the lamp.
and when the oylle faylleth the fire quenches. Right so mercy keeps the fire
of the love of god in the heart. and when mercy faylleth. the love of god
faylleth. Like as says saint Johan / who that shall see says he his brother and
his neighbor having disease and necessyte in need. and closes the door of his
heart. that is to say that he has no pity ne compassyo^. and helps him not if
he may. how says he^ shall the love and charity of god be in him. like as he
would say / That may not be. For the oylle of mercy is faylled in the lamp of
his heart / Also the good thobye taught his sone and said thus. Fair sone be
thou mercyful / as much as thou may / if thou have plente of goods give
gladly and largely. if thou have little yet of the same give gladly to the
pour. And our lord says in the gospel. Goo said he and selle all that thou
have and give it to the pour. This is the virtue that the holy scripture
prayseth most generally. And it is the virtue that most playseth god as the
scripture says. Hereof says god by the prophet. I will says he mercy and not
sacryfyse. And Saint austyn says that there is no thing that so much makes
a man amyable unto god as does pity. and to have mercy on other. Much people do
seruyse and sacrefyse to god in fastings or in pylgremages. or in sharp
penance of the body. but to do alms. they ben scarce caytyf and strayte.
Also much people of great estate to whom god has given largely of his
temporell goods do sacryfyse and seruyse not to god. but to the world. or to
the devil in that. that they dyspende folyly their goods in vanytees and in
oultrages / and in honors of the world. But for to give fo gods sake to the
pour they ben hard as ademont. Also like as mercy pleseth to god. right so
despleaseth it to the devil. For it is the armure and the virtue by which he is
most sonnest vaynquysshed. as is said in a gloss upon the psaulter / he may
not suffer the good odor of such an oyneme^te. No More than the crapaulde may
feel the smellyng or odor of the vygne. This odor might not Judas smelle ne
feel when the holy Maudeleyne enoynted the heed of Ihesu Christ with the
precious oynement. For it seemed to Judas that it was a thing lost. and had
lever the money that it cost in his purs by couetyse. Of such people that be
thus covetous and auarycyous is lord and master a devil that is called
closepurs / whom an holy hermyte saw. that he had the office to close and
shette the purses of covetous men. that they should not be opened to do
alms. The fourth thing that ought to moeue a man to mercy / is the great
largess of our lord / which gives largely to every man after that they be /
as says Saint James. and makes his son to shine upon the good and upon the
evil / like as it is said in the gospel. Sithe that the debonayr Ihesus is so
large to vs^ that he gives to us. and has given. all that we have that is
good. we ought to be large and curtoys that one anenste that other. For so
commands to us god in the gospel when he says / Be ye mercyful / like as
your fader of heaven is mercyful. He ought to resemble his fader. and ought to
ensyewe him when he is good and wise. Or otherwise he forsakes him. and
therefore says the wise man in scripture. Be ye mercyful and pyetous to the
pour and to the orphans like as thou were their fader or their mother / be thou
as their husbond. and thus shall thou be called the sone of god. The fyfthe
thing that ought to moeue a man to mercy is the honor of god. For as Salamon
says. he honors our lord that does well to the pour. For that which is
done to the pour. is don unto god like as him self witnesses in the gospel.
That which ye have done to one of the leest of my servants. ye have done to
me / this says god. The pour ben the little meyne of our lord. who so
honors them by the werkys of mercy he honors god. For who honors the
meyne he honors the lord. and who that does vylonye to the famylye and
servants. does vylanye to the lord. Hereof have we a fair and a good
ensaumple of the holy saint martyn. To whom god appyeryd in the night. after
that he had departed and given his mantel to the pour man. and he was couerd
with the said mantel. and god said to his angellys Martyn has clad me with
this vestement. The syxthe thing that ought much to moeue a man to mercy / is
the dread of the Judgment. For as says saint James Judgment without mercy
shall be do to him that does not the works of mercy. For like as god says in
the gospel. when the day of Judgment shall come / the sentence shall be given
against them that have not to their power done and accomplysshed the works of
mercy. For god shall leye a deef eere to them that now leye a deef eere to the
pour. like as it appyereth in the exaumple that he recounteth of the rich man
that would give none alms to Lazare / and by cause he refused to give to him
alms. god refused to him a drope of water when he was in the fire of hell /
In like wise did he to the folysshe vyrgyns that had none oylle in their
lamps. God closed to them the yate at the weddyng and said to them I know you
not. and so they abode without and came not in. Right so shall it be do at
the day of Judgment to the auarycyous and to the covetous men which have not
the conduytes of mercy which ledeth the souls to heaven. and makes to them a
ryzt way to come tofore god as holy scripture says. Like as way is made and
the yate opened to him that brings a present. Certeynlye acursed shall he be
by right to whom pity and mercy shall torn their back at the day of
Judgment. when god shall give sentence so ferme. stable. and dredefull For it
shall be so establysshed by Justice and confermed. that it shall never be
repeled. And then shall god do as souerayn pope bishop and king / cast out
his great excomynycacyon. For he is king and bishop as says the scripture.
for he took nature humayn in the lynage of kings and of bysshoppes This
excomynycacyon shall be cast upon them that shall be on the lift side. None of
them shall be except. They shall be wicked people whom god shall curse for their
sins and for their falsehede. Thus shall he say to them. Goo ye wicked and
cursed in to the fire of hell perdurably / which is ordained to thorryble
deuyls / and to them that have done their will. Alas this sentence how well
that it is short. certeynlye it shall be over anguysshous and over hard when
Ihesus Christ shall chase them out of his company. Such hard a departing
ought much to be doubted. The seventh thing that ought much to moeue a
person to mercy. is the fruit and the good that grows of this tree. which
appyereth in many manners First in that which mercy geteth pardon to synnars.
Of which mercy has the lettres of pardon and of Indulgence. For god says in
the gospel. Blessed be the mercyful. for they shall have mercy. After in the
same letter says he. if we pardone not that one the other / god shall not
pardone us. Also mercy is the good marchaunts purs. which wynneth oueral. and
never leseth. For as says saint Poul. mercy auaylleth to all things. A
precyouse stone should be much worth. that should be good for all things.
That is mercy which wynneth the goods temporell. the goods spyrytuell / and
the goods perdurable of glory. Of the goods temporell says salamon. honor
god of thy rychessys and of thy goods temporell give to the pour. and god
shall replenysshe thy garners of whete / and thy celyers of wine / But
understand well this word. that he says of thy rychessys and of thy goods /
and not the goods of other / as done sum that will do almesses of that
which they have taken fro other by force. by rauyne / by usure. or by other
evil cause. and maken often of other men's lether large thonges^ But of thyn
own propre good which thou hold truly honor god. For that other thou art
bounden to yield and render ageyn. Also he says that thou give to the pour
and not to the rich. and god shall yield to the an hundred double therefore.
like as he says in the gospel. Mercy is a seed that fructefyeth better in the
lene land than it does in fat. How that mercy multeplyeth the goods
temporell we have many fair ensaumples. of which I will remember so^me here.
It is said of saint Germayn of Ancerre^ that when he came fro Rome. as he went
out of melane. he demanded his deken if he had any money / he ansuerd that he
had but three pens. for saint Germayn had given all to pour people. Thennne
commanded saint Germayn to his deken that he should give tho iij pens to the
pour people. for god had well whereof to feed them that day. The deken with great
pain and grutchyng gaf ij peus / and retained the third penny / and as they
went on the waye^ the servant of a rich man brought to saint Germayn fro
his lord. CC shelynges / Then called saint Germayn his deken / and said to
him that he had stolen fro the pour a penny. For if he had given the third penny
to the pour. the knight had sent him CCC. shelynges. After it was said in the
way to Saint Germayn / that to saint Johan thamener came a gentylman which was
robbed of theuys so that he had no thing and told to saint Johan thamener his
caas. he had great pity and compassyon on him / and commanded his dyspencer
that he should give him / xv. pound. of gold. his dyspencer for couetyse gaf
him but / v / Anon a noble lady sent unto the said Saint Johan five. C. pound.
of gold. Then he called his dyspencer and demanded him how much he had
given to that man. He ansuerd and said that he had given him xv. pound. The
holy man said nay. and that he had given him but. v / pound. and when he knew
the troth by him that had received it^ he said to his dyspenser. that if he
had given that.xv. pound. Our lord had sent to him by the good woman.M. and.
v C. pou^de^ and when he demanded of the good lady whom he called to him. how
much she had given and left to him in her testament. She answered that she had
ordained a thousand and five hundred pound for to send him / And when she
saw the.M / pound raced and put out of the writing. she thought that god
would that she should send to him no more but v hundred pound. Also Saint
Gregoire reherceth of saint Bonyface. that fro that time that he was a child
he was so pyetous. that he gaf his sherte and his gown unto the pour. how be
it that his mother beat him often therefore. Now it happed that the child saw
many pour people that suffered much disease / he espied that his mother was not
at home. he ran to the garners. and all that his mother had assembled for the
year he gaf to the pour people. And when his mother came and knew what he had
don. she was as out of her wit. Then the child prayed our lord and the
garners were full of whete / Also there was a pour man as it is said that had
but one cow. which herd say of his curate in his sermon that god said in the
gospel / that a man should have an hundred fold double for all that he should
give for gods sake. The good man by the counceyl of his wife gaf his cow unto
his curate in hope to have an hundred kyen for his cow. And when he had long
tarried. and that promise abode long after / he wend that his curate had
deceived him. and thouzt that he should slay him. and aroose on a night for to
slay him and when he was in the way he fond a great mass of gold. and
then he thought that god had rendered and yelden his promise and returned in
pees.

Also of another pour man by cause that he had herd that god would so give an
hundred for one. he gaf his cow unto his curate which was rich. The priest
took gladly this cow and sent it to his pasture where as his other kyen were.
And at even the pour man's cow came ageyn home and brought an.C. kyen longyng
to the priest with her. when the pour man saw that he. thought that god had
kept his promise according to the gospel. and the said kyen were Iuged tofore
the bishop to the pour man against the priest. These ensau^ples toforesaid
shown well. that mercy is good marchau^dise for it e^creaceth well the goods
temporel. Also mercy e^petreth and geteth of god the goods spirituel and
perdurable / whereof saint Poule says that it auaylleth to all thing. For she
gives life and grace in this present life. and the life of glory without end
in that other. And therefore says Dauyd in his psaulter. that god loves mercy
and truth / For she gives grace in this world. and glory in that other.
Also mercy and alms keeps a man fro all perils and delyuerth him from
spyrytuel death / that is fro sin and fro the death of hell / For many deed
men have been raised to life by the works of mercy that have be done / whereof
there be many ensaumples in writing of the lives of saints. that is of the
death perdurable of hell. Therefore said Thobye to his sone / Be thou said he
pyteous and mercyful as much as thou may. For alms delyuerth and keeps
fro all sin and fro the death of hell. and defends the soul that it goo
not in to the derknesse of hell. Now have thou herd the branches and the
degrees of mercy. by which she grows and prouffyteth. Now the byhoueth to
see the branches of this tree. by which she mounteth. and by which it
descends.

Here after folowen the brannches of the virtue of mercy and of alms capitulo
Cxxxj
THis tree has moo branches tha^ the other toforesayd. for it extends more
than the other / whereof there been branches on the ryzt side and on the lift
side. On the right side ben the works of mercy which touch the soul. They
ben the spyrituel works of mercy. on the lift side ben the bodyly works of
mercy which apperteyne to the body. on the right side be vij branches The
first is to give good counceyl to them that have need. and only for the love
of god purely. not for to coueyte other thing temporel therefore. as done these
advocates and men of law that taken with both hands / and of that one party
and of that other. And given often times many evil counseylles for to have
money. or for yeftes. or for dread. or for favor of rich men. but they that
have god tofore their eyes. and counceyl the synnars to leave their sin and
save them. Or they that be out of sin. to keep them. to the^de that they
fall not thereto ageyn like as confessors ought to do and the prelates. and
the good men in what someuer estate they be / they done the first work of
mercy spyrytuel. and this is the first branch of the right side / The second
branch is to teache and enseygne them that a man has to govern. As a prelate
his subgettes whom he ought to feed with good doctrine. and with good
ensaumple / In like wise ought the master do to his dyscyples in doctrine in
science and in good manners. Also the faders and the moders their children in
such wise that they keep them fro sin and vices. and that they accustom
them to do well. and that they keep them fro lye^g. fro sweryng. fro evil plays
and games and fro evil company / and specially the children of great lords
and of rich men ouzten to be best informed in good manners For the children will
all way hold their first form / And therefore they ought to be informed to
do well. The third branch is to reprehende and chastyse the fools and the
wicked people of their folyes. and this apperteyneth specially to the prelates
and to the princes which oughten to chastyse their subgettes / when they know
that they be wicked. For when they suffer the sins where they might amend
them and will not. they ben partyners^

Ne no prince ne prelate ought not to suffer any wickedness in a man about
him if he may know it / For if he have about him evil and wicked meyne and if
he knows it or supposes. if he remedy it not / It is a sign that he is no
good man. for it is comynly said. such lord such meyne. and after the lord
the meyne follow. and oftymes it happeth that the lord is deffamed by his evil
meyne. and therefore / ne for hauoyr. ne for favor ne for famyliarite of
persons a lord ouzt not to doubt to take away the sins that been about
him. For he ought to doubt more god and to love him. than any man mortal / Me
ought to love the persons and hate the sins. and every prince. prelate. and
lord ought to know that ygnoraunce in this part shall not excuse them. For
they be bounden to know how their people govern them in their houses and in
their offices. and ought tenquyre by good men and true. and that dread god and
love him. For they shall not be quyte at day of Judgment for to say that they
know not thereof. The fourth branch of mercy is for to comfort the seek men.
and them that been in trybulacyon or in aduersyte or in maladye. and to help
them to their power. and to comfort them by good words that they fall not in
despayr or dyscomfort. and that their heart faylle them not. Thus commands
Saint Poul that says. Comfort them that be feeble of heart. And Salamon says
that he that is in disease of heart shall be glad and Joyous for to here a good
word. Also as he him self says. like as a person delyteth him and takes
playsyr in good odoures. in like wise delyteth the soul in great sweetness of
good counceyl and in the good words of a very friend / That is he that loves
also well in aduersyte as in prosperyte. For at need is seen who is a friend /
and in aduersyte is the good and true friend proved. and thou ought to
know that iiij things comfort much a man / which is in aduersyte. in
trybulacyo^ or in maladye. The first thing is to think on the pains of hell.
which ben so much hard sharp and horrible. that it nys but a shadow and an
enoyntyng all that that may be suffered in this world to the regard of the
pains of hell / whereof saint austyn says to our lord. O good lord brenne me
here and hew me al in pyeces. rather than thou dampne me perdurably. Also
Saint austyn says that the torments of saint Bertylmewe which was flayn al
quycke. of saint lawrence and of Saint vyncent which were burnt roasted and
laid on gredyrons / and of Saint steven which was stoned to death. Al these
torments ne ben but a bayne to the regard of the pains of purgatory. And
therefore the rod of chastysement of our lord must be suffered for teschewe the
perdurable pain of hell. God shows great semblaunt of love to them. to
whom he sends the aduersytees temporelle. for he says. I chastyse them that
I love / note this ensau^ple. The ox that shall be slain shall be well kept and
made fat. but he that shall be kept and live. is put to the yocke for to
labor the earth / A great sign of love shows the king and great honor
does he to him / to whom he sends his cup to drink of. The cup of our
lord of which he drank ben the trybulacyons. thaduersytees and the myschyefs
of this world^ This is the first sauce. with which one ought to ete such
mete. that is to think on the pains of hell. This is a sauce of vynaygre.
which takes away the savor of wine of the delyces of this world / Like as
the vynaygre takes away the savor of good wyn / The second thing that much
comfort in suffryng pacyently trybulacion. is to think on the reward of
heaven that one geteth. for like as says saint Gregory. that allegeth and
asswageth much the pain and the trauaylle. when a person has an hope to
have great reward and great prouffyte^ The third thing is to think on the
passion of Ihesu christ. which suffered death for to redeem us fro the pains of
hell. there is no thing that so much allegeth and swageth the pains and the
trybulacions of this world. This is much well sygnefyed to us in holy
scripture. there where as the children of Israhel came to a water. which was
so bitter that they myzt not drink. Then showed god to moses the prophet a
staf of tree / and said to him that he should put it in to the water that was so
bytter^ And when he had put it therein. it was all sweet. The bitter waters been
the trybulacyons of the world. The staf of tree that made it sweet. that is the
cross on which the debonayr Ihesus was hanged on for us. For who that
remembers well this sorrow that he suffered on the cross / There is no pain ne
aduersyte ne trybulacyon temporal. but it is sweet and light to suffer. The
fourth thing is to think on the spyrytuel goods that the trybulacio^s done to
them that suffren them pacyently for the trybulacyons prouen the knight of god.
A knight knows not well his stre^gthe. unto the time that he has been in
bataylle and in the prees. whereof saint Poule says / that pacyence proves a
man / and an au^gel of heaven said to Thoby. because that thou were playsau^t to
god / It byhoueth that temptacion should prove the Also trybulacions purge the
soul as the fire purges gold in the fornays. and as the flaylle the corn
when it beteth it. and as the hamer the iron as says saint Gregorye. Also
trybulacyons ben the medecynes that hele the maladyes of sin. For like as
says the holy scripture. The grievous maladye makes a man sobre. whom sin
has made dronken oftymes whereof saint Gregorye says. late it not be hard to
the that thou suffer disease on thy body. when thou art guarysshed of the
maladye of sin wythinforth^ Also by tribulacions is won the crown of
glory. when one has good pacyence. whereof saint James says / blessed is that
man that suffers temptacions. that is aduersyte and tribulacion. like as a
good knight that suffers the strokes^ for when he shall be well assayed and
preued. he shall have the crown of glory. These iiij remembrau^ces aforsayd
comfort much them that been in trybulacion. The vspyrituel brau^che of mercy
is to pardone his maltalente and evil will to every body. For like as saint
Gregory says / who gives his pens or his al^^sse to the pour and pardons
not his evil wylle^ his alme^^e is nothing worth. For god receives not the
yefte as long as the felo^nye is in the heart. for god weyeth. preyseth. and
takes the yefte after his will / And therefore our lord says in the gospel /
If that we forgive not each other / our fader of heaven shall not forgive us our
synnes^ Then he that will not pardonne and foryeue says against him self. as
often as he says the pater noster. for he prays that god pardonne hym^ like
as he pardonneth his evil will to other. It is said of the emperor theodose /
that he held it for a great shame. if one did to him vylouye or Iniurye that
prayed him to forgive him. and when he was most angry. then he foryafe most
sonnest. For he had lever draw^ to him people by debonayrte and by love. than by
dread / The vj branch of this virtue is to have in the heart pity and
comyassyon of the synnars. and of them that be in trybulacyon or in pouerte. or
in aduersyte / For that one membre ought to bear the maladye of that other
whereof Saint Poule says. who that is seek. and I am seek with him / And Saint
Gregory says. that so much is a man more parfayt. as he feleth more in him
self the sorrow of another. The vij branch of myserycorde is to pray for the
synnar and for his enemies / and for all trespasses / For so comandeth our
lord in the gospel / Pray ye said be for them that done to you evil. and so
shall ye ben the sons of your fader which is in heaven / as who should say /
Otherwise ye ben not the sons of god. and then ye have no thing in his
heritage. Now is it then great alms and great prouffyte for the soul to
pray for the synnars. for his enemies. and for all them that been departed out
of this world. These ben the vij branches of mercy of this tree on the right
side.

Here after folowen the seven branches of mercy upon the lift side capitulo
Cxxxij
Like as this tree of mercy has seven branches on the right side. so ben
there seven branches on the lyte side / These ben the vij works of mercy
corporel. which holden the body. like as the other byholden the soul before
said.

The fyyrst brau^che is to feed the hungry the nedy and the mys^ased / and this
admonesteth us the holy scripture in many places. First Thobye which said to
his sone / Ete thy bread with the nedy and the pour that deye for hungre. and
Salamon says. if thyn enemy have hungre give him to ete. and if he have
thyrst give him to drink. Also our lord says in the gospel. when thou shalt
make a great dinner. call the pour people. the blind. the lame and the
Impotent and thou shalt be blessed. For they may not yield it to the ageyn.
But god shall yield to the in the ressurection generalle. and an hundred fold
double. This is ayenste rich men that done grere oultrages of mete. for
bobaunce / pride / and vaynglorye of the world and have no pity on the pour
people. But they ought to have great dread that they fall not in meschyef. like
as it byfel to the rich gloton / of whom god says in the gospel. which ete
every day delycyously and plentyuously. and suffered the pour Lazare deye for
hungre at his yate / But as to the death of that one and of that other was a
great change. For lazare was borne with aungellys in to Abraham's bosom / and
the rich man auarycyous and gloton had his sepulture in hell. where he
desired to have one drope of water for to refresshe his tongue. Alas if all the
water of the sea had run over his tongue. it should not have been coled in that
fire perdurable of hell which may not be quenched. Therefore it is good to
feed the pour people. For there by may one escape fro the pains of hell. and
win the glory of heaven. like as says holy scripture. whereof our lord shall
say at day Judgment. Come ye blessed of my fader in to the royame of heaven
which is ready to you. For when I had hungre and thyrst ye yafe to me to ete
and to drink / For that which ye did to the least of my pour people. ye did it
to me.

The second branch of mercy capitulo Cxxxiij
THe second branch of mercy is to clothe the pour naked people. That is to
say that he that may should give to them clothyng hosen and shoon. Thus taught
Thobye his sone when he said. Cover the naked with thy gown / and Ysaye the
prophet says. when thou shall see the pour naked couere and hele him. For
such work saint Peter raised that good woman named Dorcas. For she clothed
the pour people as the scripture says / Hereof have thou a fair example of
saint Martyn as I have said tofore. The gown or vesture or what someuer
alms one gives to the pour. is a memoryal to them that pray for him that
has given it / And is represented to god of his angellys.

The third brau^ch (...) mercy capitulo Cxxxiiij
THe third (...) mercy is to lene to the pour people at their need. and to
(...) to them the debt that they owe when they may not (...) / For it is not
only alms to give. but it (...) alms to lene without vsure^ and any
prouffyte (...) evil entencyon. but purely for gods love. In (...) to
pardonne and quyte his debt / when (...) and may not pay it. and this is that
whych^ (...) commands in the old law. where he says. if one of thy
b^ethern fall in pouerte thou shall not enhard thy heart. ne wythdrawe not thy
hand fro him / But thou shall opene it to the pour. and shall lene to him
that whereof he has need / And our lord says in the gospel. lene says he to
him that has need and that requires the. without hope of wynnyng any
temporell thing. and god shall render to the an hundred fold double in glory.
This matter is ayenste the usurers. that will always have more than they lene. in
money or in seruyces. or in other things. But god commands to lene to the
pour nedy purely for his love. and he shall render to the an hundred double.
and to the pour man to whom thou have lent. or that owes to the. or that
may not pay to the. thou ought to foryeue and pardone him. For so
commands to the god in the gospel / and says thus / if ye foryeue not each
other / god shall not foryeue you. And hereof God shows an ensaumple of an evil
servant to whom his lord had pardonned his debt. and by cause he would not
pardone him that ought to him / The lord repelyd the curtosye and bounte that
he had done to him. and did do dystrayne and held him till that he had rendered
all that he ought. Right so shall our lord do. if we foryeue not each to other.

The fourth branch of mercy capitulo Cxxxv
THe iiij branch of mercy is to vysyte / comfort. and to aid the seek people
/ That is a work that much pleseth to god^ and more than trauaylle. or
fasting. or other bodily penance. whereof we find in vitis patrum. that an
hermyte demanded of one of the au^cyent faders. the which was of most
grettest merit / of him that fasted vj days in the weke and trauaylled and
labored with his hands. or of him that served the seek malades. The good
fader answered that he that fasted and trauaylled though he henge by the
nosethrylles might not compare to him that served the seek people / This work
auaylleth much to eschew synne^ and is a great remedy against sin. And
therefore says Job. vysyte thy semblable. that been the seek men that been
semblable to the in nature For they be men as thou art. and if thou so do. god
shall keep the fro sin for to do such a good work. And saint James says
that it is a relygyon holy and clean tofore god to vysyte the orphans. the
seek and pour men / the wydowes and them that been in trybulacyon / whereof is
recounted of a much great synnar which went over the sea unto the isle of
roodes. and put him self in an hospytal for to awayte and serve the seek people
/ and it happed on a time that he had great abhomynacyon of a seek man of whom
he wesshe the feet. Anon al ageyn his heart he drank of that water his full
draught / And when he had dronken. he felt a right sweet and good smellyng
odour^ and this was a great token and sign that his sins were pardonned by
this good work / Also by this work is gotten great perfectyon of holy life.
whereof the wise man says in holy scripture / be thou not ennoyed to vysyte the
seek people / For by that thou shall be confermed in the love of god Also thereby
is gotten great reward as is said in the gospel^ whereof is told that a lady
named Marye which was a much holy woman converted her husbond so much. that
they left all that they hadden. and went to the mesell hows for to serve the
seek malades. by which they came to great perfectyon / After it was showed to
the same Marye. that her husbond that had been her fellow in humylite for to
serve the seek men and wymmen / should be her fellow in the glory of heaven. Of
the same our lord gives us ensaumple in the gospel that he touched the seek
people and heled them. The servant ought not to have desdaygne ne shame to
vysyte the seek people ne to serve them. when the lord of heaven came in to this
world for to serve and vysyte them. Of whom he took the form. and semblaunce
of his servant. This says saint Poul for to serve us that were seek by sin.

The fyfthe branch of mercy capitulo Cxxxvj
THe fyfthe branch of mercy is to herberowe the way faryng men. the pour
people. and the pilgrims that have no lodgyng / This is one of the works of
mercy that pleseth much to god / as it appyereth by ensaumples of holy
scripture. First Abraham received oftymes the aungellys of heaven in semblau^ce
of pour pylgryms / and they promised to him that his wife Sarra which was old
and barayn should conceive a sone. Loath by cause he received the pour and kept
hospytalyte he received the angellys which kept and delyuerd him fro the
peril of sodom. and therefore says Saint Poule let us not leave hospytalyte.
for thereby many good men have been much playsaunt to god and in his love and in
his grace / for they received aungellys instead of the pour. It is not
meruaylle if such people receive angellys / For they receive our lord like as
he says in the gospel. For who receives them receyuen him as he says / and
that which is done to the pour is done to him. whereof saint Gregory
recounteth of a good man which was much pyteous and gladly received the pour
people in to his house. he received on a day the pour like as he had be
acustomed / and when he had supposed to have given water to a seek man that was
there. as soon as he turned him. he that was in lykenes of the pour man
vanysshed. and none knew where he bycam. whereof he much meruaylled. And the
night after our lord apperyd to him and said. that he had on other days
received him in his members. but on that day he had received him in his propre
person. Also hospytalite is better and more worth than abstynence or any other
labor / whereof is found in vitis patrum that in egypt was an holy fader
which received all them that passed forth by that had need. and gaf to them
such as he had. It happed that a man of much great abstynence was herberowed
in his lodgyng. which would fast / and would not ete at the prayer of the good
man that had received him Then the good man that had lodged him said to him.
late us goo fair brother under that tree there without. and pray we to our
lord that this tree enclyne and bow donn at the prayer of him that best
pleases god. and when they had made their prayers / the tree enclyned down to
him that received the pour people. and not to him that made the great
abstynences. there been many moo fair examples of hospytalyte but it should be
over long a thing to reherce.

The syxthe branch of mercy capitulo Cxxxvij
THe vj branch of mercy is to vysyte comfort and aid them that been in
prison and in hold. and them to deliver if they may. For to do this
admonesteth us thappostle poule that says. Remember ye them that been in
prison. like as ye were bounden with them. that is to say that ye vysyte them.
comfort and aid them. like as ye would that ye were comforted vysyted and
helped if ye were bounden in prison as they ben / Thus did Thoby which went
to them that were in prison. and comforted them with good words / And salamon
says in his proverbs. Deliver thou them says he^ that men led to dye. In
such wise delyuerd danyel s^sanne fro death. And our lord delyuerd the woman
that had be taken in aduoultrye^ which should have be stoned to death after the
law / not for by cause that Justice should not be done upon malefactors. But
in such deed and fayt he taught the Iuges what they should be. and how they
ought to Judge other. whereof in this ensaumple he enseygneth four things that
every Judge ought to have and keep in Judgment. The first thing is great
delyberacyon / and great aduysement of counceyl good and hool / whereof Job
says. The cause that I knew not. I enserched it and required right dylygently
/ and this is to understand in that. which our lord when the Jews had
accused the woman. he wrote in the earth with his fyngre. he that is without
sin of you. throw the first stone / For to stone the woman^ And by the
scripture made with the fyugre we understand dyscrecyon and great delyberacyon.

The second thing is good entencyon that he bow not ne enclyne more on that
one party than on that other. ne for prayer ne for yefte. ne for favor. ne
for love. ne for hate. and this is to understand in that when Ihesu Christ
wrote he held him stylle in the place. The third thing is good life and to
keep him well fro sin. For he that Iugeth other ought to be of good life / and
of good conscience. and live Justly. For if he be other he ought to have great
dread of the Judgment of god. which says in the gospel. that such Judgment
as ye do to other. shall be done to you / And Saint poul says thus of evil
Iuges In that thou Iugest other. thou condempnest thy self. For thou do
that. for which thou Iugest other. whereof our lord said when he aroose fro
writing / he of you that is without sin cast on her the first stone. and
when they herd this sentence. they departed and went away al ashamed. the one
after another without taking leave. for they were gretter synnars than the
woman. whom they would have stoned / The fourth thing is to have pity and
compassyon. that the Judge ought to have on him that he shall Judge. for he ouzt
more to enclyne by humanyte and mercy than tenharde him by rygour to do Justice
/ For Justice without mercy is cruelte. and mercy without Justice is lewdnes.
And therefore that one of these ij virtues holds often company with that other
in holy scripture. But always says the scripture / that mercy surmounteth
Justice. And saint Johan with the golden mouth says. that at the day of
Judgment. that it shall be more worth to render reason of doing mercy. than of
the rygour of Justice. and Saint James says that Judgment without mercy shall
be done to him that has do no mercy And therefore our lord after that he was
relyeued he enclyned him toward therth. and after delyuerd the woman. for the
Judge ought to enclyne by pity and compassyon to hym^ whom he ought to Judge /
and have great dread / and also against his will ought he to Judge the other.
For if he Judge wyckedly he shall be Iuged at the day of Judgment. Now is it
great alms to vysyte the prisoners / and them to redeem and deliver that
may. And therefore our lord Ihesu Christ would descend in to hell for to deliver
the souls of saints that were there.

The vij branch of mercy capitulo Cxxxviij
THe seventh branch of mercy is to burye the deed bodies. Of this work is
much preysed in holy scripture Thobye. which buried the deed bodies and left
his mete. And our lord praised Marye Magdalene for the oynemente that she
shed on his heed. whereof he said that she had done it in sygnefyaunce of his
sepulture. Also Joseph demanded the body of our lord / and buried it much
dylygently. The other were right besy of their sepulture^ and had great
bewayllyng and great devotion to the holiness. good. and holy life. of their
faders. and therefore they would be buried with them / Of whom Jacob said to his
sone Joseph. Burye me not in egypt. but with my faders. and therefore it is good
to be buried emonge good relygyous men for to have their prayers Nature ought
to moeue a man to this good work. whereof it is read in the nature of beestes
that the dolphyns wha^ they see a dolphyn deed. they assemble them to gydre /
an bear him to the bottom of the sea. and there they burye him / If nature and
pity moeue and stir the Jews and Sarasyns. and other myscreauntes to do
this. much more ought pity and compassyon to moeue the christian men to do
thus. why he by our faith see that the bodies be raised and rewarded with the
souls. And therefore who that loves the soul of his neighbor he ought to
love the body / and do burye it when it is d^ed with all humanyte and mercy
that he may / Now have thou herd the branches of the tree of mercy. These
been the works of mercy corporell and spyrituel /

Here after is said how alms ought to be done Cxxxix
IT is so that there is much people that lose their alms and their other
good deeds which they do / by cause they do them not as they ought to do.
Therefore I will show here shortly how alms ought to be done and how it is
prouffytable and playsaunte to god / First I wyl^ show shortly how a person
ought to do alms. and whereof he should do alms. For a man must do it of
his own good. and not of another man's. and of such good that is well and truly
gotten. God sets no thing of none evil yefte. Alms which is made of
theft. or of taking away of others good. of ra^yne. or of usure. or of other
evil gooten good pleases no thing to god. whereof the scripture says. Thou
shalt not make sacrefyse ne offryng to god^ of oxen ne of sheep. ne of thing
wherein is any spotte of sin. For god has great abhomynacyon of such
sacrefyse / The wise man says. that who that does sacrefyse to god of the
catayl or goods of the pour man. He does like to hy^ that s^e^th the sone
tofore the eyes of his fader. And Saint Austyn says what yefte is that /
which the one takes gladly^ and that other wepeth And therefore ought every
man take heed whereof he does his alms. Also he ought to take heed to whom
he does it whereof the scripture says / Beware to whom thou shalt do good.
do well to the good. That is to him that thou wenest that he be good. And give
no thing to the wicked for cause of their wickedness. Like as they do
which give to rybauldes and to menestrellys for their wyckednesse^ which is a
great sin as say the saints. but who that gives to them not for evil. but
for pity and compassyon. for their pouerte. or of their wives. or of their
children if they have any. or of their faders or moders. or for any other good
cause or reason / as for to wythdrawe them fro sin he does well Then the
alms ought to be given unto the pour / and more to them that be very pour
of heart and of will which have left for gods sake that which they had.
much more than to other that be not pour with their will. but sometime of
pure necessyte. And sum there be trewauntes and slouful for to do any good /
and might get their living if they would. And sum there be that by fayntyse
show sum hurtes and be faytours of them self that deceive the world. To
such ought a man not to give his alms. but it ought to be given to the
pour orphans. to shamefast people to pour wydowes. to the dyseased and lame /
and unto seek pour people where as it is need / and when one may do it And if
a man is bounden to give to strangers / he is much more bounden without
comparyson to his fader and mother more than to any other / For nature enseyneth
it. And God commands it. It is read of the storkes. that they nourysshe
fader and mother when they be old and may not purchase their mete. Then
nature techeth that one ought to do good to his fader and mother. and therefore
it is well ryzt and reason that myschyef fall to al them that do evil to their
faders and moders as it oftyme happeth. Also a person ouzt to take heed how he
ought to do alms and the manner of gyuyng. For iij condycyons ought to be had
in gyuyng alms The first is that a man ought to give gladly and with good
heart. For god has more regard to the heart than to the hands. whereof god in
his sacrefyse as saint gregory says / beholds not only the thing that is
given. but with what heart / Like as hit appyereth well in the gospel of the
pour woman that had no more but two mytes which she offeryd in the temple. And
our lord said / that she had offered more than all the other which had offered
great things. for more playseth sometime to god a penny that a pour man gives
gladly for gods sake. than if a rich man had given an hundred mark of
silver in grudchyng. And therefore says the wise man in the scripture. Make
always says he good chyere in all thy yeftes. And Saint Poul says that god
loves much the yeuar that is glad and curtoys. There been so^me people right
rich and be so rude and vylaynous to the pour. that when they demand hem
alms. they answer to them so vylaynously / that they call them truau^tes.
and say to them many reproaches and vylonnyes. Such alms pleseth not god
and therefore says the wise man in holy scripture. Enclyne and bow thyn eere
to the pour man without heaviness / and answer him swetelye. The second
thing that apperteyneth to do alms. is that it be done anon and hastelye.
whereof Salamon says say thou not to thy friend. goo and come ageyn to morne^
and then I shall give to the / when thou may give anone^ And also god says.
withdraw not long thy yefte fro the pour and fro them that be nedy. That is
to say^ make thou not him abide. when thou may give forthwyth / This is
ayenste many rich men which make pour men to cry after them. that have to
do with them. And so much delay them that they must often pray and require
them tofore that they will any thing do / They selle over dear their bounte
and curtosye. that they do to them / for like as seneque says. nothing is so
dear bought as that which is required and the proverb says that it is over
dear bouzt that is demanded Thus should every man hastily do for his soul. as
long as he is alive and hool. whereof the wise man says. Fair sone says he do
well to thy self if thou have whereof. and offer to god worthy offrynges as long
as thou lyuest / For the death shall not tarry but that she comes / And in
another place he says do well to thy friend tofore thy death. that is to thy
soule^ to whom thou ought to do well tofore thy death. as to thy true friend
/ that is to Ihesu Christ to whom thou ought to do well. tofore thy death in
almesses for the love of him to the pour people / For that which is done to
the pour people is done to Ihesu christ. like as he says in the gospel. Then
the alms that is done in a man's life and in his hele. is much more
auaylable. than that which is ^oon after his death / like as the lantern that
is borne before a man conduyteth and ledeth him better and more surely. than
that which is borne behind his backe^ and therefore admonesteth us saint
Poule. that we do well as long as we have the time that god has lent us when
a rich man or lord is coming unto a cite or town. he sends his messagers
tofore and his herbegeours for totake his lodgyng. and for to make ready
prouysyon against his coming. or else the lord and his people should be evil
pourueyed. The good herbegeour and messager that takes the lodgyng and makes
al thing ready to rich men in the glory perdurable been the almesses and
other good deeds that they do in their lives which ben represented by the
aungelles tofore god / The almesses that been don after the deth^ ben like as
the slow servants that comen late to the lodgyng / so that the lord is
sometime evil pourueyed and evil herberowed. The third condycion that ought to
be in alms. is that one ought give gladly and largely. after that he may
forbere at his ease / whereof the wise man says. give to god after that he has
given to the. And Thobye says also. after thy power be pyteous and merciful.
if thou have much give largely and gladly. and if thou have little depart of
that little with a good will. and every man ought to give after his estate /
and after that god has given him / It is read of a king. of whom a pour
man axed a penny / and he answered / that so little a yefte apperteyned not to him
which was a king. and of alysaunder it is read. that he gaf a cite to one his
servant / And the servant thought the yefte over great a thing for him and
would have refused it. Then alysaunder said to him I have no regard what is
conuenyent to the for to take. but to me what I ought to give. The fourth
condycyon is that the alms be don in humylite and in devotion. / to the end
that there be no vaynglorye therein. ne that the pour people to whom the
alms is given be not despised. ne for alms done with other men's goods /
ne to give for to sin / ne for to have presumpcyon thereby to be saved / Sum
people there ben that when they do alms they will that every body know it /
But the scripture says that alms should be put in the bosom of the pour.
For as says saint Gregory. It ne suffyseth only to a good man that he see of
whom he attends his reward. and therefore says our lord in the gospel. when
thou shall give thyn alms says he. late not thy lift hand know what thy
right hand does so that thyn alms be hyd. for to eschew the loos and
praysyng of the world. and thy fader of heaven which sees in hyd place shall
reward and yield it to the. That is to say when thou shall do thyn alms.
keep the well that vaynglorye which is vnderstonden by the lift hand be not
meddled therwyth. but do thy alms in true entencyon. that is vndersto^den by
the ryzt hand I say not but that one ought to do good works sometime openly
tofore the people for to give good ensau^ple / whereof god may be praised / For
right so says god in the gospel. that we should do good works tofore the
people. by cause that god should be preysed and gloryfyed. and not for the
preysyng of the people as done the ypocrites. A good servant ouzt to be
ashamed to serve his lord tofore the people / for to honor him. whereof our
lord says. who that shall have shame of me tofore the people. he shall have
shame of me tofore thau^gels^ and I shall have shame to see him. This is good
against hem that leave to do well openly. by cause they would not be reputed
ypocrytes. And therefore says Saint Gregory. that who that does his werkys
openly / that the entencyon be right to god wythinforth^ And that do it to
please god only. Also who that will do alms he ought not to despise the
pour to whom he does alms. Therefore says the prophete^ ne despise not
thy flesshe^ That is the pour man which is semblable to the. and of such
nature of flesh and blood as thou art / and of such fylthe. There be so^me
people that despise the pour and deyne not to speak to them. and if they speke^
they speak rudely and proudely. Thus did not Job that said / that he never
despised them that passed by / for any thing that they did. but gaf t^ them
clothing and mete / Also there were holy men as well kings and other many
great lords that were not ashamed to serve the pour men. how well that sum
there be that do alms to the pour. but they have them in desdayn and in
despyte. and if they were very humble. they should love better the company of
pour men that been good. which ben pour for the love of god. and may edefye
them well by ensaumple. and by word. than many of the rich men that been
about them. where as is in them but flaterye. couetyse / and vanyte. and done
them much harm by evil counceyll. and let them for to do many good deeds.
Also there been sum people that do alms enough. but nevertheless they leave
not to do great sins. such almesses shall not save them. For if they deye
in that estate. their almesses shall never keep them fro dampnacyon. Then
such manner people been like to them that make their hows on that one side / and
depesshe and throw it down on that other side. and therefore scripture says.
if thou wylt plese to god / have first pity and mercy on thyn own soul. for
who that is evil and untrue to him self. shall never be good to another / and
therefore says Saint austyn who that will ordynatlye do alms. he ouzt tofore
to love more his soul than another or any other thing except god. none should
say that he were pyetous ne mercyful that had not pity of his own soul pour
and seek. how well that he had pity on others / Also I say not that he is
pyteous ne mercyful that has no pity on his own soul. when he knows that
it is seek to the death by dedely sin. Now have I showed to the enough of
mercy. the degrees. the branches. the fruit and the spyrituel good that comes
thereof in this world and in that other. Of the fruit of this tree says Dauyd
to us in the psaulter in this wise. Blessed is he that entendeth to the nedy
and to the poure^ That is to say that he abide not so long till the pour
demand him / but that he (...) without asking. Ne he has no heart to give
that gives not without askyng. he does well that gives to the pour. but he
does much better that gives with out demaundyng. And therefore says Dauyd
the prophet blessed is he that entendeth unto the poure^ and wherefore is he
blessed / he says after in the said place / that god shall deliver him in the
evil day fro his enemies. That shall be at the day of dome which shall be hard
and evil to them that shall be dampened by cause they have not fulfilled the
works of mercy. Then shall the Judge say to them at that day^ Goo ye cursyd
in to the fire of hell with the deuyls. when I had hungre and thyrst ye gave
to me neither mete ne drink. I was seek and ye vysyted not me. I was naked and
ye clothed me not. and therefore they shall be delyuerd to their enemies. that
been the deuylles of hell. And they that have been pyetous / and have intended
to the pour shall be delyuerd that day and shullen be put in the possessyon
of heaven. Like as our lord says in the gospel. For he shall say unto them
that have done and accomplysshed the works of mercy Come ye blessed of my
fader. Receive ye and take ye the kingdom of heaven which that I have maad ready
for you sith the beginning of the world / For that which ye have done to the
pour. ye have done to me. Great honor shall god do to them / when he
shall thank them of the works of mercy. and shall give to them the glory
perdurable. And therefore says he in the gospel / Blessed ben the merciful For
they shall have mercy / by cause they have enlonged the life of the pour people
by their alms. and therefore they that have had pity of the members of Ihesu
Cryste^ and have sustained them in this world. and have comforted and aided
them in their aduersytees. It is well reason that he do to them mercy. which
delyuerth fro al aduersytees and fro al myserye. and so shall he do when he
shall give to them the life ^erdurable. whereto mercy shall led them and herberowe
them.

Of the life actyf and of the life contemplatyf capitulo Cxl
THe holy scripture witnesses and enseigneth to us ij manners of well and
goo^es. by which a person comes to the life perdurable. The first is called
the life actyf / by cause it is in labor of good works. and makes a man to
ente^de to the prouffyte of him self and of his neighbor. The second is called
conte^platyf. by cause it is in rest of good works / and ne entendeth to no
(...) but to love and to know god / Then is he idle of were (...). and like
as he were a sleep. but he is awaked (...) for to think upon god. and for to
love him / And for the love that he has to god. he put al other thynge^ in
forgetyng. like as he were al rauysshed and fyxed in god / and desires to be
dysseueryd fro the mortal body / for to be always with Ihesu Christ. The first
life. is the field of good works. where the knights of god assaye and preue
them. The second rest them with god in the chamber of clean conscyence^ The
first entendeth to feed god with the mete of good works. The second entendeth
to be ^edde and fulfilled of god by very comfort spyrytuel / Of the first is
sygnefyed by martha which was besy to feed our lord. as it is said in the
gospel. The second is sygnefyed by marye magdalene which satte at the feet of
Ihesu Cryst^ and herd his words. The first is a way and enter to the second
/ For no person may come to the life contemplatyf^ if he be not first well
proved in the life actyf like as says saint Gregory^ The yeftes and the
virtues. whereof we have spoken tofore. apperteynen to the first life / which is
called actyf. The two last yeftes of which we shall speak. by the help and
aid of the holy ghoost. that is to wete of the yefte of understanding and of
the yefte of wysedom and sapyence / apperteynen to the second life. which is
called contemplatyf / This life has two things like as we have tofore touched
that is to wete in right knowleche of god / and in parfyght love / The yefte of
understanding ledeth to perfectyon of ryzt knowleche. The yefte of sapyence
ledeth to perfectyon of love we shall say first of the yefte of understanding
after that the holy ghoost shall teache and enseygne us. This yefte that is
called the yefte of understanding nys none other thing / after the saints and
the doctours^ but a light and a clerenes of grace which the holy ghoost
sends in to the heart. by understanding a man is lift up to know his maker
and the things spyrytuel. which may not be seen bodyly. And all the things
that apperteynen to the health of the soul. and to natural reason to which
the understanding of a man by him self may not ome. This yefte is called light.
for it purges the understanding of a man fro the derkenesse of ygnoraunce /
and fro the spots and fylthe of sin. For like as the bodyly light takes
away the derknesse / and makes the bodyly things to be seen clearly Right so
this spyrytuel light purges the understanding of a man / to that which he may
see clearly and know certeynlye. as a man may know in this mortal life god his
maker / and the spyrytuel creatures. like as ^en the aungellys and the souls
and the things that apperteyne to the health of souls. That been the artycles
of the feyth / of which we have spoken tofore This knowleche is not but in
conscience well purged. pure and clean. For like as sore eyes charged with
fylthe may not behold the clear light. Right so the understanding of a man.
when it is of him self may not behold ne know spyrytuel things / if it be
not well purged fro al tatches of error and of fylthe of sin. by very faith
which purges the hertes as the scripture sayth^ But the yefte of the holy
ghoost of which we speak here perfourmeth this purgacyon at heart so that
the holy soul which is purged and enlumyned with this light of understanding
may see and know god / and all that which is to him necessary. and
prouffytable to his sauacyon. And that is the blessyng whereof god speaks in
the gospel when he says. blessed be they that be clean of heart. for they shall
see god. in presence by faith / in light and informed by the yefte of
understanding. and after the death they shall see him in heaven face to face
clearly without end as says saint Poule. This yefte takes away all ordure
and fylthe fro the heart. and makes him clean parfytelye fro al ordures of
sin and specially for the spotte of the sin of lecherye. For who that of
this sin is entatched is very blind. For he has lost the eyes of the heart
of reason and of understanding. So that he may not understand ne know his
maker. ne thing that is holsom ne health of his soul / But is like a be
that has neither wit ne reason in him self. whereof dauyd says in the
psaulter. that a man to whom god has done so great honor that he has made
him to his image and his semblaunce. by which he may know god and have him.
which he has not done to any other be / if he forgete his maker / and the
bounte that he has done to him. he is bycomen semblable to folysshe bees^ys
which have none understanding. The sin that makes most a man to be like a
foul be. is the sin of lecherye. of which we have spoken tofore in the
traytye of vices. The yefte then of understanding which is contrary to this
ordure. and destroys fro the heart the sin of lecherye^ and sets therein
purete and clennesse. out of which grows a right fair tree. That is the virtue
of chastyte by which they come to this blessyng. which god promytteth to them
that kepen clennesse of heart when he says. blessed be they that be clean of
heart. For they shall see god. By cause that they shall have the eyes of the
heart well purged and well enlumyned of the yefte of understanding. This tree
grows and prouffyteth much like to the other byforsayd by seven degrees /
These been vij things which much auaylle to live chastelye.

The first degree of the virtue of chastyte capitulo Cxlj
THe first degree is clean conscience. that is the rote of this tree. For
without clean conscience chastyte may not plese god / This clennesse.
chastyte. and purete requyren that the heart may be kept fro evil thoughts /
so that the heart consent to no sin. For who so consents to evil thought
and to evil desire of his heart. he is not chaste. how well that he keep him fro
the deed. For. for the consentyng only delybered and purposed. he should be
dampened if he deyed in the same state / Three things auaylle much to keep
clennesse of heart The first is to here gladly the word of god and the sermons
whereof our lord says in the gospel to his dyscyples. ye be all clean said he
by the words that I have said to you. For the word of god is like a fair
myrrour in which one may see the spots of the hett. The second thing is
very confession. which is the fontayne where one ought often to wasshe him of
al ordure of sin. The scripture says in the book of kings that Elysee the
prophet commanded to Naman which was a lepre. that he should wasshe him vij
times in the flom Jordan for to be clean and heled of his maladye / and when he
had wasshen him there. he was all hool and clean / The flom Jordan is as much
to say as the ^treme of Judgment / which sygnefyeth confession. where one
ought to Judge him self with great sorrow of heart and with great repentance of
his sins so that a streme of teeres run by the conduyt of his eyes. and
thus the synnar shall be hool of the mezelrye of sin. And therefore says saint
Bernard^ love confession if thou wylt have beaute^ For very confession and
hool is the beauty of the soul. The iij thing is to have remembrance of the
passion of Ihesu Christ. For no temptacyon ne none evil will may not duelle in
the heart that thinks and remembers often the death and the passion of Ihesu
Christ. For this is the armure that the devil doubts most. as that by which
he is ouercomen and leseth his power. This is right well sygnefyed to us in
scripture / where as Moses raised up a serpent of brass by the commandment
of god upon a perch on hye that all the people saw it. And al they that behold
it were helyd of the bytyng and hurtyng of the serpents. The serpent of brass
that henge on the perch. sygnefyeth the body of Ihesu Christ hangyng on the
cross. That was the serpent without venym / of which was made the tryacle of
our sauacyon / for who someuer feleth him smyton and enuenymed of pryckyng and
styngyng with the venomous serpents of hell / that been the deuylles. late him
behold by very faith on the serpent of brass / That is to say that he have
in his heart parfyte mind of the passion of Ihesu Christ. and anon he shall be
heled and delyuerd of the temptacyons of the enemy. that is the devil.

The second degree of the virtue of chastyte capitulo Cxlij
THe second degree of the virtue of chastyte. by which this tree grows and
prouffyteth / is for to keep his mouth fro vylaynous word^s. which ben of
rybauldrye and dyshonestees. or such as tornen to dishonor. For by such
words and by such wind is often quyckened and enfla^med the fire of lecherye.
whereof the scripture says. who speaks of a common woman is brennyng as fire.
And saint Poul says that the shreude words corrumpen good manners. And
therefore who that will keep him chastely. him byhoueth that he keep him fro such
words. and who that gladly speaks them. or gladly hereth them. he leseth god.
and shows well that he is not chaste / For there may none other thing issue
out of a vessel but such as is within it. if the words be foul and vylaynous
It is an open sign that the ordure and the vylo^nye is in the heart / For of
the habundaunce of the heart the mouth speaks. this says our lord in the
gospel.

The third degree of the virtue of chastyte capitulo Cxliij
THe third degree of the virtue of chastyte. is to keep well the five wits of
the body. the eyes fro folly beholding the eres fro herkenyng of folly and
vain words / The nose thrylles fro ouermoche delytyng in sweet savors and
wicked odours. The tongue fro evil speech and rybauldous langage. And the mouth
fro over sweet and delycyous metes and drynkes. These ben the ^^yates of the
cite of the heart. by which the devil enters often these ben the five wyndowes
of the house by which death enters often in to the hert^ like as says the
prophet / Many great wise men have be taken and ouercomen by this. that they
kept not well the yates / And if thou wylt have example of this matere. think
that no man was more strong than Sampson / Ne more holy than dauyd the
prophet. Ne more wise than Salamon. And nevertheless they fylle and were al
deceived by wymmen / Certainly if they had well kept their yates of their five
wits corporell. the fend had not taken so great fortresses^ For as saint
gregory says / The toure of the heart may not be taken if it be not opened to
the host of the devil. wherefore the ancient phylosophres fled in to far
places. in deserts. by cause they myzt not see. ne here. ne feel things
delectable / by which their strength and virtue should wexe feeble. ne by which
they might lose their chastyte. Other phylosophres there were that by cause
they should not be let to think on their phylosophye put out their eyes by
cause they should see no thing that myzt draw them fro contemplacyon. Then
the bodyly wits ben like an horse that renneth without bytte or bridle / which
makes his lord to overthrow or fall. But the chaste heart holds him by the
rain and by the bridle of reason.

Of the fourth degree of the virtue of chastyte capitulo Cxliiij
THe fourth degree of the virtue of chastyte. is sharpness of penaunce^ to
subdue his flesh which is rebelle. and make it subgette to the spyryte. like
as says saint poule For he that will quench the fire of lecherye. he ought to
take away the rise fagotte. and all tho things that make it to brenne and
that nourysshe the fire. These been the delyces and the eases of the body
which quyckene and lyghten the fire of lecherye and corrumpen chastyte. whereof
saint bernard says that chastyte peryssheth in delyces. And therefore who that
will keep him fro brennyng / he ought to take away by abstynence. and by
sharpness of penance of his body all the occasyons that may quyckene the
fire of lecherye. whereof the scripture says that the children that were
nourysshed with gross metes would not use delycyouse metes. and were saved in
the fournays of babylone. by which is vnderstonden the sin of lecherye.
why^he is quenched by abstynence and by sharpnes of pr^aunce. But the fat
metes delycyouses. and the strong wynes inflame and nourysshe this sin of
lechery in like wise as oylle and greece alyght and enflammeth the fire and
enforce it.

Of the v degree of the virtue of chastyte capitulo Cxlv
THe fifthe degree of the virtue of chastyte. is to flee evil company and the
occasyons of sin. Much people have fallen to sin by evil company. which
otherwise had not fallen / like as the leuayn corupteth the paste and draw it
to sauour^ Right so the evil company corupteth the good fame and renommee of
the person. An appel roten if it be emonge the sound and hole / corrupts
the good apples if it lie long emonge them A brennyng cole anon sets a
fire an hepe of cooles when it is laid emonge them. whereof dauyd says in the
psaulter. with the holy thou shalt be holy. and with the shrewes thou shalt
be perverted.

Thus then if thou wylt keep chastyte and clennesse / follow the company of
the good. For if thou love the company of evil and shrewes / thou shalt be
evil as they be. For who that loves the company of a fool^ it byhoueth that
he be like to him. according to that scripture says / Thus byhoueth it to flee
all the occasyons of sin. As to speak secretly with a woman. and in
suspecyous place. one allone to one For such things given occasyon to sin.
when there is place and time. whereof we read in the book of kings. that Amon
which was the sone of dauyd. when he had his sister Thamar in his chamber he
corrupted and defoulyd her. The lady of Joseph when she fond him allone. she
would have maad him to sin with her. but he fled as a wise man and left
her. Therefore says Saint Poule. Flee ye fornycacyon / that is to say all the
occasyons that may bring or led a person to the sin of lecherye. For one
may not better overcome the sin of lecherye ne keep chastyte than by fleyng
the companyes and the occasyons of this sin / whereof the aungel said to loath
that he should issue and depart fro the cytee of Sodom. and from all the
marches. For it suffysed not to leave the evil company ne the sin / but that
he should leave the marches of sin / It is said that s^. long gooth the pot
to water. that at the last it breketh^ And the gnat flees so long at the
flamme of the candell. that at last it brenneth. In like wise may one seek
thoccasyons of sin. that he falls therein. who so will then keep him well
fro such fire that he brenne not. he ought to withdraw him fro it.

The sixthe degree of the virtue of chastyte capitulo Cxlvj
THe syxthe degree of the virtue of chastyte / is that one be well occupied and
well set a work of good werkys and honest. For the devil which slepeth not.
when he fyndeth a man idle and slow to do well. put him self to labor and
makes him fall lightly in to sin. whereof the scripture says. that
idleness / that is to say neclygence and slouthe for to do good. is maystresse
of many euylles / and that is enemy of the soul. And therefore says Saint
Poule. Ne give thou no place to the devil / That is to say ne be thou not idle.
that the fend find not place to tempte the. For who that is idle to do good
works / he gives rome and place to the devil for to tempte him. Therefore says
Saint Gregory do allwaye sum good works that the devil find the not idle.
For he is lightly taken of the fend. that occupyeth not him self always in
so^me good works. For he that is idle may not long keep ^ym fro falling in to
sin. Of this says the prophet. that the cause of the sin of sodom the
cite. was plente of breed and wyn. and idleness. That is to understand that
they ete and drank. and dyden no thing. And therefore they fill in to sin so
horrible that it ought not to be named. Right so do much people that lose her
time / and employe it in vanytees and in oultrages of mete and drink and lewd
games. in Iolyte^s of lewd songs. of daunces / of plays not leeful^ and
other deduytes. And in such vanytees they wasten their tyme^ and therefore the
fall often in many horrible sins. and often in to the pytte of hell. For like
as Job says. They led their lines in plays. in deduytes and in delyces. and
in an only point they descend in to the pytte of hell. that is at the point
of death where as they take none head.

The vij degree of the virtue of chastyte capitulo Cxlvij
THe seventh degree of the virtue of chastyte / is devout prayer and oryson.
which much auaylleth to overcome all sins. and specially the sin of
lecherye / whereof Saint Ambrose sayth^ That prayer is a good shield ayenste
all the brennyng darts of the devil. And saint ysodore says that it is the
remedy against all temptacyons of sin. a man to run to prayer as soon as
the fend tempts him unto sin. For the accustomaunce of devout prayer
quenches all the assaults of sin. Devout prayer is much mighty unto god
when it is under set and accompanied with four things as of four pylers.
The first is true faith / whereof our lord says in the gospel. All that ye
ask and demand in your prayers* have ye good faith and steadfast believe in
god^ and ye shall have that ye demand / And Saint James says. that one ought
demand or ask in steadfast faith without doubtyng. For who that doubts is
like the foam of the sea which the wind ledeth hither and thither. And
therefore he that prays doubtyng. Geteth no thing of god. The second thing
that ought to be in prayer is hope to have that. which is demanded and
required Hereof says dauyd in the psaulter^ have good hope in god. and he
shall do that which. thou requyrest of him / And also he says in another
place. Lord have mercy on me. for my heart trusts in the. God gives to us
great hope for to require him. and to have that / which we demand of him
when he says in the gospel. That who demands. he takes it. and who so
secheth. he fyndeth. that is to understand who demands wisely. and secheth
dylygently. and knock and shoue at the door perseuerantly. And when these three
things been in the prayer / wit. Dylygence. and perseueraunce god enhaunceth
it. if thou demand wisely. Many men pray and demand which be not herd ne
granted of god. by cause they ask evil and not leefully. whereof saint James
says to them that can not demand. ye ask often says he of god / but ye get
no thing by cause that ye can not ask it / Sum ask more hye thing than
apperteyneth to them. as did saint Johan and saint James. which demanded of
god that that oue should sytte on the right side of our lord in his royame. and
that other on the lift side / They asked not wisely but it was with great
presumpcyon. And therefore our Lord answered to them hard and said to them. ye
wot not what ye aske^ then who that will pray to god. late him keep him fro
presumpcion / that he suppose not great things in him / as did the pharysee.
which auaunted him in his prayer / and despised other / But humbly ought a
person to pray to god in Iugyng and accusyng him self tofore god. which sees
every heart. and knows the maladyes of sin and the deffaultes and also
knows that whereof we have need. and that which is prouffytable for us.
be^ter than we our self / and take ensau^ple at the pour truau^tes which
shown their soores and maladyes for to moeue the people to pity toward them.
Right so ought one to do tofore god humbly to show his sins and his
deffautes to remember there. for to get grace and pardon. There ben other that
can not demand but vile and little things / as ben the goods temporal. And
god will give to the a gretter thing. he will not appease the with an appel or
with a pere as a child. but he will that thou demand great things. which
been for the health of thy soul. as his grace and his glory. For who that
demands of god rychesses. or honors. or death. or vengeance of his
enemies. he demands of god foul prayers and against him self. and therefore
god grau^teth them not. Therefore says saint Austyn / understand not of god to
be a great thynge^ the goods that he gives as well to the wicked as to the
good / and to his enemies as well as to his friends / And yet more gives god of
temporalle goods to the wicked than he does to the good. God gives them to
the wicked. to the^de that the good persons should learn to despise them as
saint austyn says. when thou prayest says saint ambrose. demand great
things. that been they that enduren without end. and not the things
transytorye^ But them that enduren without end. For such a prayer as to
demand temporalle goods. he grants them not. And therefore our good
master Ihesu Christ techeth us for to demand wisely. And forms unto us our
demand. when he says in the gospel if ye demand any thing of my fader in
my name. he shall give it you / he demands in the name of Ihesu Christ. that
demands that which apperteyneth to the health of his soul. And what thing
we ouzt to ask and demand / he enseygneth and techeth us when he says in
the gospel. Seche ye first the royame of god and his Justice. and all things
temporalle shall come to your auau^tage. For as it is woned to be said. unto the
most need. ouzt one allewaye to run. we have need of two things of the
goods spyrytuel and temporelle. But we have grettest need of the goods
spyrytuel. And therefore we ought first and pryncypally require them / and god
shall give them and do to us advantage of the second good^ that been the goods
temporell / we ought not to make of the second goods the pryncypall. as done
the covetous men. which seche not to have none other life. but this present
life. which faylleth and escapith* from them. will they or nyll they / but the
royame of god is life perdurable. That ought we require of god and desire by
merit of good prayer. And that is that god says. Seche ye first the royalme
of heaven and his Justice. That is to do good works / by whyehe we may come to
that royame / that never shall faylle. who that secheth in this wise / god
does to him advantage of temporalle goods. For he gives to his use
suffysanntlye. For no thing lacks to them that dread god and love him. like
as says the holy scripture. But the auarycyous people of the world / the more
that they have the more they lack and faylle. And Saint Iherome says / that
to the covetous man. fayllech that which he has and that which he has not.
Now think then when thou would pray god / for to demand wisely
dylygently. and perseuerauntly. And he shall give unto the all that shall be
nedeful to the prou^fyte and health of thy soul The third thing that ought to
be in prayer / is devotion of heart. that is to lift up the heart to god.
without thynkyng ouwher else. whereof our lord says. when thou wylt pray to
god / enter within thyn heart. and close the door upon the. that is to say. put
out all thoughts. seculer. flesshely. foul. wicked. worldly. and vylaynous.
And thus pray thy fader of heaven in hyddles in thy heart / and that the heart
think on none other thing. but on that which it ought to think. and saint
ysodore says. that then we pray god truly. wha^ we think nowher else. And
Saint Austyn says. what auaylleth to moeue the mouth and the lyppes / when the
heart says not a word. As great dyfference as is between the chafe and the
corn. and the brenne and the flower of whete^ so great dyfference is between
the prayer and devotion of the heart. God is not a ghoote to be fed with
leaves. God cursyd the tree whereon he fond no thing but leaves. Right so the
prayer which is all in leaves of words without devotion of heart / pleases
no thing to god. but it dyspleaseth him. and he torneth his eere. For he will
not understand such langage. who that prays god without devotion. it
seems that he mocketh god. like as he that will mock a deef and a dombe man.
that meueth his lyppes only as he spacke. and no thing says / To such people
god makes a deef ere. but the prayer that comes fro the depnes of the heart.
that hereth our lord as he says in the gospel / God is a spyryte / and
therefore who will pray god and have his request granted. him byhoueth that he
pray in spyryte and in truth. Dauyd the prophet enseygneth and techeth us
in the psaultrr to pray to god deuoutely when he says. lord mine oryson be
adressyd tofore the like to thensence Thensence when hit is upon the fire it
smells swetely / Right so does the prayer that comes fro the heart brennyng
in the love of god smells much swetely tofore god. otherwise the prayer may
not be enhaunced tofore god if it come not fro the heart. like as a messager
which brings no letters. ne has no knowleche. enters not gladly tofore
the king. Oryson or prayer without devotion is as a messager with out
letters. who such message sends to the court. he does evil his erandes^
who then will pray god verily. he ought to cry to god fro the depthe of his
heart. as did dauyd / which said in the psaulter. lord god here my wys / For I
cry to the fro the depnesse of my heart. The fervor of love is the cry fro
the depnesse of the heart. this says saint Austyn. Such a wys and such a cry
pleseth much to god. and not the noise of words polysshed. whereof Saint
Gregory says that verily to pray to god. is in the teres and bewayllynges of
conpunctyon of heart. This cry chaseth away the thieves / that been the deuylles
