which lie in awayte for to trouble and rob us. And therefore ought we often to
cry and pray unto god that he will keep and deffende us fro the theuys of
hell. Thus ought we strongely to cry to god against the fire of couetyse. or
of lecherye. that he give to us the water of teres for to quench such fire
that hit enflamme not our hertes. Also we ought to cry to god ayenste the evil
thoughts that come often to the heart. that the heart and the soul perysshe not
by consentyng. Therefore cried Dauyd to god and said. Lord save me. and keep me
fro the peril of waters. which ben now entered in to my heart. and the
dyscyples of our lord when they saw the tempest of the sea upon them they
cried saying lord save us for we been in great peril. And for these three
things that I have here said one ought often to cry to god that he save us fro
these three perils / that is to wete fro the thieves of hell. and fro the fire
of couetyse. and fro the flodes of evil thoughts and of temptacyon. Now
ought thou to know. that in all times / and in all places may a person
pray to god. But he ought specially and most deuoutelye ought he to pray in
the church on the sondayes and in festes which ben stablysshed for to pray
to god to preyse and honor him / and therefore then they seace and ought to
^eace all persons fro bodyly works and temporal. for the better tentende to
pray to god and honor him. and to spyrituel werkys. God commanded so
straytly to keep the sabotte day in the old law that he made a man to be
stoned tofore the people. by cause he had gadrid a few styckes on the sabotte
day / what shall god do then of them that do the great sins on the sondayes
and the festes. and waste the time in vanyte and in folyes / and yet werse done
they on the sonday^s. on the festes and on solemn days than they do on other
days. Certeynly they shall be more punysshed and dampened in that other world /
than the Jews that brake their sabotte day^ For the sunday is more holy than
the sabotte. So ben the pryncypal feestes which ben establisshed in holy
church for to pray to god / and to honor and thank him of the goodness and
bountees that he has done to us / and does every day. like as holy church
remembers / In such a feste as is cristemas / that is of his natyuyte how he
was borne of the vyrgyn marie. At Ester how he roos fro death to life. At the
ascencyon how he styed up in to heaven. At whytson tide how he sent the holy
ghoost upon thappostles. Also there been establysshed to keep the feestys of
saints for to preyse and worship god and his saints. and to remember the holy
miracles that he did for them for to conferme our faith. And therefore we ought
to keep the feestys of saints. and to pray them deuoutelye to aid and
socoure us unto our lord / which has so much honored them in heaven in
glory and in earth and therefore they sin grievously that keep not their
feestys For they do against the commandment of god and of holy church. But
here sum may say to me. Fair sir a man may not al day pray to god ne be at
the monasterye ne in the church. what harm is it if I goo play and dysporte
me as long as I play I think none evil. To that I shall answer. All the time
that thou employest in folysshe plays and in vanytees. and in work that is
not ordained in any manner to god / thou lesest it / For thou ought to know
that all the time that thou thynkest not on god. thou ought to acounte for
lost. this says the scripture. That is to understand wha^ thou thynkest on
vanyte / and in thing that is not in any manner ordained to god. And certeynlye
he leseth a great thing that leseth his time / this says Seneke^ For he
leseth the goods that he might do in as much as he so leseth in plays and
in vanytees. and that is not without sin for to despende the time in evil
usage. For god requires rekenyng at the day of Judgment. this says Saint
Ancelme. and therefore ought one always well to employe his time as long as he
lives in this world. And the time is short as says the scripture / Ne no man
knows how long time he has to live. ne no man knows when he shall deye. ne
how he shall pass out of this world^ who then will keep the holy days as he
owes. he ought to keep him fro doing that desplayseth god and his saints. and
well to employe his time in god. in prayeng him. praysyng. and gyuyng him
thanks of his goods. and to here the sermons and put them in eure and to
entende to other good werkys and needs that been according to god. Also when a
man is in the church he ought to conteyne him much honestlye^ and do
reverence to god and to his saints deuoutelye. For the church is ordained for
to pray god and his saints / and not for to Iangle ne for to lawghe. ne for
to Iape^ ne for to speak idle words ne for to talk to other of seculer
things. For our Lord says. My hows is the house of prayer. And therefore a man
ought not to do none other thing therein. than it for which it was
establisshed. this says saint austyn. he that shall come tofore the king in
his chamber for to empetre and get any grace he ought well to keep him fro
saying of any thing that should dysplese the king. Much more ought he to be
ware that comes in to the church which is the chamber and the house of god.
what he says and does tofore god and his aungellys and that specially that
should dysplease him. Then god will not that a man should make of his house a
market ne an ha^^e For he him self chaced and droof out of his temple with
good scourges them that bought and sold therein. Also he will not that any plee
should be made therin^ ne noise ne no seculer need / but he will that we should
entende to pray god deuoutely and praise and than^^ him of al his benefaytes /
There ouzt a man to call ageyn his heart to him self and put away all worldly
werkys and al evil thoughts. and think on his creator. and on the bountees
that god has done to him. and does every day. and to remember his sins and
his deffaultes. and to humble him self tofore god. and to require him of pardon
and grace to keep him from sin / and to have perseueraunce in good works
unto the end. Also in the church ought the great lords and the great ladies
to forgete all their glory. their richesse. their power. their dygnyte. their
hyenesse / and their puyssaunce / and ought to think that they be tofore their
Judge. which shall straytely examyne them and rekene straytly of the goods that
he has done to them of the dygnytees and estates that he has set them in.
and how they have used them and he shall reward them after their deserte.
Therefore ought they much to humble them to god. and not to gloryfye them of
their hyenesse. ne of their fair array. ne of their rich robes They may take
example of king Dauyd. which forgate his dygnyte when he prayed tofore god.
and despised him self so much that he said to our lord. I am said he a lytyl
worm and not a man. In this Dauyd knowleched his lytelnes. his pouerte. and
his deffaultes. and made him nouzt For like as a worm is little and naught. and
grows naked of the earth. al in like wise is a man of him self a vile thing
and pour. For when he enters in to the exyle of this world he brings no
thing. ne no thing shall bear away. al naked he entered / and al naked he shall
goo hens. whereof saynt^ bernard says. what is a man but foul sperme. a sack
full of dunge. and mete to worms. He is much foul and made of foul seed in
his concepcyon. a foul sack full of dunge in his life. and mete to worms after
his death. Also the great ladies that been so arrayed with gold and silver. with
precious stones and robes ought in the church tofore god well to take example
of the good queen hester / which took of her precious roobes and her
parementes when she came for to pray god / and humbled her self. and knowleged
her pouerte and her deffaultes tofore god. and said to him / lord thou know
that I hate the sin of pride. and the glory of parementes and of Jewels
which me byhoueth to set down fro my heed / in great abhomynacyon of them /
that in such things trusten. delyten. gloryfyen / and were them for to show
them and to please the fools. God has not to do with such parementes in his
church. but of a clean conscience and of an humble heart. Saint Poule enseyneth
and techeth right well how the wymmen ouzt to array them when they come for to
pray god^ he says that they ought to have honest habyte without any
oultrage. that is to understand after that it apperteyneth to the estate of
the person / For that which is oultrage in one person / is not oultrage in
another / sum is conuenyent to a queen which is not according to a bourgeys
wife. or another simple woman. Also thapostle techeth that the wymmen of what
estate they be. that they should be of simple beholding and regard and humble /
that is to understand that they should be simple. humble and shamefast. and not
afronted ne openly show her vysage. as done these common wymmen. which goon
with their neck stratched out as an heart in the launde. and look a side or a
trauers as an horse of prys. Also he will that they be not curyous for to array
their heed with gold ne silver ne with precious stones. And yet he will also
that they have in the church their hedes couerd. so that no man be styred by
them to euyl^ ne sin not in beholding of them / but they ought to be arrayed
as devout and good wymmen / which show the bounte of their heart by good
werkys / and therefore says saint Ambrose^ who will be herd in prayer. he ought
to take away fro him al sign of pride. and ought to enclyne him to god with
his heart by very confession / and by penance in profou^de humylyte. for to
moe^^ god to do him mercy. For as he says proud habyte geteth no thing of
god / but it gives cause to Inge evil of him that wereth it. Now I have showed
to the three things that ought to be in prayer. fayth^ hope and devotion. But
to that. that prayer may be perfyghtly agreeable and playsaunte to god and
worthy to be enhaunced and herd. it behooves four things / That is that it
have ij wings which bear it tofore god. These two wings ben almesses and
fastings. or other penaunces. whereof the au^gel said to Thobye / Prayer is
good when it has in him self fasting and almesse^ without these two wings
the prayer may not flee to god. For as says Saint Ambrose / good life makes
the prayer to flee to god. But sin lets it and wythdraweth it ageyn.
whereof thou ought to wete that in two manners is prayer let. like as says
saint Ysodore. One is by cause a man keeps him not fro sin and fro doing
evil and for that a person will not forgive the evil will that he has to
another. For in like wise as the oynementes will not hele the wound. as long
as the iron is within / Right so auaylleth not ne prouffyteth no thing the
prayer to him that says it. as he has evil will to another. And therefore
says the prophet. let us lift up our hertes and our hands to god. He
lyfteth up his heart and his hands to god / that lyfteth up his prayers by good
works. And thappostle says that he that lyfteth up his pure hands to god in
prayer. lyfteth up in pure and clean conscience without sin / For god
enhau^ceth not the prayer that comes of a conscience full of ordure and of
sin. whereof he says by the prophet. when ye shall multeplye your prayers. I
shall not here them. for your hands be all blody and full of sin. who ben they
that have their hands blody^ but they that dystresse the pour people which ben
under them and take away fro them their good by force / they have the hands
full of blood of the blood of pour people. for they take away fro them their life
/ and their sustenau^ce / by couetyse and by their rauyne. and do great
oultrages. and eten the morsellys full of sin. wherefore they shall pay the
scotte in that other world. For the scripture says that god requires the
blood of the pour people For they must give a rekenyng. or sytte therefore. and
therefore who will be enhau^ced and herd of god in his prayers. late him not
come tofore God the sword drawn. Ne the hands blody ne with wide hands.
That is to say in will to sin ne spotted of untruth. ne wide of good
works / For thus says our lord in the gospel. Thou shall not come tofore me
with wide hands. he comes with empty hands tofore god that comes to pray
and require him without making present of good werkes^ for to him he closes
his yate that requires him and brings no thing. hereof have we example in
the gospel / which says that the yate was shytte to the folysshe vyrgyns that
had none oil in their lamps. and god said to them I know you not. For god
knows none but them that have their lamps full of oylle / that is to say them
that have the heart full of pity and of grace purged and clean of al sins and
show it by good works / Such people hereth god gladly and opens to them
his yate. and receives gladly their prayers. Now say I then that prayer like
as it rested on four pylers as it is said tofore. and is much playsaunt to god
/ For it geteth lightly of god all that it has need. be it in body or in soul
as says the scripture. whereof saint James says that much auaylleth the besy
prayer of a ryghtwys man. For it avails to hele all maladyes of body and of
soul. and says yet that prayer that comes of faith heleth the seek person /
if he be in sin it shall be pardonned. The holy scripture says that Moses
the prophet vaynquysshed Amalech and his host / not by bataylle. but by holy
prayers. For as it is said of an holy man. Much more auaylleth the prayer of a
saint than the fyghtyng of many thousand synnars. The prayer of a good man
perceth he^en. Then shall he overcome his enemies in earth / A good old and
devout woman geteth more soon a good request of god in glory in prayeng him
deuoutely / than a thousand knights may get of land in long time by force
of arms. and therefore it is good to pray and require god with the orysons of
good folk. and specially of couentes and of relygyous people. which ben
assembled for to serve god. and for to pray night and day deuoutely for all
their benefactours. For the prayer is much worth toward our lord. For like as
says the scripture. More auaylleth. and more may do toward god the prayer of
many good persons than any can express or say. for as it is said of an holy
man It may not be but the prayers of many good persons to gyder be herd of
god and granted. The prayers and requests of all the hole covent togydre. is
sooner passed and herd of thabbot. than the request and prayer of one monk
allone / In like wise hereth god more soon the prayers of them that been
assembled for to serve him. And therefore says god in the gospel. if tweyne of
you accorden togydre to ask and require me. All that they require my fader of
heaven I shall do it. Now have I spoken of seven degrees of the tree of the
virtue of chastyte. by which this virtue grows and mounteth and prouffyteth /
Now byhoueth to say of the branches of this tree which ben seuen^ after the
seven estates of the people / that been in this world.

Of the first estate of them that been entyer and chaste of body capitulo
Cxlviij
THe first estate of the world is of them that been hool and chaste of body. and
have kept their maydenhed. but nevertheless they be not bounden to this / but
that they may be married. In such estate ought a person to keep chastyte /
that is clennesse and purete of heart and of body / wherefore the children of
rich men ought to have good kepars and honest. that they ben dylygent for
tenseygne them. and keep them fro evil company and fro sin. For evil
company fouleth often the children. and enseygne them evil games. and shrewde
words of rybauldrye. lewd touchynges and dyshoneste. by which they fall in
to the sin of lecherye. which is against nature. whereof we have spoken tofore
in the traytye of vices / therefore it needs not to reherce it ageyn. for such
matere is abhomynable. And therefore the children ought to be chastysed and well
drawn forth in good manners / and hold and keep them nyghe that they do no
harm ne sin. as long as they be young / and to accustom them to keep
thenseynemens. For also as says salamon. that which a child is learned in his
yongthe that will he hold in his old age / And the philosopher says that it
is no little thing taccustome well or evil in his yongthe for that is all. For it
is said. that which is learned in yongthe is mayntened in age / Such form as
the shoo takes at the beginning. the same holds it / forth always in such
estate. Then has chastyte need of good keeping / for else it should be sone
lost.

The second estate is of them that been corrupt capo. Cxlix
THe second estate is of them that been corrupt of body and have lost their
chastyte and maydenhede. and yet were never married ne bounden with bond that
might let them to marye. And nevertheless they be confessyd and repentaunte of
their sins. In this estate ought a person to keep chastyte / For he that is
in such estate of repentance ought to have steadfast purpoos. that never he
shall fall ageyn in that sin. but al his life to keep him to his power^ sauf
that he may marye him if he will. he or she that will keep him chaste in such
estate / him byhoueth that he chastyse his body by sharpnes of penance. this
is the ij branch of this tree /

The third branch capitulo CL
THe third estate is of them that be bounden by marriage In this estate ouzt
they to keep chastyte. sauf the work of marriage. For they ought to keep their
bodies that one to that other. and this requires the law of marriage. that the
one bear faith to the other of their bodies. For sith they be joined to gyder
carnally by marriage they been one body as says holy scripture / And therefore
ought each to love other / as them self. For like as the two ben one body. so
ought they to be one heart by true love. ne never ought they to d^parte ne to
deceuere / of their hertes ne of their bodies as long as they live. Then
they ought to keep their bodies clenely and chastely / reserved and sauf the
acts of marriage. And therefore says Saint Poul. that the wymmen ought to love
and honor their husbondes. and ought to be chaste and sobre^ and to keep them
fro al other men. sauf fro their husbondes. and ought to be sobre in etyng and
drynkyng. For ouermoche mete and drink alyghteth the fire of lecherye. Right
so oughten the men to keep their bodies chastely. and not to abandonne them to
other wymmen. Marriage is a state which ought to be holden and kept much
clenly and holyly for many reasons. for it is a state of great auctoryte. For
god ordained it and establysshed it in paradys terrestre in the estate of
Innocencye. tofore that man had ever sinned. and therefore it ought to be holyly
kept by cause that god establysshed it. and also for the holy place where it
was ordained. Also it is a great estate of dygnyte. for god would be borne in
marriage. that is of the vyrgyn marie. which was married to Joseph without losyng
of her vyrgynyte / The virgyn marye made of marriage her mantel / under the
which was conceived and borne the blessed sone of god. under this mantel was
hyd fro the devil the secret counceyll of our redempcyon and of our salvation.
Therefore it ought to be honored and clenly kept. Also it ought well holyly to
b^ kept for the holiness thereof. For it is one of the seven sacraments of
holy church. And sygnefyeth the marriage that is between Ihesu Christ and holy
church. and between god and the soul. Then the state of marriage is so holy
and honest that it makes that which was sin mortal without marriage is
without sin in marriage. and not only without sin but it may be in sum
caas cause to win the life perdurable / And it ought to be known that in three
caases may one do luxury of marriage without sin. and may have great merit
as to the soul / The first caas is when this work is done in entencyon to
have lygnage for to serve god. And in such entencyon was ordained and
establysshed marriage pryncypally / The second is when that one renders to that
other his debt. when it is required. And to that ought to moeue Justice.
which renders to eueryche his right. Then if that one refuse to that other
his right. when it is demanded and required by the mouth / or by sign as
done the wymmen that been honest and shamefast to demand such thing he or
she that refuses to that other that requires it / synneth. For he does wrong
to that other of that which is his own For that one has right in the body of
that other. but he that renders that which he owes does well and right /
when he does it in good entencyon / For Justice moeueth him to do so / and
that is neither sin ne lecherye. The third caas is when a man requires his
wife for such work. for to keep her fro sin. Also when he sees that she is
so shamefast that she never requires her husbond of such thing / and
doubts that she should lightly fall in to sin if he required her not who in
such entencyon renders or requires such thing of such debt. he synneth
not / but he may deserve toward god me ryte / For pity moeueth him to do it. In
these three things is no point of sin in the works of marriage. but in other
caas there may be sin venyall or mortal. And specially in three caas / The
first is when this work is required only for his delight and lecherye / and
in this caas may one sin venyally and dedely. venyally when the delight pass
not the bonds and the terms of marriage. That is to say when the delight is so
subgette to reason that he that in this work and in such estate. would not do
this thing but only to his wife But when the lecherye and the delight is so
great in his wife that reason is deed and so blind. that as much he would do
to her if she were not his wife. In such a caas the sin is mortal / For such
delight passes the bounds of marriage / whereof god is often dyspleased to such
peple^ and gives sometime to the devil great power to noye and grieve them. like
as we read in holy scripture. of Sara daughter of Raguel which was wife to
young Thobye. and had / had seven husbondes tofore. and all were slain of the
devil the first night that they would have layen by her and have known her. Of
whom the angel said to Thobye that he should have her to his wife I shall say
to the said he. in what people the devil puts him in. and has power on
them that putten god out of their heart and of their thought. that they ne
entende to no thing but to their delytes and for to accomplysshe their wicked
desires / like as does an horse or a mule /

And god takes away fro them sometime their lygnage and their fruit that they
may not have children by their sins. Yet may they sin mortally in another
manner that is to wete. when that one treats that other against nature. or
oherwyse than nature of man requires ne law of marriage grants. Such
people synnen more grievously than the other toforesayd. but they that in their
marriage keep the dread of our lord. and kepen clenly and holyly their marriage.
Such people plesen god /

The second caas that may be sin (...) maryage^ is when a man gooth to his
wife in such time as he ought not. that is when she is in the maladye or
sickness that comes unto wymmen oftyme. He that spares not his wife when she
is in such estate / for the parylle of the lygnage that she myzt then
conceive / should be mezel or lepre. he synneth dedely / For as Saint Iherome
says / In that estate be conceived the lame often time. the crooked. and the
lepres. And that time the woman ought for to tell it to her husbond. when she
is in that plyte. desyryng him to abide and suffer all so long as she is in
such point.

Also they both ought for to spare and absteyne them fro the work of marriage
in holy times. That is to say as in the great solemn feestys. for the better
to entende to pray god and to serve and honor hym^ And in the times of
vygyles^ of lent and of fastings commanded by holy church they ought to
suffer and forbere such work. not for that it is sin to do such thing in
that time / For in a good entency on he may do it / but sometime they ought to
suffer of that they may do. for to get the better of god that thing which they
demand of him as says saint austyn. Also in the time the woman lies in
gesyne. or nygh the time of chyldyng a man ouzt to keep him fro the work of
marriage for shame. and also for the peril that might come thereof. It is
founden in the book that speaks of the nature of beestys. that the olyfaunt
shall never abide with the female as long as she is conceived and bears. and a
man by reason ought to be better attempred than a be. and therefore ought a
man in such time wythdrawe him. But nevertheless I say not that is sin to do
the work of marriage in such time for good cause. and true entencyon whereof
god is Judge. The third caas is. that in which one may most grievously sin in
his marriage. that is in holy place. For in holy place as is the church. which
is ordained for to pray god and serve him / ought not be do lecherye of
marriage ne none other sin. for the reverence of the holy place and he that
has no regard in such holy place to do such work he synneth for reason of
the place. For such thing is sin in one place and in one time / that is not
in another. The iiij estate is of them that have be in marriage. but the death
has deceuerd them that one fro that other^ And he or she that is abyden ought
to keep and live chastely as long as he or she is in the state of wydowhede /
This is an estate which Saint poul preyseth much. and says to the wydowes.
that he or she is good that holds him in such estate. and if it playse not
them they may marye them / For better is to marye than to brenne them. for if
he bre^ne so that he conse^te to sin / he synneth. for he put his heart thereto
by will and by desire to the fire of lechery and better it were and more
auaylle to him to marye. than to brenne him self in the fire. that is to
understand of them that been in the state of simple wydowhede and not them that
been in thestate bounden by vow. they may not marye wtthoute dedely sin
after their vow. but nevertheless if the vow be simple and that it be pryuely
made without solempnyte. how be it that they sin dedely that after their auow
marye the^. nevertheless they may abide in their marriage. if there be none other
lettyng And is bounden to do penance of the vow broken / but when the vow is
solemn. or by the hand of a prelate. or by professyon of relygyon. or by
holy order that he has received. as subdeken. deken or priest. Then the
marriage is none. but they must deceuere and depart that so ben assembled by
marriage for they may not be laufully in such estate. To byholde the state of
wydowhede. ought to moeue the example of the turtle for like as says the book
of nature of beestes / Never after the turtle has lost his make she shall never
accompanye her with another. but is solytarye and flees the company of other.
Three things apperteyne much to them that b^e in thestate of wydowhede / The
first is to hyde her self and to be secretlye in her hows. and not to syewe
suspecyous felawshyp. hereof have we a fair example of Iudyth which was a
wydowe. and was a much fair woman and young of which it is said in the holy
scripture. that she held her self in her chamber cloos with her maidens.
wherefore saint Poul repreueth the young wymmen wydowes that were idle and
curyous for to goo and come and Iape and ouermoche speak. but closely and
secretly ought they to be in their lodgyng / and entende to do good werkes^
like as saint Poul enseygneth them / The ij thing is to entende to pray god
gladly. and to yield him thankynges of his benefaytes. And to be in the church
in great devotion in great repentance of their sins. and in teres weeping. As
it is said in scripture by saint luke. that the good wydowe which was named
Anne departed not out of the temple. but served god night and day in prayer /
in fastings. and in other penau^ces. The iij thing is sharpness of metes.
Saint poul says that a wydowe that ledeth her life in delices is deed by sin.
for like as says saint bernard. chastyte peryssheth in delices. in like wise
as he perissheth in the water that is so much under in depnesse that he leseth
his breeth. No man may have his heed in the water. that is to say / his heart
long in the delyces of this world but that he lose his life. That is the grace
of the holy god by which the soul lives in god / In such estate also
apperteyneth humble habyte and not proud ne curyous. After the example of
Judith which left her rich robes and her rich paremeutis / when her lord
and husbond was deed. and took the habyte of wydowhede simple and humble which
was more sign of weeping and of sorrow than of Joy ne of vayn glory. and by
cause she loved the virtue of chastyte / and that she would keep all her life.
she clad her with heyr. and fasted every day except the festes. and yet was she
fair young / rich and wise / But the ^^^nte of her heart and love of chastyte
maad her to do it. thus ouzt he^ or she to live that will keep chastyte in such
estate. and this is the fourth branch of this tree.

The fyfthe branch of the virtue of chastyte and of vyrgynyte Capitulo Clj
THe fyfthe brau^che of chastyte and of vyrgynyte is the fyfthe estate which
is in them that keep and have always kept and yet always keep and purpose to
keep all their life their body hool without corrupcyon for the love of god.
This estate is much to be praised for his dygnyte / for his beauty. and for
his bounte / For this estate has he that keeps him semblable to au^gellys of
heaven as sayen the saints. But much more have the vyrgyns of glory and of
merit than the aungellys. For the aungellys lyuen without flesh. but the
vyrgynes have vyctorye over their flesh. that is their propre body. And that
is a great meruaylle. that they keep so feeble a castle as is the body / against
so strong an aduersarye as is the devil. that secheth all thengynes that he
may to take the castle for to rob the tresour of vyrgynyte. This is the
tresour. of which our lord speaks in the gospel when he says. that the
royame of heaven is like to tresour that is hyd in a field. The tresour hid in
the field is vyrgynyte hyd in the body which is like a field. which ought by
penance to be eered. labored and sown by labor of good werkys. This tresour
is semblable to the royalme of heaven. For the life of vyrgynes is like the life
of heaven. that is the life of au^gellys / wheref our lord says in the gospel^
that in the ressurection general shall be no maryages as ben in this world*
but they shall be as aungellys in heaven. Also I say that this estate is for to
be praised for his beaulte. For it is the most fair estate that is in erthe^
except vyrgynyte clenly kept whereof Salamon says in his book of sapyence in
meruayllyng him self. O says he h^w. fair and chaste is generation with
clerenes and charity / he said well. chaste with clerenes For then is fair
chastyte and vyrgynyte. when it is clear by good life and honest. like as the
clear son makes the fair day. In like wise the clerenes of grace and of
good life makes the virgynyte fair and plesau^t to god. whereof Saint Iherome
says. that much fair and clear is virgynyte tofore other virtues when it is
without spotte and without ordure of sin. for who that is hool and chaste of
body and is corupte of heart and of thought. he or she is like a sepulcre which
is whyt and fair withoutforth and within is full of careyn of deed bodies
stynkyng and rotyn. vyrgynyte is like to a whyt robe wherein the spots be more
foul and more apparau^t / than in a robe of another color. This robe ouzt to
be well kept fro iij spots that is. of fylthe. of blood. and of fire. these
iij spots defoule more this whyt robe than other. The spotte of fylthe / is
the couetyse of the world. which ought not to be in the heart that will plese god
in thestate of virgynyte For none may please god and the world his enemy. as
says saint gregoire. and he shows that there is no friend of god that will
plese the world which is enemy of god. whereof saint Ioha^ says. who that will
be friend of the world. shall be enemy to god. and saint poul says if I would
plese the people of the world I should not be servant of Ihesu crist. It is a
sign that he will not playse the world / that his heart is al set to god / and
he that has over great array and curyous about his body is not so. for no
person secheth never beaulte ne curyosyte of roobes. ne of pareme^ts / if he
supposed not to be seen of the people. and who that secheth most of such
beauty. leseth most the beauty of his soul and of his conscience wythinforth /
by which they should plese god whereof saint Bernard says to them that sechen
these fair and precious robes. and the fair parementes for to please the world
and to show them. The daughters of babylone / ben of confusyon for their
glory shall torn to confusyon / to shame and to perdurable dampnacyon. if they
be not well ware and keep them well They clothe them says he with purple and of
fair precious robes / and under those fair robes is often the conscience pour
and foul. naked of good deeds and of virtues / and full of sins They shine
withoutforth of precious stones. of owches of gold and syluer^ but they be
foul before god and abhomynable. and saint bernard says that they that so
array them in evil entencyon. and done more than their estate requires. synnen
grievously / ^ut all the glory of the daughter of the king of glory. as dauyd
the prophet says is withinforth / that is in holy conscience and in good
virtues. where as is no point of couetyse but for to playse to god / and in
this wise the spot of fylthe defoylleth not. Also a person ought to keep him
fro the spotte of blood That is of thoughts and of flesshly desires. whereof
saint Jerome says that such virgynyte is sacrefice and offryng to Ihesu
christ. which is not entatched in the heart of any evil thought or consentyng /
for like as him self says. Nothing auaylleth vyrgynyte of body. where as is
corrupcyon of heart or of thought / or of conse^tyng. Also the fruit is not
good how well that it be fair withoutforth. when it is full of worms and of
rotynnesse wythinforth / Also he ought to keep him fro the spotte that comes
of the fire. the fire brenneth and bruleth the white robe of chastyte and of
vyrgynyte. that is when gladly they here or herkene foul words that may moeue
them to sin / For thus as says saint Poul^ and also other times we have said
it tofore. The evil words. corrupten the good manners. And therefore says
Seneke. keep the fro evil words and dyshoneste. For who that is so acustomed.
he dredeth no shame / and falls the more lightly in to sin. and therefore
who that will clenly keep the white robe of vyrgynyte. him byhoueth to keep him
well fro saying and heeryng such words as thereby he might brenne / The catte
brenneth often her skin and so does not the wild catte. Virgynyt^ emonge al
other virtues is compared and lykenyd to the flour de lys. which is a much
fair flour. and much white. whereof our lord says in scripture by the mouth of
Salamon. My friend. that is the holy soul of a vyrgyn / is as the lylye among
the thorns. Thespecyal friend of our lord is the soul of them that keep
virgynyte of heart and of body. For that is a virtue by which the soul geteth
most specially the love and the famyliarite of our lord. whereof saint Johan
theuangelist was a clean virgyn. and was emonge al thapostles most famylyer
with our lord and most pryue. as it appyereth in the gospel. nevertheless he
loved well the other / but he loved saint Johan most for his vyrgynyte. this
flour de lys or lylye that keeps his beauty among the thorns of te^ptacio^s
of the flesshe^ for the flessh that is our body humayn is but as a smoke^ that
has no charge as of him self but as thorns and nettles / that is the evil
menynges. which often pricken the soul. but the flour of virgynyte takes no
head of the thorns. wha^ it is well rooted in the love of god which defends
it fro thorns of te^ptacion. and this flour ouzt to have vj leaves and iij
graynes of gold tofore. The first leef is the hoolnes of thy body / that is to
say that the body be entyer and hool without corrupco^n of lecherye. For if a
vyrgyn were corrupt and al ayenste her will. she should not lose therefore the
merit and the reward of virgynyte. whereof Saint Lucye vyrgyn and martyr said
to the tyraunte. if thou corrupt me against my will. my chastyte shall be
doubled as touching the merit of the crown of glory. The second leef of
vyrgynyte is clennesse of heart. For like as saint Iherome says naught
auaylleth to have vyrgynyte of the body^ that has will for to marye him or
her. he speaks of them that has auowed chastyte. For who that has auowed to
keep vyrgynyte or chastyte. he ought to keep his heart clean and chaste. The
third leef of vyrgynyte^ is humylyte. For vyrgynyte with pride pleases not god
/ And therefore says saint bernard that it is a much fair thing of humylyte
with vyrgynyte. And that soul much pleases to god that in humylyte gives
preysyng of vyrgynyte / and vyrgynyte embelyssheth humylyte / I dare well say
says he that without humylyte. the vyrgynyte of our lady saint marye had
never pleased our lord. The fourth leef of the lylye of vyrgynyte is dread of
god. For they that been very vyrgynes ben woned to be tymerous ferful and
shamefast / and that is no marvel / For they bear a much precious tresour in
a much feeble vessel. Then our blessed lady the vyrgyn marie was always hyd
and had dread when the aungel appyered to her. But the dread of god is the
tresorer which keeps the tresour of virgynyte. which the devil may not take
away for it keeps the yates of the castle. wherein the tresour is enclosed.
The yates of the castle of the heart where the tresour of virgynyte is in. ben
the wits of the body. These yates kepen the dread of god. that they be not
opened to the enemy of hell. by vayn curyosyte of seeing or of heeryng. or of
smellyng. of spekyng. or tastyng / or going in evil company. For curiosyte of
seeing or of heeryng the vanytees of the world ben way and cause of the sin
of lecherye. whereof is said in the scripture that Dyna daughter of Jacob when
she went musyng by curiosyte to see the wymmen of the contre. where anon she
was rauysshed and corrupt of the sone of the lord of the town / and therefore
who will keep vyrgynyte. him byhoueth much to with draw and keep his v wits
bodyly fro al vayn curyosyte. and this ought be done by holy dread / for a
person owes always to dread to anger god. This is the sense of the v vyrgynes
of whom our lord says in the gospel. when he said that the royame of heaven is
like to x vyrgynes / of whom five were wise. and the other five were fools.
He calls here the royame of heaven holy church. which is bynethe in this
world. wherein been always good and evil. foles and wyse^ which ben members of
holy church. by the faith that they have received in baptesme. The five wise
vyrgyns sygnefye them that keep and govern well the five wits of the body of
which we have spoken. The five vyrgyns foles sygnefye them that folysshly keep
them. The v leef is sharpenes of the life of penance. For who will keep
vyrgynyte / he must much chastyse his flesh and subdue it by penance / and
that the body do the will of the soul by fasting. by wakyng in prayers. and
other penau^ces Sharpness of life is like a strong hedge for to keep the
gardyn of the heart. that the evil beestes assaylle it not / that been the fendes
of hell to the end that they may not enter. which entende and study for to
stele and take away the tresour of vyrgynyte / and therefore ought this tresour
to be well enclosed and well kept that it be not lost. For who that leseth it
may never recover it. no more than the lamp that is broken may not be made
hole ageyn / The vj leef of vyrgynyte is perseuerau^ce that is to have ferme
purpoos to keep well that is promised to god. whereof Saint austyn says in the
book of vyrgynyte and adresseth his words to the virgyns saying. Follow ye the
lamb says he. that is Ihesu Cryst^ in keeping stronglye that which ye have
auowed to god. Do ardauntly as much as ye may / that the well of vyrgynyte
perysshe not in you. For ye may not do that thing / by which vyrgynyte may
be recouerd. if it were lost / like as we have shewde by ensaumple of the
lamp / and Saint Bernard says. estudye ye to the virtue of perseueraunce. for
she only wynneth and geteth the crown of glory. The syethe leef aforsayd
enbelyssheth and makes much fair the lylye of vyrgynyte. but it byhoueth to
have withinforth three graynes of gold. which sygnefyen iij manners to love
god. For vyrgynyte without love is like as a lamp without oil. wherefore the
fools vyrgyns by cause they filled not their lamps of this oylle. were shette
out fro the weddyng. and the wise vyrgyns that filled their lamps of this
oil entered in to the weddyng with the spouse The three manners for to love god
which ben sygnefyed by the three graynes of the lylye / saint austyn enseygneth
them when he says thus / Thou shall love god with all thyn entendement
without error / with all thy will without gaynsayeng and with all thy mind
without forgetyng. In such manner is thymage of god parfayte in a man after iij
dignytees that been in the life. That is to wete / entendement. memory. and
will. when these iij things ben well ordained to god^ then ben the three
graynes of gold of the lyly / of the gold of charity which gives bounte.
beauty. and valor of all virtue. For without this gold no virtue is tofore
god neither fair ne precyouse / Otherwise says saint bernard of the manner to
love god and says thus. O thou that art a christian man. learn how thou
ought to love god. learn to love him wisely / swetely and strongely. wisely
that thou be not deceived by nycete. Swetely that thou be not moeued by
prosperyte. Strongely that thou be not ouercomen by aduersyte / In this manner
is fair the flour delys of vyrgynyte. when she is such as is said tofore. and
this is the second reason by which thestate of vyrgynyte ought much to be
preysed for her beauty. The third reason wherefore thestate of virgynyte ought
much to be preysed is for her bounte and for the prouffyt that comes of it.
For virgynyte is a tresour of so great value that it may not be preysed. whereof
the scripture says that no thing is worthy to be compared to a chaste heart /
of the chastyte of virgynyte / for virgynyte above al other estates bears the
most grettest fruit and the most grettest proffyt. They that been in marriage
and keep it well as they ouzt to do have the xxx fold fruit. They that been in
wydowhede have the lx fold fruit. But they that keep virgynyte have the
hundred fold fruit. For like as our lord says in the gospel that the seed
that falls in good land makes fruit xxx fold. lx fold / and an hundred
fold / These iij nombres xxx / lx. and an hundred apperteyne to iij estates
toforesayd / The nombre of xxx / which is of x three times which maken xxx
apperteyneth to thestate of marriage / where ought to be kept the x comandements
of the law in the faith of the holy trynyte. The nombre of lx is more great
and is of xvj times For vj times x maken lx. and apperteyneth to thestate of
wydowhede. For in such estate ought to be kept the x comandements. and with
them ought to be accomplysshed the seven works of mercy of which we have
spoken tofore. But the nombre of an hundred which is most great and most
perfyght. for it represents a figure round. which is most parfyght and
most fair emonge the other fygures. For like as the round figure / the end
retorneth to his beginning and makes it round like a crown. Right so the
nombre of an. C. joins the end to the beginning. For x times x maken an
hundred. which sygnefyeth the crown which the wise vyrgyns hadden. and how
be it that in the state of marriage / and in the state of wydowhede may be won
the crown of glory. and have more merit anenst god than have many virgynes.
For many ben in heaven of them that have been in marriage and in wydowhede which
been more nygh to god and have more merit. than many of the vyrgynes /
Nevertheless the virgynes have a specyal crown above the crown of glory
which is common to al sayntes^ by cause the vyrgyns have a specyal vyctorye of
their bodies. For (...) to follow the lamb. what someuer way that he gooth^
that is Ihesu christ. to whom they be espowses^ they have left their carnal
espowsailles. for to be with him in thespowsaylles perdurable. There shall they
been well arrayed and nobly apparaylled of a specyal parement. so gente / so
fayr^ and so auenaunt. that no tongue may tell. and therefore I will no more say^
but that which the scripture says / that speaks of the fair parementes that
they have more especyal. than they that been of other estates toforesayd / and
yet says the scripture that they sing new songs so melodyous and so fair.
that none other sing. that been not in their estate. That new song that they
sing / sygnefyeth a new Joy and especyal merit and preysyng that they have
by cause that they have well kept their estate of vyrgynyte^ And this is the v
estate of chastyte. and the fyfthe branch of this tree.

The vj branch of the virtue of vyrgynyte capitulo Clij
THe vj estate that ought to keep the virtue of chastyte. is in the clerks
ordered for to serve in holy chyrche^ as been subdekens. dekens. prestes /
prelates / and relygyouse. All the people ben bounden to keep chastyte by many
reasons. First for the order which they have received. which requires to live
holyly. by cause that the holy sacrament of the mass is so hye and so holy.
that al they that receive it be bounden to keep chastyte for they may not marye
after that they have promised to holy church. For they be appropred to serve
god in his church. and at his altar. and treaten and touchen with their
hands the things sayntyfyed as the vessels hallowed the chalyce and corporas /
And that which is gretter wythonte comparyson the body of Ihesu Christ which
the priest sacreth / and to them it byhoueth to give it to other.

Now then owen they to be much clean and live right holyly. for reason of
the hye lord to whom they serue^ that is the saint of al saints and lord of
all lords. which hates all ordure of sin. whereof he him self says. Be ye
holy as I am holy / for such a lord such meyney. for the reason of the place
wherein they serve. This is the church which is dedycate to serve god. It is
founden that emonge the paynyms and the sarasyns. the prestes of their law
that seruen in the temple kepen chastyte. and been divided and deceuerd fro the
other by cause they should not lose their chastyte^ Much more ought to be clean
without comparyson and more chaste the priests of crystyante. that seruen to
god in his temple which is sayntefyed dedycate / and approved to serve god.
yet ought they to be more holy and clean by cause they serve at the table of
god of his cup and of his mete^ The table of god is the altar. The cup is
the chalyce. his bread and wyn is his propre body and his propre blood. Much
owen to be holy all they that such service done to god. whereof saint Poul
says that it byhoueth that a bishop and the other mynystres of holy church
be chaste and without sin / This virtue of chastyte was sygnefyed in the
old law. there where god commanded to them that ought to ete the lamb
without spotte. which sygnefyed the body of our lord Ihesu crist they should be
gyrde on they raynes. The gyrdle of the mynystres of holy church owen to be
gyrde. that is with the virtue of chastyte which restrayneth and quenches the
delytes and the vices of the flesh. wherefore god commanded to Aaron which
was priest and bishop of the law. that he and all his sons should be cladde
with lynnen clothes of chastyte. and gyrde above with whyt gyrdylles of lynnen.
Aaron and the children that serueden in the tabernacle sygnefyen the mynystres
of holy church. which owen to be cladde with lynnen roobes of chastyte.
which is sygnefyed by the whyt lynnen. For like as the lynnen towayl tofore it
be well whyt it must be beten and often wasshen / In like wise byhoueth it the
flesh to be beten and corrected by penance / and often wasshen his heart and
his conscience by very confession and repentance to the end that they might
have the whyt cote of chastyte. but this cote ought to have above the whyt
gyrdle. That is to say that chastyte ought to be straytly kept. and strayned by
abstynence as much as reason may suffer which is the boucle of this gyrdle^
Otherwise may it be said that the lynnen cote sygnefyeth chastyte of heart. The
gyrdle above sygnefyeth chastyte of body. which owes to restrain the desires
and the will of the flesh for to keep the chastyte of the soul. This same
is sygnefyed to us in the aube and in the gyrdle that the mynystres of holy
church use to clothe them when they will say mass. For they owen to be chaste
within their heart and without in the body. Much foul is the spotte of sin.
and specially of lecherye in the mynystres of holy church. For they ought to
be the eyes of holy church as says the scripture. For like as the eyes
aduysen the body and thewen to him the way by which he ought to goo. Right so
in like wise owen the prelates and all the other mynystres of holy church to
show the way of health to other / Then also as the spotte of the sin of
lechery is more foul in them tha^ in other persons. Also as the spotte that
is in the eyes is more foul and grievous than in the other members of the body.
Right so is the spotte of the sin of lecherye more foul and more peryllous
in clerks / in prelates. in relygyous and in all other people of the church
than in other folk / Also all the people of holy church ben or owen to be
myrrour and exaumple there. wherein the lay people ought to look in for to take
good doctrine in good exaumple / but when the myrrour is rusty and foul men
may well see the spotte and thordure that is in the myrrour. But he that in
such a myrrour looks / sees not the spotte that is in him self ne what is in
the myrrour which so is foul and troubled. But when the myrrour is well clear
and clean. then may one well see him self therein and know his spots. Also
when the prelate is of good life and of good fame. than ought one to take
example of good life / Also the people of holy church ought to be pure and
clean of al fylthe of sin. and ought to be much holy. by cause they cleanse
and sayntefye and halowe other. For like as says Saint Gregory. The hand that
is foul and fylthy may not well take away the fylthe fro other And the
scripture says he that is foul may not cleanse another^ That is to understand
as touching his merit. for the sacrament that is made and mynystred by the
hand of an evil mynystre is of no less value to him ne werse. ne he is no
less mighty ne virtuous to halowe them that receive it. than if they should
receive it by the hand of a good mynystre For the evil of the mynystre
appayreth not the sacrament. ne his bounte neither / and also amend it not.
But always the evil of the mynystre may empayre other people by evil example.
and also he may by his bounte edefye them by example of good life. and therefore
they that sayntefye and cleanse other / in that they mynystre the sacraments of
holy church ought to be more holy and more clean than the other. For if they
be evil they shall be more punysshed than the other. This is the syxthe estate
in which ought to be kept the virtue of chastyte.

The seventh estate of the virtue of chastyte capitulo Cliij
THe seventh estate in which ought to be kept the virtue of chastyte of heart
and of body. is the estate of relygyon For they that been in that state have
promised to god and auowed that they shall live chastely. Then they be holden
and bounden by such auowe that they may never marye. after that they ben
professyd. And if they marye after that they be professyd the marriage shall be
none / And therefore ought they to set great pain and dylygence in keeping well
their chastyte. and for their estate. which is the state of holiness and of
perfectyon. For of so much as the state is more holy of so much is the sin
of them more great and more foule^ And also as the spotte is more great and
foul and more apparaunt in a whyt robe than in another cloth. And who falls
fro most hye hurts him most grievously. and for to vaynquysshe their
aduersarye that is the devil. which much payneth him to tempte. and to make
fall in to sin them of relygyon. and more he Ioyeth when he may overcome one
of relygyon / than many of other people / For like as the au^gellys of heaven
have great Joy of the synnar when he repents him and does penance and
confession of his sins. Right so enioyen the deuyls when they may overcome a
good man and make him to fall in to sin. And when he is in great estate and
parfyght so much has the fend more Joy wha^ he may deceive him. like as the
fisshar has more great Joy to take the great fysshes than the small. we read
in the book of the lives of faders that an holy man recounted how he was
bycomen a monk. and said that he had be sone of a paynym sarazyn which was
priest of thydolles. And when he was a child on a time when he entered in to
the temple with his fader. he hid him. and there he saw a great devil that
satte in a chayer and many deuylles about him. and then came one of his
princes and adoured him. Then he that satte in the trone demanded him fro
whens he came. he answered and said that he came fro the earth and that he had
moeued and purchaced many wars and many euylles so that much people were
deed and much blood shed The master devil demanded of him in how long time
he had done this. and he ansuerd in xxx dayes^ and the master said have thou
be so long time out for to do so lyte. Then he commanded anon that he
should be beten and evil treated. After him came another devil which adoured
him as did the first and the master demanded him fro whens he came. and he
answered that he came fro the sea. where he had maad many great tempests by
which many ships were broken. and much people drowned. The master asked of
him in how long time he had done it^ he ansuerd in twenty days / Anon the
maystre commanded that he should be beten as that other was tofore. by cause he
had do no more harm in so long time / After came the third devil of whom
the maistre asked fro whens he came / and he said that he came fro a cite.
where as he had been and meued stryt and debate and had purchaced medlynges that
much people were slain. and also he had slain the husboud of a weddyng / The
maistre devil asked him in how long time he had done it. and he ansuerd in x
days. Then he comau^ded that he also should be beten. At last came another
devil which adoured the maistre devil / the prince of the deuylles demanded of
him fro whens come thou. he ansuerd that he came fro an hermyte. where he had
abyden xl year for to tempte him which was a monk in the sin of lecherye.
and he had so much labored that that nyzt he had ouercomen him and had made
him to fall in the sin of lecherye. Then the maistre devil e^braced and
kyssed him. and set a crown on his heed. and made him to sytte by him. and
said that he had done a great thing and a great prowess. Now said the good
man the monk that he had seen this and herd it. and thought that it was a
great thing to be a monk. and for this cause and vysyon he was bycom christian
and a monk / In these words aforsayd may appyere that the deuylles have great
Joy / when they may make a man of relygyon to fall in to sin. for after
that a man is in relygyon. he is like to him that is entered in to a field of
batayl for to fight against the devil and all his temptacyons / when our Lord
would be tempted of the devil he went in to deserte. For the deserte of
relygyon is a field of temptacyon^ Relygyon is called deserte. For like as
deserte is a place sharp and dry and far fro people. So ought to be the
state of relygyon sharp and of holy and parfyght life which is a strong help
and a strong armure against the fendes of hell. Sharpnes of penance is the
remedy against lecherye. For who that will quench the fire of lecherye in him
self. he ouzt to take awaye^ and withdraw fro him all the flesshly delytes.
eases. and soulaces of this world. For all relygyouse people ought to take away
and cut fro his flesh and fro al his body al delytes and worldly* eases by
fastings / by wakynges. by de^o^te wepynges. by discyplynes and by other
penau^ces. Else the fire of lecherye may not well be quenched / who that will
take a cite or a castle. he ought as much as he may to take away and
wythdrawe fro it all the vytaylles / al metes. and the water for to enfamysshe
them. For after that the castle is enfamyned and all vytaylle is take fro it.
It may not long be holden ne kept against his aduersarye. Right so the castle
of the belly. which is the fortress of the flesh. may not hold against the
spyryte when it is enfamyned by fastynges^ by abstynences and by other
penaunces. Also the estate of relygyon ought to be wythdrawen fro the world
that they that been in such estate ne feel ne retche no thing of worldly
things / For they ought to be deed to the world. and live with god as says
Saint Poule / For like as he that is deed bodyly has lost all his wits
bodyly. as seeyng^ spekyng / tastyng heeryng and smellyng / Right so owen the
relygyouse to be deed as to the world that they feel no thing that
apperteyneth to sin / so that they may verily say the word that saint Poul
thappostle says of him self. The world said he is crucyfyed to me. and I to
the world. Thappostle would say that like as the world held him for foul and
for abhomynable like as one were hanged. Ryzt so had he the world for foul and
for abhomynable. as to him that is hanged or crucyfyed for his trespace / In
like wise does he that is in suck estate does flee the world and hate it.
That is to say the couetyse and shrewdness of the world. that he feel no
thing by love ne by desire. so that his conuersacyon be in heaven. as saint
Poul says of him self / and of them that been in thestate of perfection Our
conuersacyon is in heneu / For if the body is in earth the heart is in heaven by
love and by desire / A good relygyouse person ought to have no propre in
earth. but he ouzt to make his tresour in heaven. like as says our lord in the
gospel / If thou says he wylt be perfyght* goo and selle all that thou have and
give it to the pour. And thou shalt have thy tresour in heaven which never
shall faylle. The tresour of a relygyouse man is very wylful pouerte. For the
very pouerte of the spyryte and of will is the money of which the royalme of
heaven is bought / whereof our lord says in the gospel. Blessed be the pour of
spyryte. for the Royalme of heaven is theyres. Certain who that is pour of
spyryte / that is of the will of god. he secheth not in this world no
dely^es. ne rychesses. ne honors / but put it all in forgetyng. In such wise
ought to do good relygyouse people. that will mount up in to the montaygne of
perfectyon. whereof the aungellys said to Loath when he was goon out of the cite
of Sodome^ Rest ne tarry thou not nyghe the place that thou have left. but
save thy self in the montaygne. For he that is goon out of the conuersacyon of
the world ought not to hold him nyghe the world by his will ne by his desire
/ But ought to wythdrawe him as much as he may. And to entende to his health
without lookyng bacward or behind hym^ That is for to say that he set not
ageyn his heart to the world The wife of Loath against the commandment of the
aungel beheld the cite fro whens she came out which brenned and therefore she
was t^rned in to an image of salt. The wife of Loath sygnefyeth them that after
they have left the world^ and ben entered in to relygyon / return ageyn
bacward by will and by desire / which have their body in the cloystre. but the
heart in the world They be like thymage of salt. which has but the lykenes or
semblaunce of a man^ and is as hard and cold as a stone / Right so ben such
people cold of the love of god and hard with out humor of pity and of
devotion. and they retche nothing but of the habyte of their relygyon / and no
thing of the obseruaunces and works. Thymage that was of salt sygnefyeth in
scripture wit and dyscrescyon / For like as salt gives savor to the (...).
Right so ought every relygyouse person to have wit and dyscrescio^ in his
deeds. and in his words. This image then of salt ought to give wit and
understanding and example to them that been in religyon. and after return to
that which they have left. And therefore says our lord in the gospel to his
dyscyples. Remember you of the wife of loath. That is to say. Behold ye not that
which ye have left for the love of me. lest ye lose the life of grace. like as
the wife of loath lost the life of the body by cause she looked to the place which
she had left. wherefore our lord says in the gospel who that puts his hand
to the ploughe and looks behind him. is not worthy to the kingdom of heaven.
For-lyke as he that ledeth the plough sees always tofore him to lead strayt and
to conduyte right his plough. Right so ought he to do that puts his hand
to the plough of penance or of religyon always he ought to have the eyes of
his heart tofore / That is to say his understanding and his will to that.
which is to sore him. and not behind. That is to the goods perdurable which
ought to be tofore the heart and not to the goods temporal. which ought to be
behind. Thus did Saint Poul which said that he had forgoten that / which was
behind him / That is the world and all the couetyse of the world which he
praised at naught. And went allewaye tofore him. For he had always his
entencyon and his desire to god But many men of relygyon setten the plough
tofore the oxen For many there ben. and that is their ^ommage. that more sechen
the things bodyly and worldly / than the things spyrytual / They put that
before which should be behind / that been the goods temporal tofore the goods
perdurable and spyrytuell Such relygyous persons ben in much great peril of
their dampnacyon. For they have ^ought but the habyte of their relygyon. By the
example of Saint Poul. the good relygyouse persons forgete the world / and
leave it byhynde them. and the goods perdurable they have tofore their eyen^
and goon tofore always fro virtue to v^rtu. till they come to the montayne of
Joy perdurable. where they shall see god clearly / and shall love him
perfyghtly / and shall adoure him perdurably. This is the beneurte or the yefte
of understanding. which ledeth them that kepen cle^nesse of heart and of body.
like as we have showed before. And therefore says our lord in the gospel. that
blessed ben they that been clean of heart. For they shall see god. This blessyng
begins here. for they been purged fro derknesses of error / as to the
understanding. and fro the spots of sin / as to the will. and therefore
they see god by faith enlumyned of clerenes. which comes of the yeft of
understanding. ^y which a man knows his creatour^ and all that apperteyneth
to the health of his soul / without slydyng / with out doubtyng. and without
waueryng in the faith of Ihesu Christ where they be so Joined and fermly
founded. that they may not depart them for death ne for to suffer any tormente
what someuer it be / And therefore been blessed they that be clean of heart in
this mortal life. For they have the eyes of the heart. the understanding and the
will so clear and so clean that they see god and believe him by faith ferme
and certain like as we have said tofore / wherrof our Lord said to saint
Thomas. by cause thou have seen me. thou have byleued me^ But they ben blessed
that have not seen me bodyly. and have byleued me certeynlye. but this blessyng
shall be perfyght in the life perdurable. where he that is clean of heart. which
here sees him by faith. that is always derkly^ There in his glory shall see
him face to face al clearly as says saint poule. That is the blessyng to
aungellys and to saints which see him in his precyouse vysage. to know one
god in three persons / to byholde clearly in that myrrour where al things
shynen. angellys and all the saints loken therein. and merueylen them. and taken
there their glory. and never may they be full for to look therein. For there is
all beauty. all bounte. all swetenes / and fontay^e of life perdurable. and
all that which heart may will and desire / But yet I shall say a little / For
like as says the scripture. The eyes mortal may not behold Ne ere here / Ne
heart of man think. what that god has arrayed and maad ready to his friends that
louen / seruen him and keep his commandments. and that keep them fro sin.
whereof Saint Amelme sayth^ Soul says he lift up thyn entendement there aboue^
and think as much as thou may what well. how great. and how much
delectable is that good which conteyneth in him self the Joy and the delight
of all goods / And not such Joy and such delight as is founden in
creatures. but as much more Joy. as the creator and maker is more great and
more worthy and more excellent. than his creatures. O says he thou faytour
thou man that ghost so folyly for to seche diverse goods. to thy soul and to
thy body. love thou and seche one good. wherein ben all goods. and he shall
suffyse the. For the good that god has granted and given to his friends. that
is him self which is the souerayn good. of whom comen and sourden al other
goods. as stremes that yssuen out of the quycke fontayne. Certeynlye right
blessed shall he be says saint austyn which without vylonye shall see the vysage
dyscouerd and the glory of god. and shall be transformed in to thymage of
glory. where as he shall see god as he is / The which sight is glory and
crown with out end. and all the reward and merit of saints / This shall be
all the good of man^ This says maistre hughe of saint vyctor. The man that made
all and formed. For therefore would god bycome man. which made in him self al
men blessed in body and in soul / by cause that the man saw him with the cyen
of his body in his humany^e. and that the soul saw him in his deyte. so that
he fond swetenes and delight in his creator and maker. within and without.
within in his deyte and without in his humanyte. This shall be the Joy of every
creature his Joy. his dely^e ^ life perdurable of this blessed vysyon / That is
the blessyng that they attend which keep clennesse and chastyte of heart and
of body /

Of the yefte of sapyence Capitulo Cliiij
THe last yefte. the souerayn. and the most hye^ is the yefte of sapyence or
of wysedom. which is a grace that the holy ghoost gives to the heart
contemplatyf. by which he is esprysed of the love of god. that he desires ne
secheth none other thing but to see god. to have him. to delight in him / to
love him / to honor and serve him. and dwell with him / This is the so^me of
perfection. and the end of contemplacion The yefte of understanding of which
we have spoken tofore makes god to be known and the things spyrytuel as by
sight and simple byholdynges. But the yefte of sapyence makes to feel and
know god by taste. then sapye^ce is none other thing but a sanery knowleche.
which is with savor and great delight of heart. for otherwise knows nothe the
wyn that drynketh it in a fair vyrre or glass / if he drink and taste it not
and savor it. Many phylosophres knewen god by scripture and by the creatures.
like as by a myrrour wherein they beheld by reason and by understanding his
might. his beauty. his wit and his bounte. in that which they see the
creatures that he has made so great so fair and so well ordained: Then they
knew him. by simple byholdyng of understanding and natural reason But they
never felt him by taste of right love ne by d^uocyon. Right so ben there many
christian persons. clerks and lay. which well know him by faith and by
scripture. but by cause they have their taste dysordynate by sin. they may
not feel him. no more than the seek person may find taste or savor in good
mete. The yefte of sapyence which the holy ghoost puts in a ^erfyght heart.
purges and cleanses it fro all ordure of sin. and lyfteth up so ^he
spyryte of a man that he Joins him to god by ardaunt desire of love. so that
he is al with god / there he fedeth him. there he nouryssheth him. there he
fatteth him. there he delyteth and rests him. and there he slepeth / There he
forgeteth al his trauaylles. al his flesshly desires and erthely. and him self
/ so that he remembers no thing but god whom he loves above al things.
This is the last degree of the laddre of perfectyon that Jacob saw in his sleep
which touched heaven / by which aungellys mounted and descended. The degrees
of this laddre been the seven yeftes of the holy ghoost. of which we have
spoken tofore^ By these seven degrees mounten the aungellys. These been they
that leden the life of aungellys in earth by purete and clennesse of conscyeyce.
which have the heart in heaven by very desire and holy conuersacyon. when they
prouffyte fro virtue to virtue / till they see god clearly and love him
parfyghtly. But when they be mounted unto the last degree sometime byhoueth it
them to descend by humylyte / for of so much as a good man is more parfyght
of so much is he more humble. and less preyseth him self. Then a good man
and a parfyght ought to be like as a tree which is charged with fruit. For the
more that the tree is charged and laden with fruyt^ the more he enclyneth and
boweth to the earth. In another manner may be vnderstonden that the aungellys
descenden / For the good men that leden the life of angellys in earth by their
holy life when they be mounted in to the souerayn degree of contemplacyon where
the yefte of sapyence ledeth them. so that they be Joined to god. that they
forgete all that which is under god for the great swetenes that the heart
^eleth. which is so rauysshed in god which passes al other delytes. So that
it byhoueth them often to descend fro this swetenes and such rest and fro
such delight that they feel of the comfort of god. which have give them to
souke in such sweet contemplacyon / where they that been parfyght ought to
entende. Another reason there is^ whereof it byhoueth to descend fro the hye
degree of contemplacyon where the spyryte of sapyence has led him. For the
corrupcyon of the flesh of the body of the creature humayn is so great / that
the spyryte may not in this mortal life long abide in so hye estate of
contemplacyon / ne feel that great sweetness. which passes all the great
delytes that may ^e felt in this world / like as they know that have proved
it. whereof the countrepoys of the flesh is so heavy that it draws down the
spyryte. will it or nylle it. And therefore this great swetenes that the heart
contemplatyf feleth by the yefte of sapyence in this mortal life. nys but as a
little taste by which one may assauoure and ^ele how god is sweet and sauoury.
But when he shall come to that great tavern* where ^he tonne is / and shall be
set a broche. that is in the life perdurable. there where god of pees^ of love
/ of Joy. of soulace. and of all swetenes shall be abando^ned to every person
in such wise. that al shall (...) filled. like as dauyd says in his psaulter.
For all the desires of the heart shall be accomplysshed when god shall make
descend upon his friends a floode of pees. like as says the prophet. whereof
they shall so much drink. that they shall be all drunk. Of this dronkesse
speaks Dauyd in his psaulter and says thus / Of the glory of paradys shall
all be dronken says the prophet to god. of the great plant that is in your
house. And ye shall give them drink of your swetenes and of your delyces. For
with you is the fontayne of the life perdurable. which faylleth not. That is
god him self which is the fontayne of life which may not deye. whereof sourdeth
and descends upon all the saints that been and shall be in heaven a flode of
Ioye^ of delight / and of pees so great. that al they that drynken thereof ben al
dronken. That is the pees and ^he blessyng that shall be in the world that is
to come. For which Joy to win and to have. one ought to live sobrely in
this world as says saint Austyn. For none ne drynketh of this river. ne is not
drunk of the plant of Ioye^ but if he keep sobrenes. This is the virtue that
the yefte of sapyence planteth in the heart. against thoultrage of glou^onye /
For sapyence enseygneth sobrenes like as Salamon says. which says thus
Sobrenes is a tree much precyou^ for it keeps the health of the ^oule and of
the body as scripture says. and of the oultrage of glotonnye. of etyng / of
drynkyng comen many maladyes and oftyme the death. For of ouermoche etyng and
drynkyng deyen many folk and often the death takes them sodeynlye. like as one
takes the fysshe with an hoke / that is to say the morsel in the mouth. This
virtue of sobrenes ought one to keep above all things. For the goods that it
does to him that well keeps it. First sobrenes keeps to reason and to
understanding his fredom and fraunchyse. so that it puts and takes away
dronkenesse. For he that is dronken is so surprysed of wyn. that he leseth
reason and understanding. and is like as he were drowned in ale or wine. And
when he weneth to drink the wine. the wine drynketh him. The second good that
sobrenes does. is that it delyuerth a man fro over foul seruytude / that is
fro the seruytude of the bely^ For the glotons and they that been oultragous of
wine and metes maken of their belly their god as says saint poul. Certainly he
puts him self in great fylthe. and in foul seruytude. that serves so foul
a lord as is his belly. out of which may no thing issue but fylthe and
s^ynkyng ordure. But sobrenes keeps a man in his seygnorye. For the spyryte
ought to have seynorye upon the body / And the body ought to serve the soul /
like as the chambriere serves her maystresse. and sobrete keeps this order.
The third good that sobrenes does / is that he keep well the yate of the castle
against the host of the devil. that is the mouth which is maystre yate of the
castle of the heart / which the devil assaylleth and makes war to as much
as he may / But sobrenes deffendeth the yate and thentree^ that is the mouth.
And when the yate of the mouth is open. thoost of sins entren lightly. And
for naught fyghteth he against other sins that reteyneth not his tongue / who
has this virtue of sobrenes he has the lordshyp of his body. like as a man
maystryeth the horse by the bridle. Sobrenes has the first bataylle in thoost
of the virtues and keeps and deffendeth the other virtues. wherewyth the devil
tempted first Adam our first fader and Eve our first mother. that was toward the
mouth that they should ete of the fruit which god had deffended. and the devil
overcame them when they consentyd to the temptacyon. For to keep sobrenes
nature enseygneth us and the holy scripture / Nature techeth us. For emonge
beestes a man has the least mouth after his body. Also a man has his members
double / as two eyes. two eeres / but he has but one mouth. and therefore
nature techeth us that one ought to ete and drink lytyl and sobrely. For
nature is sustained with little mete. and by ouermoche mete is often beten down.
The holy scripture enseyneth sobrenes in many manners by many examples. like as
they may see that connen understand scripture / and byholden the lives of
saints. Also every creature techeth to us sobrenes^ For in all nature god
has set a right mesure. which always holds the moyen between ouermoche
and over little. after that which reason enlumyneth and enseygneth by the grace
of god / For in these temporal goodes^ that which is ouermoche to one^ is little
to another. That which should be oultrage to a pour man / should be little
oftymes to a rich man / but sobrenes and attemperaunce setten oueral mesure.
As well in spirituel goods as in fastings in wakynges and in other works of
virtues which been done and made for the love of god and for the health of the
soul as much as reason will / The virtue of attemperaunce is of sobrenes / This
virtue keeps mesure resonabl^* not only in etyng and drynkyng but in all
virtues. like as says Saint Bernard. For this virtue sets al thoughts and
all the menynges of the heart / and all the wits of the body under the
lordshyp of right reason. as says Tullius the wise man / so that reason
enlumyned by the yefte of sapyence. holds in pees the lordshyp of the heart
and of the body. And this is the end and thentencyon of al virtues / that the
heart and the body be well ordained to god^ so that god only be lord and
souerayn in such maner^ that al be in his obedyence. And this makes sobre the
love of god which puts him with all the heart to the will of god. whereof
Saint Austyn says. that the virtue of attemperaunce and of sobrenes is a love
which keeps him in entyernesse without corrupcyon. and wythdraweth us fro the
love of the world. which troubles the heart and puts it to disease / and
takes fro him right knowleche of god and of him self. like as a person sees
not clearly in water troubled. But the love of god which is pure and clean.
and is departed fro al erthely love and fro carnal affection sets the heart
in pees. For it sets it in his propre place. That is in god. there he
rests / there he is in pees. Ne he has no pees ne Joy ne rest but in god
/ whereof our lord says in the gospel / ye shall be oppressyd in this world.
but in me ye shall find pees. And Saint austyn said to god. Lord mine heart may
not be in pees unto the time it rest in the / such love comes not of an
erthely heart. ne of the maryce of this world. But it descends fro that hye
roche upon which is set and founded the great cite of heaven and of holy
church. That is Ihesu christ. which al is set and founded fermely by true
faith that been the holy hertes of good men. Fro this hye roche descends that
fontayne of love in to the heart that is well purged and taken away fro the love
of the world / This well is so clear that he knows him self and his maker.
like as one sees him self in a fontayn well clear and clean. upon this fo^tayne
he rests and the heart fast by. after the trauayl of good works. So as we
read of our lord Ihesu christ. that when he had so much goon that he was weary.
he satte down and rested him upon the well This is the fontayne upon which a
good heart that will save him self-resteth him in the love of god. This fontayne
is so sweet that he that drynketh thereof forgeteth al other swetenes and al
other savor. and therefore it is so sweet and good to drink. for of so much
as the fontayne feleth better the erthe^ so much is it more holsom and better
to drink. This is the fontayne of wit and of savor / For he that drynketh
thereof. he knows. feleth and sauoureth the great swetenes that is in god. and
that is the souerayn wit of man. to know well his maker / and to love him.
dread him. serve and honor him with al his heart. For without this
phylosophye. all other wit nys but folly. Such wit sets the holy
ghoost in the heart / when he gives the yefte of sapyence. which fedeth and
nourissheth the heart with spyrytuel Joy / and makes it drunk with his holy
love. that is the wit which the holy ghoost sets in the heart that is well
purged and clensyd fro all ordures of sin like as tofore is said. This
spirytuel wit that comes of the parfyght love of god makes the heart sobre
and attempred in all things by mesure. so that the heart that is in such
estate is in pees like as it may be in this mortal life. For in this world none
may live without tournoyes and bataylle of temptacyon. which god sends for
to preue his knights / and by cause they can use the arms of virtue / For
otherwise they might not be good knights. if they were not proved how they can
resyste to temptacions. And men be woned to make tournoyes in time of pees /
but when a good knyzt has ouercomen the tournoye. he retorneth home to his
house. and there he rests him at his ease. Right so does the good heart when he
has well foughten and ouercomen the tournoye of te^ptacio^s and well strongely
resisted them. Then he comes ageyn to him self and rests in god. which
