comfort him after his trauayll which he has resysted against the sins. so
that he forgeteth there al his trauaylle. and thinks on no thing but on god
in whom he syndeth all that he desires / This is the fruit that the tree of
sobrenes bears which comes of the yefte of sapyence. like as I have showed
tofore. Sobrenes nys noue other thing. but to keep right mesure in all things.
and in vij manners ought a person to keep mesure. which ben like to seven
degrees by which grows and prouffyteth the tree of sobrenes.

Of the first degree of sobrenes and of mesure capitulo Clv
THe first degree of sobrenes is that a man ought to set mesure in his
understanding / Specially in the points of the artycles of the faith. he
passes mesure which will seche reason natural. in that which is above
reason. and above the understanding of a man / as done the heretykes and
myscreau^tes which will mesure their feyth after their understanding but they
ought to mesure their understanding and reason. unto the mesure of the faith as
done good christian men. Therefore says saint poul. that a man should not be wise
more than faith bears. but by sobrenes after the mesure of the faith that god
has given to us. and salamon says to his sone. fair sone says he put in thy
wit mesure. that is to say be thou not of thyn owen propre wit / so fyxed
in thy presumpcion. but that thou bow and enclyne the for to believe good
counceyl. and thou leave thyn own wit for to obey to him that is more wise
than thou art. and in especyal in the artycles of the faith a man ought to leave
his own wit and his understanding to bow and enclyne. and also put him self
in seruage of the faith. as says saint poul. and not for to enserche ne
inquire naturell reason there where as is none. as don the melancolyous men
which ben like to him that secheth muskles emonge frosshes. or he that secheth
here in the egg. or under the hyde.

The second degree of sobrenes and of mesure capitulo Clvj
THe second degree of sobrenes and of mesure / is that one put mesure in
thappetyte. and in the desire of his will so that he late not the rain of the
bridle ouermoche at large that he run not after the desire of his flesh. ne
to the couetyse of the world. whereof the wise man says in the scripture Ne
ensyewe not says he thy couetyses ne the desires of thy body. ne of thy
flesh / And beware and keep the that thou accomplysshe not thy will / For if
thou do to thyn heart his desires / thou shall make Joy to the fendes of
hell. like as he that does to his aduersarye against whom he must fight when
he yeldeth him vaynquysshed to him. he yeldeth him ouercomen of the devil that
consents to evil desires. And therefore says saint Petre thappostle. I
conjure you as estraungers and pylgryms. that ye make abstyne^ce of flesshly
desires anh keep you well / For they make their bataylle and war against the
soul. He that is a pilgrim and a stranger is out of his land and contre.
And is in the contre where as there be many theuys and robbeurs that espyen the
pylgryms and lain in a wait in the ways / wherefore he ought to keep him well
that he fall not in their hondes^ and think how he may goo surely. All the
good men in this world ben strangers and pylgryms. They be strangers. for
they ben out of their contreye. that is heuen^ which is the heritage to good
men / They be pylgryms for they think not but to perform their Iourneyes.
till they come to their heritage. That is the cite of heaven. which the good
pylgryms sechen as says saint poul^ which have not. ne entende not / ne will
not have any heritage in this world. Such pylgryms as will goo surely. see that
they put them self in good company and in sure conduyt. The good company
which ledeth the right way and conduyteth surely is faith and love. Faith
shows the way to pylgryms^ And love be^eth him so that the way greueth him
not or litel. who that has such company has no care ne retcheth of theuys
which awayten the wayes^ They ben the deuylles which taken and robben all
them that goon not in such company. Tho ben they that will here done the will
of their body / and accomplysshe their desires / and bryngen them self in the
net of the deuylles of hell / Faith and the love of god wythdraweth the heart
fro evil thoughts and fro evil desires that they consent not thereto. like as
one holds the hawke by the gesses. to the end that he flee not at his will /
And if he be not retained by the gesses of faith and love. he flees
perylously. so that he perysshe and falls often in the net of the byrdar of
hell / That is the devil which ne secheth ne entendeth but for to take good
men. Therefore the good men and wise ought to restrain their will and their
evil desires by sobrenes and attemperau^ce^ whereof the wise Seneke says. if
thou wylt get the virtue of sobrenes and of attemperaunce / thou must put fro
the and take away thy desires. and set a bridle against thy couetyses. For
like as a man holds an horse by the bridle. that he goo not at his will /
Right so ought one to reteyne his heart. his desires. and his will. by the
bridle of sobrenes and of attemperaunce^ that he abandonne him not ne give him
self all over to the vanyte and to the couetyse of the world.

The third degree of sobrenes and of the virtue of attemperaunce capitulo Clvij
THe third degree of the virtue of sobrenes and of attemperaunce is to set and
keep mesure in words / whereof Salamon says that the wyle and well attempryd
mesureth his words. And Saint Iherome says that by the points of words is
the life preuyd. That is to say. after the words may one know the wit and
^he folly of a man. like as an hog or a swyn is known by the tongue / if he
be hool or mezel. And therefore says the wise man in the scripture. That the
words of a wise man be peysed in a balaunce. that is to say that a wise man
ought to peyse his words in the balaunce of reason and of dyscrescion. that he
be not reprehended There ben sum people that may not be stylle ne keep them
fro spekyng. be it true or be it lesyng. which ben like to a water mylle
without skluys that always tourneth after the course of the water. For they have
as many words as water at mylle^ But the wise men set the skluys of
dyscrecyon for to reteyne the water / fro folisshe words that they pass not
the mylle of the tongue. And therefore says the wise man in the scripture.
Reteyne thy words in the skluys of dyscrescyon^ For like as says Salamon. who
suffers the water to have his course at will. it is often cause of plee. and of
stryf and of many euylles that comen of a shrewd tongue. like as I have said
tofore in the traytye of vices / where as I have spoken of the sin of the
tongue. Therefore says the wise man in scrypture^ Put says he thy words in the
balaunce. and a good brydel and good kepar to thy mouth. And take heed that
thou fall not by the tongue tofore thyn enemies which lain in awayte for
tespye the / who that peyseth not his words in the balaunce of dyscrescyon /
and reteyneth not his tongue by the bridle of reason / which owes to
wythdrawe his tongue fro folysshe words. he falls lightly in to the hands
of his enemies. They been the deuylles of hell which every day and night
awayten and espyen us. when thenemyes which warren the castle find the yate
open. they entren lightly. Right so the deuylles which warren the castle of the
heart / wha^ they find the yate open that is the mouth. they take lightly the
castle. And therefore says dauyd in the psaulter. I have set good guard to my
mouth against mine enemy. that is against the devil / The gar^e of my mouth is
reason and dyscrescyon. which examyne the words tofore that they issue out of
the mouth. That is the balaunce of the wise word as I have said tofore. Now
ought the word to be peysed tofore that it be spoken. And it ought to be
known that truth holds the word right. Truth accords the entencyon of
the heart. and the word of the mouth to gydre. so that the mouth say nothing
but truth. like as it is in the heart. This brau^che ought not to hang on the
right side ne on the lift. For neither for love pryue. ne for prouffyt
temporal. ne for hate of other. ought not to be left to say the truth.
there as it ought to be said and need is. Ne lesyng ne falsenesse ought not to
be said for no person.

Of the iiij degree of sobrenes and of mesure capitulo Clviij
Like as a person ought to keep mesure in spekyng / Right so ought be to keep
mesure in heeryng and herkenyng / For as much may one sin in evil heryng /
as in evil spekyng. Then he that gladly hereth to speak evil of another. is
parto^ner and fellow of the sin of him that says it. For none ought to say
gladly evil of another. specially to a great man / if he wene that it pleseth
to him that hereth it. whereof an holy man says. that there should be none
myssayer ne evil spekar. if none would here him. These great and hye lords
ought well to keep them and take heed what they here and what they believe. for
they find but few that tell them truth / And flateryes and lesynges ben
great chepe in their courts / The grettest derthe that is about these great
lords is of veryte and of truth. and therefore been they often deceived / For
they here gladly and byleuen lightly that which pleases them / Seneke says
that there lacks no thing to great lords but true spekars. and sayers of
truth / For of liars they have great plente^ A man ought to have his eres
open. for to here gladly the good words. which auayllen and prouffyten to the
health of the soul. And a man ouzt to have his eres closed and stopped to
lewd and folisshe words which may noye and grieve. and may not help. whereof
the wise man says in the scripture. Stop thyn eres with thorns. and herkene
not the evil tongue. The evil tongue is the tongue of the serpent of hell.
which the evil sayers bear. and enuenymeth him that hereth them / Against
such tongues one ouzt to stop his eres with thorns of the dread of our
lord. or of the thorns. of which our lord was crowned in remembrance of his
passyon^ they should not gladly here the evil sayers. ne the flaterers. ne lewd
words ne dyshonest / In another manner may this word be vnderstonden. Stop
thyn eres with thorns. The thorns that pricken. sygnefyen hard words / by
which one ought to repreue the evil sayers. and show to them that they will not
gladly here them. There is a serpent which is called in latin as^^s which is
of such nature that he stops one of his eres with the earth. And that other
ere he stops with his (...) to the end that he here not thenchauntour. This
serpent enseygneth to us a great wysedom. that we should not here thenchauntour.
That is the flaterer / the liar / and evil sayers which enchaunte often the
rich men. who that would stop one of his eerys with earth / and that other
with his taylle. he should not retche to be enchaunted of the devil. ne of evil
tongues. He stops one of his eeres with earth* that thinks that he is of
the earth. and to the earth shall return. And thus a man remembers his
Infyrmyte and his vylete wherefore he ought to humble him self and no thing
preyse That other ere he ought to stop with his taylle for remembrance of
death which he ought much to fere and dread. who that thus could and would
stop his eres. he would not gladly here ne remember. ne say. ne herkene
words that should dysplease god. Thus shall he be well mesured in heryng in this
fourth degree of sobrenes and of attemperaunce.

The v degree of sobrenes and of mesure Capitulo Clix
THe fyffhe degree of the virtue of sobrenes. is to keep mesure in habyte in
vestymentes^ and in precyouse roobes where a man or woman passes often mesure.
and does great oultrage. and by cause that the making of them is over
curyouse^ or over proud or over great and excessyf of dyspences it is great
sin oftymes and causes many other to do sin and in such things one ought
to keep mesure. For if over precyons and over curyous array were not sin. our
lord would not have spoken so hardly in the gospel. ayenste the evil rich man
which clad him so proudly with soft byse and precious purpre. And certeynly he
is much a fool^ and a child of wit. that of a gown. robe. or what someuer
precious clothyng it be / that is proud thereof / for there is none of what so
hye estate he be / but that he is cladde and arrayed of deed beestes and for to
consydere well. it is all but vanytee and fylthe. and al bycometh ordure.
Certeynly he or she should well be holden for a fool that would be proud to bear
the habyte or the vesture which should not be but as a sign. and a memoryal of
the shame of his fader. and of his sin / This is the usage of clothes. which
was never found but for the sin of Adam our first fader. and of Eve our
first mother. for to cover their confusyon and ours. wha^ we see a biere of a
deed corpse. which is couerd and apparaylled above / It is a sign that there
is within a deed body. Right so it happeth oftymes that under these fair
robes. the soul is deed by sin. Specially in them that gloryfye them and ben
proud. If the pecock be proud of his taylle. or the cock of his crest^ / it
is no meruaylle. for nature has given it to them / and they do after their
nature / But a man or a wyman that has wit and reason. which knows well
that nature has not given to him such a robe or gown he ought not to be
proud of the arayement of his body. which is not but of deed beestes^ or of
that which comes fro the earth. ne also of the queyntys^ or parements that be
in his heed. Therefore says the wise man in the scripture / Ne glorefye the not
in fair roobes. And Saint Poul says that the wymmen ought to array them with
sobrenes and mesure. That is to say by mesure without oultrage. after that
thestate of the person requires. certeynly it is not with out oultrage when
a person has for his body so many gowns and roobes that many pour men
might be sustained of the surplus and of it which is ouermoche. yet if they
were given at last for gods love. it should be somewhat / but they be given
to rybauldes which is so great sin. Therefore ought to be kept in such
things mesure and good ordenaunce. after that / that the state of the person
requires. as I have said tofore.

The vj degree of the virtue of sobrenes and of attemperaunce capitulo Clx
THe syxthe degree of sobrenes and of attemperau^ce. is that eueryche keep
mesure in good manner / whereof Seneke says. if thou art sobre and attemperate^
take good head that the moeuynges of thyn heart and of thy body be not foul ne
dysauenaunte / For of the dysordynaunce of the heart comes the dysordynaunce of
the body / Sum be so chyldysshe and of so nyce manner. that they make them
self be holden for a fool. It apperteyneth to a man of value which is in great
and hye estate. that he be well ordained and well amesured in all his deeds and al
his sayenges. and of fair and good countenance to fore al people. so that none
take evil example of him / and that they be not holden for a fool^ For as a
philosopher says. A child of age / and a child of wit and of manners ben
all one. and the scripture says that a child of an hundred year shall be
cursyd. That is to say that he that is of great age. and lives as a child
shall be cursyd. whereof saint Poule says of him self when I was a child I did
as a child. but when I came to the age of a par^yght man I left my
chyldehode. For who that holds a man of age for a child. he holds him for
a fool. And therefore says saint poul. Be not a child of wit But in malyee
be little as a child. which has no malice / Now is it then a fair thing /
honest. prouffytable and honorable and specially to great men of hye estate
to keep mesure reasonable. in countenance and in all his governance. and that
he be well ordained ouerall tofore god and tofore the pople. And this is the vj
degree of this tree.

The seventh degree of the virtue of sobrenes and of attemperaunce Capitulo Clxj
THe vij degree of the virtue of attemperaunce and of sobrenes is to keep mesure
of ouermoche drynkyng and etyng. for thoultrage of etyng and drynkyng does
much harm to the body and to the soul. like as I have said tofore. Therefore
says our lord in the gospel. take good head that your hertes be not grieved ne
charged with glotonnye ne drunkenness. That is to say that ye do no oultrage
of etyng and drynkyng. Sobrenes keeps mesure in etyng and drynkyng that he do
none oultrage. Of thoultrages that a person does in etyng and drynkyng / I
have spoken tofore where as is treated of vices. there as I spoke of the sin
of glotonnye. to which this virtue of sobrenes and of attemperaunce whereof I
have here spoken is contrary specially. whereof I will now no more say. Now have
thou herd whereby this tree of sobrenes and attemperaunce g^oweth and
proussyteth. And if thou wylt know the branches of this tree. byholde the
other virtues which be contained in th^s book* and thou shalt find oueral
this virtue / For as I have said tofore this virtue is such that it sets
mesure in all things. The virtues of which I have spoken tofore been
branches of this virtue. for it shows it self in all the other. wherefore I
will set none other branches but the virtues toforesayd. This tree bears
much fair fruit. That is pees of the heart like as I have tofore shewed^ For
he that has this virtue. he has his heart dysseuered fro the love of the world.
and is Joined to god by charity / that is the dear love of god which puts
al other things in oblyuyon. which be not ordained to god And in such manner
the heart rests in god / where he has all his comfort and his Joy. that he
thinks on none other delyte^ Such comfort and delight sets the holy ghoost
in the heart that is parfyte in the virtue of sobrenes and of attemperaunce.
which comes of the yefte of sapyence. like as I have said tofore. Certeynly
who that my^t have such pees of the heart. and feel that he rested in god /
which is the end and the accomplysshement and the su^me of all good desires he
should be well blessed in this world and in that other. For then should he win
that blessyng that god promyseth in the gospel to them that keep this pees
entyerly without brekynge when he says blessed be the peasyble. For they shall
be called the sons of god. They be peasyble says saint austyn that ordeyne
and setten all the moeuynges of the heart. under the seignor^ of right reason of
the spyryte. they be called by right the sons of god / for they bear the
semblaunce of their fader. which is god of pees and of love so says saint
poul. Then pees and love of god is the thing that mooost pleseth god. and
makes a man reasonable and resemble to god. and the contrary to the devil
which is enemy of god / Also they be called the sons of god For they follow
their fad^r more nyghe than the other. For pees and love follow them more nyghe
than any other virtue Also they say their hours to their fader Ihesu Christ. For
god came not in to this world but for to make pees between god and man / between
man and aungel. between man and him self. for when he was borne the aungellis
^ongen for the pees that god had brought in to the earth / Glia in excelsis
etc^ and therefore that the peasyble people seche no thing. and purchacen but
pees as much as they may. toward god. toward their neighbor and toward them
self / they be called specially the sons of god. for they do the works of
their fader. Therefore then by cause they be the sons of god. ben they
blessed in this world by specyal grace. but this blessyng shall be blessed when
they shall be in peasyble possessyon of heritage of god their fader. that is of
the royame of heaven where they shall be in sure pees and in parsyght pees /
where al their desires shullen be accomplysshed. There shall not mow be evil ne
sorrow ne aduersyte ne defaulte. But habundaunce of all goodes^ and plente of
Joy and glory without end* That shall be pees honorable pees delectable /
pees perdurable and pees which surmounteth all wit as says Saint Poule.
And sithe this pees passes all wit and sense it passes all words. For
heart may not think. ne tongue deuyse. ne ere here the pees and the glory that
god keeps to his friends. and therefore I can not say that thing that may be
suffysau^t to the lawde and preysyng thereof. whereof now I will say no more. But
here I shall fynysshe and make an end of my matere to the praysyng and lawde of
our lord. to whom be given al honor. which bring us in to his company /
there / where as is life perdurable Amen.

THis book was compyled and made at request of king Phelyp of France in the
year of thyncarnacyon of our lord / M.CC^lxxix. and translated or reduced out
of frensshe in to english by me wyllyam Caxton. at reques^e of a worshipful
merchant and mercer of london. which Instauntly required me to reduce it for
the well of all them that shall read or here it. as for a specyal book to know
al vices and branches of them. and also al virtues by which well vnderstonden
and seen may dyrecte a person to everlasting bliss. which book is called in
frensshe. le liver Royal^ that is to say the ryal book. or a book for a king.
For the holy scripture calls every man a king. which wisely and parfytly can
govern and dyrecte him self after virtue. and this book shows and enseygneth
it so subtylly. so shortly^ so perceyuyngly and so parfyghtly. that for the
short comprehencion of the noble clergy and of the right great substance.
which is comprysed therein. It may and ought to be called well by right and
quycke reason above al other books in frensshe or in english. the book ryal
or the book for a king. and also by cause that it was made and ordained at
request of that right noble king Phelyp le bele king of France. ought it to
be called Ryall / as tofore is said. which translacion or reducyng out of
frensshe in t^ english was achyeued. fynysshed and accomplysshed the (...) of
Septembre in the year of thyncarnacyon of our lord. ^CCCC.lxxxiiij / And in the
second year of the Regne of King Rychard the third /
